An Unexpected Visitor

by ZimEyebright

Summary

The Darkhold's magic wavers for a mere moment as Wanda completes her enchantment over the town of Westview, yet a mere moment is all it takes for the shroud of Agatha's secrecy to slip and for Rio to find her.

Agatha's camouflage fails long before Wanda steals her magic, Rio find her at the beginning of Wandavision, chaos ensues.

X

Rio however, didn’t look upset at all to see her. If anything she looked thrilled, shooting a wolfish grin at Agatha over Wanda’s shoulder, as if to say found you bitch .

“Hello,” Wanda’s voice, which startled Agatha back into the present, was both infuriatingly pleasant and welcoming, “can I help you with something?”

Rio’s sharp grin remained in place as those dark eyes of hers continued their slow perusal of Agatha's figure, taking her in from the bottom of her kitten heels, to the perfectly pinned dark curls around her face. At long last, her gaze slid away from holding Agatha hostage to answer Wanda’s question.

“Hi neighbour, I was just passing by and thought it polite to introduce myself. I’m Rita Valdez, I live at number 17, just right down the street from here”.

A Characteristic Moment

The energy source had been easy enough to sniff out, like a bloodhound on a fox she had found it quickly.

It had turned out to be a witch, a single witch, who whilst in the throes of unbearable grief, had bewitched an entire town to play make believe with her, like a spoiled child demanding creative control of the games at recess.

It was hilarious really, how power in different hands could be used for different means. This particular witch for example, had used it to make real-life dolls of her neighbours which was an utter waste of such power. Yet the thought of it in more capable hands, in more knowledgeable hands, well, it would be unstoppable.

From there the question was born, the question of how .

How had this witch gathered such power within her palms. What had she traded, sold, bartered, or even stolen to gain power enough that her magic practically conjured itself, running on the conception of a thought, rather than the rituals of casting that Agatha herself had been taught and depended on for centuries.

She knew then that this wouldn’t be a quick job; it would take time and it would take patience.

The time needed, Agatha had plenty of. The patience however would be a stretch, yet for power like that, she would do what needed to be done.

It hadn’t taken long to set herself up as a long-term resident of Westview. Just another neighbour who had been ensnared by an evil witch’s spell, who was amongst the ranks of people who could claim the title “victim”.

Ralph had been easy enough to enchant, man-child that he was. All she had to do was ensure the wi-fi didn’t go down, keep his fridge stocked with sugary snacks, and he would stay where she had put him. She was certain she had never known quite as content a prisoner as that airhead.

His house would do as a base, although she had several severe opinions on the upholstery and the artwork was a bit bleak, almost morbid, which was saying something considering the fact she was an actual witch.

Her timing, fortunately, could not have been better, as she had managed to thread herself into the fabric of Westview just as those final scarlet tendrils had finished transforming every modern feature into it’s 1950’s equivalent.

Looking down, Agatha was begrudgingly pleased to find herself dressed in a vintage swing dress, quite similar in fact, to the types of dresses she had chosen for herself during that actual decade. The colours of the chequered material were still a mystery to her however, as every shade of colour other than black, white, and grey had been strained from the town, like soap bubbles from a sponge.

Deciding to have some fun whilst undercover she gathered up a large potted plant from Ralph’s hallway, slapped a ribbon on it, and bustled over to greet the neighbours.

After all, the sooner she started to unpick Wanda’s mind, the sooner she would be able to gather all of that delicious power into her chest and wreak havoc.

Her first interaction with Wanda was going just as Agatha desired; she asked her questions, ran circles around the other woman and poked at her façade, eager to see how this all-powerful witch might twitch at having some of her less than perfect surfaces scuffed with questions pertaining to wedding rings and birthdays.

Unfortunately though, that was as far as she got before her plan was derailed like a train careening off the tracks, for there was another knock at the door; three sharp raps of knuckles against wood.

Wanda looked surprised, as though shocked that her well-crafted sitcom was going off script.

They both paused, unsure. Agatha glanced between Wanda, the door, and then at the faceless camera man for a cue or a hint.

“Well, who could that be?” Wanda’s curiously polite, perfectly poised house-wife tone rang out into the empty space between them.

With quick feet she stepped up to the front door and pulled it open. Immediately her face lifted into a courteous smile as the person on the doorstep was a stranger to her.

Not to Agatha though, not at all .

For it was Rio Vidal, the bane of her existence, stood in the doorway, silhouetted by bright sunlight, looking for all intents and purposes like a long-lost star of the golden screen. Her dark hair was pulled up and away from her face in a side part, lightly curled and falling just above her shoulders. And Unlike Wanda and herself, Rio was dressed in tailored capris, with a snug white shirt neatly tucked in to the waistband of her trousers.

Like everything else, she was shrouded in the black and white colouring of 1950s network television, but this, if anything, simply amplified her beauty, causing the already naturally dark shades of her hair and eyes to pop against the neutrally grey background surrounding her.

It only took a few short milliseconds for Agatha to register all of this information, for in the next few, her lips were drawing back in a fierce sneer and she was choking back a furious scream at having her ex-wife, of all people, show up unannounced.

She hadn’t seen Rio Vidal for over a century, not that the distance of time nor geography actually made the pain of that unhealed gouge in her heart ache any less. If anything, it made the history of it all the heavier.

Rio however, didn’t look upset at all to see her. If anything she looked thrilled, shooting a wolfish grin at Agatha over Wanda’s shoulder, as if to say found you bitch .

Agatha felt her stomach plummet then as evidently something had changed in Westview, something she had been unaware of. Something must have caused a weakness, or a breach in the Darkhold’s shroud of magic, that cape of darkness that had kept her hidden from Rio for so long.

Shit .

“Hello,” Wanda’s voice, which startled Agatha back into the present, was both infuriatingly pleasant and welcoming, “can I help you with something?”

Rio’s sharp grin remained in place as those dark eyes of hers continued their slow perusal of Agatha's figure, taking her in from the bottom of her kitten heels, to the perfectly pinned dark curls around her face. At long last, her gaze slid away from holding Agatha hostage to answer Wanda’s question.

“Hi neighbour, I was just passing by and thought it polite to introduce myself. I’m Rita Valdez, I live at number 17, just right down the street from here”.

Her voice was as dark and silky as it had been on the day they had met all those long years ago, and Agatha was proud of the way she stopped herself from shivering at hearing it again.

Wanda retained her expression of neighbourly friendliness, although the twitch of her eyebrow indicated that Rio’s sudden arrival and presence in her false world was as much a surprise to her as it had been to Agatha. Still, she was polite as ever when responding to Rio's introduction.

“Oh well isn’t that sweet, and such wonderful timing too. I'm Wanda, come on in!”

Wanda span with one hand still on the door handle and the other gesturing in front of herself, indicating for Rio to step inside before sweeping it outwards in Agatha's direction. Rio, staring at Agatha the entire time with a dark glare, stepped through the door to follow Wanda towards the couch, where she was quick to sprawl out, sitting not at all like a lady from the 1950s would.

“You see Rita, Agnes also thought it a good time to drop by and say hello,” Wanda’s smile grew as she fell into the rhythm of her character, allowing the sharp edges of reality to be rubbed away by the false personality she had assigned herself, “I won’t worry over introducing you ladies, as surely you already know one another!”

Wanda laughed first and Agatha forced a loud bark of laughter only a few moments too late, intent as she was to continue on with her plan, even with the unexpected issue of Rio Vidal turning up as "Extra Number 7" in another witches absurd grief fantasy.

Rio didn’t laugh at all, but she did widen her grin to show more of her teeth. It would have been unnerving if Agatha didn’t still find it attractive.

Damn her.

“We sure do know each other, very well indeed,” Rio’s voice dropped a few octaves and the innuendo in her words was as clear as the day was bright.

Agatha jumped in, speaking through gritted teeth, “Oh Rita, how lovely it is for you to drop by so... unexpectedly ”.

Rio stared at her, eyes intent and possessive in their perusal of her, “I would have dropped by much sooner if I could have”.

Her meaning was stark and the message between her words was clear. Agatha felt a mixture of emotions start pooling in her stomach: fear, apprehension, concern. All of those feelings were ones she had might have expected to feel at Rio's sudden reappearance in her life, yet what surprised her more were the other emotions swirling in amongst the rest; dashes of joy, flashes of nostalgia, and a sprinkling of relief at seeing her again. It was a confusing mess and Agatha felt it sensible to retreat, to take some space to reassess Westview’s chessboard now another player had been added into the mix so suddenly.

Slapping both hands on her knees, she got to her feet with a bright, overly loud tone, “well, I had better be on my way. I have a whole turkey cooking in the oven and I just know Ralph won’t even notice the house is on fire until the television starts melting”.

Agatha swept to the door, addressing Wanda over her shoulder, “feel free to pop by for a cool glass of iced tea whenever the notion takes you hon, I can’t wait to get to know you better. I’m sure we will be life-long lady friends”.

Choosing not to say farewell to Rio and instead simply ignore her presence, Agatha grasped the door handle, along with the belief she had made a swift escape, when a hand weaved between her arm and the dip in her waist, trapping her own beneath it against the cool metal.

“I’ll walk you back and make sure you get home safe to Ralph ,” Rio’s voice was a whisper, so close she could feel the exhale of her words against the hot skin on the back of her neck. Agatha became all too aware then of the proximity of the body behind her, of it's warmth. Far closer than necessary in her opinion.

Wriggling slightly to free her hand, she drew her elbow forward before pushing it back harshly into Rio’s diaphragm. In order to cover the violence of her actions, she shot Wanda an overly shocked expression, leaning into the slapstick comedy that was so well adored during this era of television.

She felt Rio's hand loosen over her own and heard a small grunt the moment her elbow made contact, which was then promptly followed by the laugh track Wanda had somehow rigged to run whenever something remotely humorous happened.

“That’s quite alright toots, I know the way”.

Rio’s hand tightened over hers again, her nails digging in sharply against the skin of Agatha's hand, “I insist ”.

Realising there was no way out of this situation without physically fighting with her ex-wife, which wouldn’t be the first time nor the last, she sighed heavily, managing to claw a smile back onto her face.

After all, she didn’t really want to fight with Rio in front of Wanda and break character so soon into her scheme, that would be risking her shot at snatching all of that lovely power.

“Fine then hon, but only to my garden gate. I don’t need the neighbours making up rumours about me and my gal pal, alright?”

She glanced over her shoulder to study Rio’s expression, which she could see was wildly amused at Agatha's attempt at appearing straight.

“Rumours are ghosts of the truth,” she felt Rio’s nose nuzzle closer, disturbing the curls styled over her ear, “isn’t that what they say?”

Coughing loudly, Agatha threw herself backwards in order to pull the door open, managing as she did so to loosen Rio’s hold on her hand. Taking a few desperate steps forward she put some much needed space between her body and Rio’s.

Stumbling slightly in her fluster, she managed a final, “farewell Wanda, I’ll see you real soon. I’ll bring over a tuna and Jell-O pie for you and your husband to enjoy together, the Jell-O really absorbs that fishy taste, you won’t be able to get enough,” before beginning to storm back down the pathway, mumbling the entire way about rogue ex-wives and stupid green witches.

Rio was hot on her tail, she knew this because she could hear her laughing as she started to skip after her, prancing from one side of the street to the other.

She didn’t bother even attempting to insist the green witch leave her at the garden gate as she had asserted at Wanda’s house. Instead, she simply flew up her own pathway and slammed her front door open, leaving it swinging on it’s hinges, knowing that it was futile closing it anyway; Rio would just climb through the window or down the chimney if she did try and shut her out.

The moment they were alone and Agatha had spun around in her living room, fists clenched and crackling with purple, Rio shot her a dangerous grin and jumped, using the momentum of her body weight to push Agatha backwards and up against the wall, drawing that damn knife she insisted on carrying everywhere with her so she could press it against the soft skin between her clavicles.

“I’ve missed you,” Rio said, pitching her voice up girlishly.

“I hate you,” Agatha spat through gritted teeth.

“How long has it been Agatha?”

“Not long enough”.

Rio’s face darkened as the tip of her blade pressed more firmly against Agatha’s skin, causing her to wince slightly at the sting of pain.

“You hid from me, you wrapped yourself up in all that dark magic and you hid yourself away from me ”.

Agatha felt something she had felt only rarely in her long, long life: Guilt. Tendrils of the stuff started to claw up her throat, not so much at Rio’s words, but at the expression on her face, at the fury in her eyes that had so clearly been born from heartbreak.

Agatha knew why she had done it though, and she stood by that why even now.

It was for the space she had so desperately needed after losing Nicky, after having him ripped away from her.

Yet, she had always known her and Rio’s relationship had been a co-dependent one. After all, the pain she had felt whilst being the executioner of their strange dynamic had been catastrophic enough, so she could only imagine the tsunami of fury and hurt that Rio would have experienced over all these years as the side of the coin who didn’t get a say, who didn’t get a choice when Agatha ripped herself away.

If Rio had done to Agatha what she herself had done to Rio, leaving Agatha alone in a world without her or Nicky before hiding in a way so she could never find her, well, Agatha would have summoned Rio in the only way she was certain she couldn't have ignored, without breaking any of her own ground rules that is.

So she could understand Rio’s upset, she got it.

But still, there was a lot at stake and she didn’t need a vengeful ex ruining the scheme she was running right now, especially when the pay out of power would be beyond anything else she had ever experienced.

“Why are you here? How did you even get in this... thing too?” she waved a hand around herself, indicating the black and white world they were both wrapped up within.

Rio grinned again, her eyes widening with that edge of madness that her ex-wife always seemed to be flirting with. It made Agatha’s heart sputter to life in her chest, like a little electric shock of longstanding attraction had just been applied to it's flesh, awaking the old muscle after a long slumber.

“I wanted to see you, and I wanted to know what you were up to,” Rio glanced around, casually taking in the furniture and features from another time, “there is a lot of power bubbling in this town, all thrumming under the surface. Can you feel it Agatha?”

Rio took another step closer, bracketing Agatha’s kitten heels with her leather saddle shoes, so close that whenever Agatha breathed out and her chest expanded the material of her dress grazed Rio’s shirt.

“I can feel it Rio,” Agatha tried to laugh, but it came out more like a strangled gasp at feeling Rio so close to her again, “why do you think I’m here”.

The green witches’ lips twitched in amusement as she stared down at Agatha’s face, eyes burning a trail from her eyes, down to her lips, before dropping even lower to take in the remaining space between them. Frowning slightly, she took another half step closer, eliminating the space entirely by pressing the length of her torso against Agatha’s.

As much as they would deny it, even under oath, the moment their bodies touched they both sighed as though an ancient weight had at long last been lifted from their shoulders.

“Does it feel like me Agatha? Does it feel like my power to you? Like home ? Is that why you want it so badly?”

Rio’s question exposed Agatha in a way she despised. She hadn’t prepared for this; for this sudden reunion, Rio’s abundance of questions, nor her intoxicating presence.

So Agatha shifted the focus back to the issue at hand, “what’s your play here exactly? You came here, dressed the part, and even thought of an alias, didn’t you Rita . So what is it you want? Why are you here?”

Rio smirked, “I haven’t decided yet. All I know is that this is where you were, so I came to find you. I might have to nip off now and again, you know…” she lowered her voice, as though they were sharing secrets, “for a business trip or two. But yeah, I think I will stay for the time being, at least until I figure out what exactly it is I am feeling, or what exactly it is I want to do to you”.

She added pressure to the knife still poised at Agatha’s throat, nicking the skin and causing a hot trail of blood to weep down the hollow of her throat, the red coming through as a dark black against the white of her skin in their current monochromatic world.

“I need to figure out how I am going to punish you. But until then, I will watch you flounder here, grappling against powers you haven't even begun to grasp or understand”.

Agatha gasped at both the pain and the pulse of heat she could feel low in her stomach at Rio’s words. Her eyes started to water as she bared her teeth in an expression that resembled a grin. However before she could respond, Rio took two steps backwards and slid her knife back into its sheath on her belt.

A mask descended over Rio's features then, as though she really was just a neighbour dropping by to ask for a cup of sugar or a couple of eggs. She started to walk towards the front door, turning only to murmur two words to Agatha, who was still pressed up against the wall as though Rio had left a shade of herself in her living room.

“Te Veo”.

Those damningly familiar words finally jolted Agatha away from the wall towards the couch, where with a hiss she grabbed a pillow in order to scream herself hoarse.

Magic Shows & Miniskirts

Chapter Notes

Thank you all for your kind comments and kudos! I really appreciate it <3

I hope you enjoy this next chapter too! xoxoxo

Agatha had kept herself busy over the remainder of the 1950s, doing as all good housewives should and spent her time ignoring her fake husband, studying witchcraft, preparing her basement for magical emergencies, and avoiding her ex-wife.

Rio had attempted to gain entry to her house multiple times, but now that Agatha knew the green witch was also residing in Westview, she had taken some time to put up a few magical defences against unwanted intruders. Her work had resulted in several roars of frustration resounding from the porch, which were much like music to her ears as she sipped her morning coffee, twitching the curtains aside to wave at Rio, even letting her dressing gown slip down her shoulder slightly just to rub salt in the wound.

Not that her defensive spells were much help to her whenever she left her house, keen as she was to keep up appearances as the nosy neighbour.

However, her luck held out for a short while and they didn’t have a proper run in for a few more days, not until the day Agatha awoke to find everything around her had changed once more, modernising in one easy sweep to appear 10 years newer.

Wanda had fancied a change evidently.

So, the 1960s. Another wonderful decade, if not one of the best to be a witch in modern America. Agatha was sure she hadn’t worn a bra once over the entire era.

Studying her own personal upgrades in the mirror she frowned, unhappy to see that her clothing was far closer to the more conservative dresses of the 50s. She had been hoping for something slightly more liberal. A nice off the shoulder peasant blouse maybe, with a long skirt, chain belt, and a pair of tinted teashade's would have done the job nicely.

Oh well. It would appear Wanda’s impression of the 60s was far more rigid, which considering what she had learnt about Wanda’s youth in the Soviet Union came as no real surprise.

Sighing, she grabbed Señor Scratchy, who she had already tucked away in his travel cage, ensuring he had plenty of lettuce leaves and carrots to nibble on throughout his afternoon, and made for Wanda’s house.

Befriending the other woman had been a surprisingly easy job. As it turns out, Wanda was desperately lonely, even with her enchanted husband at her side. She had a keen ear and was very eager to be a hearty member of her captured community, always offering to help with different events whether it be calling the numbers at bingo, or helping to organise an afternoon tea dance.

Today Agatha had arranged to drop Señor Scratchy off with Wanda as he was to be part of Wanda and Vision’s magic act. The irony of which was indeed not lost on her, that a genuine witch’s familiar was helping in a so-called magic show consisting of childish parlour tricks. Still, the loan of her dearest pet bought her something valuable; Wanda’s trust.

She made it to Wanda’s house without any interruption’s, handed Señor Scratchy over, and had even managed a banterous exchange with Dennis the mailman. Yet just as she was righting herself after judging the state of Dennis’s polyester uniform, she felt a presence behind her.

Agatha closed her eyes, preparing herself mentally.

For she knew precisely who was lurking behind her, as she always knew when Rio was near. It was a skill impossible to not pick up after centuries of loving a person. Although the simmer of power she could immediately sense sparking over the back of her neck was always a bit of a giveaway.

Moments later, she felt warm hands slide over the dip of her waist to tug her back into a firm torso, as a pair of warm lips nuzzled beside her ear to whisper a single word, “boo”.

Agatha felt herself instantly melting back into the embrace, the motion of which felt as natural to her as breathing. Yet the moment she saw Wanda returning from placing Señor Scratchy inside her home, she jerked away from Rio’s touch, suddenly remembering that Westview, at least currently-cursed Westview, possessed the mindset of the 1960s, where being seen in the arms of another woman would win you a prison sentence, and not a colourful parade through 5th Avenue.

She turned quickly, intent on telling Rio to pack it in when her tongue caught on the roof of her mouth and seemed instantly content to stay there. Her eyes popped wide as they dropped down to take in the extent of Rio’s outfit.

Fucking Hell.

Rio had probably designed it herself, for she was the only resident in Westview wearing an outfit that showed this amount of skin. She had gone for a white and black chequered miniskirt, black turtleneck, and thick, black platform boots that contrasted beautifully against the strip of skin visible between where her skirt ended and her boots began. Her hair was fairly normal, and not styled in a classic 60s beehive or bouffant. Instead she had chosen to keep it shoulder length and straight, with only the ends curling outwards slightly. Half of it was pulled back into a neat bun and feathered bangs framed her face, drawing attention to the eyeliner she had used to emphasise just how pretty her dark eyes were.

The Bitch.

“Morning sweetheart,” Rio murmured, drawing closer to gently tug on one of the tight curls by her ear, causing it to spring down and then bounce up, falling out of position.

Whilst Swatting Rio’s hand away Agatha scowled at her, only just managing to rectify her expression into one of neighbourly warmth the moment Wanda joined them back by her garden gate.

“Rita!” Wanda cried in friendly greeting, “how lovely to see you again”.

Rio smiled at Wanda, a lazy smirk as she looked the other woman up and down, “Wanda,” was the extend of Rio’s greeting, yet by the way Wanda smiled and blushed, it had apparently been enough.

Having had quite enough of that , Agatha grabbed Wanda’s wrist and wrapped it around her own arm, intending on dragging her to Dottie’s soiree before Rio could beg herself an invite.

Yet her efforts were, of course, in vain.

Wanda for one refused to be dragged, instead she turned back to face Rio who was still standing on the sidewalk outside Wanda’s home, picking the leaves from her front hedge, only to rip them up into small pieces and throw them over the street and the two women now stood in front of her like confetti.

“Rita?” Wanda’s voice was politely perplexed. It was obvious she was not entirely comfortable around someone as strange as Rio, yet she was still being driven by her moral compass, which would not allow her to exclude Rio from a gathering with the other woman of Westview. “Would you care to join us for lunch? Dottie is having a bit of a get together before the neighbourhood talent show later today”.

Rio grinned another one of her sharp, wolfish smiles as she slipped forward like the wraith she was to drag Agatha’s other arm over her own, clamping it close to her waist as she nodded, “I have some time to kill”.

“Well then, it was meant to be!” Wanda commented happily before beginning to lead the three of them, who were now all linked by their arms, down the road, babbling all the while.

Agatha however, was struggling to take in a single word the other woman was saying, as Rio had brought her free hand up and started to gently brush the tips of her fingers over the skin of Agatha’s forearm, a distracting caress that she knew, Rio knew, would drive her insane.

Fortunately, it didn’t take them long to get to Dottie’s house which was only one street over from their own, where Agatha was quick to wriggle free from both of the arms wrapped around her own. She managed as well, to dodge Rio’s last minute attempt to drag her back towards herself with a well-timed sneeze in the other direction.

Smirking, she watched as Rio’s frustration at Agatha’s slipperiness descended over her face. Rio was not the only one who knew what made the other tick after all, and Rio was always so beautifully riled by the prospect of a chase.

Dottie spotted the trio approaching her house and was quick to wave them around the back where the other women had gathered, offering them drinks as she did so.

Agatha introduced Wanda.

Wanda then introduced Rio, as Agatha was pretending Rio didn’t exist.

Fortunately, Wanda had taken it in her stride the moment all the other ladies of Westview stared at Rio as though she was a stranger, which she was. Agatha was surprised Rio not knowing the neighbours hadn’t planted a big red flag in Wanda’s mind, yet alas, she seemed more concerned with magic shows and keeping the world in shades of grey than putting massively obvious clues together.

From their introduction it was immediately clear that the gaggle of other women found Rio a perplexing puzzle of a person. Some of them frowned at the amount of leg she had on show, other’s ogled with confused appreciation. All of them reared back when she smiled at them in that mad way, with her eyes wide and eerily vacant, but then immediately leaned back in, evidently charmed and intrigued by this unusual, attractive stranger who had come for tea.

Agatha found herself relying on the large selection of alcoholic drinks Dottie had lined up to get her through the entire event. She spent the soiree entertaining herself with a glib comment here or an unnecessarily graphic description of her fake husband’s ass there. She liked the way they would all bristle and clutch their pearls prudishly. Plus, it had the additional benefit of causing that crazed glint to appear in Rio’s eyes, a look that always made Agatha's blood heat up, even if she refused to admit such things out loud.

It was, surprisingly, all going rather well. Shockingly Rio had done little more than eat an entire bowl of olives, pips and all, whilst glaring at Agatha when it all suddenly went off piste again.

One of the ladies had introduced the topic of husbands, bemoaning the fact her own spent all of his time either working or at the bar with his friends.

Dottie had then commented on her own marriage and from there had been a domino-line of women airing their relationship grievances. Until it reached Wanda at least, who was so sickeningly in love it made Agatha want to retch.

“Oh, well…” Wanda stuttered the moment everyone’s eyes settled on her, their gazes expectant and demanding she join their ranks of feminine fury, “Vision is a wonderful husband, he takes good care of me and I love him very much”.

Agatha would have been sick and she very nearly was, if not for Wanda distracting her by throwing her under the microscope instead, “how about Ralph, Agnes? Any complaints?"

Fortunately, Agatha who spent a lot of her time making up bizarre stories about her fake husband for her own amusement, was quick to ad lib, “there are many, many things wrong with Ralph, one being he just cannot keep up with me you know…” she lowered her voice, eager to scandalise the other ladies, “…in the bedroom . I guess I'm just too much woman for him".

They all tittered and gasped, each of them absolutely scandalised at her crude answer. Yet it was Rio who was the first to reply.

“Wrong person for you then isn’t it, Agnes ”.

Agatha’s eyes narrowed sharply in Rio’s direction, “not at all, Rita ”.

Rio’s smirk was as attractive as it was bold and Agatha immediately regretted even bringing up the bedroom, joking or otherwise, for she knew instantly that Rio, who didn’t know what a verbal filter was let alone possessed one, was about to say something highly flammable.

“If Ralph can’t keep up with you then he isn’t right for you. You should be with someone who satisfies you, someone who knows how to tire you out”.

Agatha bristled where she sat, finding herself to suddenly be the scandalised pearl-clutcher as she raised a nervous hand to twiddle with the collar of her dress. She forced a polite smile onto her face as she glanced around at the other women, taking in their affronted expressions before turning to glare at Rio again, who was now leaning back with her arms stretched out behind her, one leg crossed over the other looking far too good in that minskirt and far, far too pleased with herself.

Immediately, Agatha knew exactly what petty button to press.

Things had been strange since the 1970s dissolved around them, having been promptly replaced by the neon colours and block patterns of the 1980s.

Strange in the sense that ever since that particular afternoon in her shadowy hallway, her dynamic with Rio seemed to fluctuate between moments of gentle tenderness to instances of furious resentment. As for all the moments encompassed in the grey between those grand sentiments, well they both gained far too much pleasure from irritating the other, like children on the playground pulling pigtails.

Still, Agatha refused to let Rio’s presence distract her from the mission at hand, so she continued to play the role of “nosy neighbour” as successfully as any Broadway star might have.

Although, the way Agatha saw it, whether the babies were a figment of Wanda’s curse or real-life human children, it made no difference to the screaming racket they made at all hours of the day.

Their crying had woken her that morning in fact, around 5am, which was an ungodly, cursed hour. Agatha had rolled over and glared from her nest of pillows and blankets at the bedroom window, where early morning sunlight and the screaming cries of demanding babies were drifting through the glass.

“Agnes!” Wanda replied cheerily, turning from the two cots she had been worrying over to say hello to her neighbour.

Put simply, Rio looked good. Really good. Frustratingly good.

“Rita!” Wanda greeted in the same cheerful voice she had welcomed Agatha a few moments earlier.

Rio’s responding smile was sharp, although her eyes were still hidden behind the dark lenses of her sunglasses.

“Wanda,” she said in cool greeting before turning towards Vision, “Vision,” she added politely. Finally, Rio’s head tilted and her gaze landed on Agatha. She raised a hand to lower her sunglasses until they were resting just below the bridge of her nose, allowing her dark eyes to peer over the top of the lenses and graze a hot trail up Agatha’s spandex covered figure.

After a scorching second, Rio murmured her final greeting, “Agnes”. Her voice had dropped in pitch and was loaded, heady with tension and heavy with hunger.

Agatha didn’t often get embarrassed; she considered herself far too old for such inane reactions. Yet, Rio looking at her like that, talking to her like that , in front of Wanda and Vision no less, caused a hot blush to rise up her throat and along her cheekbones until even the tips of her ears were bright pink.

“ Rita ,” Agatha squeezed through gritted teeth, her forced smile doing a terrible job of disguising a frustrated grimace.

Rio took a few steps closer to her and pulled the aviators from her face with a dangerous smirk, “did you miss me, baby?”

Agatha gaped at Rio's boldness and felt her flush darken. Distantly, she heard Vision cough to cover a shocked laugh and was suddenly hideously aware of their audience. She peered sideways to take note of Wanda and Vision’s reaction, only to immediately notice the way one of Wanda’s eyebrows arched as she and Vision exchanged a curious glance.

Eager to tame this fire before it burned her, Agatha laughed loudly, obnoxiously so, before slapping a hand on her hip again, “ baby ? Oh Rita, aren’t you just a riot? The only babies I see are these two little miracles”.

She stepped forward to peer into the crib closest to her.

On glancing in, she noticed the name “Billy” stitched onto his green blanket. Unable to resist the maternal urge that suddenly consumed her, she gently traced the tips of her fingers over the soft skin of his little hand.

Baby Billy, who had been crying this entire time, paused to sniffle slightly before turning his hand over to grip one of her fingers with his small fist. He then immediately started crying again, even with Agatha caught in his tiny clutches.

Instantly, Agatha felt her damaged heart crack and her throat tighten. Nicholas had always done the same when he had been small, taking any opportunity to grip one of her fingers in his much smaller ones, taking comfort from the presence of his mother, even whilst being too young to even realise he was doing so.

Her sudden stillness caused the others in the room to pause too, exposing each of them to a stiflingly awkward atmosphere the instant Agatha’s charismatic energy evaporated from the room, leaving only a parent’s silent grief in its wake.

Wanda exchanged another loaded look with Vision before stepping forward to brush a gentle palm against Agatha’s shoulder, “Agnes? Are you alright?”

Rio’s possessive touch broke Agatha out of her trance, as her insistence on using romantic terms of endearment, even in company, caused a frustrated scowl to break out on Agatha's face.

Rio squeezed her waist again, a hint that she should at least pretend to be normal.

“Yes, sorry!” she laughed awkwardly, all the while trying to wriggle out of Rio’s firm grasp, “I just adore babies and seeing these two little bundles of sweetness so upset, well it upsets me too, you know”.

Peering up whilst hunting through the depths of her bag, she grinned at Wanda, “fussy babies! We dare you to stay awake!”

Wanda and Vision stepped to the side then and started to have a bit of a to-do, trading hushed whispered back and forth, each of them cringing at every loud, piercing cry their children were taking turns to emit.

It was making Agatha's head pound painfully too, so the moment she felt the glass bottle of her relaxation potion in her palm, she pulled it from the depths of her bag and started to spray the sweet-smelling concoction just above their cribs, eager for the natural aroma of lavender to soothe them enough to sleep.

It had always worked a treat for Nicky, after all.

The moment they realised Agatha was spritzing something at their children though, Vision looked over with a concerned expression on his face, “oh?”

“Lavender!” She told him loudly, “it’s supposed to have a calming effect. Ralph sprays it on me every night, but there’s no taming this tiger!”

Vision flushed bright red at her words, however her glee at his discomfort was cut short the moment she felt a firm palm slap her ass, “who would want to tame you? That’s criminal”.

Rio’s voice was confident, with not an ounce of shame at being so outrageously flirtatious amongst company.

Agatha immediately yelped and jumped away from Rio, as she once again started to flush heavily. She covered her embarrassment by quickly pointing towards the kitchen, all the while trying to ignore the perplexed expressions on both Wanda and Vision’s faces, “I’m just going to… just going to look for, for the… the thing that I need. You know, the thing…”

In a bid to distract herself, she started searching through Wanda’s cupboards, hunting for their alcohol, whilst continuously grumbling quietly to herself about Rio and her consistently rising levels of sheer audacity.

“Agnes,” Wanda’s voice was a hushed whisper, coming from just over her shoulder.

Agatha, having not heard Wanda follow after her, closed her eyes tightly before spinning around to face the other woman. She made sure her forcefully joyful smile was back in place as she said, “yes hon? I'm just looking for your dark liquor”. She slapped a dramatic hand against her chest the moment Wanda's eyes widened, “not for me, for the twins! What sort of babysitter do you think I am?”

Wanda’s surprised expression dropped back into one of troubled concern, like something beyond the false reality of her sitcom was bothering her, “Agnes… we’re friends, right?”

Agatha’s grin, if at all possible, got brighter, “of course we are hot stuff! Why? Is something wrong?”

A sheepish look stole across Wanda’s face then, making her lips tug down slightly at the corners, “no, nothings wrong really, it’s just… may I ask you something? Something personal?”

For the first time throughout this interaction, Agatha felt uncertainty stir in her stomach.

Her smile dimmed slightly, “er, sure hon, what’s on your mind?”

“It’s kind of awkward, but you and Rita… are you… is there something… have I split…” Wanda suddenly stopped herself from speaking. She glared down at the floor for a short moment whilst evidently gathering the courage to spit out her actual question. Then it came all at once, like she had to say it quickly in order to say it at all, “is there something going on between you and Rita?” Her voice got lower, a whisper, “something romantic?”

Agatha could tell her face must have dropped in surprise because Wanda was quick to take a desperate step forward. She grasped Agatha’s hand, “it’s not a problem if there is, I swear! I just…”

She frowned then, a look crafted from frustration and concern, “I am just worried that something might have come between the pair of you... something that I might be able to… to help you fix?”

Agatha’s eyebrows shot to her hairline as she processed Wanda’s words. This was the closest Wanda had ever come to breaking character and admitting that the world they were all living in was indeed a fallacy of her own creation. Wanda’s candidness surprised her, but it didn’t take Agatha long to piece it all together. Wanda was evidently concerned that Agatha and Rio had been in a relationship before her curse had swept through the town of Westview in a wave of scarlet, only for it to split them apart, pairing Agatha with a random man to make their presence more appropriate for a sitcom set in the 1950s.

Thinking quickly, Agatha lied, amending the truth to suit herself and make Rio look foolish, which was always a benefit in her opinion, “aah you caught wind of Rita's little crush, did you?” Agatha leaned closer, making her voice a whisper, “she has always had a bit of a thing for me, to be honest. She even asked me to junior prom, but I, of course, had to let her down easy. Bless her sweet, gentle, yearning heart”.

A small wrinkle appeared between Wanda’s eyebrows as she stared back at Agatha intently. It was clear she was trying to puzzle out the truth of Agatha's words. Whether it was the actual truth, or whether it was her curse pushing a false narrative to keep a pair of lovers apart.

Evidently, Wanda was comfortable with hostage-taking and kidnap but drew the line at homophobia. Which honestly, Agatha respected. If anything it made the other witch more likable. But right now, in Agatha's current situation she did not need her relationship with Rio studied closely, especially by the witch who was still pulling all of the puppet strings.

“You must have known her a long time if you went to high school together?”

Taken aback by the question, Agatha paused as a stream of memories started to pass through her consciousness; the soft drag of woollen cloaks, husky laughter on frosty mornings, hot palms tracing the sensitive skin of her waist, the sound of a child's laughter echoing throughout a once happy home.

Suddenly, the ghosts of what had once been consumed her.

“Yeah,” she eventually breathed, unaware of how her eyes had softened whilst looking passed Wanda towards the door, towards Rio, “we have known each other practically our whole lives. She… she’s my best friend”.

Wanda, who had been witness to the flood of emotions encompassing Agatha's expression, looked suddenly distraught, “and something… something big came between you?”

Still lost to her past, Agatha nodded with distant, wet eyes, “something big did come between us, yeah”.

“Can you remember what that was... specifically?” Wanda’s voice was politely inquisitive. Lightly toned, which was in direct contrast to her actual question, as once again she was poking at things she probably shouldn’t be. It was immediately clear to Agatha that she was trying to uncover whether the “something” in question was her curse.

Unable to actually admit the truth without revealing herself, Agatha, in a snap decision, utilised the spell’s existence as a convenient excuse and simply smiled brightly again, “nope!”

Then she turned and started to rifle through the next few cupboards, still intent on finding a bottle of alcohol, which she eventually did, tucked behind some old cans of tuna and tomato soup.

Agatha turned with a whoop whilst holding the bottle aloft in victory, only to see Wanda’s eyes still studying her closely. The other witch looked sad and most worryingly of all, guilty.

This plan had quite obviously backfired, as it was clear Wanda was now blaming herself for whatever rift she could sense between Rio and herself. Yet Agatha’s ability to explain, or even reassure the other witch that the "something" in question was entirely separate from the curse, had been muted.

So with the intention of distracting Wanda from her complicated relationship with Rio, she strode forward with a broad grin and linked their arms together.

“Come on, lets go see if this helps that frustrating teething pain of theirs”.

However, the moment the pair of them turned back into the living room, they were met with a scene that caused Agatha’s heart to melt and run molten through her veins, carrying the love that still burned so strongly for Rio around her body.

Rio was sat on the sofa, leaning back into the cushions with her usual air of casual comfort, yet this time she had a twin in the cradle of each arm. For once, both babies looked settled and were babbling quietly to themselves, whilst staring up with innocent fascination at Rio’s face. Billy had even managed to wriggle a small arm free from his swaddle to grab a handful of Rio’s dark hair with his little fist. Rio, who didn’t appear to mind that a baby was now tugging on her hair, was simply staring back at them, eyes roving with simple awe from one chubby face to the next, then back again.

Agatha couldn’t help the sound that left her then, a very quiet yet exceptionally heavy, “ oh ”.

It was all so much; Rio holding babies, the babies finding her ancient presence a calming one, Rio being surprised, again , that an innocent life could take comfort at being held in her arms.

Wanda was stood beside her with a gaze that flickered heavily between the two of them. She absorbed Agatha’s suddenly wrecked expression, before glancing at the gentle vision Rio made holding Wanda's son's close to her heart.

“It doesn’t look like they are going to need this, after all,” Wanda's voice was soft as she pulled the slipping bottle of bourbon from Agatha’s slack grip. She then gave Agatha's shoulder a gentle nudge, pushing her towards Rio.

Agatha drifted closer to Rio without thought, like a ship heading home through a storm.

Rio looked over the moment Agatha perched on the couch beside her, being sure to not disturb the now snoozing babies when she sat down next to the three of them.

Her dark eyes were misty as they captured Agatha’s own, “hey,” was all she said in gentle greeting.

“Hey,” Agatha parroted quietly, her voice just as soft.

They were both aware no further words were needed in this moment, that there was an unspoken understanding of who exactly they were both thinking of. Yet, for the first time the memory of their son didn't just instigate the drowning depths of their grief. For the presence of the new born twins reminded them both of the happiness they had shared as his mothers, of all the moments they had laughed together in this exact position, one of them cradling a baby and the other sat close by creating the ultimate image of an entwined pair connected through the love they had for one another, and the love they shared for their child.

Rio smiled at her then, an expression as full of pain as it was disbelieving joy. She peered down at the young lives cradled in her arms, both of them snuggled comfortably into the crook of an elbow, before looking back up at Agatha with a hesitant glance, as if to say, can you believe it .

Agatha felt her own eyes pooling then as she smiled back. Unable to resist the contact she knew they both desperately needed, Agatha lifted a hand to the back of Rio’s head and gently ran her fingers through her hair, before tracing her fingers over the side of her neck to cup Rio's jaw. Finally, Agatha nodded, intent on reassuring Rio that she could most certainly believe it. For Rio was many, many things, several of them bad, heaps of them questionable, but she had always been an exceptional mother who had loved their son fiercely, and he had loved her the same.

Agatha would reduce anyone who said otherwise to ash.

“Well, it looks like we finally found the cure to the boys tears,” Vision’s voice was a hushed whisper, almost reverent.

At the sound of his voice breaking the silence, Agatha turned from Rio to look towards Wanda and Vision, who were stood together with their arms wrapped around the other, smiling softly at the image of their friends holding their boys.

Wanda hummed softly, eyes glued to Agatha’s hand, which was still gently cradling Rio’s jaw, “a cure indeed…”

Then she nodded to herself, as though determining a route forward through a problem only she was aware of.

Agatha swallowed heavily, sure that Wanda was currently doing what any witch worth her salt would do with the clues she had managed to piece together; she was plotting.

And Agatha, Agatha was suddenly certain that her life in Wanda’s world was about to get a lot more complicated.

A Change in the Plans

Chapter Notes

The next time jump was bigger, shooting the town of Westview twenty years into the future, rather than the standard ten Wanda had chosen for the past four upgrades.

This time, it was the beginning of the new millennium greeting the residents of Westview with CD Walkman’s, low-rise jeans, and glittery butterfly clips.

At least, these were the items that had appeared in Agatha’s house once the spell had completed its changes.

When the transformation occurred this time, Agatha had clenched her eyelids tightly together whilst the magic had sparked around her, wrapping everything in sight within it's scarlet fronds, making different items glow bright red as their particles were rearranged, modernising the entire town in under a minute. This was the issue Agatha had found at not being under Wanda’s spell. Because, unless she was asleep, Agatha would feel the painful burn of magic across her skin every single time Wanda decided to redecorate. This was a very different experience to all of those townsfolk caught entirely within the enchantment, as they would be frozen in place, blind and deaf to any changes occurring around them, even changes to their own clothing.

Eventually though, as all things did, the burst of magic came to an end and the heat of sorcery fled, leaving the room feeling far chillier than it had been before the shifting energies of transformation had warmed everything up. Agatha knew then, once everything felt suddenly cooler, that it was safe to open her eyes to see what changes had been made.

She had been in her bathroom this time, in the middle of brushing her teeth and readying herself for the day. So the moment she unclenched her eyelids, she was able to study her reflection. Fortunately her hair was still long, thank fuck , and loosely curled, hanging prettily over her shoulders. Her make-up had been done well too, and she was extremely pleased to see her eyebrows had been left alone, aware that the era the town had now been sequestered into was infamous for the ultra-thin eyebrow; a trend Agatha had always despised, then and now.

Her gaze dropped down her own reflection, following the line of her body as her eyebrows rose high up towards her hairline.

She whistled appreciatively, turning to get a full look at the black velour tracksuit that the eighties-styled clothes she had been wearing had been transformed into.

Tilting her head slightly, she read the mirrored words emblazoned on her rear, “Naughty,” she murmured to herself slowly. Her lips pulled down in a contemplative expression, before she shrugged in blasé agreement with the statement, "true".

Whilst walking from the bathroom to her bedroom, she was pleased to see a few modern amenities added here or there. It was still the turn of the millennia, so nothing too exciting, yet she was pleased to see an actual television in her bedroom instead of just a radio.

It was at this moment, just as she was heading towards the collection of video's neatly stacked beside the TV, eager to see what movies Wanda’s magic had picked out for Agnes to enjoy, that the flash of a figure passing her bedroom door made her jump and spin around.

“Who in the hell?” she hissed, immediately darting after them.

The moment she entered the hallway, another glimpse of a body turning to head down the stairs caught her attention.

“Hey!” she yelled, intent on finding out who exactly was clambering around her house without permission.

Echoing footsteps sounded from below, the thud of boots on hardwood floors, as she hurried after them down the stairs.

The interloper was heading away from her towards the front door, so she couldn’t immediately identify who it was. She could tell though that it was a man from the breadth of his shoulders and the narrowness of his hips.

She felt anger spark in her blood then, fuelled by a mixture of impatience at being forced to chase this intruder down, and the sheer audacity of this stranger being somewhere he shouldn’t be.

“Hey fuckface!” she yelled the moment she landed on the bottom step, having jumped several in the middle, drawing her purple fire close to the surface of her palms.

The man didn’t run though and he didn’t do anything threatening either. Instead, he span in place and waved happily at her with a friendly smile on his face.

“Good morning, ma’am,” he said, voice bright with morning pep, “did you sleep well?”

She dropped heavily off the final step, eyeing him warily. Her arms rose up to cross tightly across her chest as she dragged unimpressed eyes up his body to the top of his head, taking in the wrinkled shirt and messy hair.

“Ralph!” She barked, throwing her arms from where they had been crossed upwards in a gesture of pure exasperation, before dropping them heavily to slap against the side of the thighs, “what the hell are you doing out of the attic?! How did you get out?!”

He frowned at her, looking perplexed, “I have to get to work,” he pointed a thumb over his shoulder towards the front door.

She scoffed, “since when do you work ?”

He laughed, although it was an awkward sound, one of confusion not amusement, “erm, ever since I signed the lease on the attic room?” Ralph chuckled again, this time more genuinely, “obviously! As if you would have let me live here without proof of income”. He shook his head in amusement, before continuing, “I remember how your wife joked about smothering me in my sleep if the rent was ever late”.

His laughter petered out then as his eyes fogged over and he got lost in the false memory embedded in his mind, “at least I think she was joking”.

Ralph frowned at the floor for a few moments, obviously trying to clarify his thoughts through the scarlet fog no doubt holding his synapses captive. Within a few short moments though, he jerked his head up, his bright smile was back in place too, almost as though someone had pressed reboot on his system.

“Well, it’s been great chatting to you Mrs Valdez, but I really need to get to work. I don’t want to be late!”

And with that lovely little bomb dropped in her lap and left to explode, he waved and turned back towards the door.

He didn’t make it far though, for the moment his back was to her she swiped a single hand and he was unconscious, slumped in a heap on the floor within seconds.

It was hard to breath through her mouth with the intensity in which her jaw was clenched. She was certain that if she were to see herself right now, that the vein in her forehead would be bulging and her eyes would be crazed.

“ Mrs Valdez! ” she hissed, disbelieving the name as her own even though it made a sickening amount of sense.

The sound of a key in a lock sounded out then, momentarily distracting Agatha from her anger. She looked up just in time to see the door thump to a premature stop the moment it met Ralph’s unconscious body.

Rio’s face appeared through the narrow gap, a broad predatory smile on her face.

“Honey I’m home,” she crowed, whilst beginning to shunt the door back and forth against the weight blocking her entry, which in turn caused Ralph to groan slightly as he was pushed further into the hallway, still unconscious.

Agatha fumed silently, watching this pantomime play out in her hallway.

She was finding it difficult to think of the words that would communicate just how she was feeling about this new amendment to Agnes's life.

Until finally, she settled on an exhalation of roared frustration and snapped her fingers, causing a spark of purple to shoot towards Ralph, who was promptly transported in a puff of smoke from the hallway to the basement.

She would deal with him later.

As for Rio. Well, she would deal with her now.

With another flick of her wrist the front door slammed shut behind her wife . Rio, of course, didn’t jump, but her grin did broaden, giving her that feral, unhinged edge that always made Agatha feel slightly weak in the knees.

“So,” Agatha spat, spinning on her heels to head towards the kitchen and pour herself a glass of whiskey, even though it wasn’t even ten in the morning yet, “you have been re-cast, have you?”

Rio, who was now wearing era appropriate cargo pants and a black tank top, sauntered after her. Her hair was pulled back in a high ponytail, and she was fiddling with one of the hoop earrings she had in, which frustratingly enough, drew the eye naturally to the slender line of her throat and the sharp jut of her jaw.

“I did,” Rio replied, eyes dropping to take a lazy stroll up Agatha’s body, evidently appreciating the velour tracksuit and the way it clung to her body’s curves, “finally got the part I wanted”.

Agatha sighed, as the majority of her anger drained out of her. She slumped forward, leaning her forearms on the counter, before groaning “why would she do this to me? I thought she liked Agnes!”

Rio smirked and stalked closer, taking a moment to read the word printed across her pants, “what? Print "naughty" across your ass?”

Agatha ignored Rio's question, choosing instead to huff loudly and lay her forehead down on her arms so her torso was practically laying on the work surface. Rio didn’t allow her to sulk for long though, as she promptly slapped a hard palm against Agatha's ass.

“I don’t know whether to feel thrilled that you’re wearing this, or rip Wanda’s throat out for putting you in it. She must have looked to know how good this would look on you”.

The action jolted Agatha into a standing position again, although with Rio behind her and the counter in front, she had no escape from the warm body behind her, nor the hot palm that stayed cupped against the round curve of her rear.

“Rio,” Agatha’s voice was a breathed warning, a thin, delicate line that she knew Rio wouldn’t hesitate to trample all over.

Rio’s voice drew nearer to her ear, so close she could feel the gentle flutter of her words as she spoke, “what? You’re my wife now aren't you?”

Agatha shuddered when Rio’s other hand lifted to pull her hair away from her neck, exposing her throat to soft lips. Immediately, Rio started to drag her mouth up and down the tender flesh, tracing the straining tendon that had appeared when Agatha's head tilted to one side without conscious thought, giving Rio more access to the sensitive skin of her throat.

She was surprised at how deep her voice sounded as she quipped, “I was your wife before too, or were you lying about that?”

Rio’s teeth nibbled on the thin skin above her pulse, which was fluttering like the wings of a nervous bird, before drawing away slightly to husk into Agatha’s ear, “you have always been my wife, even Wanda could see that you belong to me”.

One of Rio’s hands trailed up the curve of her hip, stopping for a moment to palm it greedily, before dragging it up and around to her stomach so she could tug Agatha’s body back into her own. Simultaneously, her other hand traced upwards to grip Agatha's throat. Slowly, she pressed the pad of her thumb into the soft flesh under Agatha’s jaw, pushing her head over even further to expose more of her skin to Rio's hungry mouth.

Agatha could feel her resolve to stay away from Rio's warmth dissolving like ice over a fire, turning first to liquid before disappearing entirely in a cloud of steam. Her body arched backwards into Rio's, as one of her own hands travelled to tighten Rio's hold over her own throat and the other crept around to the small of Rio’s back, intent on holding her close.

Rio, having sensed Agatha’s eager reaction to her seduction, slipped the hand she had over Agatha’s stomach under the thin velour jacket she was wearing to run a greedy palm over the hot skin of her abdomen.

“Fuck,” Agatha hissed when Rio got bolder and bit the side of her throat, hard. This had always been an element of their relationship that they had both always enjoyed, the ferality of the act.

“Let me come home to you,” Rio’s words were whispered into the skin she had just bruised and claimed, “let me live here again," the palm under her jacket dragged upwards, trailing over the sensitive skin of her breast to settle headily over Agatha's pounding heart.

Agatha had been two seconds away from agreeing, from spinning around in the circle of Rio’s arms to capture that damn devilish mouth with her own, from reacquainting herself with the taste of Rio's lips, when the slap of a newspaper against glass, flung by an unbothered teenager on a bicycle at the kitchen window, violently lurched Agatha back to reality.

“We shouldn’t,” she whispered, clenching her eyes tightly to try and force her heart back into its normal rhythm. She didn’t push Rio away, unable to push her away when being close to her felt so much like returning home after a long journey, as comforting as the smell of a wood fire on an evening claimed by frost. So instead she pat the hand on her stomach twice, indicating that Rio should release the possessive grip she had on her body.

A tired, almost grief-ridden sigh sounded from over her shoulder, before the hands gripping her loosened, then slipped away completely.

Agatha resented how desperately she wanted their warmth back the instant they were gone.

She inhaled deeply, before turning to point towards the stairwell that led down to the basement, determined now to move on from whatever had just happened between the two of them.

“Ralph is no longer my husband in Wanda's narrative. He thinks he's our lodger now, so obviously Wanda has made a few changes".

Rio stared at her for a few short moments, eyebrows raised in resentful disbelief that Agatha was just going to pretend like they hadn’t been three seconds away from consummating their marriage.

Again.

Finally though, she exhaled slowly, folded her arms and leant back against the counter behind her.

“Well duh,” she said, with slightly more ire in her tone than normal, which for Rio was saying something, “Wanda obviously thinks she split us up”.

Agatha nodded, “she does. She asked me when we were over there the other morning if something big had come between us, something that she could help us fix”.

Rio’s eyes widened, she looked impressed, “bold of her to hint at the curse with someone she believes to be trapped by it. Meddling with perception magic like that could cause the entire thing to collapse”.

Agatha sighed tiredly and wandered to the fridge. Immediately, she started to pull out all of the ingredients needed to make pancakes; one of Rio’s favourites.

“I know," she groaned, "and now she has gone and changed Ralph’s role from husband to lodger, and yours from neighbourhood lurker to my wife”.

Rio smirked knowingly, eyes intent as she watched Agatha’s hands start to stir the pancake batter, “technically, I was already your wife”.

The stirring of the batter got slightly more violent as Agatha felt her frustration grow at just how true Rio's words were. She had feared Wanda would do something like this after that disastrous morning at Wanda’s house with the twins, pushing her and Rio together like dolls.

Slapping the whisk down beside the bowl, she turned to slam a frying pan onto the cooker, let a slab of butter melt down to a greasy puddle before pouring a generous portion of pancake mix into the pan.

Whilst the pancake bubbled from beige to golden brown, Agatha kept her face tucked down as she thought through her options and tried to figure out the best way to deal with all of these curveballs.

Rio, to her credit, remained quiet, giving Agatha a moment to ponder things silently.

It only took a few minutes until the pancake was cooked, so whilst still lost to her own thoughts Agatha slipped it from the pan onto a plate, spun and shoved it across the counter towards Rio, who had, in her boredom, started to carve a geometric pattern into the wooden work surface with her curved knife.

Agatha grabbed the syrup from the cupboard and pushed it towards Rio, choosing to ignore the vandalism. It wasn’t her house after all and to be frank, she didn’t give a shit.

“Right,” she clapped her hands together, “Wanda’s going to crack soon enough, but I need to think of something that will speed things up, then I can finally get out this damn town”.

Rio, who had poured so much syrup onto her plate it had overspilled and was now seeping onto the graffitied work surface, looked up at Agatha with a fierce scowl. Although, it did lose some of its power with the way her cheeks were bulging from the amount of pancake she had shoved into her mouth.

“Let me guess?" she spat through a mouthful of pancake, spraying crumbs across the kitchen island towards Agatha, "you want to speed things up to get away from me again?”

The question was heavy, loaded with ammunition from their past that had grown rotten with furious resentment and desperate pain.

Agatha’s voice abandoned her in the face of Rio's bluntly spoken, yet terrifyingly accurate perception. She had grown used to not having anyone around who had the undeniable ability to call her out like that, who actually knew her and the reasons she made the choices she did better than herself.

What made the accusation worse was how true the allegation actually was.

Because she did want to get away from Rio again. Although her reasons had changed, having transformed and mutated with every moment they had spent together over the last few weeks.

Agatha knew it was cowardly, she knew it was unfair and selfish, but she couldn’t stop that instinct she had to run. To get as far away from Rio as possible, if only to protect herself from just how vulnerable Rio made her, from how soft Agatha became around her.

Because Agatha knew now, she knew, without a single doubt how much she still loved her wife. How desperately her body, her heart, even her magic yearned for the witch stood staring back at her. It had been a confounding thing to be confronted with, especially after an entire century of trying to persuade herself that the burning emotion she felt storming through her veins at thoughts of Rio was now hatred and no longer love.

She had managed it eventually, had convinced herself that she didn’t even like the green witch, let alone loved her anymore. Yet the moment their hands had brushed, her fallacy had crumbled to dust around her, causing swirling tides of her own lies to choke her with the truth; that she loved Rio as deeply, as truly, and as furiously as she always had. As she always would.

Yet the thought of Rio knowing the truth, of being forced to feel as exposed, as vulnerable as Agatha had when Nicholas died and her heart had shredded itself to a bloody pulp beneath her ribs, was beyond her wildest terrors. Even the possibility of experiencing pain of that calibre, of that potency again shot fear through her heart, for Agatha knew she wouldn’t survive it a second time. She had barely survived it the first. So she had to go and she couldn’t let Rio follow her. It had to be soon too, because Agatha knew the longer those dark, knowing eyes continued to perceive her, the more likely it became that she would give in to her base instincts and throw herself at Rio's feet, pleading with her to stay, to love her again, to simply exist with her for eternity.

“Plus, I think I have an idea of just how you can use your ex boy-toy to get into Wanda’s head”.

“Hhmm?” she managed to grit out through her tightly clenched jaw, afraid if she actually opened her mouth to speak, words she hadn’t authorised her mouth to say would jump from her throat.

Rio’s responding grin was wolfish, as though entirely aware of the affect she had on Agatha’s body.

“I know how to get in Wanda’s head. We’re going to have to enchant him though,” she jerked her chin towards the basement, where Ralph was probably still lying in an unconscious heap.

“Oh?” Agatha finally felt confident enough to actually speak, although her voice was admittedly far huskier than normal, “how so?”

“Let’s just say, I know a guy,” Rio shrugged flippantly, before wandering over to draw her fingers through the puddle of syrup again. She took her time sucking them clean, her gaze holding Agatha hostage across the kitchen as she did so. Finally, once she was satisfied with just how fast Agatha’s breathing had become, she removed her fingers from between her lips with a salacious pop and shrugged again, “or at least I knew a guy. Found him in Sokovia with more holes in his body than a golf course before I led him home”.

Mixed Messages

Chapter Notes

Thank you for all your kind comments and kudos on the previous chapter - I really appreciate it <3

I hope you enjoy this next instalment too! xoxoxo

Taking the twins Trick-or-Treating had turned out to be a surprisingly enjoyable venture, although it had certainly helped that every single one of their Halloween troupe had mischief running through their veins.

Their evening had started out with at least an attempt to make sure everyone was well behaved, with Agatha leading the twins and Wanda's fake brother from house to house and ordering them to collect extra candy for her and Rio, who was sweeping after them all, still enshrouded in her robes of Death. The carnage from that point was unfounded, as they each started to pelt eggs at cars, houses, and each other.

Agatha, on noticing the chaos Rio had managed to sow behind her back, glared at her smirking wife before starting to storm over towards her. However, just as she was raising a hand to gesture at the raw egg now smeared across the sidewalk, she passed Billy who was continuously throwing eggs at Herb's post-box, yet kept missing.

It was such a sad sight that quite suddenly, as though she was momentarily possessed by a particularly puckish ghoul, she grabbed an egg from the tray in Billy's hand and grinned down at him. "You have to aim it like this sweetheart," she raised her hand and pulled the egg back over her shoulder, "you want to line it up straight, draw it back and not let it go until your arm is back over your head alright, helps keep it on target". She did so, demonstrating for him the perfect way to vandalise the neighbours house.

The egg did as she had hoped and splattered against the metal side of the post box. Immediately, Billy grinned up at her with amazement, "woah!"

She couldn't resist smiling back, "your turn champ".

His grin brightened as he snatched up another egg, pulled it back as she had shown him and let it loose.

"Yes!" he cried, throwing a fist up in victory the moment the perfectly aimed egg splattered against the post-box.

"That' a boy!" she cheered, clapping her hands at his success. Moments later, she was choking back a guffaw of laughter the moment Herb's furious face appeared at the window, staring out at his post-box with wide, shocked eyes.

"Oh shit! He's seen us! Come on kid," she threw Billy a devilish smile, one born of chaotic camaraderie, before grabbing his arm to drag him back down the street towards the others, who were hiding behind the trunk of a large oak tree, cackling all the while.

Agatha had then tried, valiantly she might add, to put her foot down and steer them all back to the type of Trick-or-Treating behaviour children didn't get sent to juvenile detention centres for. But after a single glance at the devious smiles of Rio, the twins, and Fietro, she soon found herself with an armful of toilet rolls, giggling like a child as the five of them successfully TP’d Mrs Hart’s house.

Their antics caused them to be late meeting Wanda at the Halloween festival, although the other witch didn't seem to mind nor be aware of the trouble her children and their babysitters had been getting up to in her absence. They stayed for a brief catch up with Wanda, who had invited them to stay and join her family at the festival, however they declined and once the boys had been safely deposited back with their mother, each of them hyped up on the mass amounts of sugar they had consumed and the adrenaline of lightweight vandalism, Agatha and Rio headed back to their house.

The entire evening had felt light, joyful, and nostalgic. In truth, Agatha felt her heart brightening as it had done outside of Wanda’s when they had first dropped off Fietro, basking in the simple warmth of Rio’s presence.

Yet the moment they stepped across the threshold and the door shut soundly behind them, tension as thick and as sweet as syrup swallowed them both. It was as though someone had left a tap of the heady stuff running whilst they were out, and as a result of their negligence, their hallway was now filled with it.

Agatha couldn’t help then but compare the sensation of wanting Rio to what an addiction felt like, having experienced that desperate desire for more every single time she had siphoned a witch's power. It was a heady, aching, want. That demanding feeling of desiring a single taste of whatever sin was in control of a person's darkest needs. She had tasted her lips again after all, could even recall, vividly, the exact pressure of Rio’s kiss. The seal of restraint had been broken between them, and it was a well-known fact that once something had been broken, even if it was repaired, it was always weaker for it.

The hallway was dark, a mass of shadows permeated only by a single beam of light slicing through the small panel window above the front door.

Rio’s eyes were on her, Agatha couldn't see them in the darkness, but she could feel their heat all the same; they were an exceptionally heady and demanding weight on her shoulders.

“It’s late,” Agatha found herself whispering, even though they were the only two in the house.

Rio’s shadow moved and she knew without having to see, that Rio had tilted her head to the side in that endearingly curious way she so often did.

“It is,” was Rio's hushed reply.

A breath rattled from between Agatha’s lips and she could feel her chest start to heave from the pressure building in the narrow space separating them.

“Maybe we should…”

She didn’t get to finish her sentence, for in the next moment Rio swept forward and encased her against the wall with both her arms on either side of Agatha’s head; a domineering figure still shrouded in her dark robes.

“Should what? ”

Rio’s words were a challenge, a definitive gauntlet that had been thrown at her feet.

Not a witch to bend to the will of others, Agatha clenched her jaw and tilted it haughtily into the air. She knew that she couldn’t allow a seduction to take place, not like this, not when the issues wedged between them were still there, undiscussed and haunting like phantom anchors, dragging them down into the darkness.

“Should go to bed sweetheart,” Agatha answered simply, ensuring her voice was gentle, knowing well enough that Rio, as much as she might deny it, often desired tenderness, having lived her entire existence as an entity the majority fled from. She heard the bones in Rio’s knuckles creak as her fists tensed against the wall beside her head. A heady frustration bled from Rio's body then. It was born from the hunger they both felt for the other, a hunger that kept nipping at their heels, like a rabid fox eager to pursue a fleeing rabbit.

But then, as predicted Death softened at her kind tone and at the loving endearment. Leaning closer, Rio rested her cloaked head against Agatha’s shoulder, just under her chin. Rio's hands dropped too, landing lightly on the dip of Agatha's waist. It was the exhaustion of centuries weighing on a figure more mortal than most would ever believe.

“Let me stay with you tonight”.

Rio’s words were a whispered plea spoken against the sensitive skin of her throat.

Agatha’s arms lifted and wrapped around the figure resting against her, holding her tight. She paused before replying though, gifting herself a moment to consider if this was a sensible course of action or whether it made better sense to re-route from their current destination and send Rio to her own bed.

But then Rio said something else, something that destroyed Agatha's ability to say no, like a cannonball through a barricade made of paper.

“I have known three lives. I have known the frigid air of my existence before our paths crossed, I have known the blazing heat of being yours, of you being mine, and I have known the barren, desolate, freezing solitude of having lost you, lost you both. Please, please don’t ask me stay out in the cold for another night. It’s a weight beyond even the crown on my head or the duty that binds me”.

Before Rio had finished speaking Agatha was already nodding her head, a frantic unconscious movement as her arms tightened around Rio in a protective embrace. Holding her close, she summoned a flurry of amethyst clouds to surround them and deposit them directly onto her bed.

Her magic had done as casted, removing any trace of make-up from both of their faces, replaced clothing with soft bedclothes, and cleansed their teeth until they were sparkling.

They landed together on a bundled pile of bedding; a nest of duvets, blankets, and pillows that had been left unmade that morning. Agatha manoeuvred them both, holding onto Rio as tightly as she was clinging onto Agatha. she slid down until she was laying flat on her back and Rio was nestled into her side, with one arm wrapped tightly over her stomach and one leg thrown over both of Agatha’s, keeping her close. Her head nestled into the space beneath Agatha's jaw, where her throat met her shoulder.

Agatha noticed the moisture then, as tears slid from Rio’s eyes to pool in the hollow of her throat.

“Oh sweetheart,” she cradled Rio’s head close to her heart as her own tears started to well and bleed.

“I looked for you in every single face,” the words were a whimpered confession, so quiet Agatha would have missed them if any other noise had permeated the moment, “every single time I felt the pull of a soul in need of me, I would hold my breath until I saw their face, until I knew it wasn’t you lying on the floor, glassy eyed and freezing cold”.

It was defining moment in Agatha’s long life, the confirmation of her selfishness. She had always known it was a trait she possessed, had relished in it even, yet the realisation that she had never once considered this reality, that Rio, bound to her duty as the sun was bound to rise, would be forced to continue her work. That the very act of it might mutate into a warped torture of her mind, as she waited for the day Agatha’s death was the one finally beckoning her closer.
