Agatha felt a sob choking up her throat, the sensation similar to vomit in the way her own guilt was making her sick. Yet Rio didn’t stop speaking, as though now she had started, she was unable to stop.

“And even then, when I knew that the person laying dead at my feet wasn’t you, I still looked around, desperate to see if they might have perished at your hand, waiting for a trace of your magic, or hoping perhaps you might leave me a clue like you used to, a hint as to where I could find you, a trail for me to find my way home”.

Agatha’s breathing was ragged as she listened to the glistening, bloodied truth of Rio’s pain.

“But you never did, and I was always so cold, so cold I couldn’t sleep”.

In a desperate bid to at least attempt to right the wrong, Agatha pressed her lips against Rio’s forehead as she drew the swathe of blankets tighter around Rio’s shoulders, nestling her within them, ensuring she was finally warmer.

Silence descended then, the only noise coming from the gentle sway of the curtains as a sharp October breeze swept through the open window, causing the heavy material to rustle against the wall.

Finally, when the emotions blocking her throat had drained enough for her voice to escape, Agatha spoke.

“I’ll keep you warm tonight sweetheart, I won’t let the cold touch you again. Sleep now”.

Rio’s breathing had already deepened and her muscles had already started to relax, turning buttery and soft against Agatha’s body, yet she managed to mumble, “promise?”

Agatha squeezed her eyes tightly together, adding the harm she had inflicted to the woman she loved to her long, long list of sins. A fresh wave of tears moistened her eyelashes and dripped down the sides of her face before she tucked her face slightly to nestle her lips against Rio’s forehead. Then, as though swearing an oath whispered the words, “yes my darling, I promise”.

And at long last Rio slept, Rio slept like the dead.

XXXXXX

The following day Agatha awoke to a flat screen television on the wall, Rio’s chest pressed tightly against her back, and Rio's arm wrapped snugly around her waist.

Glancing around, Agatha quickly noticed several other new additions to her bedroom including a smartphone on the bedside cabinet and a reading tablet on the desk. It was technology far more advanced than that available during the turn of the Millennium.

Rio shifted closer, mumbling something incoherent under her breath the moment Agatha wriggled slightly to see if anything else had been modernised. Agatha paused, then sighed the instant she truly registered Rio's embrace; which was both warm and familiar. A siren call, beckoning Agatha to sink backwards into it, to greedily indulge in the sensation of being cradled close, of being loved.

But that blaring alarm, the one that had been silenced so effectively by Rio’s tears yesterday evening had started to scream in her mind once more, spreading a sense of panic throughout her body, warning her that she was getting closer to an edge she wasn’t prepared to leap off of. For Rio, as much as Agatha loved her, represented everything that had very nearly destroyed her.

Agatha suddenly needed distance, so with gentle fingers she grasped Rio’s wrist and tried to wriggle free without waking the green witch. Of course, the moment she did so, Rio awoke and tightened her grip, hauling Agatha’s body tight against her own.

“You have never, in the three hundred and fifty years I have known you, been able to get up without waking me”.

Rio’s voice was husky from sleep, sparking a pulse of heat that started to simmer low in Agatha’ stomach. Suddenly aware that her body was about two seconds away from giving up the last few tethers of restraint holding her back from simply straddling her wife, she slapped an impatient hand at the arm still holding her captive.

“Well maybe if you didn’t have the hearing of a bat, I would be able to slip away. Now, let me up”.

Rio snorted from behind her, “a bat? I’m literally a vessel of natural power. As if you could sneak away from me”.

“I managed it well enough before”.

The moment the sharp words slipped from between her lips she regretted them, closing her eyes tightly to await Rio’s reaction.

However, instead of anger or acidic words in response, as she had been expecting, Rio simply exhaled once and slipped her arm from Agatha’s waist. Several inches of space appeared between them then, making that small slither of mattress appear as wide as a jagged crevasse, waiting to swallow them both whole.

“That you did,” was all Rio murmured quietly before standing from the bed and treading softly towards the door. Agatha stayed where she was, amongst the rumpled bedding still warm from Rio’s body heat, waiting for a final jab or insult.

Yet Rio said nothing else, choosing instead to pull the bedroom door open and quietly close it behind her, leaving Agatha to fester in a puddle of her own guilt.

Agatha closed her eyes again and exhaled heavily, attempting to breath out some of the turmoil she felt. However the moment she opened her eyes, she found she had been transported onto a simple sofa in a plain, bare room.

A camera was set up to film her from the shoulders up and a glazed-eyed man wearing a baseball cap with the word “PRODUCER” emblazoned across its peak stood beside the stand. He raised his hand and flicked the camera to rolling.

“So, another fight with your wife. What was this one over Agnes?”

His voice was monotone, like a bad actor reading directly from the pages of a script, with no inflexion or rhythm to his speech pattern.

Agatha glanced around and then down at herself, realising then that her pyjamas had been transformed into a purple v-neck sweater and dark slacks.

“What?” she snapped at the producer, frustrated that whatever madness was currently occurring, was happening right at the moment she needed it to happen least.

He repeated the question in exactly the same tone, “so, another fight with your wife. What was this one over Agnes?”

Agatha felt a scowl settle on her face, for this farce was undoubtedly linked to Wanda’s newest update of Westview's least favourite programme. After all, sitcoms followed certain tropes and a fairly modern inclusion was the art of the confessional; if done right, it created comedy gold.

This entire addition was new, however what was even more unusual, was the fact the sitcom aspect of Wanda's enchantment now appeared to be taking place, even when not in direct view of Wanda or Vision. Usually, everything to do with the television show Wanda was insistent on creating happened only within proximity of her family, and had never happened when Agatha had been alone at her house.

Gathering herself, she was quick to get in character with a bright grin, “oh you know how it is when us ladies sync up. It's pistols at dawn in our household until one of us caves and grabs the chocolate ice cream with fudge chunks from the freezer”.

The blank-faced man didn’t react to her answer, but he did ask another question, “Rita seemed upset. Are you going to apologise Agnes?”

Agatha felt her grin tighten into something malicious and forced herself to inhale deeply, intent on maintaining Agnes’s peppy façade, “well in that case, I’ll be sure to grab the salted caramel from the freezer too”.

The producer didn’t look impressed or pleased with her responses, but she must have said something right, for he brought a hand up to the camera and switched it off. The moment he did so, she blinked and found herself back in her bedroom, still dressed in the clothes she had been magicked into.

“Well shit,” she grumbled, realising things were getting even more difficult than they had been before, in more than one way too.

XXXXXX

Rio wasn’t in her room, nor was she in the kitchen. The bathroom was empty, and the living room was vacant.

Agatha, who was insistent on reminding herself that she didn’t actually care where Rio was, and that she just wanted to ask whether she had also been dragged away for a confessional interview, frowned heavily as she retraced her steps upstairs, wanting to ensure Rio hadn’t doubled back to nap in Agatha’s bed.

She swung the bedroom door open and ripped the covers from the mattress with clawed hands, pulling them into an untidy pile on the floor. The bed was empty, just like everywhere else.

Agatha glared furiously at the empty mattress as thought it was personally responsible for Rio’s sudden disappearance, when a sudden pool of inspiration flooded her mind.

“The garden!” she clicked her fingers knowingly, where else would a green witch retreat to?

She hurried down the stairs and through the kitchen, only to growl under her breath on reaching the back decking.

For the garden was empty too, and there weren’t even any blossoms growing amongst the brittle winter grass to indicate Rio had been there recently.

“Where the fuck is she?” Agatha hissed, trying hard to swallow the panic she could feel beginning to bubble up her throat at Rio’s sudden absence.

Storming back through the house, she pulled the curtains aside from the front room window and stared out the glass. Scanning her narrowed eyes up and down the street she felt her heart start to pound with anxiety at the green witch's disappearance.

Suddenly, a breeze fluttered around her. Agatha turned quickly to find Rio perched on the arm of the sofa with a guarded expression on her face. She wasn’t dressed in modern clothing, nothing at all like the clothing Agatha was wearing. Instead she had resorted to the clothing she had always preferred; a forest green jacket crafted from weaved vines, grass, and leaves and dark trousers, decorated with golden ruins, threaded in intricate patterns along the matte material. The clothing was tight on Rio's figure, highlighting the attractive curve of her hips and waist.

And, just like usual, the most common emotion Agatha felt in reaction to her own weaknesses, whether that be the flare of attraction she felt at seeing Rio in her own clothing, or her desperate fear at Rio's sudden absence, Agatha felt fury burn in her stomach.

“Where the hell have you been? I was looking for you”.

Rio shrugged and pulled the dagger from her belt to fiddle with it, “I had business to attend to”.

Agatha scoffed harshly, “oh business , was it?”

Rio’s gaze snapped up to Agatha’s, her eyes harsh, “yes, it was. You know I am bound to it”.

Agatha did, she knew better than most.

Choosing to ignore the bait she could feel loaded in Rio’s words, she gestured upstairs, “well go and get changed then. We need to go and see if Wanda is close to cracking or if she needs another push”.

Slipping from the sofa, Rio wandered towards the fireplace and dug her knife into the stone mantle, causing a hideous screeching noise to resound through the room.

“I am not going to get changed”.

Agatha laughed, loudly, spitefully, “you can’t walk around Westview like that, they already think your bananas. We don’t need to draw any more attention to ourselves”.

“You misunderstand me. I am not going to get changed because I need to leave again. Something has happened, a disaster of sorts across the sea and there is a town in need of me”.

Agatha drew back as though she had been slapped and her mocking smile froze into one of strangled fear, “you’re leaving?”

“Yes”.

Agatha crossed her arms and raised her chin arrogantly, trying to minimise the physical evidence of her anxiety, “for how long?”

Rio stared at her; eyebrows raised with disbelief at Agatha’s sudden demands, which contrasted violently with every other time she had ordered Rio to leave.

“For however long it takes,” Rio barked a frustrated laugh, “I thought you would be pleased to be rid of me, it’s all you have spoken about since this all started”.

Agatha’s mouth dropped open, uncertain as to how to respond to the statement. It was true after all, yet now facing the reality of it, of Rio being gone again and she alone, it left Agatha's skin prickling with a heavy desire to pull Rio close and not let her go.

Yet as always, Agatha's pride reared its head as those shutters of self preservation, forged violently through a mother’s hatred and a community's neglect, rattled shut at the first sign of rejection.

“Who said I wasn’t pleased?”

Rio’s gaze became heavier. She looked suddenly exhausted, “well, in that case, your wish has been granted. I hope whatever power you find here finally sates you. Nothing else seems to”.

And with that Rio swept toward the wall and dragged her dagger down the wallpaper, slicing it neatly in two. A section peeled back away from the wall, revealing a dark cavern backlit with a green glow, as though several thousand fireflies were hovering just out of view.

Rio raised her foot to step through and the image of that, of Rio leaving with her shoulders heavy with the burden of loving a witch as difficult to love as Agatha, caused her to jolt forward to grip Rio’s wrist tightly between desperate fingers.

“I didn’t say I was pleased either,” her own voice sounded foreign to her ears, unused as she was to hearing it quite so distressed.

Rio took pity on her and paused her departure, turning slightly to look at Agatha over her shoulder, “that’s the problem Agatha, I am not sure which one is the truth and honestly, I’m not sure you do either”.

Agatha felt tears pool in her eyes as she tightened her grip on Rio’s wrist, “let me figure it out then, give me time to do that”.

Rio looked away, smiling. It wasn’t a happy smile, it was overloaded with self-deprecation and a fracturing heart, “if you don’t know the answer after one hundred years away from me, then I think that is truth enough. And I do have a job to do”.

Desperation spurred Agatha closer, “will you at least come back afterwards? You won’t disappear?”

Rio’s smile hardened, “what? Like you did?”

Agatha swallowed hard, closed her eyes and took the hit; she knew it was deserved.

“Yes, like I did” she admitted quietly, her words little more than a whisper, “you have to promise me you won’t do that to me, I know I don’t deserve it, but please don’t. I couldn’t stand it”.

Rio’s eyes travelled down to her own wrist. Those dark eyes studied the fingers gripping her arm so tightly the blood was straining to flow through, turning the tips white with pressure. Slowly, her gaze lifted to capture Agatha's eyes.

“Please my love, please come back to me,” Agatha pleaded, and for the first time since their paths had crossed again, allowed the truth to be visible through her eyes. She was desperate for Rio to see her swirling confusion, her fearful hesitation, her earnest desire, yet also, underneath it all, to see the bruised, scarred heart that still only beat for the green witch before her and the child they had shared and lost.

Agatha waited and felt relief sweep through her body the moment Rio’s gaze softened minutely.

Rio didn’t speak, but she did give a single sharp nod of her head, which for Rio was as good as a signature on a contract. Then she turned to escape through the thin door she had crafted, leaving Agatha with a heart full of sorrow and an unspoken fear that this might be the first promise Death, who was the rule of law in the natural world and the keeper of oaths, may just renegade on.

The moment Rio was through the makeshift doorway, the wallpaper zipped back together, sealing shut. The only evidence anything peculiar had ever happened to it was a single indented line down its centre.

Agatha blinked her eyes closed, trying to exhale the pain out in a single ragged breath and pull herself together, to gain focus back on the plan in hand.

Yet the moment she opened her eyes, she found herself once again sequestered away in that same empty room, perched on a lonely sofa with the blank-faced producer staring at her.

He flicked the camera on.

“So, Rita left you”.

Agatha bristled, “she hasn’t left me”. Her voice was biting, with not a single hint of Agnes in her tone or expression, she was entirely herself; feral and furious. “She has business to attend to, she's coming back”.

The producers face remained slack, aside from a single eyebrow twitching upwards by half a centimetre, “she didn’t look very happy, she looked tired, fed up”.

Agatha felt her heart pound painfully in her chest at the truth of his words, “we had a fight, but that won’t stop her from coming home. It never does”.

She wasn’t sure who she was trying to convince anymore; the producer or herself.

He remained silent, giving her space to expand on her statement. The only noise in the room was the gentle hum of the camera equipment.

“She will be back,” she reinforced her point through gritted teeth, “she will come back to me, she always does”.

“We’ll see,” was all he said in that same blank voice, encapsulating Agatha’s fears with two simple words.

The producer then lifted a hand and flicked the camera off. Reality warped around her moments later and she was promptly sent back to her living room, where she spent the remainder of her afternoon staring at a slither of wallpaper with a single line running through it.

An Interrupted Broadcast

Chapter Notes

Thank you for all of the lovely comments & Kudos! I appreciate it, truly!

In this chapter things take a slight twist as we start to transition between Wandavision and Agatha All Along. I had this idea in my head for the past few chapters and it just felt right to do it, so I hope you guys agree! Fingers crossed!

Anyway, I will stop wittering on now and simply say, I hope you enjoy it! <3

It might be fair to assume Agatha spiralled, although she was unwilling to admit it, even to the very end.

She had waited, for several days she had waited, biding her time for when Rio would return as she had promised. Yet, she didn’t reappear, not even after a full week of playacting as the gossiping neighbour and enduring several passive aggressive interviews with the blank-faced producer, Rio had still not come home.

Initially Agatha remained resilient to her own doubts. She had reassured herself, both verbally and mentally, that Rio would come back, that she always did, that she always would. But when day four slipped passed without any sign of her wife, Agatha’s mood sunk into a far darker recess.

From that point, the reality of it all and the pain of that last conversation stuck to the forefront of her mind, like a photograph superglued to the interior of her consciousness. It was the look on Rio’s face as she had left, that heartbroken smile of hers. Her words followed soon after, spinning amongst Agatha’s thoughts. It was primarily Rio's confession, the one she had whispered against the skin of Agatha's throat, of how she had searched for her across the years. It echoed in her mind every moment of the day, as though someone had pushed play on a cassette tape inside her brain and she was unable to find the off switch.

Sadness followed soon after. It was an emotion Agatha despised entirely, even though she was intimately familiar with its cold hands upon her heart. Then as another day passed, sadness mutated, transforming into a feeling Agatha hated even more than simple melancholy: guilt.

After all, Agatha and guilt had never seen eye to eye. It would have been impossible to have lived the life she had and committed the crimes she did if she had ever allowed that particular emotion to rule her.

So, Agatha did what she always did when confronted with the consequences of her own actions and an array of emotions she despised; she doubled down and became vicious.

And who better to aim all of her pent up fury at, than the woman currently prevailing over a fantasy world that Agatha both envied and hated? For Wanda had everything, literally everything Agatha coveted.

Wanda had her great unlimited mass of power, she had her dead lover; reanimated and conscious, she had her children !?

It was an injustice of the highest order that Wanda got everything she wanted, that she could hold a town hostage in order to live out her perfect life. Yet, all Agatha had gained over the centuries was an abundance of heartbreak and grief.

She had power sure, but she had ripped it from the hands of dead witches who had all tried to kill her, she had a love in her heart so all-encompassing that at times Rio’s absence made her feel mad, truly insane with the loss of her. Yet she couldn't keep Rio, she couldn't be with her because of all that still remained between them, as thick and as obstructive as a concrete wall, and her son? Her son was dead.

Her thoughts followed this dark pattern for the remainder of the week, when she was suddenly struck with a dire, dreadful concept, one that sent her spinning down a reckless path. It was the thought that if Rio, the woman she loved above all others, the woman who knew every single inch of her dark, corrupt soul, no longer considered Agatha a person worthy of pursuit, well, she would have to embrace the only thing she had left. Of course, it was that same ugly darkness that had kept her company from the start, corrupting any spark of goodness she might have possessed if her mother had actually loved her, if her son hadn't been snatched from her arms whilst she slept, if her wife would simply come home.

And the darkness, as it always had been, was ravenous, and oh so eager to gape open and swallow her whole.

As a result, her determination to discover answers to her original quandary doubled, fuelled by her need for distraction from the bloody, ragged hole in her chest where her heart had once sat. She focussed all of her attention on getting the truth to the questions that had been haunting her since discovering this great orb of scarlet energy: where was Wanda sourcing her immense power? And how, how could Agatha possess it?

Her final campaign had started out successfully enough, as every piece she had set to fall did so when designed to, like a grand wave of domino's, one tipping into the other until the larger picture was revealed.

Wanda had trusted Agnes to care for the twins, whilst she had what basically consisted of a magical breakdown, causing the warped reality she had wrapped around the town of Westview to flicker and flash back and forth between the real world and the hex. The twins had followed Agatha trustingly, both of them happy to sit on her sofa and pet Señor Scratchy.

It had been easy enough from that point to spell them to sleep and then transport them in a cloud of purple smoke to the enchanted room attached to her warded basement. She wasn’t a monster, so she had made sure it was filled with everything two young boys might enjoy whilst waiting for their babysitter to question their mother; bunkbeds set back against the wall, two plush beanbags set on a comfortable rug, a large flat screen on the wall that was hooked up to a selection of video game consoles. A fridge was in the corner, stocked full of cartons of chocolate milk, cans of soda, and ample snacks to feast on.

The spiteful part of her had considered removing some of the luxuries she had added in a moment of weakness, but they were sweet boys, sweet boys who reminded her far too much of the son she had lost, so she left them their modern comforts, especially as she couldn’t guarantee them their mother’s life once she had finished her interrogation.

An opportunity then presented itself to get Wanda alone too. Agatha played the doting neighbour, swooping in to drag Wanda away from a confrontation with Geraldine. From there, it had been a matter of luring Wanda into her enchanted basement where her wards were already drawn and waiting.

Their journey through Wanda’s life had been as insightful as it was frustrating. Frustrating because it became clear very quickly that Wanda’s chaos magic stemmed from a life drowning in death and submerged in grief. Yet, Agatha, who had existed for centuries before Wanda had even been born, who had been despised by her mother the moment she entered this world, who had been attacked with the intent to kill by her own coven, whose true love had taken her son's spirit whilst she slept leaving her to wake with his cold, still body in her arms, who had enough rage running through her body to fuel a country, was unable to utilise magic in the same subconscious way Wanda did with such ease. And just to add insult to injury, had also mastered it's application without any sort of tutoring or magical education.

It was, put plainly, downright offensive.

Naturally things had digressed from that point, ending in a grand battle between the two of them. It felt especially cathartic to finally use the full extent of her magic, to at long last, wipe clean the mask of Agnes and step into the power she had been forced to hide for weeks.

Her Arrogance had been her downfall in the end, alongside her greed for more, always more.

She had assumed herself to be the player always two moves ahead, yet Wanda had spun the world out from under her by using Agatha's own knowledge against her, exposing the giant wards she had seared into the circular, glowing walls of her hex before stealing every ounce of magic Agatha possessed.

Wanda had floated back to earth, hauling Agatha alongside her, who had no more power to resist the enchantment she had been captured by, who could only bow her head in humiliation as the ground grew closer. Her legs collapsed beneath her the moment her feet touched tarmac, although she did try to retain an unphased exterior, even whilst kneeling in defeat before the scarlet witch.

“Good girl,” she murmured, glaring up at Wanda from under her brow. She was unused to feeling shame settle into a horrible tangled mess beneath her ribs, especially after three centuries of reigning victorious over her fellow witch. It was a humbling experience, and it did not suit her. She didn’t like it. At all .

“So what now? Just going to lock me up somewhere?” Her voice was brittle with barely disguised fear, a final attempt at bravado. Although Wanda’s response made panic quickly spread throughout her body.

“No, not somewhere. Here”.

“Here?”

“I’ll give you the role you chose. The nosy neighbour”.

And for the third time in Agatha’s long life, she begged.

“No please”.

Wanda’s face was resigned. It was the expression an executioner wore having decided to finally drop their axe, “I’m sorry”.

“No, you’re not, you’re cruel. You have no idea what you have unleashed, you’re going to need me,” she pleaded.

“If I do, I’ll know where to find you,” Wanda’s eyes drifted over her face as a curious wrinkle appeared between her brows, “I really liked you Agnes. Or Agatha, I suppose. I thought we were friends”.

“Wait, wait, wait!”

Those were the last words Agatha heard from within her own consciousness, for in the next moment, Wanda leant closer and tapped a soft finger against her temple and in a single whisp of magic, secured Agatha as a prisoner within her own mind and drew the mask of Agnes firmly over everything Agatha knew and everything Agatha was. A ripple of power sizzled over her skin and within seconds every thought, memory, hope, fear, and dream from her long, full life were encased in scarlet tendrils and replaced with daytime television, book club, and almond milk lattes.

Glancing up from blinking at the sidewalk, Agnes grinned at finding Wanda, her best friend, standing over her, “oh hiya hon!” Her eyes roved across Wanda’s body, appreciating the scarlet outfit she was donning, “say, that’s some kind of get up you’re wearing. Did I leave the oven on? Or is that just you hot stuff?”

Wanda smiled down at her with a pleased, somewhat endeared expression on her face, “you live here now. No one will ever bother you”.

“Okie-dokie artichokey,” she chirped back, content to remain in the town she had been born in.

Wanda smiled again, Another amused twitch of her lips before starting to turn away from Agnes, who was sat on the floor? Outside?

Yet, before Wanda was able to turn away entirely, a blazing line of flashing, green light appeared beside her, as the point of a curved blade sliced downward through the glowing air. A section of the street in front of her lifted then, as a figure, covered in mud and leaves and holding a bouquet of wildflowers, stepped through the strange slither of space onto the street, right in front of them. As quick as it had appeared, the rippling doorway disappeared with a final flash of green light.

Agnes felt her heart brighten on realising it was her darling wife, “Rita, honey! You’re finally home from your business trip! Oh how I missed you!”

Rita however, didn't looked pleased. If anything she looked furious, as angry as she did whenever the Westview Wolverines lost the softball league. Agnes could tell, for she had been quick to notice how badly Rita's hands were shaking, which was a fairly common reaction from her wife to upsetting emotions. What was unusual though, were the sparks of green energy flashing from her palms and the wide eyes that were wild, almost feral.

Wanda too, had noticed the return of her lovely wife and turned to greet her.

“You’re a witch too ?” her voice was stricken, brimming with rage as scarlet energy swirled around her palms and her pupils flashed red.

Rita’s voice was two-toned, almost bassy when she pointed a finger at Agnes and roared back, “ what have you done?! ”

Agnes was currently not much use to either of them, mainly because, in all honestly, she was finding it difficult to drag her eyes away from her wife. She just looked so beautiful, especially when she was angry and covered in soil, just like she was right now. It wasn't unusual for her to be covered in dirt after all, as she was so often sprinkled in the stuff after spending an afternoon in the garden. Rita was always so keen on ensuring their garden was kept as their own secret oasis, spending hours at a time mowing the grass, repotting plants, and trimming back any dead leaves or branches. She sighed dreamily and let her eyes drift in lazy appreciation down her wife's body, before zoning in on the bunch of wildflowers she was still gripping so tightly their stems had started to bend and were now clearly at risk of snapping.

A blush dusted Agnes's cheeks as her smile grew bashful and she couldn’t resist asking after them as she pointed up towards Rita's clenched fist, “Are those for me, my love?”

As though her words were an incantation, Rita froze and stared down at her with, much to Agnes’s surprise, her mouth drooped in shock and her dark eyes brimming with… heartbreak? Now, that couldn’t be right. Agnes was right here, they were married. What was there to be devastated over?

Rita’s voice was low, almost timid as she repeated Agnes’s words back to her, “you’re love?”

Agnes’s responding smile was a beaming grin, for she was unable to stop the love she felt pounding beneath her breast for this woman from pouring out of her in every way it was possible to express it, “of course you are my love, you’re my whole heart, sweetheart”.

Rita’s lower lip quivered as slow tears started to drip down from her beautiful eyes. Agnes frowned, suddenly feeling extremely shaken at the sight of her wife’s distress, especially as her upset had been in reaction to the words of love they shared so openly and so often in their marriage. Agnes got to shaky feet, unsure why she was even sat on the tarmac in the centre of town in the first place.

“Rita, sweetheart? What is it? What’s wrong?” Agnes tried to bridge the space between them, arms open, eager to embrace her.

Yet Rita, who had turned towards her with the evident intention of collapsing into them, didn't get to, for a bright beam of scarlet energy suddenly struck her in the chest and sent her spinning through the air to land in a pile of limbs several feet away.

From the way she reacted though, it was as though Rita had never been hit in the first place, for she was quickly back on her feet and flying towards Wanda. She raised both hands and started to fire bolt after bolt of green crackling lightning at their neighbour, who managed to block every blazing attempt with a swipe of her arm.

“ What have you done to her?! ” Rita screamed, “ you bring her back to me! Right now! ”

Wanda threw a wave of energy towards Rita as she hissed from between clenched teeth, “you were both in on this scheme, were you? In it together to steal my power from me?”

Rita hissed, her eyes wide and sparkling manically, “I don’t need to steal your power, chaos magic is beneath me”.

Wanda scoffed, “oh yeah? And what makes you so special?”

Rita didn’t answer her question, instead she drew a stream of magic into her hand and flicked it out like a whip to wrap around Wanda's ankle before tugging it backwards so the glowing chain would tighten and pull Wanda over onto the concrete. Rita hauled it hard, dragging Wanda back towards where she stood with an orb of emerald energy sparking around her. Wanda hissed in pain as her hands and knees scrabbled hard against shards of rubble and chunks of brick as she tried to fight against the energetic vine hauling her backwards, managing at last to grip the curb's edge and halt Rita's ability to reel her any closer.

It felt like the right time to try and diffuse whatever this was, so Agnes stepped between them with a nervous smile stretched across her face, “gosh, you’re both angrier than a pair of hissing kittens,” her brow drew downwards in concern then as she glanced between her furious wife and her seething best friend, suddenly feeling desperately unhappy that they were so upset with one another, “what’s got you both in such a twist, huh? Can’t we sort this out over cocktails?”

Her intention had been to calm the confrontation down, yet almost instantly, her words had the opposite effect. Because the moment Rita realised Agnes was addressing them both, a ripple of suffering anguish swept across her features as she stared back at her, replacing her anger momentarily and unknowingly gifting Wanda the key to her agony.

For in the next moment, Wanda pushed out a wave of scarlet energy, throwing anyone standing in the square off their feet, before swiping a sparking palm toward her ankle to banish the tendril of green magic still wrapped around it. Agnes, who had also been thrown backwards in the blast, scrambled back to standing, just as Wanda's jeering tone echoed out towards Rita, who was also hauling herself back up into a fighting stance with a manic feral grin slashed across her face.

“So it wasn’t all fake huh? You two were actually together before I came here? Actually in love ?"

Rita hissed at Wanda through clenched teeth and drew a wave of speeding air upwards so she could throw it towards Wanda who was forced to brace against its onslaught.

“You have no idea who you are quarrelling with!” Rita’s voice was a terrifying blend of fury and demand, with a bassy echo that carried even over the rushing noise of power being hurled across the square, “now undo the enchantment you have placed on her, now !”

“Rita honey?” Agnes shouted, trying hard to intervene again, even whilst holding both hands over her head to protect her face from the loose rubble and litter that was now swirling above them all, caught in the storm her wife had... conjured? Somehow? “Why don’t we just go home. We can put on that show you love? The gardening one?”

“This is your wife's punishment!” Wanda shouted at Rita, ignoring Agnes entirely. “She plotted this entire thing, she has been lying to me for weeks! She forced me to relive the darkest moment’s in my life!” Wanda’s voice was a violent roar; it was the voice of a broken woman whose only reserve was stemming from the well of anger she held inside. “And now, now the only things I had left in this pitiful world I will have to lose! Because of her! My husband ! My sons ! My entire life ! because of her , because of all she tried to steal from me !”

Rita rushed forward then as her own fury pushed her closer to Wanda. As quick as a flash, another whip of green light shot from her palm to wrap around Wanda’s throat. Rita tugged her forward, like a curling vine wrapping around the branch of a tree.

Rita’s voice was pure poison as she spat out, “you cannot comprehend the horrors I will do to you unless you fix her ”.

Wanda didn’t look fearful though in the face of Rita's threats. She didn’t look concerned and she didn’t look cowed. Instead, she laughed, a manic crazed laugh that was promptly reduced to a spluttered choking when the magical vine around her throat started to tighten, squeezing the air from her lungs.

“Nothing you do to me is worse than what I will have to do to myself,” Wanda hissed with what air she had left, as her eyes flashed towards the overturned minivan her husband and sons had been sheltering behind since the battle started.

Rita tugged Wanda that final foot closer, reeling her closer with the glowing vine that she then replaced with her own clawed hand. With a single tug Rita dragged her closer, until their faces were mere inches apart. Rita’s teeth were clenched and her eyes were wild, reminding Agnes of the kind’s of animals they would watch documentaries on together, all cosied up on their couch, learning about lions or wolves from the Discovery Channel.

The next two words Rita spoke were a hissed warning through clenched teeth, a final demand, “ free. Her ”.

Wanda’s mouth was bloody from their fight when she grinned up at Rio, her white teeth glistening as red as the magic swirling in her pupils, “no. She needs to be punished”.

Rita shook Wanda by the throat with one hand as she drew the curved dagger from her belt with the other, yet before she could even try and use it, a cloud of red smoke engulfed Wanda, transporting her swiftly out of Rita’s reach and back towards Agnes who, on realising neither of the women were going to listen to her, had taken cover behind a street bench.

“Wanda, honey I don’t know why Rita is so mad, but let me talk to her - I'm sure we can sort this out!” Agnes started to speak the moment she realised her best friend was standing beside her, yet Wanda didn’t reply, instead she grabbed Agnes’s shirt and tugged until her back was pressed to Wanda's front.

“Hey now!” Agnes cried, having had quite enough of whatever had made two normally reasonable women brawl in the street, “now I know you two girls are having a tough day, but there is no need for physical violence!”

Yet once again, Agnes was ignored, for Wanda was too busy glaring at Rita with blazing eyes, who had started taking dangerous strides closer. Strangely enough though, with every step she took her face shimmered, appearing from some angles almost... skeletal?

She didn’t know her wife could do that. Huh, the more you know and all that.

Wanda didn’t appear phased either, as she quickly held up a hand to draw a wall of scarlet fire between them, preventing Rita from getting any closer.

“And I have just thought of the most fitting punishment for you too,” Wanda spoke loudly, so Rita would hear her over the hum of her magic.

“You cannot punish me ,” Rita hissed through her bony mouth, an eery sight even for Agnes who loved her with her whole heart, even if she did have some secrets they would definitely be discussing over a bowl of Agnes’s homemade casserole later that night.

Wanda’s scarlet barricade blazed in time with her temper, holding Rita at bay the moment she brandished her own wave of emerald energy and poured it towards the red wall blocking her path.

“You are an accomplice in her treachery, committed an offence against my family, are a liar, and you deserve to be punished for your crimes, just as she does”.

Wanda’s voice was stern and final, like a judge decreeing a sentence after a long, tiring month in court.

Rita didn’t reply with words, only screamed with fury as she started to slash at the wall of scarlet with her curved dagger in desperate, rage-fuelled strokes.

“So, as a result of your deception I will be forced to pull this whole hex down, destroying my home , collapsing my family , killing my husband , and reducing my children to little more than atoms. So, you definitely do not get to continue living in matrimonial bliss with the woman you love, I won’t allow it”.

Rita’s voice was barely human as she threw herself at the red mirage, her temper so great that the magic holding her back started to shudder and weaken, “ don’t touch her! Don’t you touch her! ”

Her wife's anguish caused tears to pool in Agnes’s eyes, yet the moment she tried to wriggle free, intent on holding Rita and soothing her fears, Wanda's grip on the back of her shirt tightened and she hauled her backwards even harder, just as Rita’s punishment drifted from her tongue.

“So, Rita if that is even your real name,” Wanda spat, sounding disgusted, “this is for you”.

And with that, Wanda raised a hand from where she had been gripping her tightly to tap a gentle fingertip against Agnes’s temple, causing a single spark of scarlet energy to sink through skin and bone.

A shudder ran through Agnes's body and she managed to take a single shaky step forward before her eyes rolled back and she dropped heavily to the floor, aware only of the seething, primal scream that echoed nearby as all went dark around her and the pavement, like an old friend, greeted her once more.

XXXXXX

The next few hours were nothing more to either Agatha or Agnes than shadowed darkness, glimpsing dreams, and shades of faces, or one face in particular really.

Awareness bled back slowly after that as her senses returned to her one after the other, like a polaroid photo gaining clarity as it develops.

Her hearing was first; the rustle of her own body against soft sheets, a gentle breeze sailing through an open window and causing curtains to brush against one another.

Then smell came second; laundry detergent, fresh cut wildflowers, alongside an undercurrent of something earthier, like the scent of dry soil after a rainstorm.

Touch followed soon after; the soft give of the pillow beneath her aching head, a hand holding hers, it’s palm rough but ever so gentle.

And finally sight, as her eyes cracked open, first only to bleary shapes and merging colours, like the spread of watercolours across a damp canvas, just for everything to sharpen into focus quickly after a few painful blinks.

Her bedroom was as it had always been, with her television on the wall and her hamper in the corner. Agnes glanced around, taking note of a bunch of drooping, broken-stemmed wildflowers in a vase on her bedside cabinet, before finally focussing on the person sat beside her, who was cradling her hand with her head bowed over it, looking almost like she was praying.

Her movement must have alerted the woman to Agnes’s waking, for she looked up the instant Agnes shifted. Immediately, Agnes was met with brown eyes shimmering with unshed tears and a face so pretty it made her inhale sharply. The woman's face crumpled with relief the moment their eyes met, “you’re awake," her voice was strained, rusty from tears.

Agnes stared at her curiously, allowing her eyes to travel from dark eyes, down the long, elegant slope of her nose to parted lips. After a moment of heavy silence and study, Agnes sat herself up with her free hand and as she smiled timidly at the beautiful woman in front of her, finally found her voice.

“Not that I’m sorry to wake up and see such a beautiful face looking back at me,” Agnes grinned, feeling shy, “because seriously, did I die and go to heaven, or is that just you hot stuff?”

The woman’s jaw dropped in shock, evidently slightly disturbed that Agnes was bold enough to flirt with her moments after opening her eyes from what she assumed was some sort of concussion? Caused by... something? Maybe a freak accident of some kind?

The woman didn’t say anything though, so Agnes was able to continue asking what she had been intending to since she had awoken in her bedroom with this beautiful woman watching over her.

“But, if I could ask, without appearing rude or ungrateful; who exactly are you? And why are you in my house?”

Agnes hadn’t thought it an unreasonable question, nor asked in particularly abrupt manner, yet the way the beautiful woman’s face collapsed in despair did seem like a slight overreaction to her innocent query. Brown eyes flashed the most peculiar shade of green as tears started to drop down over her cheeks. Her lip trembled on a slack jaw, appearing as though she was attempting to speak but had forgotten every word or motion required of the mouth to communicate verbally.

“I’m sorry hon, I didn’t mean to upset you,” Agnes murmured, not quite sure what to do with this overtly emotional stranger in her bedroom.

The moment she spoke, the darkhaired woman’s devastated gaze shot up to capture hers and as their eyes locked, Agnes watched with an uncertain frown as the stranger’s distress suddenly transformed into a spitting fury. Her hand tightened around Agnes’s own and her brow dropped heavily over her dark eyes, giving the woman a menacing, threatening aura, making her look dangerous, in fact she looked deadly.

Yet, much to Agnes’s surprise, she didn't feel frightened or concerned at having this angry, somewhat feral stranger in her bedroom, she felt merely confusion, over a lot of things in fact. The sensation of which then multiplied twice when the stranger opened her mouth and spoke, in a voice as furious as it was solemn, “I’ll get you back my love I swear it. And then, once I know you are safe and yourself once again, I will find the scarlet witch and she will learn that there are far worse fates than simply dying”.

Agnes blinked before a slow, patient smile bloomed over her face, “ah, right… well, that sure sound’s exciting hon. Now, what time is it? Did I miss Jeopardy?”

Shattering the Screen

Chapter Notes

GUYS. This is long. And it is kind of a journey, so I hope you're up for it. It was a bit of a labour of love if truth be told, so I really, really, really hope you enjoy it.

Also, we get a little insight into Rio's POV for the first time, so I will make it clear whose POV we are in with a cheeky little title.

Thanks as well, of course, for all the lovely comments & kudos - you guys are the sweetest!

I hope you enjoy! <3

See the end of the chapter for more notes

RIO

Rio hadn’t been born when time began, it had been far simpler than that. It had been an unassuming transition from non-existence to existence and at first it had been silent.

The universe was quiet for a long time, a silent vacuum with naught but a sporadic wave of sound from some distant exploding star, spreading its energy out across the plane of darkness that Death had hewn her robe from.

Slowly though, as more stars died and their matter mixed and their elements curdled, life began.

Rio had watched as microscopic organisms adapted, as bacteria formed, as fungi and plants worked together to leave the ocean floor, as corals appeared, and then fish, and then insects, each one developing over eons of time. Her view had been similar to that of a zoetrope, one that displayed the process of evolution through a sequence of progressive changes, like flickering images flashing from one to the next in sporadic, bumpy, sometimes ugly jumps.

Yet, it wasn’t until humanity had bloomed from the constant turning of time that the point of Rio had then become clear. For the veils of the beyond had fluttered, an ache had started in her sternum and soon she followed that feeling until she took her place as guide; the being responsible for ferrying the masses from one plane to the next in a constant cycle of death and rebirth.

It was at that point she had learnt the clinical, black-and-white definition of what it was to have a purpose. But, it wasn’t until she met Agatha Harkness, that the true meaning of the word purpose, of what it actually meant to have something, or rather someone, driving an individual forward, came into sharp focus and she started to understand the why of it all.

The why of humanity.

Agatha was her spark in the dark, the breeze that stoked a smouldering ember into a blazing fire. She had kissed Rio’s mouth, exhaled life into Death and in a single instant, everything Rio thought she knew of the universe, the assumptions she had ignorantly made were promptly scrambled and rearranged into a new mosaic, one that revolved around moody blue eyes, dark, wild hair that flowed over proud shoulders, and a pouty mouth that hid a sharp tongue.

So, when Wanda had touched a gentle finger to Agatha’s temple and removed every trace of Rio from her mind, Rio had felt that hollow emptiness, the one that she had existed in, quite unknowingly, before Agatha had taught her what it was to be human and set her on fire from the inside out, the one that had tried to drown her when Agatha had run from her, promptly returned. With its maw open and gaping, waiting to swallow her whole.

It was a pain beyond comprehension. One she wasn't entirely sure she would survive, which was absurd considering she herself would never know the peace death brought. It was an agony comparable to being doused in oil, set on fire, and left to burn. But without ever actually dying or being extinguished. A consistent, aching, shredding, violent pain that howled from the cavern beneath her ribs where her heart, black and shrivelled as it was, sat.

The days following Agatha waking from scarlet magic dissolving all evidence of Rio from her mind were the hardest she had ever lived. And she had existed for all eternity.

She had been forced to lie, almost immediately, for one thing. Not even given a grace period to comprehend the horror of what had been done to the woman she loved, or the agony of their love having been ripped from Agatha's mind as though it were merely a stray weed growing amongst flowers.

She had used her real name, the name Agatha had always known.

"I'm Rio, Rio Vidal… you’re neighbour," she had managed to choke out, hoping desperately that it would spark some sort of familiarity in Agnes's eyes. Yet, she had been met with nothing but dim politeness and that same beaming smile Agnes had been donning since her eyes had opened and asked a question as futile as whether she had missed a particularly bad quiz show.

"Rio Vidal..." Agnes had repeated brightly, "well, ain't that as pretty as a meadow in May. It just rolls right of the tongue, it's beautiful".

That first night, Rio had tried to draw Agatha to the surface with her own magic. She had snuck back into Agnes's bedroom once she had fallen asleep, placed one glowing palm against her forehead, the other against her heart, bowed her head and wept. She had sent wave after wave of energy through Agnes's body, hoping to untie the scarlet knots currently holding her mind hostage. Yet, after a few minutes Agnes's eyes had shot open, her pupils had flashed red, and she had screamed herself hoarse, clutching her head between her hands as though someone had stuck a burning poker through her ear and scrambled it around. Rio had tried that a few more times, but after the fourth attempt, when Agnes's body had collapsed from exhaustion once the pain finally subsided, Rio stopped trying to force her way through Wanda's curse. It was clear, after all, that magic alone wasn’t going to free Agatha from this spell.

It was fortunate in a lot of ways that the character Wanda had forced Agatha to adopt was laid back and desperately lonely, because now Wanda, the woman Agnes believed to be her best friend, was gone, she clung to Rio's apparent friendship like a clinging vine climbing a tree. That first night, she had insisted Rio stay, first just to wait out her own concussion, then it had been for dinner the following night, then it had been to go to the farmers market the following morning. It didn't seem to even cross Agnes's mind to ask or question why the stranger who supposedly rescued her from a car accident was now practically living with her. But, Rio wasn't going to turn her nose up at a turn of good fortune, although their proximity did cause issues.

The primary issue laid at the feet of that familiar darkness waiting to swallow Rio whole. It was always there, waiting and watching, inching closer every time Agatha, or rather "Agnes," glanced her way, with familiar eyes that held no depth, that were as shallow as spring puddles, like Wanda had reached forward with clawed fingers and scooped the very essence of Agatha out from between her ribs, leaving only a muted, poor imitation of the woman Rio loved.

The second issue was temptation. Agnes, who at her heart was inspired by Agatha's own traits, including her queerness, was as gay as Agatha and even more flirtatious with it, which was saying something. She wasn't backwards in coming forwards when it came to her own attraction, and fairly soon into her friendship with her new "neighbour," Agnes made it very clear that she would be interested in far more. She would smile at Rio from under her lashes, she would blush whenever Rio entered the room, and she would trace Rio's body with hungry eyes, eyes that were disarmingly familiar and would often cause Rio to double-take, certain that at last her witch had returned to her. Although, it was comforting in a strange sense too, because even if her Agatha had been locked away within her own mind and had Rio wiped from her memory, it was clear that her body recognised Rio, or at least recognised it's longstanding attraction to her. It was a small comfort in the labyrinth they were currently lost within. Yet, on the whole it was a complication. One Rio did not need, because all she wanted to do, whenever Agnes would stare at her with those dark eyes, promising her all manner of dirty deeds, was lean into the sensation of being loved by this woman, this woman whose hands she would recognise against her skin in the dark, whose weight was as familiar as the earth's breeze upon her neck, whose lips she had memorised the pressure of. It was the direction Rio's internal compass was set to, to just go to her when Agatha beckoned, like a flower towards sunlight.

So it was a torture of it's own to deny them both the comfort of a warm embrace and the bliss of a familiar kiss. But she resisted, because Rio knew that it wasn't truly Agatha, it wasn't really the woman she loved. And she knew it wouldn't be right nor fair to either of them to give into the fallacy Agatha was currently being blinded by.

They existed within this agonising purgatory for an entire year. And Rio, in between collecting the mounting piles of dead souls from around the world, the one’s who were forced to wait for Death to drag herself away from a small town in New Jersey and finally grace them with her presence, Rio simmered, and she plotted, and she researched, and she kept watch. She would check on Agnes under the pretence of neighbourly concern, which quickly changed into neighbourly friendship, which Agnes was all too willing to indulge her in, whilst occasionally attempting to seduce Rio into neighbourly lust.

And then, like all monumental moments, which most often occur on the most mundane of days, a wave of scarlet power had exploded through the living room they had been sat in together, causing Agnes to slump forward, unconscious.

Rio jumped to her feet, eager to close the space between them and ensure Agnes was well. Yet, the moment she did so, Agnes awoke, sat up and stared at Rio with a hard, pointed stare, one world’s away from the beaming smile Rio now associated with Agnes. It was the one Agatha would have worn more often if she hadn’t been weighed down by a mountain of grief, the full one where her eyes scrunched and her entire face brightened.

Agnes scoffed, “Oh boy, here we go again. Who called the feds in?” Her voice was lower, almost a drawl.

Rio’s brows rose high on her forehead, unsure as to what was happening. She played along though, curious to see what had just changed, “I suppose the right answer would be the Chief of Police?”

Agnes scoffed and got to her feet, a lolloping stride instead of the dainty, hip-swaying walk Agnes usually used, “the body has been bagged and tagged by my team. It’s in my morgue. You have no right to come storming in here and demand access to a file I haven’t even had the chance to review properly”.

Then, just as Agnes was drawing a chair from beneath the kitchen table in a wide swing, as though pulling a car door open, she slumped forward as a second flood of scarlet magic burst around them both. Rio was quick and caught Agnes’s falling body in a soft cloud of emerald smoke, laying her gently on the couch with a pillow beneath her head.

A deep frown marred Rio's brow as she stood over Agnes, who was still out cold. Uncertainty reigned as she waited for her to wake, unsure what she could do to help her witch. She swiped a gentle hand over Agnes’s forehead, trying to see if she could gain any clarity with her magic as to what was occurring, when she suddenly discovered something that made her freeze, something that made hope start to bleed from her black heart.

Because, for the first time since Wanda had bewitched Agatha’s mind, Rio’s magic didn’t spark defensively at the blockade of scarlet power simmering just below the surface of her mind. No, for the first time, it felt as though the door to Agatha’s mind had been left unguarded, as though the usual chains of scarlet energy that fortified Agatha’s mind against any attempts to free her had been loosened and dropped to the floor with a metallic rumble.

For the first time since Wanda had pressed her finger to Agatha's temple, the door to Agatha's mind was unlocked.

Which meant, all Rio had to do was find a way to open the door .

Hope spread throughout Rio then like the first rays of dawn, slowly at first with only weak beams banishing the shadows before blossoming into a morning of blinding sunlight.

Something must have changed, something important and now the door was unlocked. It would be possible for Rio to explore, to search, and to find the real Agatha, who was still locked up in the depths of her own mind.

So when Agnes finally awoke, with a different version of herself settled onto her features, Rio was ready and willing to play along, determined now to get to the bottom of this cruel sorcery and end it once and for all.

AGNES

Episode 1: The Sopranos (The O'Connors)

The Red Witch was causing problems again, big problems. Herb’s report had told her as much. It had been written there, in black and white, that the Red Witch, or at least that’s what she was called within certain circles, had started asking questions about the parts of the city the feds knew belonged to Agnes, even if they couldn’t prove it. It was a stupid nickname in Agnes’s opinion, a little old fashioned and chauvinistic too, that a capable woman was demeaned by such an archaic term, only to then be further belittled by the colour of her hair. Even if Agnes hated the bitch, she didn't hate her because she was a woman, she hated her because she was a cop.

Agnes after all, although on the other side of the law to the Red Witch and her team of bumbling officers, could respect the mettle of a woman who had worked hard enough to make a formidable name for herself, especially in a field predominantly dominated by men.

She was rather sensitive to the topic, if truth be told, as it was a bone of contention in her mind and an exceptionally touchy subject. Primarily because, although Agnes had inherited her empire, one built on an array of crimes including, but not limited to, arms sales, money laundering, and hired hitmen, she refused to have the efforts she had put in to ensuring the family business thrived labelled as little more than the result of good luck or nepotism.

Agnes had bled for this fucking kingdom. And she wouldn’t allow a fed, even a pretty fed with green eyes and red hair, to rip it all apart.

So, she had ordered a hit. A neat, tidy one that could never be traced back to her or any of her people. It would require outside help though, someone new who had no ties to her organisation.

In the end it had been Phil who had stepped forward and whispered a name into Agnes’s ear when she had summoned her inner circle and demanded they find someone fresh, someone who would be entirely new to New York, let alone the O’Connor family.

The name was one she had never heard before, although it would be a lie to say it’s utterance didn’t make a puzzled frown blossom between her brows as a frisson of something ran up her spine. It was a name she didn’t know nor could she recall, yet it still felt… familiar. Like she had heard it in a dream and promptly forgotten it upon waking.

“Vidal?” she had questioned, voice sharp as she sat on the stiff backed arm chair in the basement of the nightclub her family owned, the basement where all of her most important meetings took place.

“That’s the one boss,” Phil repeated, awaiting further orders.

She hummed and ran a hand over the back of her dear companion, a white rabbit who she had christened Scratch, “have a meeting arranged. As soon as possible”.

“Right away Ms O’Connor”.

The appointment had been organised without complications and the following evening Agatha found herself in the same seat, with the same white bunny in her lap.

Her henchman were scattered around the room; an intimidating scene which had been their intention. A sharp rap of knuckles against wood soon broke the silence.

“Come in,” she ordered. Promptly, Phil opened the door and held it for a woman to enter before him.

Agnes allowed her gaze to drift in a lazy meander up the stranger’s body, as a single eyebrow rose with sincere appreciation. She was an attractive woman, very attractive in fact, with dark hair pulled back in a low bun, a pouty mouth, and eyes that held an intensity that might have been hard to look at if Agnes wasn't quite so formidable herself.

“Rio Vidal,” Agnes stated, not standing to greet her.

“Agnes O’Connor,” Rio replied, her voice a smoky low echo in the quiet room.

“I have heard you are the sharpest shooter on the eastern seaboard,” Agnes allowed a small smirk to grace her face, “so, you had better not miss”.

Much to Agnes’s delight, Rio smirked back. It was a bold, confident expression, the type that Agnes rarely had pointed in her direction by her employees.

“I didn’t realise I had even been hired yet,” Rio glanced around then, taking in the details of the basement office, which included a broad oak desk, several filing cabinets, a drinks trolley stacked with ample bottles of liquor, and a small hutch in the corner for Scratch.

Rio’s smirk brightened into an actual smile, “is it always like this up here for you? With extras and scenery too? No wonder you always liked to perform. I always said you were an actress born a witch”.

Agnes frowned, suddenly lost amongst the waves of confusion thrashing against the inside of her skull, “what are you talking about? Performing?”

Rio’s eyes snapped back to her own and her shoulders straightened, “oh, nothing. I was just thinking out loud. Whose the target?”

Agnes’s frown remained plastered on her features for a few moments longer, before the roaring noise in her mind finally settled to that normal familiar hum, “the Red Witch. I need her dead, and I need it done quietly”.

Rio’s face darkened gleefully at the thought, “I’d love nothing more”.

Agnes smirked, “that’s wonderful to hear. Now, as far as payment goes, I will pay you half now and the rest once it’s done, and done to a satisfactory manner. I cannot, under any circumstances, have either the feds or the press getting wind of our involvement in this. It needs to look like a rogue hit, or at least like an accident”.

Humming in consideration, Rio took several steps closer, until she was stood directly in front of Agnes's chair. It was a clever move, for it immediately put Agnes on a back foot as she was forced to remain seated whilst looking up into Rio’s face; a face that now looked particularly pleased to be standing over her in such a domineering way.

Surprise filled Agnes as Rio reached out a hand to run gentle fingers through the soft fur on Scratch's back, causing all of the henchman surrounding them to inhale sharply, for they all knew no one other than Agnes was allowed to pet her dear companion.

Agnes felt a jolt of shock zip up her spine, followed closely by a simmering heat. Her jaw dropped to scold Rio for her boldness, but Rio spoke first, halting Agnes's tongue before it got the chance to move.

“I don’t think this version is the right one for this, we need something else”.

That same flood of confusion roared back to life, causing Agnes to wince at its volume, “what?”

“We need to go again”.

Dizziness crept upon her now, making Agnes's vision darken and her ears ring, “again?” she managed to mumble.

“Again,” Rio ordered in a voice that echoed before everything went dark.

Episode 2: Glee (Sectionals)

It had been a long, hard journey but they were finally here and she could not be prouder. Her class of misfits had done it, they had pulled together and finally become the team Agnes always knew they could be.

She had designed, if she did so say herself, the ultimate mash-up of Lorna Wu and Stevie Nicks for the kids to perform. It was the perfect blend, and had taken her hours to craft, trying to draw on all of that magical 70s whimsy that both performers exuded so easily.

The kids had been thrilled when she had shown them and they had spent weeks practicing to prepare for this moment. Their last rehearsal had gone perfectly, all of them pitch perfect and dancing on beat. Or at least it would have gone perfectly if she hadn’t shown up right at the end.

It had all been going so well too. Agnes had just dismissed the kids after a gruelling two-hour rehearsal, flapping a hand at them to hurry home and get a good night’s rest, all whilst shouting after them to not be late for the bus in the morning, which she had arranged to ferry them all over to the venue on the other side of town.

Once alone, she leant against the piano and exhaled through a happy grin whilst bringing both hands up to cup her cheeks in an attempt to still her smile from widening even further. This felt right , it felt like this might just be the year that her team wins, the year they finally beat their rival team; the Scarlet Soprano’s.

And, it was at that exact moment Agnes's evening turned for the worse and her smile slipped from her face. Because as she had turned to collect her bag, she had found instead, her very own nemesis leaning against the doorframe with her arms crossed across her chest and her hip cocked at a frustratingly attractive angle, one that highlighted the deep curve of her hip.

Agnes felt her brow drop into a scowl as she watched the cheerleading coach swagger into her choir room, staring around as though she had never seen it before.

Rio whistled, sounding faux impressed, before giggling? Very unusual behaviour from the usually caustic cheerleading coach.

“Now you have to admit, this is a new low, even for you,” she glanced at Agnes then, her dark eyes skimming up and down her body, “a sweater vest ? Really?” Rio snorted derisively.

Agnes felt her jaw lift stubbornly and crossed both her arms tightly across her chest, “better than another red tracksuit. Seriously, do you own any other clothes?”

Rio swanned closer, running a single finger along the polished wood of the piano that was still set between them as she circled around it, “why? Do you want to see me in something else? Or just nothing at all?”

Agnes’s eyes widened in shock, surprised that the cheerleading coach would imply something so licentious. She felt a hot blush spreading up her cheekbones and down her neck as she scoffed uncertainly.

“What on earth are you talking about?” Was all she could think to say, bringing a hand up to clutch her own throat and hide the flush she could feel burning under her skin.

Rio smirked and drew closer still, until she was stood toe to toe with Agnes. She didn’t respond right away, taking her time to glance around and take in the staggered seating set to one side of the room to watch performances, the motivational posters stuck to the walls, and the array of instruments resting on stands around the room.

“When I have you back, I am never going to let you live this one down”.

Agnes frowned as a loud roaring started to sound in her mind, as though someone had turned on a blender right by her ear, “huh? When I’m back? Back from where?”

Rio’s smirk softened into a gentle smile. Her hand lifted and she brushed her fingertips against Agnes’s cheek, “we’re getting closer, I can feel it”.

The roaring got louder, making Agnes wince. With eyes and teeth clenched from the pain she managed to hiss out a final question, “feel what?”

Rio’s answer resounded through her mind, before it suddenly felt like she was falling and the world around her started to collapse.

“Feel you, sweetheart”.

Darkness swallowed her.

Episode 3: Game of Thrones (Westview Remembers)

The tales of old had not lied, when they warned the living that Winter was Coming. It was as brutal and as violent as their forebears had described, freezing entire families in a single night and causing every plant to shrivel and shrink beneath the soil, until all that remained was barren twigs and empty fields.

Her Kingdom had been prepared though and their stores were filled with enough wheat and barley to see them through the long months ahead. Her kingdom was well fortified too. It was a simple land filled with good, hearty folk who worked hard through the long days of summer and offered their fealty to the O’Connor name with brave loyalty.

She was grateful for it, for the Red Queen who reigned over the southern isles had declared war on Agnes’s kingdom and she had been forced to raise the banners and call the men to arms.

Agnes was watching from the ramparts of her castle with a thick, fur cloak wrapped around her shoulders to keep winter from gnawing on the exposed skin of her throat, as the men below practiced their drills and sparring form. A line of archers were also practicing firing their bows at a line of targets off in the distance, and she felt a thrill of pride run through her at how capable they all were, how willing they were to fight for her and their homeland.

A bugle sounded from the gates and Agnes peered over to see who was arriving with enough prestige to warrant an announcement. With such an entrance, she had been anticipating an entire troupe, yet only one person entered, dressed in a thick, emerald travelling cloak with the hood pulled up, hiding their face from view. Driven by her own curiosity, she swept from the ramparts and down the steep, stone staircase to greet the stranger who had just entered her courtyard.

“You there,” she ordered, once close enough to be heard, “remove your hood”.

The stranger did as they were bid and drew it down, exposing the face of a traitor.

Agnes hissed as her eyes widened with fury at seeing the woman who had betrayed her kingdom’s trust, who had sold her secrets to enemy rulers whilst stealing her most valuable treasures from the vaults below. “You dare show your face here?” she brandished a regal hand towards the robed woman, “guards! Seize her !”

They can't have been within hearing range though, for none of the guards moved from their posts to do as she had ordered them to, leaving Agnes pointing a determined finger at Vidal, who tried to cover a snort of laughter with the back of her hand.

Agnes felt a scowl tightening her features as she allowed her eyes to drop in judgement over Vidal’s outfit, which was most frustratingly of all, dashingly handsome. She was wearing clothes appropriate for travelling across miles of rough terrain including a pair of thick leather breeches cinched at the waist by a broad leather belt, which had a curved dagger hanging off of it. A white shirt was visible beneath a thick emerald green tunic. She also had dirt smudged across her face and leaves in her hair from where she had slept amongst the undergrowth.

“I’m impressed,” Vidal grinned, “this is your most cinematic attempt yet. The ramparts are my favourite,” she pointed then, over Agatha’s shoulder towards the top of her castle.

“My ancestors built this fortress with stone gifted to them by the old Gods,” Agnes replied, voice haughty with disdain for the woman in front of her.

Although it was clear her words were not having the impact she hoped they would, for Vidal smothered another guffaw of laughter behind the back of her wrist, “it’s a creative use of the couch, I’ll give you that”.

Agnes scowled, “you besmirch my family home after all you have done?”

Vidal’s smile slipped, although it didn’t disappear, instead it became almost thoughtful, “all I have done, I have done out of duty or out of love”.

The moment Vidal mentioned the word love, Agnes felt her heart clench painfully beneath her ribs, as though it was reaching out, trying to grasp something that felt close, closer than it had in a long while.

“Love?”

Vidal stepped closer and swept a single hand down Agatha’s arm so she could grasp her hand gently and bring it to her lips, “yes my lady,” she answered, her voice equal measures of solemn and sincere, “love”.

A pain erupted then within the heart pounding violently in her chest, suddenly it felt like something was desperate to escape.

Agnes shook her head, trying to shake some sense into it, “I don’t understand, I can’t…”

“It’s alright. This was always going to hurt, just keep pushing sweetheart, you’re almost there. We’re so close”.

Agnes shuddered as flashes of purple sparked in her peripheral before everything went dark and her castle started to crumble around her.

Episode 4: Bridgerton (The Diamond of Westview)

Her mother’s predictions had turned true the moment the clock struck midnight on her twenty third birthday. For Lady Agnes O’Connor was now officially a spinster, a spinster who was firmly on the shelf and no longer expected to parade around the parlours of London in an attempt to snare a wealthy a husband.

It wasn’t as though she hadn’t received offers. Countless gentleman had asked for her hand; Count Ralph of High Attic, Lord Herb of Walgreens, and Count Dennis of Postalshire had all practically begged for her to be their wife. But she had a secret, one that Agnes shared with only her own beating heart.

For Lady Agnes O’Conner didn’t hold a single ounce of desire for a man, no, Lady Agnes O’Connor wanted a woman. And not just any woman, she wanted one woman in particular.

The woman in question though, was not a possible suitor. The most glaring reason being her gender, which the entire ton would be scandalised to even hear whisper of. The second most obvious reason however, was the fact the woman who Agatha’s heart pined for so ardently, was a servant. A stable hand specifically, one her family had rescued from the orphanage when she was just a girl. A girl who had grown into a beautiful young woman, one who had the power to make Agnes’s heart beat furiously from just a single glance of those dark eyes.

These issues, large as they were, hadn’t been enough to prevent Agnes from admiring her love though, whom she had run down to visit the moment her awful mama had released her from their breakfast table.

“Good morning! What a beautiful day it is today!” She greeted loudly the moment she spotted Rio in the stables, sweeping rogue pieces of dry hay and straw into a neat pile in the corner.

Rio turned to face her, her lips twitching up into an amused grin as she did so. Her eyes though, for some reason, widened in what appeared to be surprise? “Oh, wow,” she mumbled, chuckling lowly beneath her breath.

Agnes frowned, uncertain as to why Rio would be laughing at such a simple polite greeting, “what is so amusing?”

Rio’s eyebrows rose to new heights as that same smirk remained plastered on her lovely face, “I just wasn’t expecting a British accent this time round, if truth be told. It’s not bad though, bit pitchy in places”.

Agnes’s frown deepened, “what on earth are you talking about?”

Rio chuckled again before waving a dismissive hand at her, “nothing, nothing. What were you going to say when you came in here?”

Immediately, as though someone had shouted action and slapped a clapperboard in front of a camera, Agnes’s face shifted back into a flirtatious smile, “don’t you remember what day it is? It’s my birthday!”

Rio hummed and leant the broom up against the wall, “of course, of course it is. And did you get all the gifts you asked for?”

Agnes drifted closer, taking a step forward for every one Rio took back, “well, my hideous mother got me a few boring books, but there was one thing I wanted desperately but have yet to receive”.

“Oh?”

Rio’s back hit the wooden wall of the stables as Agnes drew closer still, “I think you know what that might be”.

Rio’s face flushed heavily and Agnes watched with delight as her pupils dilated, swallowing her irises in their entirety until Rio's eyes were as dark as her hair. Agnes leaned in whilst grinning, intending on finally capturing Rio’s mouth with her own.

Only her mouth didn’t meet Rio’s, for Rio, in a moment of panic had sidestepped her kiss and drawn backwards, “We can’t,” she stuttered, stumbling away even further.

Agnes felt a ball of pain well in her throat and struggled not to cry at Rio's rejection, “you don’t want me?”

Suddenly, Rio closed her eyes as her fists clenched tightly. She inhaled deeply for a long minute, as though attempting to restrain herself, before finally opening her eyes. Agnes felt her own widen then, for the depths of pain staring back at her was startling, “I want you, desperately. Never, ever doubt that. But I want the real you, the you that is locked away deep inside. Let her out and then I will kiss you, free her Agnes, please and I will give you everything I am and everything I have”.

A cracking sound started to sound inside her mind at Rio's words, like someone had thrown a rock at a frozen lake, shattering it’s iced surface and causing large cracks to splinter across it’s entire surface.

She brought both her hands up and held her head tightly, trying to keep her skull together for it felt like it was splitting apart.

“Come on baby,” Rio begged, sounding desperate, “come back to me, please”.

“I don’t know what… I can’t… what is this… who are y…” was all Agnes managed to grind out between clenched teeth before she was falling and the ground met her with a resounding thump.

Episode 5: The Last of Us (Scavenging for Gold)

It had been months since she had last seen another person. Or, at least since she had seen another living, breathing human being. One whose face hadn’t been swallowed entirely by fungus or tried to inject their filthy, ravenous spores into her skin with their cracked, bloody teeth.

Rations had been easy to find when this had first started; every house, apartment, and store had contained at least one thing hidden away that was worthy of searching for. Yet, as the months had passed, food had rotted, survivors had hunted, and soon enough, everything was dwindling.

It was food Agnes was searching for now, in this abandoned suburban house in the remains of middle America.

It was pitch black, as it was safer to scavenge at night, and silent, as she was trying to remain as quiet as possible whilst pulling out the contents of several kitchen cupboards, hunting for the apocalyptic version of gold: tinned food.

A bang suddenly sounded from the floor above. Agnes froze and held her breath, waiting to see if an infected was about to come stumbling down the stairs to try and gnaw on her flesh.
