Much to her surprise though, it wasn’t a clicker, it was a woman. An angry woman who was holding a torch aloft, shining the yellow beam right at Agnes, forcing her to squint and raise a hand to protect sensitive eyes.

“What the hell are you doing?”

“Who the hell are you?”

They both spoke at the same time, the woman demanding to know why Agnes was in her kitchen, whilst Agnes demanded this strangers name.

The woman’s face dropped, looking morose for some peculiar reason as Agnes’s question settled in the silence between them.

“I’m Rio. Rio Vidal,” she answered quietly, shouldering through the veil of sadness that had dropped over her all of a sudden, before tilting her chin towards the cupboards. “Why are you emptying the cupboards at…” she checked the clock set on the wall, which for some obscure reason, was still ticking? Even after all this time? “…at 3am”.

“I didn’t realise this place was taken for the night. Had to get off the streets though, you know what it’s like out there. Nearly had a nasty run in with a few runners, so thought it best to lay low until dawn”.

Rio nodded, absorbing this information slowly before quite suddenly her shoulders slumped and she sighed heavily, looked exhausted.

“I don’t know how many more times we are going to have to do this”.

Agnes chuckled in commiseration, “tell me about it. World’s gone to shit and here we are hunting for canned peaches like they’re a stash of diamonds”.

Rio frowned, “what else can I do? What else can I do to free you?”

“ Free me ?” Agnes laughed, an uncertain sound. The world ending hadn’t exactly been a balm for those with strained mental health and there were many people she had run into who had unfortunately succumbed to the madness of losing everything. It would appear Rio too had surrendered to insanity; she must have lost someone very important to her.

Taking a few steps closer, Rio flicked the light switch which actually turned on the mains, much to her surprise.

“You got a generator rigged up here? I haven’t seen a spark of electricity since the grid went down,” she whistled appreciatively, “that’s damn impressive”.

Then, all of a sudden Rio started to speak in a voice that was double toned, one that reverberated throughout both the room and Agnes's suddenly aching skull, “ enough . Enough fallacy. Tell me your name”.

Frowning, Agnes answered, “...Agnes O’Connor”.

“ No . The witch who placed you under this spell is gone. Something has happened to her and the magic binding you has fractured. You are stronger than this, you can break through it. Now tell me, what is your name!”

A roaring, cracking sound started to pound through her head as her jaw clenched tightly together, “I told you already! Agnes O’Connor!”

“Tell me the name of the witch who caused this! Tell me the name of the Scarlet Witch: wielder of chaos! Tell me the name of the witch who has you trapped in this lie , in this hallucination!”

All she could hear was noise, like the violence emitted from the eye of a storm, when suddenly like a whisper amongst screams, two words emerged.

“ Wanda Maximoff ”.

“Yes. Good,” Rio encouraged, “yes, Wanda Maximoff did this to you. So tell me, who are you, who did she wrong?”

The gale screeching through her mind got louder still, it’s noise encroaching on violent before all fell suddenly silent. Agnes sighed in relief, only to hiss in pain a moment later when a burning started to spread across her skin, as though someone had held a thousand matches against her bare flesh, hoping to scar her.

“Is it hot?” Agnes panted, pulling at the collar of her sweater.

Rio looked pleased, “that’s it, claw your way out”.

Agnes pulled her sweater off, then her shirt searching for a relief that never came. Only beneath was a… dress? An old-fashioned dress?

She groaned in pain as the heat across her skin continued to bubble.

She pulled the dress off, then a fur cloak? A sweater vest? Another dress – more modern this time, like the sort of thing she might have worn in a nightclub.

She had hoped that would be the end of it, but clothing continued to appear, only to be pulled from her scorched skin and dropped in a messy pile on the floor. Purple jumper and slacks; velvet tracksuit; aerobic clothing; on and on it went until at last she stood staring at her own hands, hands now entirely bleached of any colour, standing in stark contrast to the bright colours of the surrounding kitchen and the rainbow of clothing spread across the floor.

“ Say it ,” Rio commanded, “tell me Who. You. Are ”.

And like a thin sheet of glass creaking under the weight of a rusty anchor, the bindings holding her mind captive snapped suddenly, almost violently as the answer to Rio’s question became clear.

Flashes of purple, of Salem, of Nicky, of the woods, of the road, of countless covens, of a blurred face with dark hair but unrecognisable features, of a cloaked figure; too far away to see who they might be, span through her mind. Certainty settled and with confident hands she gripped the final lapel of the last dress and tugged, freeing herself from the burning confines she had been trapped in for so long.

For she knew who she was, she knew exactly who she was.

AGATHA

Agatha Harkness opened her eyes slowly. She took her time, relishing the sensation of being in control of her own body once more as a deep sigh left her lungs. When finally, at long last she peered around, taking in her surroundings with narrowed eyes.

The first thing she noticed was her location; still in Ralph’s house, then.

She glanced around even further, taking in the open cupboards with their contents spilled out onto the counters below, and her own nudity.

“Huh,” she said peering down, her voice lightly curious before turning slightly to find a woman with dark hair stood by the kitchen door. She was wearing pyjamas and had her arms crossed tightly across her chest. It was a defensive position, one that contrasted heavily against the desperate mix of emotions swirling in her dark eyes.

A flicker of a memory flashed in Agatha's mind as her eyes narrowed to study the woman, who was now quite openly admiring her body, which was still very naked.

Without feeling an ounce of shame, Agatha crossed one arm over her breasts and leant her elbow on it, then with a lazy wrist she pointed at the dark haired woman, “I know you don’t I?”

The woman’s eyes snapped to hers with a desperate hunger, “you do,” she confirmed, voice solemn.

Agatha pouted and with narrowed eyes studied the woman stood in her house, when suddenly she remembered. She clicked her fingers and pointed at her, “I’ve got it! You’re the neighbour. Rita? Was it? Is that right?”

She snorted in amusement, flapping a hand at Rio as though the answer didn’t actually matter as she swept away to collect a silk robe from the hook by the door. She paid little attention to the way the other woman’s posture sunk, as though a burden recently lifted had been dropped straight back down from a great height, causing her to stumble in place.

“It’s Rio,” she eventually murmured, voice husky and verging on broken. Although Agatha, who wasn’t paying any attention whatsoever to the stranger in her house, was already moving on from their conversation, sweeping off to check on Señor Scratchy.

It was important after all, following this sort of ordeal, to be met with a familiar face, one who she knew she loved beyond all others. Not a random stranger.

Certainly not.

Until the Horizon Collapses

A Second First Meeting

Chapter Notes

Here is the next chunk - were getting into the start of AAA now :)

RIO

It came as no surprise that Agatha was harder to corral than Agnes had been. She was naturally more suspicious, more demanding, and her words were a lot meaner too.

She had returned from her search for Señor Scratchy in a blur of colourful silk, with the white rabbit safely cradled in her arms.

She had stopped in place, her flurry of motion halted suddenly on finding Rio just where she had left her, almost as though she had forgotten about her presence entirely and was surprised to see her still stood in that same position by the kitchen door.

“Er,” she said pointing at Rio with a lazy finger and narrowed eyes, “the front door’s through there...” she then gestured at her like she was shooing a dog away, “you know, ándale”.

Rio inhaled deeply, shoving every fractured shard of her broken heart down into the depths of herself, into that blank, empty place she had once existed. It was necessary, for if she focussed on the loss of Agatha’s love, of the loss of their history, she wasn’t entirely sure she would remain sane.

Agatha frowned at Rio's lack of motion and threw her hand up towards her, as though trying to forcefully expel Rio from the house. Only no magic responded, not a single purple spark. Evidently, Wanda’s magical chains fracturing and finally breaking hadn’t actually given Agatha her magic back. Nor, much to Rio’s despair, her memories.

Agatha stared at her hand in horror. Ignoring Rio, she placed Señor Scratchy gently on the floor and rushed to the living room mirror, where she immediately started to drag a finger against her palm and swirl her wrists, amongst all sorts of other magical contortions that, before at least, would have caused purple light to crackle between her hands.

“ No, no, no, no ,” she mumbled verging on desperate as she closed her eyes, centred herself and journeyed inside to where her magic had always resided.

Rio knew the moment Agatha felt it’s absence, for she roared furiously through clenched teeth and began to punch the sofa cushions with both fists, as though they had personally wronged her.

Rio sighed and took a step forward towards her frantic wife, “don't worry, we’ll get it back”.

Agatha’s rabid movements jerked to an instant stop as she stared up at Rio with wild eyes through her hair, which was a crazed mess around her face. Her eyes were blazing with unrestrained frustration as a vicious sneer twisted her mouth upwards, evidently on the verge of spewing something ruthless. Quite suddenly though, her eyes widened with intrigue and she snapped her jaw shut before any insults could escape from between her lips.

Rio sighed then as her shoulders sagged with fatigue. It was reassuring in some ways, for it was clear Agatha was exactly the same power-driven, advantage-taking woman she had always been, only with a single green thread plucked from her mind like an errant mistake removed from a broad tapestry. For, Rio knew where this was going, oh yes. Of course, it wouldn't be Agatha if it didn't. She should have predicted it.

“Get what back exactly?” Agatha asked, voice low with devious hope.

Rio, unphased by Agatha’s tone, for she knew all of her tricks, and her treats for that matter, was honest in her reply for there was little point in lying.

“Your magic. We’ll get it back”.

Agatha’s intrigue was almost palpable. Her eyebrow arched sharply and her eyes flickered down towards Rio’s fists, trying to sense a spark, “you know about magic?”

“Sure do,” Rio replied, keeping her answers short and succinct. She was curious to see how Agatha would react to this new development.

“Oh well… that’s certainly good news,” Agatha smirked as her gaze sharpened on Rio. It was a potent thing, to suddenly have the full expanse of Agatha's attention on her again as she drifted closer to ask, “what did you say your name was again? Rita?”

Rio felt the weight of their lost history drop on her shoulders as she breathed out the answer, hoping desperately it might trigger something, anything in Agatha’s mind, some sense of recognition, “it’s Rio. Rio Vidal”.

Agatha paused thoughtfully, as though digesting the words slowly. “ Rio Vidal ,” she murmured, almost to herself as her eyes glazed slightly, lost in thought. “ Rio Vidal ,” she repeated under her breath, as though plagued suddenly by a question that didn't have an answer.

“Yes?” Rio prompted, as hope started to grow like a winter blossom between her ribs whilst Agatha pondered the four syllables that her name was built from.

Then, as quickly as hope bloomed it shrivelled and died, for in the next moment Agatha shook her head as though ridding herself of something nonsensical and smiled at Rio in that particularly spiteful way she had perfected over the years, as though trying to incite another to violence.

Which is exactly what she was trying to do.

“Why is an upstart witch in my house hmm? Are you one of Wanda’s little lackeys, come to spy on me and make sure I’m still trapped in that humiliating spell of hers?”

Rio frowned, swallowing the painful remains of her own jagged hope. She didn’t deign to reply, just crossed her arms and arched an impatient eyebrow, waiting for Agatha to get this attempt at inciting her to violence over with and out of her system. It wasn’t a surprise really; she was, at least from Agatha's current perspective, simply the first unlucky witch to cross her path since waking from the curse. And Agatha was powerless too, making her even more of a ruthless hunter than she normally was, which was saying something. It made perfect sense that she would try and steal the first spark of magic she sensed.

Agatha’s eyes narrowed when her words didn’t gain a reaction, so she reassessed her prey, glancing down at Rio’s bare legs in her sleep shorts, taking in her rumpled hair. Instantly, Agatha’s eyebrows rose as a lecherous smirk spread across her face.

“Oh, I see ,” she floated closer, “you and me huh? Keeping Agnes company , were you?” she studied Rio’s face closely, “well, I hate to break it to you sweet cheeks, but Agnes is gone. She’s D-E-A-D and won’t be coming back”.

Her eyes then immediately dropped to Rio’s hands, hoping that a harsh reminder of her lost love might startle a spark from her that Agatha could steal.

A pained bark of laughter escaped Rio’s throat at the irony of her assumption, “you’re this… ," she held up her hand, showing a small slither of space between her thumb and index finger, "…close to being right, but just not quite on the money I’m afraid”.

Agatha sneered before her lips once again lifted into a sly smirk, having undoubtedly thought of some other devious thread to pull on that might upset Rio enough for her to blast a beam of magic at her chest. But Rio, having had quite enough of this fruitless game cut to the chase.

“Look, let me set you straight on a few things Agatha”.

Her stern tone caught Agatha by surprise, who splayed a hand out in a dramatic gesture, implying she should continue.

“I know what you are trying to do, and I know how you work. So, let me say this once and for good; I will never , under any circumstances, strike you with magic. It’s a closed avenue to you, so you may as well give it up now”.

Agatha gasped and held a hand to her chest, “moi?”

Rio felt her lip twitch in amusement at her wife’s antics. She had always been the same, so damn dramatic, “yes, you . Nothing you say will anger me enough to ever strike you, so you may as well accept my help and stop trying to piss me off”.

Agatha’s eyes narrowed again, this time in determined curiosity. Rio could tell she had caught her attention now, properly and for good. After all, Agatha could never stand a mystery she didn’t understand and Rio felt a sudden sharp thrill run up her spine at the knowledge her wife's sights were now firmly set on her as a target to chase, as a secret to discover. It felt disarmingly nostalgic, much like it had when they had first met and Agatha had pursued Rio fiercely, killing coven after coven to simply get her attention.

“And how is it you know so much about me huh?” she ran a hand through her long, dark hair, stretching her jaw up in a way she knew was devilishly attractive, “a fan of my work are you? Wanted to learn from the best?”

Rio couldn’t stop an endeared smile from stretching across her face, finding simply being with Agatha, of being surrounded by everything that made her wife herself; her intonations , her humour , her rudeness , her shamelessness especially after a year of Agnes’s sweetness, so damn comforting. Even if Rio was a mere stranger who had simply caught her attention.

She shrugged, “you could say that”.

Agatha’s gaze dropped again, once again skimming over bare legs and skimpy pyjamas, although this time Rio could feel the appreciative heat in her gaze, a warm familiar rush, “you want to help me?”

“I do”.

A leering edge lifted Agatha’s smile into something dangerous as she swept even closer and placed a warm palm against Rio’s sternum. Leaning closer, she whispered, “and how exactly do you want to help me, Rio Vidal? ”

Rio felt it then, as Agatha began to try and gain a sense of her power, detecting her magical core through the skin and muscle of her chest to see just how much magic was burning within Rio’s body.

Immediately, Rio’s magic responded enthusiastically to her touch, as it always had done, causing Agatha to shudder at the intense power Rio possessed. Agatha exhaled heavily and clenched her eyes tightly at the sensation and when her eyes finally flickered open again, her pupils had grown large and dark, eclipsing the moody blue of her iris almost entirely.

Agatha’s lips drew closer to Rio’s, “will you help me Rio? Will you help me find a spark?”

Their lips brushed softly and Rio felt Agatha’s hands drifting to her waist, her long fingers curling around the gentle curve. Rio felt an agonising shudder ripple through her then, for her desire for this woman was paramount, yet she couldn’t trust Agatha not to try and draw Rio’s magic out from between her lips.

It was, way back when, one of Agatha’s favourite ways to drain a witch’s magic from her body. To her, it was a seductive game, one she took great pleasure in winning. Rio knew Agatha after all, better than anyone, so she knew the moment Agatha felt Rio's magic, it's potency would have caught her attention like a predator scenting blood, and that she was now utilising another weapon in her arsenal.

One Rio had always been weakest against.

Yet, she also knew if Rio did allow Agatha to kiss her and Agatha, unknowing she was Death, drew her power into her body, it would kill her.

Which was incomprehensible.

So, with that warning blaring in her mind, Rio took a stumbling step backwards and held both her hands out in front of herself, “I will help you,” she said, voice insistent, “I will help you find a coven to draw from, but it cannot be me. I can’t let you, not from me”.

“Something special, are you?” Agatha’s voice, surprisingly, didn’t sound sarcastic. Instead it sounded sincere, deep with a curiosity Rio knew to be dangerous. Because when Agatha was like this, when she wanted something from someone, even if that something was simply the truth, she became a relentless creature, willing to do anything and everything to draw what she coveted from whoever was withholding it from her.

Rio didn’t need to confirm Agatha’s statement either. She knew Agatha could feel it in the magic pulsing beneath her skin. After all, Rio wasn’t human and she wasn’t just a witch, she was something else, something more. And Agatha could sense it.

Humming quietly, Agatha’s eyes remained narrowed before she span away to fetch Señor Scratchy from the floor. She then turned back to Rio with a broad, devilish grin, “well then, in that case Rio Vidal , we had better get ourselves ready. A coven is what I desire, and a coven is what I shall get”.

And Rio, weak as she always had been and always would be to the whims of her wife, simply nodded.

XXXXXX

They had both prepared for the day, Agatha in a swirling bustle of motion as she threw every article from Agnes’s closet over her shoulder with disgusted mutterings, one after the other, horrified that she had been wearing them for the past year.

Rio’s process was slower, more rooted in practicality, which had always been their dynamic.

Its continuity was as comforting as it was painful.

Throughout their morning together Rio caught Agatha staring at her on several occasions. Each time with narrowed predatory eyes. It was a familiar look, as it was the one she always possessed when intrigued by something or someone. Although Rio wasn’t entirely sure precisely what it was Agatha was hunting for from her; the truth about how Rio knows so much about her? Rio’s power itself? Or something else, something more... physically satisfying.

It would be a lie, after all, to deny a heady attraction didn’t still simmer between them. It was as potent as it always had been, if not slightly hotter, which was certainly an achievement, because now, Rio was something new for Agatha to pursue; a new conquest to capture, and her attention was as sharp and as debilitating as it always had been.

However, just as they were debating the best way to actually leave the house, because Agatha’s car consisted of a dining room chair taped to a broom and Rio didn’t know how to drive a car, let alone owned one, a loud boom echoed from upstairs.

They glanced at one another, unsure as to who or what had made the noise when another bang resounded down the stairs again.

“Someone’s here,” Agatha hissed and within moments Rio shrouded them both in a cloud of green light and transported them from the kitchen to the bedroom.

Their sudden appearance made the intruder jump; a skinny figure with their hood pulled up and a beanie pulled low who had climbed through the bedroom window to rifle through the drawers of the dresser, obviously hunting for something in particular.

“Hey!” Agatha roared, immediately darting forward to try and grab the stranger who was surprisingly nimble. Quickly, they dodged right to avoid her swiping hand before shooting forward to try and clamber back through the open window.

He would have escaped too, if Rio, who was quite literally Death incarnate, wasn’t present and with a snap of her fingers drew vines from the air to wrap around his ankles, wrists, and throat.

The invader started to gag as the vines tightened, limiting the amount of air he could draw in. Rio smiled in satisfaction at the opportunity to stretch her magical muscles, for they sometimes grew stagnant, causing the pressure in her sternum to build from disuse until she finally had a reason to use it.

It felt good, too good and she was certain her eyes would be glowing with the raw, unrestrained power she possessed as she flicked her wrist out to throw the stranger into the chair in the corner, drawing even more vines to hold him in place, preventing his escape.

Rio swept closer, passing Agatha who was watching her work with dark, hungry eyes. She knew why; the use of her raw power, the violence, and the ruthlessness of her actions will have hooked even more threads of Agatha’s curiosity. The truth of that thought made her black heart glow golden, for it brought her great comfort to know that even without their history tying them together, Rio was a person Agatha would always be drawn to, that their magnetism and connection was as undeniable as the tides, or the moon, or gravity, and that it always would be.

She couldn’t afford the distraction though, even if Agatha’s hot gaze on her back made her want to spin round and push her up against the nearest flat surface, because she had an intruder to interrogate.

So, with that she took one final stride closer and ripped the hood and hat from the strangers head, exposing the face of a terrified teenager.

“Who the hell are you?” Rio hissed, drawing her dagger to hold under his trembling chin, “and why the hell did you break into our house?”

“ Our house?” Agatha asked loudly from behind her, before chuckling and muttering, “even as a loser like Agnes I had game”.

Rolling her eyes at Agatha’s unhelpful commentary and entirely false assumptions, she raised the tip of the blade even closer to the teen’s trembling jaw, “answer me, right now. Or I swear to all of the gods above, I will gut you like a fish”.

“I’m sorry!” The boy shouted, face ashen with fear, “I’m sorry, okay, I swear. I was just trying to help!”

Rio’s eyes narrowed dangerously, “help who?”

“Help her,” he gestured with a tilt of his head towards Agatha, who dramatically looked behind her as though a third party had been summoned before pointing at her own chest in outrageous shock.

“Why do you think she needed help?” Rio asked suspiciously, refusing to lower her dagger until some of this started to make more sense.

The teen inhaled deeply as though attempting to ground himself before exhaling slowly, “let me start at the beginning okay, I swear I don’t mean you guys any harm. My name is ------- ------ and I-”

Agatha swept closer, eyes squinting at him curiously, “try that again”.

The teen's jaw wagged uncertainly for a moment before he said with a trembling stutter, “I- I- don’t mean you any harm, I –“

“No,” she waved an impatient hand at him, “the other thing. What’s your name?”

“------- ------”

Rio and Agatha looked at one another, eyebrows raised in a mixture of surprise and curiosity at the sigil that had appeared over his mouth, hiding his name from them.

Agatha hummed once before gesturing with the roll of her hand, “continue”.

The teenager glanced between them unsure, before carrying on with his explanation.

“I have read about you Ms Harkness, and when I tried to visit before… well you didn’t seem well... yourself. So, I did a load of research to free you from the curse you were under”.

“That doesn’t explain why you broke in here?” Rio snapped, eyes still sparking dangerously.

He flinched and avoided looking her in the eye, sensing the danger she exuded, “I needed something personal to do the incantation, something that mattered so I thought jewellery was a safe bet”.

He uncurled his fist, which had been clenched tightly in his lap and still restricted by Rio’s vines, revealing Agatha’s Maiden, Mother, Crone locket.

“You dirty little thief,” Agatha hissed, suddenly spitting with anger. Her reaction was understandable, for that locket was her most sacred possession. It represented her painful, twisted roots, her escape from her mother’s coven, and most importantly of all; their son. She snatched it quickly from his palm and held it with both fists to her heart.

Teen tried to reassure her again, having noticed how upset she was, “I wasn’t going to keep it! I promise! I just needed something to use for the spell. I’m sorry!”

His eyes flickered between the two women stood in front of him and after a short pause, tried for an endearing youthful grin, “I guess I didn’t need to break you free though did I? So, I suppose the right thing to say is... welcome back?”

Agatha bowed closer to him, eyes narrowed to study his face, “nobody does anything for free though do they? So what is it you wanted from me hmm? What was locked away behind the curse that you wanted to get your grubby little paws on?”

His answer was swift, like he had choked it up, for it fell from between his lips with an abrupt eagerness, “I want to walk the witches road!”

Agatha’s eyes widened and Rio watched as her gaze flickered between the teenager in front of her and Rio, who had taken a step back to observe the proceedings.

“The witches road doesn’t exist," Agatha said factually, although her voice was still threaded with intrigue.

He rolled his eyes, a motion only a teenager could do quite so effectively, “you’re lying”.

Agatha’s eyebrows rose at his audacity, “am I?”

“That’s just what real witches say to keep the amateurs out”.

“Oh, is it now?” Agatha asked, eyebrows still raised high on her forehead.

“Alright, confession time,” he grimaced slightly, before chuckling as though embarrassed, “I know an egregious amount about you. I’ve been obsessed since I first read up on your Salem days,” he grinned, “one of my favourite you eras, by the way”.

Agatha smirked, preening under his adoration, “it’s a good one,” she turned to Rio then with a lascivious smirk, “a really good one. You would have liked it, I’m sure”.

Rio’s heart thudded painfully beneath her ribs as she responded with a weak smile and a weaker nod, attempting to cover the pain currently pulsing throughout her body. As it suddenly felt like she had been stabbed right through the heart, causing the muscle to convulse beneath her ribs as though rebelling against this level of agony.

For Rio did like the Salem days, she liked them a lot. After all, she had been there; it was where their story had begun.

Agatha’s smirk dropped the moment she noticed Rio’s pained response, not out of concern but out of that same burning curiosity she had been staring at Rio with all day.

With narrowed eyes, Agatha turned back to Teen, “the adults are going to talk now, we're going to decide what to do with you". She then grabbed Rio’s elbow to drag her from the room and down the stairs to the living room, where their conversation wouldn’t be overheard.

“So, what do you reckon?” Rio asked, pointing up towards their stowaway, who was still trapped by Rio's vines.

Agatha grinned and fluttered her eyelashes, “kid has great taste in idols, that’s for sure”.

Rio rolled her eyes, “he should go home to his parents. You’re free from the spell, so the point of him being here is now null and void”.

Agatha smirked, “not entirely. He wants to walk the road…”

Rio’s eyes narrowed then, for she could see yet another scheme had been hatched in her wife’s conniving, brilliant mind over the last ten minutes or so. After all, Agatha didn’t know that Rio knew the road was merely a hoax to trick witches into supplying her with power.

And as powerless as she was, it made sense that Agatha would turn back to her most fruitful scheme.

So Rio, of course, decided to play along.

“But the witches road isn’t real, it’s a myth, a folktale that covens tell to their young before bed”.

Agatha’s eyes sparkled with devious hunger; it was clear she thought Rio close to being hooked on her scheme. Little did she know.

“It isn’t a myth gorgeous,” she murmured, voice suddenly low and appealing. Rio felt her cheeks flush at the term of endearment, much to her dismay, “it’s real. I have walked it before. And it’s true what they say, because if you do make it to the end you get whatever your heart desires”.

Agatha drew closer to Rio and raised a hand to run her fingers through the ends of Rio’s hair. Her eyes flickered across Rio’s face intently.

“I wonder what your heart desires hmm? Riches?”

She pondered that for a moment, “no, no that isn't right. You don’t seem the type to value wealth. How about power?”

She raised her other hand and laid it on Rio’s chest, enticing her magic to bubble and simmer beneath her skin at Agatha’s touch, “nope," she hissed in pleasure at it's potent reaction to her caress before continuing, "you have plenty of that. Heaps of the stuff. So, it must be that third option your pounding heart covets,” she drew closer, so close she could breath her next words right into Rio’s ear, causing a shiver to run down her spine and across her shoulder blades, “you want love . You want to be adored, worshipped completely by another”.

She drew back to take in Rio’s expression, smirking in delight on noticing her rapid breathing and fluttering pulse, knowing that she had hit the nail on the head. She had always been exceptionally good at reading people, at finding out what made them tick.

Her eyebrow twitched with intrigue as she stared at Rio's mouth, "and I think too, that you wish to adore in return. To worship another completely as well; an equal exchange of devotion and desire between you and someone else, someone special," her eyes darkened, as she leaned in slightly, "perhaps by one witch in particular?”

Rio jolted the moment Agatha’s lips drew closer and brushed her own. She couldn’t let her, not when Agatha was still clawing desperately for whatever spark of power she could find. Agatha was a loose cannon right now and dangerous in her greed for magic.

“You’re right,” Rio agreed, taking a step backwards, away from Agatha’s body for her own sanity’s sake, “I do want someone, a specific someone,” then in an attempt to lead the conversation back towards the witches road, she prompted, “and you think the witches road will help me find her?”

Agatha's brow dropped heavily, evidently frustrated that Rio wasn’t falling for her attempts at seduction, so with a huff she crossed her arms and pouted petulantly, “yeah,” she flung a hand out, “yeah, the witches road would help you find her . Whoever her is”.

Taming a smirk at her wife’s sudden peevishness she thought it through. The road was fake, Rio knew that much, but what they were after was a coven. After all, there was very little chance of Agatha being able to break through yet another curse to reclaim her memories, especially without her own magic to fight against whatever remaining enchantment was holding her memories of Rio hostage.

It made sense. It was the same trick that had served them time and time again. They could use the boy’s innocent charm to lure a few local witches into their scheme, use Agatha’s prestige as the only witch to survive the road as an attractive bonus, gather them all together, sing the ballad, and steal every ounce of magic they possessed.

Agatha would get her spark back and from there they could find a way to restore Agatha’s memories.

Concluding to herself that it was the right decision and a solid plan going forward, Rio looked up from staring in thought with her mouth primed to confirm her agreement, that the witches road was indeed a good idea, when she felt her words suddenly stall in her throat.

For Agatha was staring at her like she had seen a ghost.

“Agatha?” Rio asked, taking a step closer, “are you alright?”

She tried to tame her hope that a flame of recognition had sparked to life within Agatha’s mind but it was not the case, for Agatha quickly nodded, holding a hand up to her own throat in a gesture Rio recognised as one she often did when attempting to self-soothe.

“Oh yeah, I’m fine,” she reassured lightly, before blowing a raspberry and shaking her head, “you just, you just really, really look like…” she clenched her eyes tightly together and waved an impatient hand, “never mind! Anyway!”

Rio’s heart plummeted into her stomach, because she knew exactly who Agatha had just recognised in Rio’s face. Rio and Nicky had been two peas in a pod after all; it was one of the reasons Agatha had fled from her after his death. Rio's face reminded Agatha of all she had lost.

Pain flared but Rio swallowed it down, deciding it was best to just persevere for the time being and redirect them back to their objective; to steal as much magic as they possibly can and regain Agatha's power.

“So,” Rio smiled at Agatha and nodded towards the stairs, “we are going to walk the witches road, are we?”

Agatha’s responding smirk was devilish and frustratingly attractive, evidently sponsored by the belief Rio had fallen for her ploy. Slowly, with swaying hips she swept closer to start playing with the ends of Rio’s hair again, “hell yeah we are. But first… first we need to find a coven”.

Rio grinned, the wolfish one that she new always made Agatha’s eyes darken; which they did, almost immediately. It was good to know that some things hadn’t changed, especially after everything they had been through.

“ Wherever you are, a coven there shall be ,” Rio murmured, unable to stop her eyes from glancing down towards Agatha’s lips.

And the moment she did so, she knew she shouldn’t have.

Because Agatha had the instincts of a jaguar scenting blood and the instant Rio’s eyes had flickered down to savour the vision of her mouth, those lips had twitched upwards into a smirk as familiar as it was terrifying.

For it was a smirk Rio knew well, too well. It was a smirk that said two words, two words that encapsulated Agatha’s mindset when she found someone she wanted, someone she wasn’t going to stop pursuing, and someone she knew to be exactly where she wanted them.

Got you .

Wherever You Are

Chapter Notes

Evening gang, I am aware the last few chapters have been on the heavier side, so I hope this fluffier chunk helps lighten the load slightly!

As always, thank you for all your lovely comments and kudos, all feedback is appreciated and you guys have been so kind! So thank you!

Enjoy! <3

AGATHA

Wanda’s spell had felt, in hindsight, like she was under water; muffled sound, refracted light, weeds wrapped around her ankles to drag her deeper whilst gasping for breath.

It was the feeling of tightening claustrophobia, but without knowing you were even trapped; a sensation entirely built on feeling and not at all on fact.

And even now, whilst finally free from Wanda’s entrapment, she could still feel the sticky sweetness of Agnes’s presence inside her mind, like a residue covering every thought and action. It was a bitter aftertaste, one that still made her shudder and wretch whenever she found herself blurting out something as inane as “okie-dokie,” or “in a while, crocodile,” without meaning to, as if in reflex.

These subtle relics of Agnes were not helped at all either when, following her impromptu escape from Wanda's hex, memories from her time as Agnes started to drip feed through into her consciousness, each one randomly prompted by a particular item or a certain phrase. Agnes’s memories were blurrier than her own, shaded in smears of red. It was still comforting though, in some abstract way, to have at least a partial record of what she had said and done whilst not in control of her own body, which was certainly a confounding thing to try and grapple with.

What was more, with every memory that resurfaced like air bubbles popping to the surface of a still, dark lake, Agatha’s curiosity started to burn ever hotter regarding one particular person.

Because, to put it frankly, things to do with one Rio Vidal were not adding up.

Like at all .

And Agatha had a nose for fallacy, considering she herself was so good at weaving it.

At first she had assumed Rio was just a neighbour Agnes had shacked up with, which had made sense because Agatha was gay as hell and Agnes shared Agatha’s body, so of course Agnes would choose a woman to take to her bed.

But then, almost as a direct reaction to that one thought flittering through her mind, flashes of countless rejections appeared, one after the other, each one a snap shot from the past year in which Rio had gently and admittedly, rather smoothly, managed to dodge any and all of Agnes's sweet, yet not particularly subtle, attempts at seduction.

Those particular memories had caused an initial flare of offence, because why the hell wouldn’t Rio want to be with Agnes. Agnes had Agatha’s face and body after all, and she knew the power those parts of her possessed on their own, even with Agnes's measly personality covering her own far more magnetic character. Offence had been promptly replaced by confusion though, because why would Rio have been there otherwise? If Rio wasn’t there because she and Agnes were more than friends… then why the hell was she sleeping in Agnes’s house? For a year ?

That realisation had then caused even more memories to stream forward in which, nestled amongst the onslaught, was the very first moment Agnes had awoken following that final, humiliating confrontation with Wanda, the one where she had stolen all of Agatha’s carefully curated magic and then shoved Agnes’s horrid personality over her own, like a scratched record that just wouldn’t stop.

And much to her surprise and rather desperate curiosity, Rio had been there too . Right at the start, bowed over her hands as though Agnes mattered. Which was absurd, because Agnes didn’t exist . And if Rio wasn’t there for Agnes then she must have been there for Agatha but, and here’s the crux of the mystery, Agatha doesn’t know her. At all .

She would remember a face that beautiful, she knew that much.

Which in itself was a confoundingly absurd puzzle to piece together. Yet, beyond that and perhaps even more absurd still, was the undeniable comradery Agatha felt towards this random stranger almost immediately, this stranger who it turns out was also a witch . A witch with a power so potent fizzling beneath her ribcage that Agatha’s eyes had almost rolled backwards at feeling its strength under her palm.

All of this was intriguing enough without even mentioning one of the most disarming, and frankly bewildering, points. Which was just how much this stranger resembled her son.

And the longer she looked, even more similarities between the two became obvious. for he was there in the curve of Rio's cheek, in the shape of her button nose, the colour of her hair, the tone of her skin, it was all absurdly kindred, it was all so very, distractingly, painfully Nicky . So much so that even her teeth struck a chord of familiarity.

It was a jarring thing to witness, to see her beloved son’s face in the features of a stranger. And what’s more, the longer she thought on it, trying to piece her thoughts together, much like trying to force a puzzle to reveal it’s image with several of the pieces missing or entirely blank, the blurrier everything felt, as though her ability to focus, to question Rio’s presence in Agnes’s house, and to ponder her confounding similarity to Agatha's son, turned into fog and was suddenly ungraspable.

So, with all of these thoughts swirling around her mind and confusing her further, she attempted to internally summarise every piece of information she had gathered and managed to piece together so far:

1) Rio, who bore an uncanny, potentially eery resemblance to her lost child, had been the first face Agnes had seen upon waking.

2) She had then stayed beside Agnes this entire time, aside from the occasional business trip which Agatha could recall Agnes feeling particularly melancholy during.

3) She had not once been receptive to any sort of physical relationship with Agnes, yet was still here and still willing to help Agatha reclaim her power.

4) She knew exactly how Agatha operated, how she stole magic from unsuspecting witches.

5) And possibly the most absurd point of them all, even with all of these glaring inconsistencies and whilst covered in countless red flags the size of the pacific ocean, Rio still managed to make Agatha feel frustratingly safe, as though she was a person who Agatha could actually trust . Which was a novel experience in Agatha’s long life, that was for damn sure.

Her mind continued to consider each one, attempting to coalesce and merge together the known facts into different shaped theories or potential motives, like an internal Rubik’s cube that she was continuously reconfiguring until more of it matched up and started to make sense, as Teen drove them across town on their hunt for a coven.

She was sat in the front, having shoulder barged Rio out the way with a loud “shotgun!” The moment they had all started to head towards his old beat-up sedan, that had undoubtedly seen better days about twenty years ago.

Through narrowed eyes she turned to study the subject of her fascination from over her shoulder, lowering her sunglasses as she did so to the bridge of her nose, so she could consider the other woman and her mysterious motives properly.

There was more to all of this, to her, much, much more .

She knew that much at least for her instincts, which were never, ever wrong, were crying out loud that this was the case. She was missing something , something vital. And she would have bet all the magic in the world that Rio was the key to it all and that she knew far more than she was letting on.

Agatha would get to the bottom of it though, she had no doubt about that either. She always did in the end.

Suddenly, as though summoned by the heat of Agatha’s stare, Rio turned from looking out the window, causing their eyes to meet and gazes to lock.

Moody blue on golden brown.

Rio arched a brow, smirking at Agatha’s review of her, probably because most people, once discovered staring, would look away blushing, embarrassed at being caught. But Agatha felt neither shame or humiliation, nor did she look away, because she, if anything, felt even more determined to discover Rio's secret the moment she saw those distracting lips tick up with amusement.

So, in direct reply to Rio’s nonverbal challenge, Agatha arched a sharp eyebrow of her own.

“Erm, sorry to interrupt… whatever you guys have going on right now…” Teen’s irritating voice rang out, disturbing what was turning into a rather pleasant stand-off, “...but where exactly am I supposed to be heading? Is there like a meeting point? Or a signal we should blare out or something?”

Agatha scowled and slipped her sunglasses back into place before turning with a loud harumph to face the front windscreen again.

“ Wherever you are, a coven there shall be ,” Agatha drawled, whilst lazily chewing on her thumbnail.

“That’s beautiful,” Teen murmured, as though he found the words profoundly moving.

“No, it's definitely not,” Agatha disagreed, lip upturned with disdain for his puppy-like sentimentality.

Teen let go of the wheel with one hand to pull a small notebook from his back pocket, “can you actually jot that down for me? There’s a pen in the glove compartment”.

“Oh yeah,” Agatha feigned, pulling the pen from the glove box only to immediately throw it out the window, she gestured for the notebook, “did you want me to take that?”

“No, no,” Teen murmured, “that’s alri-” his sentence was interrupted though, because Rio reached between the front seats to snatch the spell book from his hand.

She hummed loudly, pulling it open to flip through the pages, “ooh, a boys first spell book?” she eyed Teen over the top of it’s pages, hiding the devilish smirk cemented onto her face, “what kind of secret things have we in here hmm?”

Agatha cackled loudly, delighted with Rio’s game as she undid her seatbelt to clamber between the seats into the back, where she landed, quite intentionally, on Rio’s lap.

“Hey!” Teen yelled twice, first at Rio snatching his spell book from his hand, only to yell it louder a second time whilst pulling on the steering wheel to correct the car’s route, it having been knocked off course by Agatha’s wayward knee.

“Yeah!” Teen said from the front, unaware of the strange tension that had started to bleed from the witches on the backseat, still focussing on the road ahead, “I found it in this old spell book I bought at an antique thrift store in the city! How cool is that? That it’s possible to actually summon him!”

The phrasing, for some curious reason, caused Agatha’s hackles to rise, even through the fog she was currently battling within her own mind, “and why is it you assume Death is a man ? I took you for a lot of things Teen, but a chauvinist?” She ticked her tongue in disapproval, “I’m very disappointed in you”.

Rio nodded and smiled up at her, “who knows? They could be. Or they could be a complete smoke-show”.

Rio’s smile faded the longer Agatha stared at her with a confused, befuddled frown, “are you alright?” she asked, the concern clear in her tone.

Quickly, Agatha shook herself free from the absurd fantasy; undoubtedly the result of residual chaos magic zipping from one synapse to the next. She shot Rio a reassuring grin, “never better hot stuff,” she drawled whilst leaning more of her weight onto Rio, whose breath, in reaction to feeling more of Agatha's body pressed up against her own, shuddered out against the back of Agatha’s neck in a few tantalising waves.

Glancing down, she winked at Rio before whispering to the flustered woman beneath her, “I smell a witch”.

“Welcome to the curious,” a wispy voice echoed out, as a figure drifted through the beaded curtain that separated the front of the shop from the personal quarters out back.

She introduced herself with an airy palm, “Lilia Calderu,” before waving the same hand towards a small round table with a crystal ball sat in the centre, which was set to the side of the shop.

Lilia drifted towards the table, cutting an eccentric figure in her cluttered store. Her hair was steel grey, curled tightly and pinned back, with a few loose ringlets left free to frame her face. She wore a brightly coloured jacket, a patchwork piece of clothing that looked well worn and well loved over a flowing shirt and relaxed trousers.

“Thank you ma'am,” Agatha simpered, as she led her ragtag group towards the table. There were only three chairs around the table; Lilia took the first, Teen the second, so with a shrug Agatha sat down on the third and promptly pulled Rio onto her knee.

Lilia’s eyes met hers over the table. She smirked knowingly and shot a pointed look towards the woman perched on Agatha's lap, “here because you miss your dear husband, are you?”

Enjoying the game and her performance, probably a little too much, Agatha closed her eyes in a mockery of grief and nodded solemnly. “I am , I do ,” she whimpered loudly and dramatically, inspiring a cackle of amusement from Rio which she silenced with a hand wrapped over her mouth, “but to be quite frank with you, what is top of mind is the location of some gold bars my darling husband Friedrich may or may not have buried in our backyard".

“Right well…” Lilia eyed them all, “whose paying?”

Agatha elbowed Teen and grinned brightly at Lilia, “he takes such good care of his mama and auntie Gertrude, don’t you sweetie pie?”

Teen rolled his eyes and pulled his wallet from his pocket. He paid for the reading and then immediately struggled to stifle a laugh when Lilia closed her eyes, swept her hands over the crystal ball, and started to warble wordlessly.

Rio’s face brightened as she too raised her hands towards the ceiling and started to chant loudly in an attempt to try and harmonise with the divination witch. Lilia stuttered to a shocked stop and glared at Rio through narrowed eyes.

“Excuse me young lady, the art of divination is a delicate practice and requires years of training and a refined understanding of the great beyond”.

“Oh, totally,” Rio agreed, blank smile set back on her face, which prompted a strangled laugh to escape from Agatha, who was once more surprised to find herself genuinely enjoying Rio’s company; she was turning out to be just as much of a wind-up merchant as Agatha was.

It was a surprisingly comforting thing to experience and something Agatha could never recall feeling with anyone else; instant harmony with another person.

It left her stunned for a brief moment as she stared up at Rio’s face, allowing her eyes to sweep over those frustratingly and absurdly familiar features.

Who was this woman? And why, why did Agatha know, deep, deep inside herself that she mattered ?

“You'll find the gold bars in an old bowling bag at the back of his closet".

Lilia’s answer jolted Agatha from studying Rio's face, prompting her to throw both hands up in victory, “oh happy days ! Thank the lord above and your daddy’s spirit for blessing us with these hidden riches, amen”.

She gripped Rio’s hips and gently pushed her up off her lap, feeling bold enough to flex her fingers and make the other witch jump slightly from the subtle teasing, “hop off of mama, darlin,” she drawled, “I’ll let you hop right back on as soon as we get home”.

“Can you like, not,” Teen sighed, eyes closed with teenage disgust as he too got to his feet before pushing his chair back under the table.

However before Agatha could reply with something else to scar him for life, Lilia started to speak once more, her tone suddenly solemn.

“There’s something else. You’ve been under the influence of another, someone you hurt. They took your agency for an entire year. It’s not the first time your witchkin betrayed you, but you survive in a way few do, in fact it’s why you’re here,” her knowing eyes flickered to Rio as she slowly got to her feet. “Other mysteries surround you now, a puzzle that once solved will provide you with everything you have ever sought,” her gaze darkened, “but I am still not interested”.

She then turned to Teen, “your bank statement will say ‘Lilia’s Leggings’ but that’s just my side hustle,” and with that she turned and swept back through her beaded curtain.

“ Lilia !” Agatha sang, prowling after her into the older witch’s kitchen, “you haven’t even heard the pitch”.

Rio followed, wolfish grin now firmly in place, “it’s a good one too”.

Lilia’s eyes swept from Agatha towards Rio and for a moment her gaze froze upon Rio’s face. Her face paled slightly, as though she was seeing something other than pretty brown eyes and temptingly plump lips.

“I don’t need to,” she mumbled, eyes dragging slowly from Rio towards Teen, who was hovering politely by the door before shooting another formidable glare towards Agatha, “what witch in her right mind would join Agatha Harkness’ coven?”

And so it continued, the back-and-forth bartering until they were finally sweeping from Lilia’s shop, having enticed her enough to divine a list for them, a list that without conscious choice, Lilia’s own name had ended up on.

“That was amazing!” Teen cried as they headed across the street, back towards his car, “and we got a team roster out of the deal too!”

“Damn I’m good,” Agatha sighed, pulling her hair from the conservative bun she had drawn it back into before entering the shop. She closed her eyes and exhaled slowly, savouring that familiar sensation of a trap tightening around her prey as she basked in the afternoon sunlight streaming over her face.

Her peace was immediately disturbed though by Rio shouting “shotgun!” And barging her out the way to get to the front passenger seat.

“Hey!” Agatha cried indignantly before immediately wrapping an arm around Rio’s throat in a headlock to haul her backwards, whilst trying to twist them both sideways so she could get to the door first.

Rio’s grin grew delightedly feral when Agatha started to fight back and the moment Agatha attempted to push her away from the door she dropped low to offset Agatha’s centre of gravity, hooked her arm around Agatha’s waist and hauled her up until she was slumped over Rio’ shoulder like a sack of potatoes.

“Ah! Put me down you creature ,” she growled, starting to pound both her fists against Rio’s back, who responded by striding over to a dry patch of grass on the other side of the road. She then promptly dumped Agatha onto the dusty ground right on her ass, so Rio, now benefitting from a head start, could spin on her heel and sprint back to clamber into the front seat whilst Agatha screamed in frustration at being bested and immediately scrabbled back to her feet in order to give chase.

“Guys, we have to gather like two more witches this afternoon,” Teen sighed, already sat in the car with both hands on the wheel and his eyes closed; evidently practicing mindful patience.

Agatha ignored him and stormed up to the passenger seat to begin aggressively tugging on Rio’s arm, trying to physically drag her from the car, “you’re lucky I don’t have my magic right now,” she hissed at her, eyes alight with competitive rage, “I’d have you gagged and bound in the back of this car with a single click of my fingers”.

Immediately, Agatha froze as she watched Rio’s amused grin darken into something wolfish and menacing.

“No, don’t you even dare ,” she ground out, stumbling backwards as Rio slowly raised her hand and clicked her fingers causing a burst of emerald smoke to snatch Agatha from the street and deposit her in the back of Teen’s sedan with both her ankles and wrists tied up with vines.

She growled at Rio through clenched teeth, struggling furiously against her bindings, “I swear to god Vidal, if you don’t free me right now I will kill you the old-fashioned way with knives and axes and iron maidens and…”.

But Rio, who had picked up Agatha’s sunglasses from where they had been abandoned on the dashboard, simply slid them onto her face with a smug, victorious grin and ignored the continuous stream of threats being thrown at her from the back seat.

“Better start driving Teen, those restraints will only hold her for about three more minutes, and I think it’s fairly safe to assume she will immediately try and climb up front to fight me the moment she can”.

Rio looked absolutely delighted as she said this, now peering over her shoulder with a beaming grin to watch Agatha's reaction, whose blazing gaze met Teen’s in the rear view mirror.

His eyes were wide with uncertainty; evidently questioning the validity of Rio’s words, which Agatha confirmed by nodding firmly at him as a sharp, feral grin spread across her face.

And with that, he gulped, threw the car in drive and sped off towards town, intent on finding another witch before the two currently sequestered away in his old beat-up car could cause an accident.

A Coven There Shall Be

Chapter Notes

What's up my dudes, I hope you're all doing well and ready for another hefty chunk of chaotic coven-recruitment!

I have very little to say this time round other than another thank you for all the lovely comments & kudos. I appreciate the time you guys take to leave feedback a lot, so thank you again <3

And of course, the standard outro: I hope you enjoy! xox

AGATHA

They had been in the car for around fifteen minutes.

Agatha had spent the time glaring out the window at a tidy shop in the centre of town, a sign declaring itself “Kale Kare” was superimposed across it's front in big bold letters.

Teen had spent the same amount of time glancing between Agatha and said shopfront, waiting for a sign that it was time to exit the vehicle and actually approach the store.

And Rio, Rio had spent the time blooming an array of colourful flowers in her palm to thread through Agatha’s hair, who, much to her own surprise, didn’t mind in the least.

when the clock struck the eighteen minute mark, Teen spoke.

“Are we like… going to go in? Or are we waiting for her to come out here?”

Agatha groaned loudly in response, an overdramatic petulant sound as she slumped forcefully back into her chair, “ ugh , why of all the witches in the world did it have to be her ?”

“Friend of yours then?” Teen asked, keeping his voice light and airy to disguise the true depth of his curiosity.

“Ha! As if ,” she scoffed, although her disdain lost some of it’s power due to the large daisy now being threaded through one of the plaits falling over her shoulder.

Suddenly, Rio jolted backwards with a hissed, “no fucking way!” This was followed promptly by the car door opening and then slamming shut as Rio scrabbled from the backseat onto the sidewalk; the backseat she had been forcefully dragged onto the moment Agatha’s bindings had fizzled and disappeared, much to Teen's demands they ' stop right now before I crash Mom's car! '

“Hey!” Agatha called, perturbed at the thought of losing sight of Rio, which in turn perturbed her further, because she had never in all her long years considered herself clingy before, “where are you going?”

She gestured for Teen to follow before rushing out the car to spin in a wide circle, hunting for a flash of Rio's familiar figure amongst the mix of pedestrian’s striding down the sidewalk.

"There," Teen said, pointing down the street a good distance, where they caught the tail end of Rio turning down an alleyway that led behind a tired looking Italian restaurant.

“What the hell is she doing?” Agatha growled, speeding after the wayward witch. Yet, the scene she found on turning the corner into the alley wasn't what she had been expecting, although in truth, she wasn't entirely sure what she had been expecting in the first place either. Because on turning the corner, she found Rio firing a beam of green light at the scampering hind of a skinny coyote, who quickly fled from the alleyway with a growl the moment the bolt of magic struck it on the ass.

“A coyote!? ” Teen yelped, “what’s a coyote doing this close to town?”

“Good question,” Agatha murmured, brow heavy with curiosity as she watched Rio’s expression. It was dark and weighted, threaded with what looked like flashes of a temper that was spitting just below the surface, like magma beneath a volcano. Physically too, it was clear she was distressed, for both her hands were clenched and her chest was rising and falling quickly, as though trying to contain her upset with a few deep, cleansing breaths.

“You good?” Agatha asked, taking a step closer to tilt her face up, capturing Rio’s gaze, “something you need to share with the class?”

Rio’s eyes found Agatha’s and like lightning through storm clouds, her fury shattered and worry bled between the fractures.

“That mangy mutt is one of the Salem Seven,” Rio’s expression hardened again as she took a step closer to grasp Agatha’s wrist tightly, “they’ve found you”.

Agatha’s stomach plummeted at the realisation, “shit,” she hissed through clenched teeth, suddenly feeling exceptionally vulnerable without magic to protect herself with. It was such a disarming sensation, so distracting, she didn’t even think to question how or why Rio even knew about her oldest enemy or the fact they had been hunting Agatha since her Salem days; it was simply a thought lost to the static of her panicked mind.

Adrenaline started to pump as a new found sense of urgency prompted her to spin in place and start speed-walking back down the alleyway, “come on then losers, no time to lose. Got witches to lure!”

And just as she was turning the corner back onto the busy high street, she heard Teen murmur to Rio, “witches to lure? ”

And Rio, god bless her heart, strange mystery that she was, simply grinned at him with wide, wild eyes, shrugged blasély and murmured in appeasement, “recruit”.

“Hey! Where do you keep your jade eggs? I’m fresh out of marbles, and my pelvic floor is all over the place!” Agatha entered the shop with a flourish, disturbing whatever spiel Jen was spouting to sell her terrible wares.

She strode forward and gestured to the two women she had been close to swindling, “actually, you gals wanna go splitsies on one? Hmm? Anyone? Anyone? Sisterhood of the travelling Kegels?”

Glancing between them, she grinned as the two mortal women fled from Jennifer’s shop and Agatha’s insistent presence, “no? no?”

She heard the shop door rattle open, then closed. She turned towards Jennifer with a big, fake smile, “Hi Jen!”

Jen stared back, looking particularly displeased to see Agatha in her store, “god, Agatha! I haven’t seen you since I made a really pointed effort to never run into you again”.

Agatha laughed loudly, boisterously, “so good!”

Jennifer matched her energy, smiling with faux interest as she asked, “how are you? Awful?”

Unwilling to continue on with what was amounting to be a painful level of small talk, and with what little patience she had for both inane conversation and Jennifer Kale specifically drying up like a puddle in the Sahara desert, she got straight to the point of their visit, “I’m assembling a coven, I need a potions guy. We’re gunna walk The Road”.

Agatha snorted a laugh as Jen, now in a state of concerned fluster, followed Rio around the store to blow out each flickering flame, all while trying to get Rio’s attention with polite a continuous stream of, “excuse me, miss, these particular candles are not for human consumption, they aren’t probiotic, they’re literally wax!”

Rio turned then, with a finger still between her lips and cheeks hollowed with suction. She hummed in contemplation before pulling it free with a resounding pop, “this one’s definitely my favourite”.

She pointed to an orange candle labelled, “spiced banana bread”.

“Okay,” Jen nodded quickly with a forced smile, as though trying to talk down an insane person before pulling it out of Rio’s reach. Jen’s eyebrows rose in disbelief, “our third? ”

“ Who even is she? I’ve never seen her before,” Jen's eyes widened as she started to shake her head with muted horror at the prospect of walking The Road with Rio.

“She’s…” the question itself was innocent enough and obviously Agatha knew the factual answer it required. She knew she should open her mouth and say, ‘ her name is Rio Vidal ’. That was the simple answer Agatha knew to be correct, yet the question still caused her tongue to stumble as she stared at Rio, who had since lowered the spider to show Teen, who was now holding out a nervous hand for the long-legged creature to creep onto his broad palm, much to Rio’s evident delight.

“She’s important, alright, very important,” the answer felt right, although it didn’t actually answer Jen’s question, “and really talented. So, just trust me, she’s one of the good ones”.

Jen scoffed, “ trust you? As if me trusting you wasn’t absurd enough, you want to walk the Witches Road together? It’s a dead end. Literally ”.

“Oh come on Jen,” Agatha wheedled, “I’m offering you the chance to finally lift the binding spell that has kept you magic-less for the last… what century?”

Teen sidled closer; charming, youthful grin in place and large spider in hand, “you look amazing”.

Jen’s narrowed eyes remained locked on Agatha's as she agreed, “I know,” before asking suspiciously, “what do you care about my magic?”

Agatha scrabbled for an answer, gesturing with her hands, “I…”

“Oh!” Jen pointed at Agatha's fingers, now as pink as the day she was born and free from the Darkhold’s sinister stains, “you lost the Darkhold, and now you’re powerless and exposed”. A smug smile bloomed on Jen’s face at the realisation, “how far you’ve fallen, witch-killer”.

Agatha felt that hit like a strike to the face but refused to gift Jen the satisfaction of knowing it.

“As least I’m still a witch,” she shot back as Rio finally joined their conversation, now bored from studying the questionable items Jen was trying to sell.

Rio and Teen's faces swung from left to right as they watched Agatha continue to squabble with Jen, back and forth like a tennis match. Which they did, for several more minutes.

It didn’t take long though for Agatha to lose her patience and consider this entire attempt a lost cause, “ugh! Have fun healing the healthy!”

Teen didn’t follow her towards the door though, instead he attempted a friendlier, more simpering approach. “Hi. I love your Insta-page by the way. You totally minimized the size of my pores”.

Jen eyed him, “who’s this? Another child sacrifice?”

Now that quip hit even harder than the first, causing Agatha to waiver slightly in her anger. However, before she could even exhale a pained breath, Rio swept closer to Jen with a dark expression on her face.

It was intense; the incredible change Rio managed to trigger with just a furious frown and a clenched jaw, transforming instantly from curious weirdo to dangerous threat. That simmering potent power she possessed flared too, causing the tips of her fingers to crackle with sparks of emerald light.

“You dare speak of such things?” Rio’s voice was a violent rumble, like thunder promising the earth lightning was on its way.

Agatha felt a flutter in her stomach; at Rio’s evident power yes, but also at actually being defended by someone else, at feeling, for the first time in her life, that she had an ally who was willing to watch her back, who would look out for her and protect her completely. It was a new sensation, one whose warm glow she could feel herself softening toward. A slippery slope, she was sure.

She was jolted from her thoughts, which were still a buzzing mix of arousal and confusion, the moment Rio’s hand went towards the curved blade she kept strapped to her belt.

Sweeping closer, Agatha wrapped gentle fingers around Rio’s hand with the intention of simply pulling it away from the knife, yet the moment Rio felt Agatha’s fingers brush along her own, she turned her hand to capture them, threading them between her own.

Agatha did a double take but allowed the contact. She reasoned that if it was successfully distracting Rio from stabbing Jen, which was the whole point of her intervening in the first place, then she would let it slide. But if Rio’s palm did happen to fit particularly well with her own, and the brush of her long fingers against Agatha’s skin caused a simmer of heat to boil in Agatha’s stomach, well that was her own damn business.

“Now Rio, violence isn’t the answer,” she tutted, smirking at Jen, “especially toward a woman who has no magic to defend herself with”.

Rio’s shoulders relaxed the moment Agatha spoke to her and with a gentle tug she was able to pull her backwards, away from Jen. Rio went willingly, only to then stand behind Agatha, hands still linked, and glare at Jen from over her shoulder, much like a muzzled guard dog might.

Agatha didn’t hate the feeling.

She didn’t get a moment to relish in the uncomfortable expression on Jen’s face from Rio’s behaviour however, because in the next moment Teen grinned in victory and flipped his phone toward Jen.

“I’m really sorry about your recent legal troubles”.

Agatha felt a devilishly proud smile stretch across her face then, as she took a moment to appreciate just how quickly Teen had managed to perfect the art of manipulation and relish the comforting heat of Rio's body hovering just behind her own.

“ Lorna Wu?! ”

Teen’s loud exclamation caused a lull in all of the surrounding table’s conversations, as several heads turned to see who had just shouted out the name of a 70s rock star in the middle of the mall's food court.

“Take it easy,” Agatha rolled her eyes, mouth still full of corndog and soda.

He didn’t listen though, continuing to talk at a mile a minute about their intended targets legendary mother, “she wrote the most famous version of the Ballad! My mom went to see her last tour right before she died, RIP.”

Seekest Thou The Road

Chapter Notes

Alright, Alright, Alright,

I hope all of you fine folks are well and had a restful holiday period, however you celebrate! I got slightly delayed posting this due to a busy Christmas time filled with way too many mince pies and beating my family at board games.

For this chapter, I had to figure out some quirks of the story - primarily how much or how little Rio knows about The Road from the get-go. So I have gone for a teensy pinch of salt and landed in the middle ground. Obviously, she's a primordial being so she isn't going to be duped by it, but at this point she doesn't know how The Road has come to be, or who is responsible for it. She is also having to play along too, because she has also convinced Agatha that she, as just a green witch, knows of The Road but doesn't know the truth of it's origins or how Agatha uses it as a trap for unsuspecting witches.

I hope all of that ^^ makes sense! It was a bit of a knot that needed untangling which was another reason this chapter took slightly longer.

With all of that out the way, I once again want to thank you for all of your extremely kind comments - seriously, you guys are so sweet, And thank you, of course, for the kudos too! I'm really pleased people are enjoying this story <3

Enjoy! xox

The Road doesn’t exist, or rather it shouldn’t exist. And yet, here they were. On The Road. So, what does that mean?

Was it actually possible? Was it an option to walk it, to claim the prize? Was it possible to walk The Road, reach the end and then utilise her winnings to gain Agatha’s memories back? Could she restore her wife’s mind in its entirety, filling in every blank space, dot every I, cross every T, and reassert herself within the fibres of Agatha’s grey matter, right where she belonged, where Rio had grafted for centuries to reside?

“Mrs Davis,” Rio corrected, squeezing Agatha’s hand in gentle reprimand.

Agatha frowned heavily as a confused pout blossomed on her face, “ who? ”

And Rio couldn’t stop the loud bark of laughter that escaped her throat, suddenly feeling lighter than she had in years at the combined sensation of Agatha’s warm hand in hers, her kiss fresh on her lips, and her wife’s terribly self-involved commentary ringing in her ears.

First Trial of Many

Chapter Notes
