AGATHA

Jen had been right; the first trial was indeed not the stuff of nightmares. On the surface at least.

No, it turned out the be a beach house. A beach house set against an idyllic backdrop of golden sand, turquoise waves, and a peach-kissed sunset.

They had, as was her new coven’s primary response to any sort of stimuli, argued over how to open the door and whether it would be considered rude to just traipse right on through.

Agatha, who didn’t give a damn about manners or rules, was the first to grasp the handle, swing the door open, and saunter across the threshold as though it were her own house.

The interior was as classy and opulent as the exterior implied it would be, with cream couches, expensive artwork on the walls, an inbuilt bar, and even a whole wall crafted from glass to showcase the expansive horizon spreading out across the distance. A beautiful view no doubt, but one that birthed more questions than answers on just where they were, on how expansive The Road really was, and the level of magic required to run such a potent hex in the first place.

It made her consider too, how unusual it was that The Road, so far at least, had presented them with a luxurious holiday destination, and not a cavern filled with spiders, or some just as horrific scene to battle through.

Yet, what was even more surprising was the change The Road had made to their wardrobes the moment they had stepped inside.

Agatha glanced down, expecting to see her familiar clothing, only for it to be replaced with an entirely different look. One consisting of grey slacks, a white cashmere turtleneck, and a brown jacket that her locket had been pinned to; which was a relief to see, that was for damn sure.

“Huh,” her lips curved in pleasant surprise whilst looking down to study her new outfit. Glancing around, she noticed all of the others had been redressed too.

Each of their prior outfits had been transformed into a particularly wealthy aesthetic, making them look like the type of people who could afford to own a house of this calibre. Rio looked particularly captivating in an emerald green velvet suit, one that had been tailored to her figure and didn’t appear to include a shirt, only a waistcoat. Agatha swallowed, feeling her gaze darken as she dragged heavy eyes across exposed collarbones and the small slither of tanned skin now visible between her waistcoat and waistband.

Teen was the first to step away from the front door, looking around with curious eyes, “it’s giving ‘ middle-aged second chance at love ’ vibes, and I’m here for it”.

Agatha stayed back, even as the others followed after him. Her eyes shot to Rio briefly at the mention of finding love, finding his statement hitting a little too close to the truth for their current predicament. Shaking her head to rid herself of as childish a notion as love, she ran a nervous hand over the door, causing her anxiety regarding their change in scenery to increase exponentially the moment she noticed the door handle was gone and their exit was sealed.

“Definitely a ' sip-your-tea-with-both-hands ' Kinda place,” Alice quipped.

Jen stared at herself in the mirror, evidently shocked to have been restyled so differently to how she would choose to express herself. “I look like one of my customers,” her voice treading the line between disturbed and amused.

Suddenly, Teen’s voice cut across the rest, “check this out!” Agatha looked over from running a hand over a particularly ugly glass sculpture to find him holding a small card aloft. From this distance, it looked like an invitation.

The group coalesced around him, Agatha managing to get there first to snatch the card from him, “what is this? A wedding? Please god, not a baby shower!”

Jen then snatched it from her, which Agatha would have normally fought her over, but she found herself promptly distracted from trying to scrap with Jen by Rio’s warm presence, which settled beside her with a comforting hand on the small of her back.

“ The Witches’ Road cordially invites you to The First Trial ”. After a quick glance around at all of their faces, she flipped it over and exclaimed, “it’s a riddle! My age has value, no fun alone, I mess with your mind, my tricks are well-known… ”

Agatha couldn’t resist pointing out the most obvious answer, “sounds like a witch”.

Jen was quick to quip back, “sounds like you ”.

Agatha wasn’t above mimicking her like a child, which she did. Moments later she felt a smirk blooming across her face at Rio struggling to stifle a bout of laughter. A glowing warmth blossomed then, deep in her heart at the knowledge that at long, long last someone finally got her. She wasn’t being reprimanded for her humour, she wasn’t being scolded for being childish, or for being rude. No, Rio found her behaviour amusing , Rio found Agatha funny .

And as she felt her smirk softening into something gentler, something concerningly enamoured, Mrs Hart solved the riddle.

“ Wine! ” She exclaimed, reaching for a bottle of expensive red standing on the table behind them.

“That’s it! Ten points for Mrs Hart,” Alice said, sounding impressed.

Arguing devolved from that point, as was their standard process. However it was clear, if not entirely obvious, that the wine would have to be consumed. Not by her though, hell no was she drinking that; it could be poisoned.

It didn’t take long for Teen to source a bottle opener, for them to open it, and pass round a glass of wine to each of them. Except for Teen that is, who had promptly asked for some and been denied by the far more boring and conservative members of this lacklustre coven. Though in her opinion, if a teenager could handle a situation as strange and anxiety-inducing as The Road, a place that shouldn’t even exist, the lad had earned himself a damn drink. Alas, she was outvoted; two to four. Rio of course, twin flame Agatha was discovering her to be, had voted for the teenager to have a drink too.

The others spread out, sipping their cursed glasses of wine and chatting amongst themselves. It was an absurd sight really; this mismatched group of covenless witches, one teenage boy with a mysterious sigil, and their neighbour, all stuck together for this moment of magical chaos.

Rio drifted towards the broad glass doors to enjoy the view, wine glass in hand. Utilising the opportunity of distraction, Agatha discreetly threw her drink on a large potted plant before turning back to study the green witch for a moment longer. Rio’s expression was contemplative, evidently thinking deeply on the trial at hand, or some other secret she was still refusing to share with Agatha. She found herself disturbed to see though, moments after Agatha had disposed of her own wine, Rio lifting her drink towards her lips.

“ Hey! ” She hissed, keeping her voice low enough to not be overheard. She scurried over and gripped Rio’s wrist, halting her upward motion. Quickly, she glanced over towards the others, who fortunately hadn’t looked over toward them, and dragged Rio out of view, pushing her into a small alcove housing a record player and a towering stack of records, “ don’t drink that! ”

Rio, who had allowed Agatha to drag her away, and who didn't look appropriately alarmed at Agatha’s alarm, simply looked down at the glass of wine in her hand, then back up towards Agatha.

“Why?” Her tone was relaxed, almost amused.

Agatha scowled, aware she couldn’t let slip the fact she hadn’t actually been here before. She had to warn her in a way that indicated she knew all the tricks of The Road, that she could be trusted to guide her safely.

“Just trust me, you do not want the hangover that wine will give you,” she tried to pull the glass from Rio, but she held fast refusing to loosen her grip.

"That doesn’t seem very fair to the others now, does it Agatha?” She still didn't look concerned at all as she tutted dramatically. The mirth clear in her eyes.

Agatha smirked, drawing closer.

She was determined to get the wine away from Rio, unwilling as she was for her new… new friend to risk her life for this task when they had three spares along for the ride, three spares she didn't give a damn about whether they made it off The Road successfully or not. Yet, if she could make the process of capturing said drink from said friend fun … well, she was only human.

“Why are you being so stubborn? ” She whispered, running her hand up the wine glass to brush enticing fingers along the delicate bones of Rio’s wrist, enjoying the feel of her smooth skin beneath her own.

“Why aren’t you being a team player ,” Rio shot back, pupils expanding even as she continued to act indifferent to Agatha’s gentle caress.

Agatha pouted, “I didn’t realise you were such a rule follower. Don’t you want to break the rules with me?” She remained bold with her hands, running one up the flat of Rio’s stomach to tease at the bare skin visible at the top of her waistcoat, and the other under her tailored jacket to the small of her back, where she tucked possessive fingers into the waistband of her pants, holding her close.

Bowing her head, she pressed a lingering kiss to Rio’s throat, “it’s fun to break the rules”. A wolfish grin bloomed on her face when she felt Rio shudder, a grin she made sure Rio could feel against her pulse, “it’s even been said once or twice that that's what they’re for; to be broken”.

She drifted her mouth upwards, ensuring her touch remained light, barely a whisper, before claiming Rio’s mouth in a deep kiss, grateful that this was something they did now, that this was something Rio trusted her to do without trying to absorb her magic through her tongue. Which was as delicious and as fizzy as Rio had promised it would be.

Rio kissed her back immediately, deepening it the moment Agatha groaned and her back arched slightly, pressing her torso firmly against Rio's. It was so good, so damn good that Agatha completely forgot the main reason she had planned on kissing Rio in the first place; entirely forgetting to run a scheming hand down Rio’s arm to take the glass of wine away whilst she was distracted.

Instead Agatha lost herself in the kiss, only to hiss with upset the moment they separated, and Rio brought the glass to her lips and downed the entire lot in a single smooth sip.

“ Damn it! ” She growled, pulling the empty glass from Rio’s hand; a pointless thing to do now it was empty. “I thought we were breaking rules together Vidal,” she glared up at her, their bodies still entwined tightly in a possessive embrace.

Rio’s smirk dropped into something endeared, a gentle, warm expression that made Agatha’s heart sputter in her chest. It reminded her of how it felt to miss a step whilst walking, when you expect the ground to be there to catch you, only to be met with empty air and the demands of gravity instead.

She lowered her face to Agatha’s, pressing a long kiss to her mouth, a kiss Agatha could feel her smile through before drawing back, “a little fact about me sweetheart; I always follow the rules”.

“How boring,” Agatha snarked before rolling her eyes and snoring obnoxiously, as though Rio had started reading an unknowable tome on quantum physics to her. Yet, even through her dramatics, Agatha felt her stomach tighten with worry over what the wine might do to Rio.

It suddenly struck her then, the reality of what she was experiencing, something she hadn't felt since a young boy had breathed his last.

Concern .

Concern for… someone else? Someone she had only known for a few days? The realisation heralded panic, which followed the worry pooling in her stomach, causing it to all mix together in an uncomfortable, unfamiliar mess.

Suddenly, as though someone had just held a livewire to her ass, Agatha jolted backwards, removing her hands from Rio’s body. This feeling made her twitchy; the sensation of giving a shit about someone else. She didn’t like it, and as far as she could see, only one person was to blame.

“Don’t say I didn’t warn you,” is all she managed to growl out through her swirling thoughts, before promptly turning to stride back towards the others, flicking her long, currently beautifully curled hair over her shoulders as she went.

Her temper bristled further, when she heard Rio chuckle quietly behind her, as though Agatha's moment of claustrophobic panic had been anticipated. As though she knew Agatha, well enough as well, to predict her reactions and moods to a situation.

Needing a distraction from the frustrating witch taking up most of her thoughts, she swept closer to the other women, who were still gathered near the couch. Although she lurched back the moment her eyes landed on Mrs Hart’s exceptionally swollen face.

“Holy shit,” Rio said, stifling a laugh behind her hand, having followed closely behind Agatha to regroup with their mismatched coven.

Alice approached Mrs Hart cautiously, “Sharon... you’re a little swollen”.

Mrs Hart suddenly looked terrified, “is it bad?”

Agatha snorted with amusement and laid herself along the back of the sofa, feeling a sense of relief easing into her nervous system at not having consumed the wine herself, “I think she looks fantastic”.

“We’ve been poisoned,” Jen’s voice rang out across the room, tone severe.

Panic ensued as everyone scampered to study themselves in any reflective surface they could find, each of them reacting in their own unique way to this particularly hilarious symptom of the toxic wine.

“Oh my god! I have jowls! " Alice panicked.

“My face! My formerly perfect face! ” Jen cried.

“Honestly,” Lilia drawled, studying herself in a hand-held mirror, “I don’t hate it”.

Amongst the chaos, Agatha crept toward the other doors, testing each one to see if any of them opened, hunting for an exit. However, the moment she spun around, frustrated to the tips of her teeth that not a single door or window would budge, she noticed Rio sat on the sofa, leaning back with her arms and knees spread out, looking devilishly handsome in that damn suit, devilishly handsome and not at all swollen.

The poison wasn’t affecting her.

It wasn’t upsetting her system at all . And it would appear as though Rio knew this to be the case too, for there wasn’t a single hint of concern or panic on her distractingly lovely face. No, instead of worrying like the others, she was just sat there, watching, reacting to their reactions, as though they were merely an immersive troupe of actors performing a captivating play.

Agatha’s eyes narrowed as she stalked toward her, not stopping until she was stood right in front of Rio, so close that Agatha’s legs had halted between the green witches, as she stared down at her with a suspicious glare.

“Why aren’t you all puffy too?” She demanded, hands gesturing toward Rio's face impatiently before dropping to land on her own hips.

Rio shrugged nonchalantly, though that familiar glimmer of amusement was still sparkling in her eyes, “I have a strong constitution”.

Agatha bowed closer, lowering her face toward Rio's to search for a single inch of swollen skin, which there was none, “...and so slides another puzzle piece into my pocket".

"Puzzle piece?" Rio asked, voice dramatically affected to sound oh-so innocent.

Agatha's eyes remained narrowed, "yes, puzzle piece. I'm collecting them all Vidal, every single one. Every time you say something unusual, every time you do something strange, every time you react absurdly; I'm collecting them all, every piece of information on you I can. And soon, soon I will figure it out and all of your secrets will be mine to keep".

Rio’s smirk transformed into a puckish grin, “keep collecting them sweetheart, you’ll still never guess right”.

Agatha felt her stomach pulse with want at both Rio’s challenging words and the woman herself, sat beneath her in a position that should be deferential, yet still managing to comport herself in a manner befitting royalty.

“We’ll see,” Agatha bit out, matching Rio’s grin with a feral one of her own. Their eyes remained locked for a short moment, the tension and secrets bristling between them like the hackles of an angry dog, before Agatha's attention was dragged away by the conversation taking place behind her.

“Do you feel tingling in the back of your throat?” Jen was questioning Mrs Hart, trying to figure out what the poison could be.

“No!” Mrs Hart answered, eyes wide with fear.

Jen nodded once before asking another, “do you taste mulberries?”

“What do mulberries taste like?” Mrs Hart whimpered.

Sensing this was going to take a hot minute, Agatha sighed and dropped to perch on Rio’s knee who held her steady with a hand on her hip. She glanced around to meet Rio’s eye, throwing up an exasperated, impatient hand at the scene in front of them, which prompted an understanding smirk to bloom on Rio’s face.

“I feel a little better,” Mrs Hart said suddenly.

Alice looked relieved, “your face is back to normal”.

“ Phew! ” Agatha said dramatically, miming wiping away a sweat-drenched brow with the back of her hand.

Mrs Hart ran curious fingers over her own face, “yay!”

Jen however looked terrified, “not yay . Very much not yay! ” Jen glanced from face to face, taking in each of their fearful expressions before explaining, “the fact that the face swelling decreased so quickly means it could only be one type of poison: Alewife’s Revenge. Face swelling is just the beginning. Next is dizziness, delirium, loss of motor-function, heart racing, hallucinations, and eventually… Death ”.

Rio’s leg muscles tensed beneath her, prompting Agatha to turn and stare at her. Finally, she reacts . Finally, a spark of fear from her calm companion. Although Agatha’s satisfaction was marred the moment she felt another disturbingly uncharacteristic spike of concern for Rio's wellbeing. So much so, Agatha couldn’t resist running her hand down the back of Rio’s head, smoothing her hair in an attempt at offering comfort; even though she was terrible at it.

Rio glanced up and caught her eye, although this time her smirk remained absent.

“How do you spell Alewife?” Teen asked, his timing as terrible as his current combover.

Her eyes scanned across Rio’s face and body, feeling an inexplicable need to make sure she was still herself and not yet a victim to the poison or it's symptoms. Once satisfied Rio’s face was lovely as it always was, she grabbed her wrist and hauled them both of the sofa, “ come on ,” she said quietly, “ let’s get out of here ”.

They didn’t get far though before Jen pointed an accusatory finger at the pair of them, “they didn’t drink the poison. You can’t cheat your way out of this! You have to drink it!”

“ Why? ” Agatha sniped back, feeling cornered, “ who says? ”

“ The Road! ” Lilia drawled.

“Oh, that’s ridiculous! We don’t all have to suffer. Teen didn’t drink!”

“He’s not in the coven, and he’s underage!” Jen argued.

Rio interrupted their argument with a simple, “I drank it”.

Agatha elbowed her and hissed out the side of her mouth, “shut up!”

Jen suddenly looked unsure, glancing at Alice for a brief moment for, before focusing back on Rio, “you did?”

“I did, tasted good. Like old grapes gone mouldy,” Rio grinned, that same unnerving smile she always seemed to adopt when talking to the potions witch, much to Agatha’s consistent amusement.

Jen glanced around, “can anyone verify Rio drank the wine?”

Teen held up a hand, “the glass over there is empty – the lipstick on it matches Rio’s current shade”. He then pointed to another glass, the one Agatha had abandoned on the counter after watering the plant with her portion, now once again full to the brim with dark wine, “that one is Agatha’s. I saw her hovering by the plant after we first poured the wine”.

Agatha pouted and crossed her arms, raising her chin arrogantly, “you know, snitches get murdered in prison”.

Teen didn’t look scared, he looked unimpressed with both her and her joke as he fetched the now full glass of wine and tried to pass it to her, “well, it’s a good thing we're not in jail then, isn’t it? Now, drink it”.

“ No ,” Agatha said, voice petulant as she pushed his hand and the glass away from herself.

Lilia approached, her expression a brewing storm, “I’m going to shove it down your gullet, so help me!”

Having had enough of this whole ‘ team-versus-Agatha ’ energy she was picking up on, a horribly familiar throwback to her original coven, she hissed out an angry, “you know what!” before grabbing the glass and chucking it at the wooden floor, shattering it into pieces.

“ No! ” Several of the coven cried as Agatha glanced around at each of them, feeling particularly smug at besting them all.

“Yeah!,” she jeered, “mmhmm!”

“On the upholstery?!” Mrs Hart groaned, devastated at the sight of red wine staining the expensive fabric.

“We are wasting time!” Lilia snapped.

“You have to drink , Agatha!” Alice implored, trying a gentler approach than the others.

She threw up a flippant shrug, “well I would, but there’s no more wine”.

Quickly, as though she could hear the clock ticking directly in her ear, Alice glanced around before snatching Rio’s glass up, which immediately started to refill with wine. Alice looked up to glare at Agatha in smug victory.

“So cute ,” Agatha jibed, starting to feel uncomfortably warm beneath her clothes from the stress of this situation, at experiencing, once again, the disdain of an entire coven for doing what any animal would and should do when in a dangerous situation; try to protect itself.

Teen’s glare was the harshest of them all, “ drink! ”

His tone took her by surprise, forcing her to do a double take. However, the moment he took an angry step forward, obviously intent on pressuring her into drinking the full glass of wine, he was halted where he stood.

For Rio had swept in between them, hand on the handle of her knife, eyes dark, almost oppressive with the strength of her outrage.

“ Back. Off ,” she growled, voice low, almost bassy as she pulled her knife from it’s sheath and held it out towards Teen’s chest.

Agatha could see the tension in Rio’s shoulders, could tell she was entirely prepared to strike Teen if he took a single step closer. So, in a bid to calm her down she placed a warm palm between Rio's shoulder blades, attempting to soothe her animosity.

Teen reared back further the moment the blade was drawn, evidently not expecting Rio to be quite as protective as she was being. He glanced around nervously before pulling the wine glass from Alice’s hand, “fine, then I will!”

Now Agatha was many things, most of them not particularly self-sacrificing or moral, but she did have at least one line she refused to cross. She didn’t hurt children, and this child, as much as she knew he would hate to be referred to as such, was about to drink poison in her stead.

So without prior thought, she snapped out a “no!” and grabbed the glass from Alice before he could.

Rio span, eyes wide with concern as Agatha hesitated momentarily to stare at the dark liquid, already gagging at the prospect of such terrible wine, before finally biting the bullet and downing the entire glass.

“ Ugh ,” she retched, “ ugh! ” It’s so cheap! ”

“Please, please! Wanda? Wanda, I’m begging you. Let him breathe , please!” Mrs Hart was pleading with a non-existent Wanda for her dead husband's mercy, her eyes glazed, staring off into the distance before promptly collapsing onto the couch, unconscious.

“So,” Teen quipped, “the hallucinations seem chill”.

Agatha was distracted from all that was happening however, because the moment the poison touched her tongue, she felt it’s toxicity take affect causing her skin to tighten, to become hot and painful to the touch.

“Hey, Potions Witch ,” she called out to Jen, demanding her attention, “it’s time to brew an antidote,” her face now the same swollen vision as all the others.

XXXXXX

They had split into groups to gather the list of ingredients Jen required to brew an antidote.

Lilia, Teen, and Alice had gone to one end of the house looking for frankincense and honey, whilst she and Rio had been sent out to hunt for zooplankton, which she had a sneaking suspicion Jen’s product's would be stuffed to the brim with.

Fortunately her face had deflated around ten minutes ago, although the dizziness that kept trying to sweep her feet out from under her was becoming rather bothersome.

It was after the third time she had swayed into the wall in the hallway, arms full of products so unable to stop herself from landing on her face, that Rio interjected, guiding her with a gentle hand into one of the bedrooms to perch on the bed for a brief moments respite.

Agatha could feel sweat gathering on her brow, so took a moment to breath through the toxin making its way through her body and closed her eyes, inhaling deeply.

She heard Rio shift slightly before a cool palm slid over her forehead. Its temperature felt like heaven, and she soon found herself leaning into it, eager for more of Rio’s soothing skin to touch her own.

Her eyes opened to find Rio crouched in front of her with a deeply concerned twist to her brow, their faces level.

"Just take a moment,” Rio ordered, flipping her hand around to feel Agatha’s temperature with the back of her hand.

“We have to get this crap back to Jen,” she insisted, finding even the action of talking taking far more energy than it should.

“We will,” Rio said, voice certain that their mission would be completed without failure, “but first, just take a minute. You don’t look too hot right now”.

Even through the poison’s toxicity she managed to scoff, “ excuse you , I always look hot”.

Rio’s responding smile held a warmth that a near-strangers shouldn't. “Well,” she drawled, running the hand that had been checking Agatha’s temperature down to tuck a loose lock of hair behind her ear; a motion of comfort and familiarity, one that caused Agatha’s heart to clench with something similar to yearning, “I can’t argue with you on that”.

Agatha smiled, unable to stop herself from doing so as her eyes locked on Rio’s. A moment of silence settled between them, the gentle kind, like that singular moment of stillness before falling into a long, peaceful sleep.

Agatha felt that same panic from before start to brew in her stomach and try to claw its way up her throat the longer they stayed in this strange purgatory. Because she felt, quite suddenly, as exposed as if she had been sat there entirely nude. It was unnerving, for it felt as though Rio could see right through her, that there wasn’t a single thought or feeling she could conceal from this woman, this woman who had secrets upon secrets.

It felt desperately unfair, like the scales between them were weighted in Rio’s favour. And it was especially precarious when she considered just how quickly her heart was beating beneath her ribs, how furiously her pulse was fluttering beneath her skin, and how her soul felt as though it had finally, at long, long last, found a place to call home.

The words slipped out without conscious thought, her voice now quiet, almost pleading for the truth, in complete contrast to the anger that had exploded out of her the last time she had asked Rio this particular question.

“ Who are you? ”

Rio’s face remained clear, her lovely eyes flickering across Agatha’s face as though trying to memorise her features. It was clear she was contemplating what to say, of how much of herself to reveal.

Her jaw dropped once as if to speak, before her brows dropped heavily over her eyes in a frustrated frown as her lips met once more, keeping their silence.

Sensing she was close to breaking, Agatha asked again, “please tell me who you are? please ”.

Sighing heavily, Rio dragged a hand down her face, “I- I can’t tell you anymore than I have”.

A spark of anger lit in Agatha’s stomach, “why the fuck not?” She closed her eyes, swaying a moment as the toxin made a wave of heat wash through her, not helped by the rush of her own temper. They didn’t have time for this, the didn’t have time for this damn conversation right now, yet Agatha had never felt so close to learning the truth.

In fact, there wasn't a single note of the anger Agatha had been expecting to be find on Rio's face as she said, “I have no idea what will happen if I do,” her features hardened slightly, “I won’t risk you Agatha. I refuse to do it for my own gratification or for yours”.

Confusion joined the mess of emotions seeping into Agatha's stomach, “ risk me? How would you be risking me?”

Rio shook her head and stood up, “come on, we need to get back. We don’t have time to discuss this right now”.

Agatha glared up at her, ever stubborn, even with sweat pooling on her forehead and nausea swirling in her stomach, she refused to move until she finally received some answers.

She didn’t get a chance to say anything else though, for Rio waved a hand and transported them in a cloud of emerald green smoke from one end of the house to the other. The rest of their coven were assembled already, having found their ingredients and brought them back to Jen, who had set the sink up to act as a cauldron.

“Where’s the zooplankton?” She demanded the moment they reappeared, her face looking just as ragged from the poison's contamination as Agatha felt.

“Here,” she held up Jen’s own products, raising a challenging eyebrow.

Jen hesitated, obviously caught.

“All natural or not, Jen?” Agatha teased.

“Drop it in,” she ordered, voice tight with a reluctant confession.

“ I knew it! ” Agatha said, throwing the products, containers and all, straight into the potion.

Teen stirred the antidote as instructed, each of them waiting with eager expressions for it to change colour and indicate that it was ready, yet nothing changed.

Jen looked sheepish as she glanced around at all of their pallid faces, “any bright ideas on how to set this sink to boil?”

“ You didn’t think of this before?! ” Agatha roared, furious at the potion witch's ineptitude.

“In the middle of a traumatic hallucination?” Jen thundered back, “no Agatha, I did not! ”

“Here,” Rio said, stepping forward to lay a palm against the side of the sink. Moments later it was bubbling away as though a fire had been lit beneath it. Agatha gaped, staring at Rio in awe. For that level of magic would usually take an incantation, or at least be physically manifesting itself on the conjurer's expression or body, making them strain and gasp. Yet, Rio’s face was smooth, her brow calm and cool, even though she too had consumed the poisoned wine.

Jen, Lilia, and Alice were all looking on with similar expressions of impressed shock. Jen was the first to snap back into action, “everyone pull a strand of hair out of your head now. A single hair only. Everybody, hurry up!”

However, just as Agatha was raising a hand to pluck said hair from her head, she froze. For a noise had echoed across the kitchen, loud enough to drown out all other sounds; the bubbling potion, the panicked voices of the others.

It was a baby’s cry, a familiar cry too, one she never thought she would hear again.

Turning slowly, her eyes found a simple pram, set between the kitchen island and the counter.

As though in a trance, she started walking towards it. Her eyes were already pooling with tears at the prospect of seeing her son again, of seeing Nicky as he had been all those years ago.

Yet the moment she reached forward and pulled back the soft blanket, the baby’s cry came to a sudden muted stop and in the place of a baby was the Darkhold; the item every witch here, except perhaps Rio, believed Agatha had traded her child for. Her darling boy.

Rearing back in horror at seeing the Darkhold again, especially in the stead of her baby, she gasped in desperate gulping breaths, for her lungs felt like they were on the verge of collapsing under the weight of her suddenly unmanageable grief.

“ Agatha! ” Jen’s voice broke through her hysteria, grounding her in reality to see that the pram was gone, that it had never even been there in the first place.

Scrabbling to turn on her knees, feeling not much more than a wild animal at this point, she found herself gasping all over again the moment she did so, for Rio had left her station and dropped to the ground beside her.

“Are you alright?” She asked, voice tight with worry.

“ Oh god ,” She groaned, finding the similarity between this enigmatic woman with pockets bursting with secrets and the son she had lost even more potent whilst his cry was still ringing in her ears. Her hands shot out, and without conscious thought she gripped Rio’s shoulders, tightly curling her fingers into the material of her suit jacket, unable to let her go when she looked so like him, when Agatha had been so close to finding him again, to seeing him in that pram, only for it to have been a cruel trick of The Road’s torturous trial.

Yet, her ability to provide whatever Agatha needed, even without her verbalising whatever that might be, was clear in the way she wrapped her arms around Agatha’s waist and lifted her from the ground, keeping her close in the halo of her arms once they were standing.

Those eyes that were the exact same shade of ochre as Nicky’s; even down to the individual flecks of mahogany, and the streaks of bronze that glowed golden when the sun hit them just right.

“Come on,” Rio urged gently, guiding Agatha back towards the sink, aware the clock was ticking on all of their lives, as the poisoned wine continued to spread throughout their bodies.

“Agatha, we need your hair!” Jen said, her words an order not a request.

“And yours too, Rio,” Jen prompted impatiently.

Rio’s gaze met Jen’s, “I dropped mine in already, before I went to help Agatha”.

Jen’s eyebrows rose in clear disbelief. She gestured at the potion, “this won’t work if you don’t put your hair in too”.

Like power incarnate, or a glimpse of something that none of them should have born witness to. It made Agatha’s pulse thrum hotly beneath her skin, a desperate mix of curiosity and hunger for that power Rio wielded so easily, and for the authority that Rio insisted on hiding behind a teasing smirk or slightly eccentric behaviour.

“Alright,” Jen finally said, giving in with a despondent shrug, “but it will be all of our funerals when this doesn’t work”.

“It will work,” Rio said, voice brooking no room for argument, “you just need to add the final ingredient”.

An expression of shock fell across Jen’s face, “oh shit, of course! I completely forgot”.

“Well... what is it?! ” Lilia demanded, slapping both hands down on the counter, shooting a furtive glance toward the clock.

“We need the blood of the unpoisoned”.

Agatha didn’t hesitate to pull the knife from Rio’s belt and grab Teen by the elbow, “thanks for being underage”.

To his credit, he didn’t fight her, instead he let her pull his hand over the sink and wait for Jen’s signal to run the blade across his palm, which sliced open as easily as hot butter on a summers day, before clenching a fist to squeeze fat pearls of scarlet into the potion, which immediately flashed a bright cerulean.

Agatha slid the blade back into Rio’s belt before they grabbing one of the cups of antidote being offered around. Each of them gulped it down quickly whilst gagging at the horrible flavour. Almost instantly, Agatha felt the cool relief of the medicine working, as it chased the toxin through her blood stream, swallowing it entirely and saving her from suffering any further side effects.

She passed a cup over for the others to force feed to Mrs Hart, who for this entire trial had been unconscious on the couch. Perhaps it had something to do with her mortal blood? Unused to handling the potent energy witch-folk dealt with so naturally?

Moments later, the timer started to beep and the oven door clanged open.

“Is that our exit?” Alice asked, voice lilting with surprise.

Lilia bent down to study it, “I am not climbing in an oven!” She turned and stared at them all, a dramatic flourish in her words and expression, “that happened to a friend of mine. She had a lovely house, and she ended up-”.

Screams erupted at the same level of ferocity as the water suddenly bursting through the windows surrounding the kitchen. Agatha was caught beneath a waterfall, yelling furiously for a long moment before her survival instincts kicked in and she started to wade her way towards the oven doorway.

“Help me with her!” Alice screamed, trying to lift Mrs Hart from the table.

“Not a chance!” Agatha yelled back, glancing around for Rio who she could see standing beside Alice. Unlike the rest of them who were all panicking at the prospect of drowning, Rio’s entire person exhumed calm, and there was a certain weight to her expression as she stared down at their unconscious neighbour.

Teen hurried over in Agatha’s stead, yelling as he did so, “we don’t know what happens if we leave her behind!”

“ Fine! ” Agatha finally agreed, stomping over to grab a limb and help haul the unconscious woman over to the exit, “god! She’s so little, why is she so heavy?! ”

Jen and Lilia were visible on the other side of the oven the moment they crouched down with Mrs Hart held between them all. “Just shove her in there,” Agatha commanded, “just shove her, shove her in there!”

Once their heavy parcel was delivered, she glanced up at Teen, “you next!”

He did as he was told, sliding into the small door with the ease of youth before she then looked at Rio, “now you”.

Rio grinned at her, looking particularly feral with her wet hair plastered around her face and the waterfall roaring in the background through countless broken windows, “beauty before wisdom,” Rio said, giving Agatha’s shoulder a gentle push.

Not a particularly self-sacrificing person, Agatha didn’t hesitate to accept Rio’s generous insistence, “all right. Me next!”

She then slid herself through the door on her back, crying a victorious wail as she did so, which quickly turned into a genuine scream when the door turned into a slide that twisted and turned between scraggly trees and heavy mists. Her lovely coat was back too.

Alice came next, which made sense considering just how chivalrous Rio had proven herself to be, as much as it frustrated her that Rio would prioritise a random witch over herself. Finally, Rio appeared, spinning down the slide, cackling madly; truly a woman of vast layers and unspoken depths.

She landed with an ‘ umph ’ beside Agatha, who had already gotten to her feet, soaking wet and kicking Jen out of her way the moment the potions witch tried to stand up.

“A little rusty there, Jen?” She couldn’t resist jibing, now her life wasn’t in imminent danger.

“A little traitorous there, Agatha?” Jen immediately shot back, shooting her a heavy scowl.

“Stop,” Lilia intervened like a mother between squabbling siblings, “we’re alive. We made it through the first test, everyone is safe”.

“Not everyone,” Teen announced, voice shaking, “Sharon’s dead”.

“Who’s Sharon? ” Agatha asked, genuinely confused.

Lilia, Alice, and Jen all looked fatigued at her behaviour, Teen however, looked scandalised.

“What?” She asked, frowning at him.

“ She’s Sharon,” Teen hissed pointing at the woman at their feet, his youth and innocence on broad display at feeling this level of despair from something as mundane as death.

“ Oh! ” She crowed, pointing, “you mean Mrs Hart”.

The other three witches ignored her, each of them kneeling beside the body to pay their respects, as Teen gently pulled her eyelids down so it would appear as though she was sleeping. Rio however, remained where she stood, still dripping wet in her black jeans and t-shirt, eyes fixed on the corpse as though it had wronged her in some way.

“You good?” Agatha asked, skirting Mrs Hart and her mourners to draw closer to Rio.

Rio’s neck snapped round to stare at her the moment she heard her voice. A flash of panic suddenly crossed her face, before her eyes started to flicker between Agatha and Mrs Hart, as though trying to figure out the answer to an equation that included the two of them.

“Hey,” Agatha soothed, assuming she was distressed at the other woman's death too. “It’s alright, she lived a… you know… she lived a life,” running a hand down Rio’s arm to comfort her, even through a frown of confusion. For everything she learned about this woman made her make less sense in Agatha's mind. She didn’t panic after drinking poison, she didn’t consume nor need the antidote, she wasn’t worried when the kitchen was literally flooding.

But this, a body , was enough to stop her, was enough to freeze her energetic momentum in place as though an arctic breeze had suddenly swept through the clearing they were gathered in.

Rio didn’t say anything, she just continued to stare at the body, even as Teen and Alice grabbed sturdy branches to use as makeshift shovels and started to dig a shallow grave.

“Guys!” Agatha crooned, finding the thought of hanging around frustrating beyond reason, “I don’t think that’s necessary, Mrs Hart wouldn’t mind if we-”.

She was promptly cut off by four voices yelling at her simultaneously, “ Sharon! ”

“Alright, alright, damn! ” She gestured placatingly with both hands, willing them all to calm down.

Suddenly, as though someone had flicked a switch within her mind, Rio shot forward to grip Agatha’s hand and tug her away from the others. “Listen to me,” she implored, voice serious and face set.

Agatha couldn’t help but smirk at Rio grasping her so tightly, “I’m listening hot stuff, although if you’re trying to snatch me away for a quickie you don’t need to ask, I’m in”. She then tried to lead Rio deeper into the trees, but was stopped short when Rio didn’t move.

Turning, her eyebrow rose in question as she tugged on her hand once more, implying Rio should follow her. But again, Rio remained still, her face heavily pained.

“I can’t Agatha, I can’t right now,” her voice was a pleading whisper.

Agatha frowned, “why?”

Rio’s jaw dropped uncertainly as her eyes flickered towards Lilia who was still bowed over Mrs Hart, chanting a haunting song of farewell, “I- I can’t because I have to go-”.

Immediately Agatha felt her throat tighten and her muscles tense beneath her skin at the prospect, “what? Why? ”

Rio tugged her closer, running her other hand down Agatha’s arm so she was gripping both her hands tightly, “I can’t explain right now, but I have to leave for a short while”.

Agatha’s frown, if at all possible, became heavier, “you cant just leave The Road, Rio. It’s The Road ”. She emphasised the realm’s name as though she found Rio simple, which to be fair, considering what the green witch was suggesting, wasn’t entirely removed from the list of possibilities. “You know, The Witches Road . Incredible magic, kind of a ' stuck-here-until-you-solve-it ' sort of situation”.

“I need you to trust me. I know none of this will be making a lot of sense, but I need to leave for a while; a few hours max and then I’ll be back. I promise,” Rio implored.

A whisper of a memory was tempted from the back of her mind at Rio’s words, it was a memory dressed in scarlet, one from her time trapped as Agnes. Several clear moments of Rio leaving intermittently followed. Agnes would always ask her to stay, Rio would then always insist she must go but would return without failure; much like she was doing now.

It was of equal measures comforting and disturbing. Comforting because Rio had indeed always returned, but disturbing because Agatha still didn’t know why?

She felt herself reacting, as she so often did to situations that caused her to feel unsure or vulnerable, with anger.

“So what? ” She snatched her hands back, putting them on her own hips instead as she glared at Rio, “you just leave , go flouncing off to wherever without answering a single question, and leave me here to carry on without you?”

Agatha saw a spark of frustration ignite in Rio’s eyes, “it’s not that simple”.

She sneered in response to Rio’s weak excuses, “it is actually, it is that simple. What the hell could be more important than this?”

Rio remained silent, her eyes dark with irritation. Whether it was at herself or at Agatha, she wasn’t entirely sure.

But Agatha had grown tired of her excuses, of the constant secrecy. Of questions without answers, of similarities and power and memories that didn’t belong to her.

She had grown tired of silence.

Scoffing harshly, she crossed her arms and dragged her eyes up from Rio’s boots to her eyes, which were still heavy with the weight of words she refused to say.

“Whatever,” Agatha scoffed, shrugging as though she didn’t give a shit. Which she didn’t, or at least that’s what she was insisting on telling herself, “you go do… whatever it is you feel the need to do. But don’t expect me to be sat here waiting for you like Agnes did”.

With that she turned on her heel and stalked off between the trees, leaving Rio behind to fend for herself, just like Rio was planning to do to her.

And If the action made her feel sick, and if the thought of Rio leaving her behind, even after only knowing her for a few short days, made her want to bawl like a child, well that was her own damn business.

A Heated Second Trial

Chapter Notes

This chapter is another long one you guys, so I hope you are settled comfortably!

It was one of the hardest ones to write, but I am happy with the result! So I hope you are too :)

Once again, thank you all so much for the kindest comments and generous kudos. You guys are so sweet and supportive, and it really keeps me motivated, so thank you!

As always, I hope you enjoy <3

AGATHA

Agatha wasn’t surprised by how little time it took for the others to notice Rio’s absence, she just would have preferred anyone other than Jen, the witch she had the least patience for, to ask the pivotal question, “Where the hell is Rio?”

Agatha sighed and closed her eyes, trying to claw together what little patience she had left. “Rio has…” she paused, grasping for an excuse although she too was in the dark, “she has had to step off The Road for a few hours, alright,” she kept her voice light, eyebrows raised and smile tight, daring anyone to question her.

Which they immediately did. Of course.

“ Stepped off The Road?” Jen repeated disbelievingly.

“ A few hours? ” Alice questioned, still waist deep in Mrs Hart’s grave, “what do you mean?”

“You can’t just step off The Road,” Teen argued, as though Agatha had designed the game rules herself and had been caught breaking them. He pulled his spellbook from his back pocket to rifle through it, hunting for any forgotten notes that mention a get-off-The-Road clause that he might have missed in his initial research.

Lilia remained silent, her eyes wise and heavy on Agatha’s face as all the other voices continued to rise in volume, echoing throughout their small patch of forest. She allowed them to carry on for a few moments before the pitch of them all squawking at her became too grating, and she felt compelled to throw out both hands and silence them with a loud, obnoxious shushing noise.

“Rio’s gone alright. For how long specifically? I don’t know,” she stared at each of them in turn, demanding they remain quiet with the potency of her glare, “she told me she would be back, and all we can do right now is hope that she is telling us the truth”.

Noticing Jen was gearing up to demand yet even more answers, Agatha silenced her with a loud clap of her hands, “right then, now that’s all cleared up. Shall we? Alright,” She spun, throwing her coat out behind her to act as a full stop to this particular interaction.

But no one followed her. Instead, each of them stayed still and continued to stare at her as though disbelieving the depth of her indifference.

She grappled to hold onto her small, remaining thread of patience and turned to soothe whatever issue was now causing them to move so damn slowly, feeling very much like a frustrated teacher might whilst herding a whole class of kindergarteners around.

“Okay, so what’s the problem now?” She asked, glancing around impatiently.

“A woman is dead Agatha,” Lilia scolded.

“Yes,” she nodded slowly, “and Alice and Teen are kindly digging a grave for her. So, they’ll catch up when they can. Vámonos!” She tried to lead them away a second time, but again found their stubbornness to be a stronger foe than she had anticipated.

“Okay,” she finally relented, “Mrs Hart shouldn’t have been here, but it’s no one’s fault except her own that she insisted on talking about garbage removal in the middle of a summoning spell, alright”. She threw up a conciliatory hand, “of course The Road killed her, more power for the rest of us!”

Agatha had hoped that final claim would have pleased them; it pleased her after all. But apparently their desire to appear righteous outweighed the truth, which was that every single one of them was on The Road for the exact same reason Agatha, she was just the only one being honest about it.

“Setting aside your staggering callousness, we still have the issue of our incomplete coven,” Jen drawled, standing from the log she had been perched upon.

“Oh, okay. Yes, okay, now I know the confusion,” she swirled one hand over the other, “we needed the whole gang to access The Road. But after that, it’s anybody’s game. It’s like the Ballad says, Burn and brew, with coven two, and glory shall be thine .

She was lying through her teeth, making it all up as she went. An impressive feat if she did say so herself considering only a few days earlier she had been shored up within her own mind, still Wanda’s prisoner.

Suddenly, a pain sparked deep in her skull at thoughts of Wanda. Suddenly, memories blurred, and the residual presence of scarlet magic in her mind seemed to glow in ominous warning. She shook her head, eager to dispel the distraction, and the thought of any ounce of Wanda’s magic still being present within her body. She felt disturbed by the idea of it still having an effect on her even now, like Wanda was some sort of twisted puppeteer and Agatha merely a doll with strings to pull on.

Jen’s irritating voice dislodged her thoughts from their current predicament, dragging her back to reality, “the Ballad clearly says, with coven true, glory shall be thine ”.

Agatha scoffed, “no it doesn’t! It’s coven two ,” she insisted, holding up two fingers to illustrate her point.

“ That doesn’t make any sense ,” Jen argued childishly, elongating the vowels and dragging out her words.

Her immature behaviour sparked a twin flame in Agatha, for she promptly spat back, “it does if you’re a student of the Ballad!”

Lilia’s familiar drawl interrupted their argument, “her mother recorded the most popular version of the Ballad, so maybe we ask Alice”.

“ Okay! ” Agatha threw up a hand, spinning round to face Alice and implore her to agree with Agatha's point. She had written the damn song after all, she knew the words. And Lorna Wu damn well knew them too.

Alice didn’t affirm either of them though, instead she asked Agatha another question she found herself lying to answer.

“How many witches left The Road with you last time?”

Thinking quickly, Agatha solemnly held up one finger.

Jen looked unsure for a brief moment before her expression hardened into something stubborn, “well, whatever. We still need a Green Witch”.

“Well, our Green Witch has stepped out for a minute,” Agatha snapped, unwilling to consider any alternative options, or the thought of Rio not keeping her promise and leaving Agatha here on The Road alone, “so, we’ll just have to make do without one until Rio comes back”.

“ If Rio comes back,” Jen murmured, tone baiting.

“ When ,” Agatha intoned, her voice edged dangerously, “ when she comes back”. Having had quite enough of the entire interaction, she threw a lazy hand towards Alice and Teen, “get digging then. You have fifteen minutes to get her in the ground, or else I’m leaving without you”.

And with that, she threw her coattails behind her and spun to saunter off between the trees, suddenly desiring nothing more than a moment to herself. Or at least, a moment with the only witch who was no longer beside her.

XXXXXX

Alice’s trial was next, that much was obvious almost immediately.

The five of them had crossed the threshold to discover a house stolen directly from the 1970s. The entire room was constructed from either warm stone or dark mahogany. The floor was polished, records and portraits of different musicians decorated the walls, and musical instruments were spread out sporadically, as though a band had just stepped out the back door from a recording session for a quick cigarette break.

Immediately, she caught a glimpse of her own reflection, jaw dropping open with just how good she looked, “oh, check me out!” Her outfit was everything she would have chosen for herself, in fact it was everything she had chosen for herself during that particular decade, including skin-tight golden flares and a navy sleeveless jacket, one with floating pieces of fabric for sleeves, and an intricate design upon it’s lapels.

The other’s drifted over to stare into the mirror too, their eyebrows raising almost instantly in appreciation for their own new looks.

“I mean seriously, we’re an album cover waiting to happen,” Teen quipped. Agatha couldn’t disagree with his statement; even she had to admit everyone looked good .

“The Road changes for the coven,” Lilia reminded them all, parroting Agatha’s earlier words, which had been entirely made up.

“The Road isn’t subtle,” Alice sighed, staring morosely at herself. Agatha couldn’t help but wonder if she could see her mother reflecting back at her in that moment, their similarities even more obvious now, not just by being one another’s closest kin, but by seeing herself surrounded by her mother’s world of music and 70s décor.

“Oh!” Teen threw his hand up like an eager student, “I was just thinking about the invite on the mantel. Maybe there is like, a riddle, or a kick-off for this one, too”.

“Alright,” Agatha gestured for everyone to spread out, “you heard the teenager. Look around and see if there is a clue or a hint hidden amongst the gaudiness”.

For once, they did as ordered without asking any questions or arguing back, and for a few still moments the only sounds resounding throughout the large room were gentle footsteps and the brush of fingertips over shelves.

Yet, as promptly as the silence had settled it was disturbed by a loud creaking sound.

“What is that?” Alice asked, voice sharp and alert.

Everyone started to spin on the spot, glancing around to source the origin of the noise, whilst subconsciously grouping together in the centre of the room; almost like a real coven might have.

“It’s getting louder,” Lilia said, clinging to Jen’s arm tightly.

Agatha turned in a circle, determined to locate the threat when she noticed movement coming from the corner of the room. It was a large potted plant, as round as a tyre, with a curving palm tree shooting from the earth it held, the same earth that was spitting out in small clumps, right onto the floor in sporadic bursts.

“What the fuck? ” Agatha drawled, breath baited and held as she watched the entire plant pot start to shudder and shift, as though something large was stuck within its ceramic walls.

All of them screamed then, a resounding chorus of fear, as a clawed hand erupted from the earth, leading to a bent elbow, before an entire body was birthed from deep within the plant pot in a contorted mess, spilling out onto the polished floor amongst a cascade of dark soil. The body continued to bend and crack into place, until to all of their surprise, Rio was stood before them with a broad smile on her face.

“What’s up guys!” She greeted with a wave, cricking her neck one final time with a horrendous crack, “did’ya miss me?”

“ Rio! ” Jen shouted, eyes wide, horrified at what she had just born witness to, “you scared the shit out of us!”

Rio didn’t look disturbed by this revelation, in fact she looked thrilled by it, “I did?”

“Yes, you asshole,” Alice sniped, before waving a hand at Rio’s entire person, as though trying to make sense of her sudden presence, “where the hell have you been? And why did you use a plant instead of the fucking door? ”

Rio’s expression remained blank, “you mean that wasn’t the door?” She pointed behind her at the plant pot, now cracked open with soil spilling from it, and the tree it once held securely leaning precariously against the wall, it’s knotted roots exposed to the air.

Sensing they weren’t going to get any answers from the green witch, Agatha hadn’t been able to after all, so the others certainly wouldn’t, Agatha gestured for them to resume their search for the trial’s starting point, “she’s a tourist guys, ignore her. Keep looking”.

With muted grumbling they did so, drifting away in pairs to recommence their hunt.

Rio shook the soil from her body and glanced down, humming slightly at her new clothing which was a frustratingly attractive blue dress, skin tight and crafted from a mixed medium of solid silk and sheer tulle, the fabric decorated decadently with small silver disks and partially draping over Rio’s head too, creating a hood that gave her outfit a sharp, mysterious edge.

“Stylish,” she commented to herself, eyes drifting up from reviewing her own clothing to study Agatha, who was still stood in the centre of the room, arms crossed tightly across her chest, glaring at her.

Rio’s eyes widened the moment they traced Agatha’s outfit, evidently appreciating the low-cut neckline, and flares that were so tightly moulded to her hips the curve of her body was on evident display.

Rio whistled appreciatively, “you look to die for sweetheart”.

Still utterly furious at Rio for leaving, and for insisting on holding her secrets so tightly to her chest, even though Agatha knew , maybe not literally, but at least deep down inside herself, that those secrets were her business too, she didn’t respond. Instead, she tilted her chin upwards and strode away, determined to finish the damned Road, even if Rio wasn’t taking it seriously.

She stalked through a darkened doorway toward the back of the house, which turned out to be a recording booth, decked out with a full studio bench covered in buttons and dials, a trolley full of old-school microphones, and two padded chairs on wheels, one of which she slumped into with her eyes closed, needing a minute to sort through her thoughts.

So, Rio had kept her word. She had indeed come back.

But that still left the gaping black hole of a question as to where she had gone? And as to what had been so damn urgent it couldn’t wait a few days?

Well, there were two more questions to add to the ever-growing pile of queries she had regarding the beautiful stranger who had lived in Agnes's house for a year.

Her mind settled into that period of time, once more trying to scan through the red haze of magic that covered Agnes’s memories, hunting for something, something else, anything at all, that might give her a clue or a hint as to just who Rio Vidal was to her.

Flashes of instances rushed past her minds eye the longer she pondered it, highlighting an array of moments.

There were ample domestic scenes: Rio laughing at the television whilst shoving handfuls of popcorn into her mouth; Rio making them both coffee; Rio holding Señor Scratchy close to her face, finding comfort in the warmth of his soft fur.

There was an abundance of memories consisting of Agnes lusting after her roommate too, each one a snapshot moment focussing on a particular feature or trait Agnes had found painfully appealing: toned arms pushing the lawnmower; Rio grinning, wide and feral with a streak of soil across one cheek; Rio guiding Agnes with a steady palm on her lower back through a door she was holding open.

Before finally, another memory started to drift into her consciousness. It was an important one, one that had been hidden beneath the layers of other less poignant memories.

It was the moment she had awoken as Agnes following her battle with Wanda. A scene she had revisited before yes, yet now it had returned with a starker clarity, one that included audio, audio of the exact sentence that had passed from Rio to Agnes upon waking.

The words resounded in her mind, spinning around and sharpening her already ravenous intrigue, prompting her to sit up straight in her chair, feeling quite suddenly, as though she was on the cusp of a breakthrough.

Rio’s voice had been dark, filled with grief, and wet with unshed tears, “ I’ll get you back my love, I swear it. And then, once I know you are safe and yourself once again, I will find the scarlet witch and she will learn that there are far worse fates than simply dying ”.

“I’ll get you back? ” She mumbled to herself, staring down at the bright carpet The Road had outfitted the recording booth with, not seeing it at all for how deep she had ventured into her own memories, “be yourself once again?” She whispered, repeating out loud each prevalent point from the memory she had just unearthed, “the scarlet witch?! ”

Her teeth clenched tightly as she realised who exactly Rio had been referring to, of course, who else would it be; Wanda Maximoff .

Her spiralling thoughts, and all the connections she was drawing too, were all promptly interrupted by Rio darkening the recording booth’s doorway with a wary, “knock, knock”.

Still running on the high of remembering the details of such a pivotal moment, she locked Rio’s gaze with her own and repeated, with a tone verging on accusatory, the green witch’s words back to her.

“ I’ll get you back my love, I swear it. And then, once I know you are safe and yourself once again, I will find the scarlet witch and she will learn that there are far worse fates than simply dying ”. Pausing a moment, she watched Rio’s brow drop with confusion, evidently not recognising the sentence nor its origins, “that’s what you said to me. When I first woke up as Agnes, you were crying, your head was bowed over my hands, and you said those exact words ”.

She allowed the silence to swell, wanting Rio to feel the discomfort of it pressing against her, to feel the trap that had been set and how it was now tightening, limiting her opportunities to evade Agatha’s questions any longer.

Rio however, much to Agatha's frustration, didn’t flinch or cringe, or have any other number of reactions Agatha had anticipated she might. No, instead the only giveaway Agatha’s words had impacted her at all was the slightest twitch of her mouth, as she did what Agatha was discovering to be an unconscious habit, and stuck her tongue into the inside of her cheek.

Agatha could feel her impatience rising at the lack of reaction from Rio, fuelling her to throw both hands up in exasperation, “well? Nothing to say?”

Finally Rio reacted. She sighed heavily and closed the door behind her, sealing them in the recording booth together and took a few steps closer. To Agatha’s surprise though, she looked more concerned than caught, almost wary as she studied Agatha’s face, eyes flickering from her eyes to her chin and back again, as though scanning it for a detail Agatha was unaware she possessed.

“Well, what do you want me to say Agatha?” Rio's voice when she finally spoke was subdued, like she was trying to talk down the ramblings of an insane person.

Agatha’s temper flared, both at Rio’s consistent attempts to avoid providing her with any clarity, but also at the insult of being spoken to in such a way, as though Agatha should doubt the validity of her own memories.

Hissing through clenched teeth, Agatha shot to her feet. The wheelie chair she had been sat on shot towards the wall from just how quickly she had stood, and Rio too stumbled backwards as Agatha swept closer, herding her against the bench of dials and buttons with a sharp finger that she jabbed into her chest, directly over her heart.

“You had better start talking, or even without magic I’ll make you sorry if you don’t,” her lip curled as she spat her threat in Rio's face, “what the hell did you mean by ‘ getting me back? ’ and what the fuck did you mean by when I’m ‘ myself ’ again?”

Rio’s face remained passive, although she exhaled gently, relaxing her body to lean back against the bench behind her. Agatha’s eyes flickered across her face, once again seeing her son in her features; in the shape of her eyes, the slope of her nose, the colour of her hair, and the tone of her skin. All of it was Nicky, all of it was her darling boy, yet this woman was a stranger.

Or was she?

Was that the secret? Was that what Rio had meant by getting her love back? Was that why Rio desired vengeance on the Scarlet Witch?

Had something else been taken from her? Aside from her own agency, had Wanda stolen some of her past too, some of her soul. Had she stolen Nicky’s other parent from her mind?

The finger she was stabbing into Rio's chest softened it's attack before hardening again, although this time it was her entire fist as she grabbed tightly to the collar of Rio’s dress, needing a physical link to the present as a wave of connections and possibilities swept through her mind.

Who was Nicky’s other parent?

Her mind started to hum under the strain of searching for answer, an answer she was sure that had been there before, but was now shrouded from her, as though someone had pulled a curtain across the truth, hiding it from view.

Did he even have another parent?

She squeezed her eyes tightly together.

The answer became clear then, like the glow of a lantern through fog; Yes . Yes he did .

She had named him Scratch, Nicholas Scratch. For he was a child conceived without a seed, he had been born of two mothers, he had been made from scratch .

Her eyes widened with horror as the reality of what Wanda had stolen from her settled in her fatigued mind.

That same, familiar pain started to pound in the back of her mind, in the same place it had earlier when she had been arguing with Jen about the Ballad’s correct lyrics, and the time before that too, when she had lost her temper and raged at Rio for keeping so many secrets. Rio’s expression finally shifted, as alarm cloaked her features. Quickly, both of her hands shot out to hold Agatha’s waist, supporting her weight as her knees buckled beneath her from the waves of agony suddenly echoing around her skull.

“Agatha,” Rio’s voice was tight with worry and sharp as a whip, “you need to stop . You need to stop trying to figure this out! I mean it”.

Agatha clenched her eyes tightly together, trying to centre her thoughts even through the sparking pain emanating from her mind, “then tell me the truth! And I can stop trying!”

Rio’s fingers flexed on her waist, “I can’t!” She thundered, sounding for the first time since Agatha had met her genuinely panicked, “I can’t! I don’t know what will happen if I do! You’re already in pain just trying to think about it! Fuck knows what will happen if I tell you everything! ”

Agatha forced her mind to clear and inhaled deeply, feeling relief trickle in like cold water on a dry, burning throat as the pain finally started to recede.

“Alright,” she eventually whispered, panting hard from experiencing such agony. She could concede that there was a definitive connection between Rio’s secrets, and the ache that would pierce through her head the moment she thought about them in too much detail, “alright, I’ll stop”.

Rio sighed, evidently relieved that Agatha had agreed to stop digging for anymore information. And if Agatha were in a better mood, she would have snorted in amusement at Rio thinking such an absurd thought, because as much as she could admit the two things were indeed connected, it certainly wouldn’t prevent her from hunting for the truth she desired to possess.
