“That was ahead of us,” Jen warned, as they all span around, intent on turning back on themselves to source another route through. Only they were forced to stop again when another feral scream echoed from behind them, trapping them on a very narrow stretch of Road.

“That’s behind us!” Alice mirrored.

Tension mounted as they all started to look around, hunting for an exit, or any means of defending themselves, when suddenly Teen’s voice broke through the panic, anchoring them all to reality with his ridiculous suggestion.

“What about a hexenbesen?”

And with that question spoken aloud, like a pin to a balloon, the atmosphere deflated from one of fright to one of bickering disbelief, as Agatha, Jen, Alice, and Lilia all groaned out pained refusals. Rio, on the other hand looked thrilled and pointed at Teen in eager agreement, “Yes!” She insisted, flicking her hand at him to emphasise her categorical support for him and his suggestion.

“That’s a terrible idea!” Agatha insisted, scowling at even the notion of it.

“ Yes! ” Rio said again with another determined point toward Teen, staring directly at Agatha in stubborn opposition.

“Well, if you’re all too cool for a practical means of escape!” Teen quipped, evidently annoyed his plan was being disparaged so quickly and so openly.

Any further arguments were promptly cut off by a loud screech, one that sounded far closer than any of the others had before.

“Brooms are great!” Alice said, as she rushed closer to one of the stone banks bordering them, and started to rip a large root from the rock's scarred face. Each of them were quick to follow, hauling different roots and plants together to build a broom for their fellow witch.

Immediately, Agatha started to pull vines of ivy down from a rocky ledge, with the understanding a hexenbesen enchantment worked most effectively when the broom had been decorated with the witch it would carry in mind, as though small emblems or trinkets emphasised the casters desire for the recipient of their gift to be carried safely. And even though Agatha’s memories of Rio had been plucked from her mind like an apple from a branch, she knew just from Agnes’s scarlet-shrouded memories alone, how much Rio adored plants. So, it felt fitting to pull the evergreen vine from it’s home and twine it around Rio’s broom.

Covertly, She glanced over, curious to see what Rio was choosing for her, as it was an unspoken understanding that the two of them would build a broom for the other, without question. To her surprise, or with retrospect it wasn’t a surprise at all, Rio’s eyes were already settled upon her, and sparkling with that same lingering hunger that always seemed to be present whenever her gaze landed upon Agatha's person. Although her hands were busy still, securing Agatha’s broom with strips of dried root, evidently prioritising safety over aesthetics.

Agatha’s heart gave a needy little whimper at Rio’s expression, at the knowledge this witch, a woman she couldn’t even remember , was so clearly devoted to her wellbeing that everything she did was designed to ensure Agatha’s safety; both emotional and physical.

It was a reverent thing to witness and a heavy weight to bear. Not from a place of ingratitude for once, but rather at feeling, quite spectacularly too, that she was unworthy of such depths of piety.

Suddenly, another crying shriek jerked her back to reality and with haste she and Rio completed the hexenbesen ritual and swapped brooms, their hands brushing slightly as they did so, causing a stirring of heat to bloom beneath her skin. A heat she was forced to ignore and tamp down on the moment a member of the Salem Seven leapt at Teen from the rocky outcrop above, throwing them both onto the ground with a violent, resounding thump.

Thinking quickly, Alice used her broom to swipe the feral witch away from Teen, and within a few panicked minutes they were all soaring up toward the sky, with only the wild shrieks of the Salem Seven, and Rio’s gleeful whooping echoing around them, as the ground shrunk away and the broad expanse of The Road’s night sky welcomed them all with a stunning show of twinkling stars and a huge glowing, luminous moon.

The peace that followed felt surreal; almost abstract in comparison to the series of adrenaline-inducing events that had occurred since jolting awake. The gentle hum of laughter and light conversation sailed past Agatha’s ears, carried on the wind as their troupe embraced the serenity of the moment; of an instance of sisterhood that, for the first time since their makeshift group had formed, felt like it possessed a genuine element of covenhood.

Agatha inhaled deeply and allowed herself a brief moment to feel her lungs expanding with fresh air, to centre herself, and steer herself away from the fear the Salem Seven always managed to provoke into motion whenever she heard their feral shrieks echoing on the wind.

Her eyes, almost as though they were the tide and Rio the moon, were drawn back to stare at the green witch from over her shoulder. She managed to capture Rio in a rare moment of respite, where all of that constant tension the green witch held inside, obviously with the effort it was taking to keep all of her secrets so close to her heart, to worry over Agatha, and to make up excuses to sneak off to do whatever deed demanded her time and attention, had been left on the ground below, leaving her, quite simply, a witch gliding on a broomstick, glowing under the moon’s opulent light, with the breeze teasing at her dark hair.

She was, to use a word that didn’t do the scene justice, although Agatha wasn’t sure one actually existed that could encompass it in any case, beautiful. And for a single blinding moment Agatha felt all of the air her lungs had been holding onto, in that subconscious motion of breathing every human possessed, stutter in her throat, causing her to inhale sharply at just how stunning Rio was whilst sailing high above the straggly tree tops of The ever-winding Road below.

A heavy frisson of want started to ache deep inside her body, although this time, it wasn’t sexual. It was an ache to simply know her, to know her in a way that would mirror the devotion she could see so clearly in Rio’s eyes anytime her gaze landed upon Agatha’s face. She wanted so desperately to understand it, she wanted to learn everything about her, and she wanted back what had been stolen from her, this woman and their history, in it’s entirety.

And it was as she was staring at Rio that her mind made another connection.

The mysterious Her Rio was searching for, the one she was hoping the end of The Road would help her find.

The Her was Agatha. Of course it was, it all made so much damn sense. So much so, she almost felt embarrassed that she was only now realising this to be the case. Not to mention the potent level of spitting jealousy she had felt at even the thought of Rio yearning for anyone but her .

Another beat of tenderness pulsed throughout her then, knowing that of all the things in this world Rio could wish for when granted an impossible request, was for Agatha’s mind to be returned to her, and for the memories that had been stolen from her to be released from the scarlet prison they were currently being held in.

Her gaze, which had gentled with undisguisable yearning, was jolted from it’s current focus when Rio’s broom, along with her own, started to twist upside down, before starting to steer downward too, aiming for the leaf-strewn Road below.

“What’s going on?!” Lilia shrieked, clinging desperately to her broom.

“It’s The Road!” Agatha called back, “it’s forcing us down!”

“We’re going to crash!” Alice cried; voice filled with terror.

“It won’t let us leave!” Agatha managed to yell before her voice was drowned out by all of their screams, a mixture of winding wails as their brooms continued to spin down towards the ground with terrifying speed.

All except Rio that is, who was cackling manically, as though she was merely on a day out at a theme park instead of hurtling towards a messy and painful death.

At the last moment, just before they made contact with the dirt, their brooms levelled out and they continued flying forward, only this time skimming the leaves covering The Road’s undulating path, causing them to flurry around them like a stormy autumn’s day with the burst of air their flight made as they shot by.

A dark figure appeared on the path ahead, a figure shrouded in black, with a gaping maw from which thousands of iridescent cicada's emerged in a single heaving mass of clicking wings and scrabbling legs. Without any option to avoid the impact, Agatha led her makeshift coven directly through the storm of insects, and right through the shrouded witch too, who shrieked with fury at their determined resilience to her pursuit.

Their flight ended when the ground finally met them, throwing them all together in a writhing heap of arms and legs.

The screams of the Salem Seven continued to echo all around as Agatha got to hurried feet, only to see the sanctuary of the next trial materialising in front of them. As quickly as possible, they piled through the cabin doorway and when Agatha finally shut it, sealing them inside, a resounding thump on the outside of the door indicated just how close to being caught they had been.

Agatha breathed out an “ oh my god! ” As everyone drooped with fatigue, taking a few minutes to breathe deeply and recover from the furious flight they had just endured.

It took a moment for Agatha to take note of their new location and the style The Road had chosen for them too. She had a moment of recalling Wanda’s hex and how her fake television show would run through the decades, because this entire set, including her new outfit, had been plucked directly from the 1980s. It had evidently been inspired for the 80s penchant for slasher films revolving around groups of friends spending the weekend away in a cabin in the woods.

A large purple shirt was her main article of clothing; comfortable and baggy, covering shorts that were short enough to be hidden beneath the shirt entirely, making it look like she was basically wearing nothing on her bottom half. Lifting a hand she brushed fingers over her hair, relived to feel it’s length had remained the same, only now pulled up into a messy side ponytail.

The rest of the coven had been restyled too, including Rio whose long legs were bare in skimpy shorts. Agatha’s eyebrows rose in silent appreciation as she dragged distracted eyes up the full length of them, admiring the subtle indentation of muscle that became clear with every step she took forward, and the way her tanned skin glowed gold under the yellow lamplight.

“Okay,” she eventually said, having caught her breath and valiantly pushed Rio’s long legs and bare skin to the back of her mind, “all right? Okay. We’re okay,” she reassured them all, just as her fingers found a cicada shell in her hair, which she promptly plucked out to throw on the floor.

Jen, of course, was the first to argue back, “no we’re not! The entire Halloween aisle’s outside waiting for us!”

Agatha drew patience close and ground out a semi-polite response, “and it doesn’t look like they can get in, does it? So, all we have to do is complete the trial and continue on before they can reach us. Okay?”

“How?” Alice shot back, arms thrown up in exasperation, “kiss, marry, kill?”

“I mean…” Rio drawled, sauntering closer to Agatha to tug on her ponytail, “that get’s my vote”.

“Absolutely not,” Jen said sternly, immediately putting an end to that particular train of thought.

“I was joking,” Alice said quickly, counteracting Rio’s agreement, who, now she had been loudly outvoted, simply shrugged and started to saunter around the room, fiddling with random nick-nacks and other things that had been added to the trial scenery, like the background dressing on a film.

Everyone dispersed to hunt for the next clue, each of them still breathing heavily following their hectic escape. Agatha watched them all for a brief moment, eyes jumping from one to the next, until her eyes, quite naturally, were drawn back to Rio, who was currently fiddling with a rubix cube toward the back of the cabin, where the shadows were deep enough to hide the kisses Rio had just joked about. The same kisses, now they had been mentioned, Agatha was determined to claim.

Glancing around to ensure the others were still occupied, Agatha sauntered closer to Rio, raising an eyebrow in obvious amusement as Rio struggled to solve the puzzle cube.

“All of that power bubbling beneath your skin and you’re foiled by a child's toy? ” She couldn’t resist prodding, feeling a spark of that heady, familiar attraction rush through her the moment Rio’s dark eyes shot up to glare at her, genuinely annoyed that she couldn’t beat the cube's colourful riddle.

“It’s obviously rigged,” Rio said through a scowl, as her eyes dropped back to study the toy with petulant venom.

Agatha chuckled, “it obviously isn’t . It’s a puzzle solved through logical thinking”.

Rio’s eyebrows rose in amusement, “oh, is that so? And am I to assume you, Agatha Harkness, are logical enough to solve it”.

“Yep,” Agatha said with pep, whilst rocking from her toes to her heels in overt innocence, “I can show you how to beat it, if it’s annoying you that much”.

Rio held it out for her to take, but Agatha, always the first to grab any opportunity presented to her and twist it with both hands until every single drop of gain could be wrung from it, simply shook her head and refused to take it.

Rio pushed the rubix cube closer, impatiently gesturing for Agatha to take it, “show me,” she said, her tone a command.

“Ooh, demanding aren't we?” Agatha couldn’t help but drawl lewdly as she sauntered even closer to Rio, “I’ll show you how to win the puzzle game, but you’ll owe me for it”.

A knowing smirk started to bloom on Rio’s face, “for showing me how to solve a puzzle cube?” Her voice was low, almost disbelieving that Agatha was intending to take a conversation over a toy, where they both knew it was going.

“Yeah, for solving a puzzle cube,” Agatha parroted mockingly, at last plucking it from Rio’s hand.

Playing along with Agatha’s game, Rio’s smirk deepened, “and what debt will I owe for this demonstration?”

Agatha pretended to ponder it for a short minute, humming quietly as she lazily started to twist the rubix cube around, “hmm, I’ll have to think about my terms, but I should warn you it will be something wicked, and will probably involve you losing all of your clothing”.

Rio laughed in shocked delight, evidently surprised at Agatha’s audacity, which, if they had known each other for as long as Agatha had deduced they must have from yesterday's revelation's, was amusing in it’s own right.

Agatha’s grin broadened as her hands picked up speed, moving so quickly that she solved the rubix cube in a boast-worthy amount of time. Then, as though it were merely a cheap trinket, she held it out for Rio to double-check each side of the cube consisted of a single wall of colour. “Here you go. I held up my half of the deal, so you’re now contractually obliged to hold up yours whenever I decide to cash in”.

Rio took the cube back from her and studied it closely, “I don’t think so. You didn’t even show me how, and you did it really quickly to show off. Seems like a crooked deal to me”.

Agatha gasped in mock outrage, “ crooked? As if I would ever try and trick an innocent witch into doing something deviant”. Sensing another opportunity, she drew closer to Rio and wrapped both arms around her waist from behind, so she could cradle both her hands and the rubix cube with her own, “I can show you like this if that's any better, it will give you an opportunity to really focus on my fingers”.

“ Agatha ,” Rio drawled in warning, immediately picking up on the overtly sexual undertone of Agatha’s words, “what did I say last night?”

Again, Agatha feigned innocence. “I resent the implication that I am doing anything but showing you how to beat this puzzle, just like we agreed,” she whispered into Rio’s ear, denying the claim she was actively attempting to seduce the green witch, which was exactly what she was trying to do. “I was just going to say that the rubix cube is a toy of strategy, pattern recognition, and memory”. Rio melted slightly, her body drooping to rest against Agatha’s as that physical wall she was intent on keeping between them started to tremble and shake, just as Agatha intended. “It could even be argued it’s a lot like having sex with someone”.

Rio snorted at that, obviously aware of what Agatha’s was trying to do but unable to find the strength to pull away. Smirking at Rio's weakness for her, Agatha doubled down, continuing to whisper words into the green witch's ear whilst guiding her hands to mess up the puzzle she had just solved, so they could solve it again together.

“What?” Agatha sighed out slowly, relishing the goosebumps that erupted across the back of Rio’s neck at the feeling of her breath brushing her skin, “you don’t believe me?”

She knew if given enough time to respond Rio would say something sarcastic, something that might ruin the sweet tension she had worked hard to build. So, before Rio could say anything, she continued to speak. “A rubix cube takes patience, just like good sex. To win it you have to pay attention to the patterns emerging, the same way you should pay attention to your lovers body. It takes focus, it takes spatial awareness, it takes a certain level of imagination, as you have to think ahead and consider what positions might work most effectively ”. As she spoke she guided Rio’s hands through the motions of the puzzle, showing her the rhythm of it, demonstrating the times to keep a section as it was and the times it was best to change it, “a lot of twisting and turning is involved, alongside a need for dexterous fingers, and of course…” she hauled the last two sides into position, completing the cube for a second time in as many minutes, “...satisfaction is oh-so sweet the moment you slide into home plate and claim the win”.

She could tell Rio was affected by her efforts because her breathing had quickened, yet just as Agatha was moving Rio’s plait from her neck in order to free up enough tanned skin for her lips to start exploring properly, Alice, the bitch, interrupted the moment with a banal question, “whose trial is this?”

Rio answered, her voice shaky as she staggered from Agatha’s grip and back towards the others, much to Agatha’s growing frustration, until she heard Rio’s answer at least, “it’s Agatha’s trial”.

“How do you know?” Teen asked, voice lilting up with curiosity.

“A blood moon – when the veil between the living and the dead is at its thinnest,” Rio explained, turning to pin Agatha with dark, hungry eyes, her chest still heaving, “who better to commune with the dead than someone who’s put so many in the grave?”

Agatha rolled her eyes and walked on sullen feet back towards the others too, annoyed that she hadn’t managed to steal a single kiss, and had managed instead to make herself even more frustrated than she had already been after last night. Which was saying something.

Rio’s answer, and her ability to deduce that this was indeed Agatha’s trial, didn’t surprise her. The fact she spoke of Agatha’s long list of victims with something resembling reverence however, or even pride at how many lives she had snuffed out, certainly did.

It was becoming the case that for every new thing she learned about Rio, and every time Rio exposed more of herself for Agatha to hungrily recommit to memory, she gained an even deeper understanding of precisely why the two of them had been drawn together in the first place, even without her memories to act as proof. It just all made an awful lot of sense, especially with how complimentary and cohesive their unique brands of chaos blended together, complimenting one another like a sunset across a broad, dark lake; it simply worked, no further justification was required.

“We have to Ouija,” Teen announced from behind her, having scouted a Ouija board from the pile of 80s boardgames. She turned to find him turning the box upside down so the board and planchette fell onto a squat coffee table, surrounded by an array of colourful beanbags.

All of their watches beeped simultaneously, indicating the trial had started. The rest of the witches drew together as Teen read out the rules to all of them, “number one – do not use the Ouija board alone. Number two – do not speak over each other”.

He threw a rather pointed look towards Agatha, even though literally all of them started to argue against that particular point, which she did too, obviously, demanding loudly, “ it’s not written there! Show me that! ”

He silenced them all by continuing to read aloud over the top of their raised voices, ignoring all of their complaints and questions, “three! Do not taunt the spirits”.

Once again, an accusatory glare was thrown her way from Teen, and much to her disgust, everybody else too.

“ What? ” She said, feigning innocence.

He repeated the point to emphasise it, an unnecessary effort in her opinion, before finally finishing the list of rules. All of which, felt more like suggestions rather than strict rules with terrible consequences.

Still, it was clear from the timers starting that this was indeed the correct game to play for this particular trial. So without much fanfare they gathered around the board and started the first round of attempted communication.

A devilish voice on her shoulder whispered a particularly hilarious idea in her ear, one that quickly took shape as she started to push the planchette to spell out a name they would all recognise.

Teen spelled it out for them aloud, “ M.R.S/H.A.R.T ”.

“ Mrs Hart ,” Jen gasped fearfully, before continuing to address her dead neighbour with a voice threaded with nerves, “hey girl, feeling better?”

“How’s your face?” Alice asked lightly, evidently going for a gently banterous approach to communicating with the recently deceased.

“No taunting!” Lilia scolded, which was the perfect opportunity for Agatha to rip the board from beneath her distracted fingers.

“ Your hands! What did you do?! ” Agatha cried, slipping into character as easily as an otter slid into a stream.

Lilia looked horrified, “I didn’t do it!”

Agatha didn’t hear her however, all she heard was the resounding ACTION from the clapperboard in her head, before she started to writhe and shake as though an angry spirit had indeed possessed her.

“ Oh, my, ” she drawled, adopting a strong New England accent and inflecting her words just like Mrs Hart would have done, “ what a journey! There I was, living my tiny life in the burbs, baking casseroles , linking into conspiracy theories on Facebook , drinking before noon , and there you were bringing chills and thrills and bringing on my own early demise! ”

“Listen Mrs Hart...” Lilia said, attempting to appease the angry spirit she thought they had disturbed.

“She’s not Mrs Hart,” Jen corrected.

“She’s Sharon Davis,” Alice supplied.

“I am ,” Agatha insisted, blank smile on her face, “I’m Sharon Davis”.

Jen’s voice was annoyed when she popped her façade, “she’s Agatha”.

“ What? ” Agatha giggled, continuing on with her impression, primarily because she found it funny.

“She’s scared,” Rio told the others, pointing out a truth Agatha would have much preferred stayed a secret, before looking up at her with dark eyes and a challenging smirk, “come on sweetheart, you’re not afraid of something as lame as ghosts are you?”

Now forced to claw around for her dignity, she stretched her neck slightly, “okay, I thought that was pretty good”.

“The clock is ticking,” Rio said, slapping her palm against the cushion beside her with an emphatic motion, “it was a good impression though, I’ll give you that”.

Feeling rushed to do something she really didn’t want to do, Agatha flapped her hands and begrudgingly dropped down to join their circle, “fine. Well let’s get to it. Right?”

Her question preceded a nervous glance at each of their faces, as the reality of the specific door she was opening became even more paramount. It was the not-knowing that made the entire affair far worse to face, because she didn’t know which ghost from her past, of which there were plenty , was currently waiting on the other side, eager to torment her.

Faces ran through her minds eye, flickering from Evanora’s hateful sneer to Nicky’s sweet smile. She would prefer her mother if truth be told, as horrifying as that reunion would be, because the thought of her son being used in such a heinous way was beyond comprehension, not to mention revealing a past that she didn’t want to share with any of them. Except perhaps the green witch beside her, who might well have a claim all of her own to Agatha’s child. But that was a thought for another time, as she placed trembling fingers onto the planchette and started to repeat the same infernal chant again, her voice far more serious this time round.

“ D.E.A.T.H. Death ”.

The next word sent yet another wave of alarm through Agatha's body, sharpening the fear she could already feel buzzing just beneath her skin.

“ P.U.N.I.S.H. Punish ”.

And the answer that followed the next question of “punish who?” Grabbed those first few initial alarm bells and tripled them, as though the bell tower of a grand cathedral had blossomed beneath her ribs and was trying to alert her to Sunday service.

“ A.G.A.T- ”.

She knew where this was going, and she now knew precisely who was waiting for her. For there was only one soul on the other side who would use the word PUNISH in that particular manner. For it was a word Agatha had become intimately familiar with throughout her miserable childhood and even worse teenager years. A word that had been weaponised against her for every single transgression she had ever committed, however light or accidental they might have been at the time.

It was a twisted woman’s twisted weapon, utilising the act of parenting to instil terror in a child for the mere crime of existing.

“ Stop! All right, stop! ” She bellowed pulling herself up to stand on wobbly legs, not willing nor ready to face this trauma, the trauma The Road had no right to pick out from her psyche in order to design it’s sick games.

Agatha had endured too many people prodding and poking through her thoughts and memories over this last year, taking things that should be sacred, stealing moments that should be safe.

Yet the rest of the coven, aside from Rio who had also shot to her feet and was trying to coral Agatha toward another room in order to calm her down, just continued to spell out the word the planchette was spelling again, and again, and again.

“ A.G.A.T.H.A/A.G.A.T.H.A/A.G.A.T.H.A… ”.

“ Stop! ” She heard a voice rasp desperately, not at all aware it was her own with the level of panic that had overtaken her actions and words, scrabbling away from them all, “ stop it! Stop making it do that! ”

Suddenly, that same fear dragged her forward to grab the board and throw it, putting a stop to that horrific chant of her name that was haunting her just as well as any ghost might.

whatever entity had been trying to communicate with them roared in fury, making a rapturous noise erupt all around them, as a swirl of wind so powerful it dragged books from shelves and pillows from chairs swept around the room.

All of them were screaming at one another, each of them afraid and unsure of what to do until Jen pointed out the answer with a disturbing level of relish, “they already told us! Punish Agatha! ”

The noise stopped, yet Agatha’s fear only seemed to grow as the witches she had not yet considered a threat started to circle around her, pointing out her flaws, her mistakes, and insisting to one another that to punish her was the only way to win this particular trial.

Yet, like a light from the darkness, Rio swept through the circle they had formed around her, and with her knife held aloft and pointed directly at Jen, so close that the shining blade brushed the skin of her chin, she placed herself between Agatha and the others.

The cabin seemed to darken as she did so. It almost appeared to pulse with a power not entirely of this world. And it was clear too, that whatever entity had been taunting them from beyond the grave wasn’t responsible for this sharp change in the atmosphere either, for the room suddenly became minutely warmer, as though the ghoul had been pushed away with the mere force of Rio’s anger.

Jen, Alice, and Lilia all took a nervous step backwards, as Rio said two simple words in opposition to their stance, “ Try. Me ”.

Agatha didn’t know what happened beyond that moment though, because in the next instant that same freezing cold she had only moments ago felt recede, suddenly returned and coalesced around her entire body. Everything suddenly went black, and then when her vision returned, it was as though she could only witness the scene through a hole as large as a pinprick. It felt like she had been shunted to the back of her own body, whilst something large, dark, and evil slithered between her skin and bones to take control of her autonomy.

Moments passed in flashes from that point onwards, and it became even harder to orient herself the minute all of the lights went out in the cabin, pitching them all into darkness, because, quite suddenly, she found herself looking at her coven from an entirely different angle, one that a bird may have shared if the roof didn’t block it’s view.

The panicked voices from below echoed through her mind slowly, as though they were travelling through treacle, only to be blocked out by a voice she hadn’t heard in centuries, a voice she had purposefully tried to forget.

“I always knew you were a demon born of human flesh, you beastly child. Look at the monster you have become, Killer-of-Witches”.

If Agatha had been in control of her body she would have shuddered in fear, yet her mother had taken over complete control of her faculties, so all she could do was whimper silently and feel every ounce of terror the child in her had felt when faced with that same hateful voice, the one that had preceded every beating, and inspired every instant of fear she had experienced before she had finally severed that painful, rotting, familial tie.

“Where’d she go?” Lilia’s voice echoed around her, almost in slow motion.

“ Agatha ,” Jen drawled, “let’s talk about this for a minute. We’re sisters in the craft, remember?”

The sound of rattling breathing overpowered all other noise then, growing louder and louder until she realised her own lungs were the cause.

“Does anyone else hear that?” Alice asked quietly, voice fearful.

A light blinded her vision next, as Teen pointed his torch upward jolting her into action to try and push her mother’s spirit out of her body. They dropped to the ground, and as their energies fought for internal control, her body continued to contort and bend horribly.

Teen scrabbled away and her mother zoned in on his face, pushing Agatha’s spine into a crab-like arch with which to pursue him with, as Rio’s voice finally became the loudest in the room, asking in a concerned drawl, “sweetheart, you okay?”

Even Rio’s voice wasn’t enough to drag her back into control of herself though, and within a blinding flash her mother had Jen against the wall with Agatha’s hands around her throat, squeezing the life out of her.

the moment the cabin lights came back on, it was over as quickly as it had started; her body was her own again. Her head was pounding, feeling very much like her brain had been stretched to accommodate an intruder. Her body hurt too, feeling achy and sore from the ways in which it had contorted into positions she had never before attempted, or thought physically possible if truth be told.

She opened her eyes slowly, flinching at the brightness of the lights, and realised she had been flung, quite violently, onto the balcony overseeing the main section of the cabin. The others were all in a panic below, unsure where she had ended up, or if she was still possessed with the spirit of a ghost that had tried to choke Jen to death.

And it was Rio’s voice too, that alerted her to the fact her mother’s spirit must now be physically manifesting, for her answer to Teen’s fearful questions was an emphatic, “ that is a ghost. I hate ghosts”.

Agatha’s hateful mother’s voice echoed out in response, her haughty tone the exact same as it had been in Salem, nearly four hundred years ago, “Evanora Harkness of the Salemites”.

Figuring there wasn't going to be a better opportunity to enter the conversation, Agatha grabbed the balcony’s ledge and hauled herself up, pushing wayward hair from her clammy face as she did so with a shaky hand, “hey mom, it was nice having you in my body for a second there. I’ve never felt so close to you before”.

Evanora ignored Agatha, choosing to address the other’s as though Agatha hadn’t even spoken, “my coven risked everything to kill her. And you fools have willingly joined her”.

“Stop embarrassing me in front of my friends, Mom,” She couldn’t resist drawling, still struggling to keep herself upright on abused muscles.

Agatha wasn't sure if Jen's next question was about her mother or herself, “so what do we do? Do we banish her?”

Lilia’s answered Jen’s question, “emotion ties them to this plane. They have unfinished business”.

“So lets finish her business,” Teen said quietly, before raising his voice to shout at Evanora, “what do you want?”

“You must finish the Witches Road without Agatha,” her mother answered, her voice a detestable command.

“She means punish Agatha,” Lilia deduced quickly.

Her mother was quick to confirm Lilia’s deductions, “leave her, with me! ”

Rio’s voice sliced through the conversation like a sharpened blade through flesh, “no! No way! ”

Agatha crept closer the moment Evanora’s odious stare fell upon Rio, lip curled back almost disdainfully as she swept her gaze from Rio’s feet to her hair.

“Mom?” Agatha drew her mother’s ire back onto herself, “why do you hate me still?”

Her voice was nervous, and it felt, humiliatingly so, as though she was sixteen-year-old Agatha again, anxiously asking her mother the question she had never received an answer to, and no longer the grown woman who had lived entire lifetimes since her mother had tried to kill her, and died for the attempt.

It was a question any child would want to know the answer to; what was so wrong with them that even their parent, the one person whose love should be unconditional, couldn’t find it within themselves to do so.

And it hurt, far more than she would have ever predicted, that even now , three hundred and fifty years since ending her mother’s life in an act of self-defence, that Evanora couldn’t find an ounce of affection or empathy for her child. The child she had despised for merely existing, for having a gift that she didn’t understand, and a hunger for knowledge, that if nurtured, could have brought wonderful blessings to her covens doorstep.

And with her glare as disgusted as it always had been when staring down at her daughter, Evanora answered Agatha’s question without hesitation or pause, “you were born evil. I ought to have killed you the moment you left my body”.

“We have to go,” Jen’s voice cut through Agatha’s heartbreak. A word she despised, for it meant her mother still had the power to do so in the first place.

Yet even Jen’s determined, spiteful voice was drowned out in that moment by every single piece of wood holding the balcony in place cracking in two, by every pillow and beanbag bursting and spilling their feathers and innards out onto the floor in rattling waterfalls, and every light bulb in the cabin flickering violently as Rio drew both her hands up in front of herself, and in a voice preceded by a bassy echo took control of the entire scene with unquestionable ease.

“ Shut your mouths, all of you! ” A pulse of emerald power shot outward from Rio’s body, stunning them all, including Evanora, into silence. Agatha’s jaw dropped as she watched in shocked awe as Rio stepped toward Evanora with deadly intent, “who summoned you here, wraith?”

Rio’s voice sounded ethereal and regal, as though she was stepping out from behind the mask she had been hiding behind, and was finally exposing the true depths of herself at long last. Her mother’s ghost flinched back as Rio stormed closer, though she didn’t fade or disappear, stubborn bitch that she was. If anything, it appeared as though Evanora’s sneer became deeper as she stared at Rio.

“I know you ,” her mother hissed, “I know who you are to my daughter, the sin you shared together. I know how your darkness defiled her body, how your unnatural evil grew inside of her”.

If Agatha had thought Rio looked dangerous before, she had underestimated Rio’s power, for in the next flash of the cabin light’s Rio’s face changed momentarily, appearing ghoulish, almost skeletal in appearance before it was once again flesh and blood. Yet with a single swipe of Rio’s hand, she pushed Evanora’s spirit backwards with a thunderous gale of air, one her mother’s phantom body couldn’t fight as she was pinned against the cabin wall, and a satisfying spark of fear flashed across her ghostly features.

“You dare speak to me in such a manner, witch? Do you have any idea of the things I can do to your soul? Of the places I can send you for all eternity?”

Her mother gasped and her eyes widened with fright as they focussed on Rio’s face, “oh,” she suddenly cried, “oh mercy, I didn’t- I didn’t know who- what - you are!”

Agatha could no longer see Rio’s face, for she had turned her back and was facing Evanora who was still pinned to the wall, yet whatever was written across Rio’s expression must be startling, if not entirely terrifying, for although her mother was already a ghoul and the same colour as a cloud, she paled further still.

Rio’s voice was a harsh growl as she continued to berate Evanora, “you plead for mercy, something you never found within yourself to give to your very own child . You will pay for your sins Evanora Harkness, now that I have finally found you, after years of searching for your wayward soul. Here you are, delivered to me, trapped like an insect beneath a pin”.

Evanora’s spirit seemed to expand at that, her panic causing her to flash in and out of existence, until with a wild pop her physical form devolved into a single orb of light, one that immediately started to shoot around the room, hunting for an exit out of the trial they were all trapped in together.

Realising there was no escape to be had, the orb aimed for Agatha instead, evidently intent on taking control of her body once more in order to force herself off The Road, or maybe to use her body as some form of shield against Rio's anger.

Everyone started to scream and squeal in reaction to Evanora's flight. Lilia jumped onto the sofa as though her mother's sailing soul was a scuttling cockroach, whilst Jen and Alice both started to leap for it the moment it flew past, trying to catch it with their bare hands, although it was a phantom and simply flew right through their flesh.

Then, as if the scene wasn’t chaotic enough, a loud, resounding bang started to echo on the front door, as though whoever was on the other side was using something hard and heavy to try and ram the door down.

Agatha, who had managed to duck and dive every attempt her mother had made to smack her in the face and as a result re-possess her, watched then as Rio drew the blade from her belt and sliced it through the air, right as Evanora was sweeping past, causing her soul to freeze in place and crash to the floor, where it lay sputtering; a sad, flickering orb on old, dusty floorboards.

Rio’s teeth were bared like a creature from a fairy tale, and her voice was an undisputable order as she threw an arm out towards the Ouija board in the corner, on which the planchette had started to spin wildly in an attempt to communicate something else to them.

“What does it say?!” Rio demanded, as she crouched to secure Agatha’s mothers soul with her knife to the floorboards below, pinning the spirit in place even as it wriggled and writhed against it's restraints.

Teen, who had skidded on his knees to read whatever message was being imparted, spelled out a name Agatha had never uttered to anyone in this room, not within current memory at least.

“ N.I.C.H.O.L.A.S/S.C.R.A.T.C.H. Nicholas Scratch! ” He yelled the answer out just as the Ouija board went still and a staircase descended from the wall, as though it had been buried within the structure of the cabin this entire time.

Agatha jerked towards Teen and the Ouija board, feeling the blood drain from her face in both shock at hearing Nicky’s name spoken so bluntly; without the reverence he deserves, but also at the thought her son's soul was here . That Nicky was in this very room, that he was waiting to speak to her.

She didn’t get a minute to even try and communicate with him though, for the front door started to splinter under the strain it was enduring and her mother’s spirit started to flicker, as though she was close to pulling herself free from beneath Rio’s knife.

Rio, who had taken several concerned steps toward Agatha the moment her son’s name had been exclaimed aloud, suddenly jolted to a halt and spun around with anxious eyes to consider the failing door. Then, as though she were their undisputed leader, she started barking orders at all of them, “you need to go! All of you, you need to carry on down The Road and I’ll catch up soon!”

Teen scrabbled to his feet and was quick to take heed of Rio’s demanding tone, corralling Jen, Lilia, and Alice through the hatch. He threw one final nod toward Rio, like a soldier on the battlefield acknowledging their general, before he too fled the room, following after the others.

Agatha felt frozen in place, stuck in a room that her mother had tormented her in, stuck in the same room she had heard her son’s voice in too. Unable to move on from either moment, she felt herself fracture internally at the mixing, queasy mess her emotions were creating in her stomach, like some hideous boiling broth that consisted of her most ardent hopes and her most hateful memories.

“ Agatha! ” Rio said, voice urgent now the door was creaking under the strain, and splinters of wood were flying towards them, through which feral hisses could be heard, “you need to go! Follow the others. I’ll catch up!”

Rio’s final words jolted her back to reality and she found herself frowning in confusion, “what do you mean catch up?! Are you insane?”

She grabbed Rio’s wrist and tried to drag her towards the door, but Rio held firm and gently pulled her fingers from her body, “go! Please, I’ll deal with this lot. I need to do something, something important”.

“What the fuck is so important you can’t run for your life?!”

And much to Agatha’s anger, Rio chuckled as though Agatha had said something foolish, before her expression suddenly softened into something warm yet urgent, “please, just listen to me. Go on ahead. I’ll be right behind you, I just have a job to do first”.

Yet Rio underestimated Agatha's stubbornness, for she quickly crossed her arms and arched an eyebrow, “I’ll help you with whatever little job you have to do. Now come on, let’s get to it before we’re both murdered in cold blood!”

Rio’s face flashed with panic at Agatha's refusal to leave her. Moments later, her expression shifted, turning into a regretful cringe for what she was about to do, “forgive me for this sweetheart,” she said softly before Agatha could determine what she meant, which was to snap her fingers and cast Agatha from the trial; up the staircase, through the door, and drop her by the others, who were all panting and back in their own clothes, in a cloud of emerald smoke.

Agatha was, much like Rio had done outside Lilia’s shop, dropped right on her ass, from which she immediately hauled herself up with a furious roar, before storming back the way they had come from, right past the others, determined to reach the last trial and drag Rio out of there by her hair.

Yet the Road just kept stretching onwards in an ominous undulating wave and the cabin, the cabin that Rio was in, was gone.

XXXXXX

RIO

The moment Agatha was expelled from the room, and even though Rio had spun to face however many of the Salem Seven were forcing their way into the trial, the door gave a final judder and was suddenly still, as though they too had been forced back onto the primary stretch of Road by Rio’s magic.

A dark fear started to bleed throughout her mind then at the thought of sending Agatha to a place the Salem Seven could reach easily, not to mention the fact their feral hunting senses were so in tune with Agatha’s scent, that the moment she was gone they knew their quarry was no longer hiding within the cabin.

Desperate to speed along the process and not feeling particularly charitable towards her wife’s despicable mother, she pulled her knife’s point from the floorboard, keeping Evanora’s soul pierced through it and dangling on the tip, before flinging it violently at the wall, until the physical manifestation of Evanora was once again pinned to the wall, her face drawn and eyes wide with fear at the too late realisation of precisely who she was facing.

“Dark mistress,” Evanora started to simper through a quivering lip. Rio was certain if ghosts could cry she would be sobbing for clemency, “have mercy , oh ancient one. Have mercy on an old woman’s soul”.

Rio didn’t have the patience nor the desire to make this situation easier for her, “you beg for something you never gifted. No, witch, you have earned a fate worse than what lays beyond the veil. Although I do not currently possess the time to decide precisely what it is I want to do with you”.

Within a flash, Rio summoned her Robe; she allowed her flesh to dissolve, and her true face to gleam below the cabin’s dim lights. Evanora shuddered with horror at her appearance as she tried to wriggle free, which was futile for Rio’s power was absolute.

“No, for now I shall store you where I can keep a close eye on you, and when I have the time to decide what punishment befits your crimes, I shall revisit your fate Evanora Harkness of the Salemites”.

And so, without further delay Rio drew an old jar from the never-ending depths of her Robe’s pocket. It was an antique-looking thing, with cloudy glass and algae growing across the threadbare swath of black cloth that sealed it's top.

Rio swept a hand over the jar, the black cloth disappeared, and with a single sharp inhale Rio drew Evanora’s shrieking, clawing, begging spirit into her mouth where she chewed her down to size, before spitting it into the jar for safekeeping. Then, with another brief glide of her hand, the lid was back in place, sealed until Rio decided otherwise.

Within moments she stored Evanora’s soul back within Death’s Robe, and dissolved the evidence of her true self, reclaiming her human face and the outfit The Road had dressed her in for this trial.

Then, on hurried feet, she fled up the staircase, and started to sprint the moment the cabin dissolved around her to reveal the familiar Road, with its twisting path and scraggly trees upon its border, like row's of ancient soldiers, ordered to guard it for all eternity.

Yet, even after running for ten, even fifteen minutes, she couldn’t find the others. There was no sign of any of them, no sign of anything at all, until she came across a scene that caused her blood to chill in her veins, and her black heart to freeze to a block of ice beneath her ribs.

It was Agatha’s locket, her most treasured possession, laying face down in the dirt beside a bubbling pool of thick mud, mud that looked as though it were moving, writhing with someone’s desperate attempts to haul themselves free, even as the mud continued to drag them down, down, down deeper into The Road’s greedy underbelly.

Prophetic Revelations

Chapter Notes

Hi guys - I hope you are all keeping well! <3

It's another long one! And again, I have made a choice here that I am hoping you guys will be pleased with!

As always, thank you so much for the comments/kudos/support! I am stoked you guys are still enjoying this story. Your kind words of encouragement and engagement really do motivate me to keep writing and finally finish this much-longer-story-than-I-ever-planned-it-to-be! :')

So, with all my blabbering complete and out of the way, I wish only to say I hope you enjoy chapter 17 <3

RIO

The mud, in which Rio was elbow deep and clinging with desperate fingers to slippery clothing, smelt, most absurdly of all, of nothing.

It didn’t hold the aroma of earth or loamy mildew as most mud did, it didn't have scraps of leaf litter breaking down within it’s gloopy mass, and it didn’t, on closer inspection, have any earthly energy either; not the kind Rio could sense with a mere brush of her fingers at least.

Yet, as she hauled the body she had found in the depths of this clinging puddle of sludge upwards and out, these observations merely flickered through her subconscious like sparrows, for her conscious mind was far too focussed on finding her witch and dragging her to safety to take any real notice of them.

At first she felt triumph start to quicken beneath her ribs at finding a body still within grasping distance. Yet, when the head of said body finally breached the surface, with a loud, rattling gasp for air, disappointment swiftly drowned out any sense of victory that had started to develop within her heart. For the head she had freed was young, male, and had short curly hair the colour of a starless night.

With a growl she roughly hauled him to the edge so he could drag himself the rest of the way, and within seconds was immediately back on her stomach, with both arms buried up to her armpits in mud searching desperately for another brushing glance of warm flesh or drifting hair.

Her fingers felt naught but slippery mud though, so with another wild roar she slipped even further forward until her head and torso were also wading through the thick gloop, now with even more fervid desperation. Absently she noted fingers gripping the waistband of her trousers; Teen had evidently crawled to freedom and was anchoring her search.

Then finally, there .

A drag of hair against her wrist. Both her hands shot in the direction she had felt the tickling caress and soon found purchase on long hair, then shoulders, and finally underarms which she hooked both her hands under and with all of her strength, which was bolstered by her magic, dragged Agatha to the surface. Teen’s anxious face appeared stark in the blue light from The Road's glowing moon, as he quickly grabbed Agatha from Rio to drag her the rest of the way out of the mud, and onto the leaf-strewn ground beside them.

“ Is she breathing?! ” Rio’s voice was a desperate, fearful growl as she clambered back from the edge to start unbuttoning Agatha’s coat and the top two buttons of her shirt, intent on freeing her chest to check her lungs were still moving.

Rio felt her stomach drop through itself, far too aware that being who she was prevented her from doing anything to stop nature from following its own rules, and it’s rules were simple; if something stops breathing, then that something stops living.

She placed a shaky hand on Agatha's chest and closed her eyes, trying to feel Agatha's lifeforce and that thread every human who had ever lived possessed that linked them to Rio. almost immediately, a pulse of fear echoed in her mind like a rumble of thunder at just how thin Agatha's thread felt when Rio pulled on it; she didn't have long left.

She could feel tears dribbling down her cheeks in a wild torrent as she stared up at Teen, “ do something! Save her! ” She demanded of the pale teenager, a person who could interfere and save a life that was seconds away from blinking out, unlike Rio.

Her voice jolted him to action and he dropped to his knees beside her, as the mud from all three of their bodies started to pool into a slick brown puddle onto the leaves beneath them.

“I was a boy scout and we did like loads of first aid stuff,” he was babbling anxiously even as he started to administer compressions onto Agatha’s chest, before tilting her head up slightly to exhale air into her lungs. He did this three more times with no change. Until, through her tears, Rio watched a new, fierce determination fall across Teen’s brow as he hovered both his hands above Agatha's chest, closed his eyes and started to whisper words Rio couldn’t hear through the pounding fear rushing through her mind.

When his eyes shot open again, they were glowing blue, radiating light the same way Agatha’s shone purple whenever she was in the midst of conjuring a powerful spell. Rio frowned, not expecting Teen to be so capable at handing, nor possess at all for that matter, such a potent class of raw magic. Magic whose signature felt almost familiar , as though his magic was a song built from the notes of another melody, one she had already heard before.

His hands, still hovering above Agatha’s chest, moved upward toward her throat which at last jolted movement from her still body. In a sudden flurry of motion, Agatha’s eyes shot open as she slouched sideways, coughing violently to expel a large clod of mud from between her lips, one that had evidently been blocking her airway.

Her rasping breaths were ragged but not dangerously so, as she held herself up on shaky forearms and took a moment to pant her fatigue away. Rio scrabbled forward on her hands and knees to cradle Agatha’s face and hold it up to study, needing to see her pupils dilate in the moonlight, to feel the proof she was breathing upon her face, to see the perspiration on her forehead, and all the other beautifully empirical evidence that life still thrived within her wife’s body.

“Are you alright?” Rio asked, voice a shaky whisper. Her heart didn’t start to settle until she saw the corner of Agatha's lips quirk up into a tired smirk.

“All the better for seeing you, hot stuff,” she croaked, further proving her wellbeing with an ill-timed joke.

Rio’s responding smile was lost somewhere between relief and fear, a wobbly expression that she was certain made her look even more tragic than the tear tracks still shining on her muddy face.

With a shaky hand she held out Agatha’s broach to her, who took it from her with a relieved exhale and a long slow blink, emphasising just how worried she had been it was still at the bottom of the muddy puddle she had been floundering in. Genuine gratitude blossomed in Rio’s black heart for Teen then, as he slumped backwards onto his ass in the dirt, worn out from the energy he had expelled to save Agatha’s life. Rio met his eye and nodded at him once, a serious, solemn gesture for she was intent on showing him just how sincere her thanks were. He acknowledged her gesture with an unsure, tired smile and a short nod of his own, still entirely unaware he had just earned the respect and eternal gratitude of an immortal deity.

Rio fussed over Agatha for a few moments longer, wiping the thick sludgy mud from her face and helping her sit up properly. Then finally, once she had comfortably reassured herself that Agatha was alive, that she was breathing, that she wasn’t going to die before Rio had found a way to free her memories and reaffirm herself as the love of Agatha's life (as much as Agatha herself would deny such a claim), she threw a curious, demanding glance between the pair of them.

“What the fuck happened?!”

“Ah,” Agatha sighed as she clambered to her feet, and with a grimace, started to haul her mud-caked coat from her body, it having been made from a material that had become heavy and cumbersome with sludge. “Yes, well…” she turned to drop her filthy coat beside her, before using both hands to slick her hair back away from her face, “it was a joint effort”.

Rio frowned, feeling a spike of confused frustration start to burn in her gut at Agatha’s evasiveness, “what the hell does that mean?”

“It means...” Agatha drawled, stepping closer to Rio so she could start swiping some of the excess mud from Rio’s face and shoulders too, “that one of those Salem bitches came out of nowhere and jumped him”.

Agatha tilted her head toward Teen, who had since started searching through the other mud puddles for the rest of their missing coven.

Rio’s frown deepened, “that doesn’t explain how you both ended up in the fucking mud though does it, Agatha?” Rio could hear the frustration and impatience in the tightness of her own voice.

Agatha glanced over her shoulder to ensure Teen was out of hearing range before lowering her voice even further, “turns out our young friend over there has power beyond his own knowledge,” Agatha’s eyes widened in that curious, hungry way they always did whenever she discovered a new potent power source. “ chaos magic ,” she breathed out reverently, voice awed and ravenous. “He has no idea how to control it, probably didn’t even know it was there bubbling beneath his palms. What went down was this: Salemite number one jumps on his back, he starts falling all over the place trying to get her off and stop her from clawing his eyeballs out, when, in a moment of panic, he sends out a big’ ol billow of magic that throws all of us, including himself from the mere fucking force of this thing, off The Road, right into the gloopy mess you found us in”.

Rio’s eyes widened as she recalled the blue power that had crackled over his palms and in his eyes as he saved Agatha’s life, “he saved you with it too, he cleared your airway. Kid's a quick study”.

“ Huh ,” Agatha considered this new information carefully, throwing another almost-maternal look of affection over her shoulder towards the teenager still scrabbling on his hands and knees for their coven-mates, “clever boy, just like his mother". She turned back toward Rio then and winked in that familiarly frustrating way. It was an expression that implied she had figured something out, something that she was going to use and keep to serve herself for as long as she so desired.

Turning, Agatha sauntered over to Teen, tapped him on the shoulder and said something Rio couldn't hear. Whatever it was upset him though, because he was quickly back on his feet to tower over her with that familiar look of righteous indignation on his muddy face.

“His mother?” Rio repeated to herself quietly, frowning for a short moment before, as though the single rock holding back a landslide of understanding had just given way, her comprehension of precisely what Agatha meant, snapped into place within her mind, like a riddle answered through implication alone.

His mother.

His mother .

Of course.

His mother who wields chaos magic with the ease of an archer dispensing arrows.

His mother whose arcane signature was that very melody Rio had found so familiar, just rearranged to serve her son instead.

Her mind span through the realisations, turning back to that horrific day when Wanda had stolen Agatha’s memories of Rio from her mind, and left her trapped behind the façade of Agnes. Of how her hex had disintegrated, how Wanda's screams of anguish could be heard from down the street as her dead husband returned to the grave and her children, children who were born from scratch, much like Rio’s only child, had disintegrated and returned to the swirling mass of the universe.

Or so Rio had thought.

Her head shot up as she studied him. Agatha’s back was turned to her as she and Teen continued to speak, so Rio forced her human façade to fall away, allowing, for a brief moment, her true face to show and her innate power to shine through. As quickly as possible she scanned his body with eternal eyes, studying the blood that thrummed beneath his veins, taking note of the DNA threaded throughout his flesh.

Kaplan . That is his family line.

And yet, here were traces of Wanda’s child too .

She reclaimed her human face and clothing, although not before hauling her Book from her robe, her Book that had every name of the dead or dying scribbled within it’s mildew-stained pages. Flickering through it, she searched for the name Kaplan and paused the moment she spotted a discrepancy.

One she probably should have noticed before now, but one that had been overshadowed by Rio’s personal tragedy of being erased in her entirety from her wife’s mind.

For there, in black ink was the start of an entry, an entry that was incomplete with the horizontal line of the L in KAPLAN dragging off the page; as though the universe’s pen had been pulled forcefully from the parchment before the word could be finished.

And so, there it was, in black and white. And alongside it, Rio’s understanding of the situation, followed by the heart-shattering realisation of what it actually meant .

Because this discrepancy shouldn’t exist, and it was Rio’s universe-bound duty to fix it .

And in order to fix it , she will have to take him .

Laughter broke her out of her silent stupor, drawing her eye back towards Agatha who was gripping both of Teen’s shoulders and staring up into his face with glowing maternal pride. On his face was a spark of bashfulness and a light flush at having his powers celebrated in the way Rio knew Agatha would be celebrating them. Providing this lost, lonely, magical child with all of the reassurance the vicious witch stored away in Rio's robe had never given her wife when she was his age.

Up to this point in her existence, Rio had never experienced a panic attack before.

No, the closest she had come to one before was the moment Agatha had disappeared from beyond her senses, shrouded by the Darkhold and out of Rio’s reach for good.

But now, facing the realisation that she was going to have to do it all over again , that she was going to have to take another child from her wife, well, it just about made her lungs collapse and her heart implode at the maddening injustice of it all.

And what was worse, Agatha didn’t even know that this wasn't the first time Rio had been forced to do such a thing to her. Nor the very reason why she had to in the first place, considering Rio’s true identity was something she hadn’t yet disclosed.

Perhaps this was her punishment for falling in love with a mortal witch. Perhaps this was simply the pattern she has been cursed to repeat until Rio finally understood that love, or at least the human definition of the thing, wasn’t something she had any right to feel or experience. That perhaps her feelings, these ever-growing, vibrant sensations that bloomed between her ribs like vines of ivy whenever she felt Agatha’s warmth beside her, or felt the radiance of her smile upon her face like the sun's warm beam on a cold day, were merely an anomaly of the universe, something that should never have been possible; Death’s very own mutation of matter and purpose.

Perhaps this was indeed Rio’s fate, the ultimate cosmic joke; that she was to be poisoned and ruined by the one thing all the poet’s of the world agree had the power to transcend even her dark veil; love.

“Rio!” Agatha snapped impatient fingers in front of her face. She quickly jarred back to reality to find she had been bracketed on either side by Agatha and Teen, both of whom had been trying to get her attention for the past minute or so, “finally,” Agatha quipped, “were you sleeping with your eyes open just now? That's like super creepy if you were. Even for you".

Rio simply stared at her with wide, panicked eyes, fixating on her smiling face, an image she would never get to see again after she did what she had to.

Agatha however, who was entirely unphased by Rio’s strange mood, simply pointed at Teen as though she was a magician and Teen her glamourous assistant, “show her, Teen”.

He grinned, looking proud as punch as he said, “my name is Billy Kaplan”.

Ah there it is , Rio thought to herself, feeling her stomach plummet at the confirmation of her theory; for the seal that had concealed him from all witch-folk was no longer required now Agatha had figured out his identity, confirming he was indeed Billy Maximoff in William Kaplan's body.

Agatha snorted at Rio’s lack of reaction, “tough crowd”.

It was clear she had just assumed it was another one of Rio’s quirks though, for she quickly spun in place and started to saunter down The Road as though she wasn’t still covered in mud, hands in her pocket and chin tilted up arrogantly, “come on, lets go find the next trial”.

Teen started to walk after her but halted the moment his eyes fell on the bubbling puddle of mud beside them, “what about the others though? Shouldn’t we keep looking for them”.

Agatha spun and whilst still walking backwards, shrugged flippantly, “even witches can’t hold their breath for that long, kid. If they’re in there, they’re goners”. She then gestured for him to follow her, as though she hadn’t just implied half of their coven had just met a grisly end, and turned to continue walking down The Road’s long winding path, “come on, last one to the next trial is a loser”.

Rio started to follow after her, deciding it was wiser to bide her time, aware that taking Billy will have to be a strategic moment, one that limits the pain of the action for all involved. Including herself.

She had to think it through, and she had to be tactical about how she should reveal this reality to the both of them. She would need Billy to come willingly after all, for the risk of his wayward soul taking flight the moment he realised she was onto him was too great.

And Agatha… well Agatha was a whole other battlefield. One that her own heart was in the centre of; unarmed, unshielded, and no doubt mere hours away from being crushed beneath the weight of her own dark duty.

She drew to a halt beside Billy, who was still standing beside the mud, unsure of which direction to take or which part of himself to follow; his brain which evidently wanted to follow after Agatha, or his heart, where his loyalty to the others lived.

Deciding to throw him a bone, primarily due to the gratitude she felt for him helping Agatha in a way Rio couldn’t, she nodded her chin toward the puddle of gloopy mud, “they’re not in there”.

He looked surprised that she was talking to him at all, then eager as what she had said registered in his mind, “they’re not? How do you know?”

She shrugged, feeling the weight of the universe and her duty balancing on her shoulders like rusty anchors, dragging her down into a familiar darkness.

“I just do,” was the only answer she would provide, before passing him to follow after her wife, her wife who she was certain would truly, without question, despise her for what she was about to do.

AGATHA

The next trial was perhaps, the most cinematic of them all. The scene was a majestic one, regal even; a soaring turret of dappled stone, lit only by the flickering amber glow of torches, with a single table standing in the centre of a circular room. A deck of tarot cards were set upon it’s varnished surface, waiting for the fortunes hidden between cards to be revealed and made true.

This was, quite obviously, Lilia’s trial.

Which would have been evidenced by the tarot cards alone, yet even more weight was added to her theory by the fact all three of them had been dressed in the costume of a famous witch from modern day cinema or television. A portrayal Lilia, over the last few days, had driven home how much she despised, by the endless rants on the appropriation of witch culture.

Agatha span, enjoying the twirl of her coattails and the flare of her fitted purple trousers beneath her new tailored jacket. Her skin was green, so it was pretty obvious who The Road had cast her as; the Wicked Witch of the West. A witch so evil the entirety of Oz celebrated her demise.

She glanced down to take in her outfit, noticing just how closely it resembled a school uniform, wondering momentarily why it didn’t consist of the black robes made famous in the original film.

Ah . Suddenly the penny dropped. So she was Elphaba; a misunderstood witch who was demonised beyond measure, yet who, although misconceived, had a heart of gold.

She tried to swallow the snort of derision that tried to escape at that particular comparison before turning to study Teen and Rio, curious to see who they had been cast as in this unusual play.

Teen was wearing an elaborate costume primarily crafted from black leather and dark blue velvet. The costume alone was pretty ambiguous, yet when paired with curved horns and exceptional eye make up, it was clear he was dressed as Maleficent.

Unsure but unbothered to find out why he had been cast as that particular witch, her eyes continued on toward the only other figure in the room. And the moment they locked on target, Agatha felt the muscles keeping her jaw in place loosen from awed surprise, leaving her standing there gaping, without any pretence or shame, directly at Rio.

Agatha didn’t know which famous witch she had been styled after, nor did could she say what piece of media her image had been stolen from.

All she knew was Rio was standing in the centre of the room in a blood red, fitted dress that was as low-cut in the chest as her 70s outfit had been. In contrast to the tight bodice, the sleeves were airier and draping away from her wrists in a triangular style that reminded Agatha of the type of dress a queen from a fairy tale would wear. Rio's hair had grown significantly, and now reached her hips. It was gently waved, with two plaits pulled away from her face and curled together into an elaborate knot on the back of her head, and around her throat was a decadent choker, with a centrepiece that looked similar to Agatha’s own broach in size and style.

All of that was enough to grab Agatha’s attention, yet most shocking of all, was the fact Rio’s dark hair was now a rich auburn, a colour that complimented her tanned skin and her dark eyes almost too well.

“ Holy shit ,” Agatha finally managed to mumble. Her legs started to move without conscious thought, taking her closer to Rio who was running curious hands over her fitted bodice and grasping the ends of her now visible hair to study it’s new colour. Agatha drew to an unsteady stop in front of her, causing Rio to glance up with curious eyes the moment she did so, as though unsure as to what it was Agatha was staring at.

So, in order to make her thoughts clear and avoid any misunderstandings, she repeated her earlier sentiment of, “ holy shit ”.

“You good?” Rio asked, taking a step closer to tilt Agatha’s chin up so she could see her face from beneath the brim of her witch’s hat.

“Fuck me Vidal, you look good ,” Agatha husked, starting to circle Rio so she could get the view of her in that dress from the back too.

“I do?” Rio asked, sounding genuinely intrigued as she started to spin in a circle as well, trying to catch a glimpse of herself like a dog might chase its tail.

“Yeah,” Agatha said, voice husky as her eyes continued to trace up and down Rio’s body, “ you do ”.

Rio smiled, although Agatha was quick to notice that it wasn’t like her other mad grins, for it didn’t brighten her entire face. Instead, it looked as though something was bothering her, something that had taken root inside her thoughts and started to rot, preventing her joy from blooming to it’s full potential.

Agatha frowned for a moment before an answer became clear. Rio was probably, much like Teen, grieving the loss of the others. So, in a quick bid to distract her, Agatha tapped a finger against her own chin as she studied Rio once more, this time from a more analytical perspective rather than a lustful one.

“I have no idea who you are supposed to be,” her brow furrowed. “Billy!” She called out, not removing her gaze from Rio's own, “any ideas who she's supposed to be? I’m assuming this particular witch is from this century, which is why I don’t know her”.

Teen, who had been studying his cheekbones in the mirror, turned towards them. His head tilted curiously for a brief moment before his eyes widened with realisation, “aah, I know who she is! She’s Melisandre from Game of Thrones!”

” Melisandre? ” Both Agatha and Rio parroted simultaneously.

“Yeah!” Teen’s excitement made it clear he was a fan of the show, “she’s this badass bitch who can cast fire and shadows! Oh yeah, and she can resurrect corpses and like give birth to monsters”.

Rio’s eyes gleamed in that wild, feral way that made Agatha’s heart pound, which it did immediately, as she murmured a satisfied, “neat”.

Teen gestured towards the table in the centre of the room, “it’s a tarot challenge! I know this… kind of”.

The three of them gathered around the table. Teen picked up the deck of cards as an anxious expression spread across his face. “I’ll read for one of you two, I guess,” he said, looking between Agatha and Rio.

“Read for her,” Rio ordered quickly, almost suspiciously so. Agatha turned and stared at her through narrowed eyes from below the shadowed brim of her hat.

“Always so quick to dart out of the spotlight, aren’t you?” Agatha drawled, “afraid we’ll discover something dark and dangerous about you, Vidal?”

Rio’s cheek twitched as though she wanted to laugh at Agatha’s accusation. “Something like that, Harkness,” she murmured before pulling the seat out for Agatha to sit, “please, humour me”.

Agatha hummed petulantly and took the offered seat, although she ensured her narrow-eyed glare remained fixed on Rio suspiciously.

”You’re lucky I’m only ever interested in hearing about myself," she said through a scowl before turning back to face Teen, who had sat himself opposite her and started to shuffle the deck of cards. “Go on then,” she spread a dramatic hand over the table, “let’s hear how my future is panning out, oh great and mysterious Teen”.

He gave her a long-suffering stare from across the table as he pulled a card from the deck, “you do know you can say my name now, right?”

Smiling brightly, she ignored his question and slapped an impatient hand on the table, “come on psychic Sally, time’s-a-wasting”.

With a roll of his eyes, Teen turned the first card over and studied it with a frown, “the horse drawn carria-”.

“The chariot? ” She drawled pointedly.

He glared at her, prompting her to raise both eyebrows at him in condescending disbelief and say, “it’s literally written on the card”.

It was his turn to ignore her now, as he continued on with her tarot reading, “right, so obviously you’re leaving somewhere behind, and you have these sphinxes with you, and they represent your… your mysteriousness”.

“You have a real gift,” Agatha commented, voice as dry as a bone left in the desert.

“This card hasn’t really come up much for me,” he sniped before slapping it down into one of the empty square’s that had been carved into the table’s surface, evidently for this very purpose. However, the moment the card touched wood, a swooshing sound echoed around them, followed swiftly by a violent clang as a sword fell from the ceiling, driving itself with the force of it’s fall into the wooden floorboards, triggering as well, the ceiling to start dropping closer inch by ominous inch.

Both she and Teen jumped. Rio however, ever unfazed, simply drifted toward the sword to tug it from the floor, where she then started to swing it around in precise, well-formed stances.

Agatha, who never found it hard to stare at Rio doing anything, leered over her shoulder to admire the flex of Rio’s arm muscles as she swung the sword above her head and mimed driving it into an imaginary foe.

”You have excellent form,” she husked, before yelping in pain the moment Teen kicked her in the shin under the table.

”Concentrate!” He snapped. Obviously the stress of the sword-covered ceiling slowly lowering itself towards them was getting to him.

She scowled at him in warning, but relented and gestured impatiently for him to draw another card.

”Seven of Swords”.

She gave a pointed glance toward Rio who was still throwing the sword around and then at the ceiling, “at least you’re on theme”.

“I know this one!” Billy chirped, far too proud of himself, “It’s about deception and betrayal!”

She hummed, “check, check”.

He glanced back at the card and frowned, “but it’s reversed… so that means the opposite”.

Rio came back to stand beside them, having slid the sword into the belt of her dress to rest beside her knife, “it mean’s she’s telling you the truth,” she told him, before shrugging “at least this time”.

Immediately picking up on the gauntlet of teasing Rio had set down before him, Teen smirked and said “well, that can’t be right,” before slapping the second card on the second square, causing, once more, a razor-sharp sword to drop to the floor with an ominous clang.

Having had quite enough of being both the object of their mockery, and existing under the threat of a slowly descending death, Agatha snatched the deck from Teen’s hand, “ my turn . Tarot is a con like any other! There’s no magic to it, there’s no skill!” She started to explain, whilst shuffling the cards in order to redraw them for him instead.

“That’s not true!” Billy argued, “It’s about intuition, knowing which card to pull. And it’s about interpretation, divining their meaning”.

“Kid has a point,” Rio commented lightly, as though their discussion was about little more than the weather.

Choosing to ignore them both, Agatha said instead, “ eenie meanie miney mo! ” Before throwing the first card she pulled from the deck down onto the table with a dramatic smack.

A sword clanged into the floor beside them, far closer than the previous two. Rio collected it as she had the first, sliding it into her belt to rest alongside the others as Agatha started slapping card after card down onto the table, causing sword after sword to drop from the ceiling. One of the cards would end up in the right place eventually, it was merely a matter of trial and error.

“ Slow down! ” Teen cried, fearfully looking at the ceiling, before staring at Rio with wide eyes and raised eyebrows, imploring her to do something to stop Agatha’s tarot tirade. Yet she simply shrugged at him, before pulling a few more swords from the floor, completely at ease in a room primed to kill her.

Agatha chose to ignore him again, right up until the moment a sword fell directly where he had been sitting. Fortunately, it missed him by a grazing inch, as he threw himself to the floor just in time to avoid being impaled.

“Your turn is going great,” he quipped sarcastically from the floor, clinging onto the table with scrabbling fingers.

“This is a numbers game,” she told him flippantly, “we keep at it until we get the right cards in the right spots, or the ceiling runs out of swords!”

“I’m not sure how much math you did back in Salem-” Teen started to say, voice sullen and filled with teenage frustration before Rio interrupted him.

“Literally none, she refused to do any arithmetic. Claimed it was the devil’s work and that it would turn her into a witch,” Rio told him with a snort of amusement at the memory.

Agatha scowled, feeling annoyance bubble in her stomach for several reasons.

The first; Teen and his unrelenting sarcasm.

The second; Rio’s eagerness to pull back the curtain on the reputation she had worked so hard to build over centuries .

And the third; the fact Rio could recall these moments from their shared past with ease, a past that was still little more than a black hole swirling through her hexed mind.

“We still have time!” She growled, pointing to the hourglass with snappy irritability.

”I wish Lilia was here,” Teen groaned.
