And as though he had summoned her with his yearning alone, a cupboard door swung open spewing Lilia, Jen, and Alice out to land in a heap on the varnished floor.

” You’re alive! ” Billy cried joyously, running over to wrap each of them up one by one in a warm embrace. “Thank god,” he sounded near tears as he squeezed his grip around Alice’s shoulders who squeaked at the tightness of his arms, “I thought I’d killed all of you guys!”

“Relax baby, we’re cool,” Lilia reassured him, “young witches lose control of their power all of the time,” she eyed him closely, looking, if Agatha didn’t know any better, like an excessively proud parent, “your magic’s got a kick to it kid, you should be pleased”.

“A kick; a kick in the head more like,” Jen drawled, not quite as forgiving as Lilia or Alice over their trip through a muddy portal. Although, Jen's attention was promptly stolen by the outfit she had been dressed in for this particular trial.

“What the fuck,” she scowled and pinched the edge of her ragged robe, causing a few of her grey locks to fall over her shoulder into her eyeline, “ what. The. actual. Fuck. Is. This ”.

Spinning she stared at Lilia, before throwing out a petulant hand, “so you get Glinda, and I get the Evil Queen?! And not even the hot Evil Queen, oh no, I get Crone Evil Queen?! ”

Her attention fell on Alice who had joined Rio in admiring the many swords she had collected from the floor. Agatha was unsure why Rio had done so, for it wasn’t like they could transport them all even if they wanted to. Yet Rio’s quirks were, as always, as endearing as they were curious, and Agatha couldn’t deny the fond smile that bloomed on her face as she watched Rio show Alice just how well balanced the swords were, both of them completely unaware they were the current focus of Jen’s jealous upset.

”Oh for fuck’s sake! Rio got Melisandre! And Alice got Nancy Downs! ”

Jen’s outrage caught Agatha’s attention, and she couldn’t resist studying Alice either, who had been dressed in a short black skirt, a white shirt, and a baggy leather jacket. It was an outfit that was purely 90’s, one that was made complete with dark eyeliner and a studded choker.

All in all, Alice looked hot. And Agatha, ever the faithful agent to chaos and all she entails, couldn’t resist whistling in lusty appreciation, eager to show Alice just how well her new look suited her, whilst also managing to annoy Jen too. Simple pleasures and all that.

“Looking good Alice,” Agatha drawled through a smirk which was directed at Jen, whom The Road had dressed in a large baggy robe and gifted a monobrow.

Jen, polite as ever, pointed both of her middle finger's at Agatha who couldn’t resist blowing her a kiss in reply, “don’t be jealous Kale. Only one witch in this coven has a one way ticket to my bed, and her name rhymes with Cleo Ridal”.

Jen snorted with disdain at Agatha’s taunting, as Lilia stepped toward the table to study the tarot reading they had been in the middle of ruining, when the others had burst through the cupboard door.

“Who massacred this spread?” She asked, judgement plain in her voice.

“ He did! ” “ She did! ”

Both she and Teen pointed at one another simultaneously.

Lilia rolled her eyes and started to pluck all of the cards off the table to reshuffle the entire deck, “who’s the querent?”

“You mean the subject?” Teen asked, ever the eager student, “me, I guess I’m the queer-ent”.

Agatha’s forced fake chuckle was drowned out by Rio and Alice's genuine ones.

“The querent shuffles and cuts,” Lilia told him, passing the deck to Teen who quickly did as ordered before passing them back to her.

“Now please ask your question,” she told him, settling herself into one of the chairs with the regal grace of an ancient monarch.

“How are we gunna get out of here?” Agatha asked loudly. It was, after all, the most obvious and important question to ask in their current situation.

Lilia glared at her, “Teen must ask”.

“ Ask her how we’re getting out? ” Agatha whispered at him across the table very loudly.

“It must be vital to his journey on Earth!” Lilia scolded her, just like a teacher would berate a misbehaving child.

“I’d say it’s pretty vital,” Agatha quipped, pointing at the ceiling which was still inching ever closer to all of their grisly deaths.

Teen looked between them both for a moment before asking the question that had evidently been playing on his mind, “am I William, or am I Billy?”

“That’s a very good question,” Lilia told him kindly, before explaining what each card’s placement meant. The reading continued for several minutes, although even Lilia’s cards, whilst being read and placed correctly, caused the swords to continue falling from the ceiling. Then suddenly, as though someone had opened her mind and plucked her consciousness from it, Lilia sagged in her seat and fell silent.

“ Er ,” Agatha pointed at her, glancing at Jen and Alice who had both drawn closer to Lilia to check she was alright, “the lights appear to be on, but no one is home”.

“Lilia,” Jen said, shaking her shoulder impatiently.

“Don’t be so rough with her,” Teen scolded, grabbing Jen’s wrist to pull it away from Lilia’s shoulder.

“She was doing this in the tunnels...” Alice explained, ever the voice of reason and calm, “...kept talking about you...” she nodded at Teen, “...about the trial, about bookshelves, about gaps, flashes in time, and the Scarlet Witch”.

“The Scarlet Witch? ” Agatha growled, prowling closer, “Lilia knows about him?”

Alice nodded, shrugging nonchalantly, “we all do now”.

Billy grinned sheepishly, “can’t help who your parents are and all that”.

“God, don’t I know it,” Alice said sadly, thinking of a misunderstood mother who she had despised for far too long.

Agatha however simply scowled and pointed out, “you all had the pleasure of meeting my mother”.

Teen and Alice’s responding grimaces spoke a thousand words.

Agatha watched then as the card Lilia had been holding in a limp hand slipped from between lax fingers and landed on the table, causing the sword directly above her seat to come screaming down, right towards her still body.

“ Shit! ” She hissed, and without prior thought for self-preservation, an anomaly in Agatha’s long life, she found herself leaping forward and pushing Lilia from her seat before the soaring blade could run her through.

“ Agatha! ” Lilia cried, apparently back in the room from her vacation to wherever-the-hell-she-just-been, “ what are you doing?! ”

It was obvious Lilia was talking about the fact she had ended up sprawled atop her after Agatha's act of selfless heroism, “did you not see imminent impalement in your future?!”

Being good really was overrated; you save a life and all you get in return is grief, she couldn't help but think as Lilia groaned in irritation and began to push her off and onto the floor with impatient hands.

“ Lilia! ” Agatha yelped as she was shunted sideways to land on her ass, “I’m trying to help you!”

“ Yeah, yeah, yeah ,” Lilia drawled sarcastically, managing to finally haul herself to her feet, a motion not made any easier by her large, fluffy skirts.

Rio approached Agatha, who was still sat on the floor with a disbelieving, resentful expression on her face at Lilia’s lack of gratitude. With a small smirk, Rio held a hand out to help Agatha off the floor as she said, “that was very brave, sweetheart”.

“I know,” Agatha pouted, annoyed no one was giving her act of selflessness the appropriate attention or praise it deserved.

Rio tried to release her hand, but a sudden, overwhelming desire to keep her close came over Agatha, so she tightened her grip instead and hauled Rio into her side, so she could wrap a possessive arm around her waist.

“You know...” she couldn’t resist whispering into her ear, even though both of their eyes were still trained on Lilia, who had started shuffling the cards with a newfound intensity, “...I didn’t think I had a thing for redheads until right now . I thought Wanda had set that particular boat on fire as it set sail, but seeing you like this...” she gave the ends of Rio’s hair a teasing tug, “...well, it’s doing wonderful things for me”.

This was the point in the conversation that Rio would normally smirk and whisper something devilishly wicked into her ear, yet Rio’s responding smile was like a small flame flickering in a furious gale; weak and hopeless.

Agatha frowned, tugging Rio back towards her the moment she tried to look away and back towards Lilia, who was now giving herself the reading? Which did make sense in some warped, of-course-The-Road-would-design-it-like-this sort of way.

“Hey, what is it? What’s wrong?”

Rio sighed; a sound crafted from sadness. Her eyes flickered across Agatha’s face, as though she was trying to absorb every minute detail before she shook her head, “nothing”.

“No, don’t do that,” Agatha ordered, refusing to be locked out of Rio’s thoughts in the same way she was locked out of her own, “tell me what’s wrong”.

Rio’s eyes started to shine with unshed tears as her mouth dropped open, as though she was uncertain of what was about to come out, “I-”.

She didn’t get an opportunity to answer however, for screams of fear from the others dragged their attention onto the ceiling which was still moving towards them, and getting nerve-wrackingly close.

Lilia though, was frozen in place, a single card held above the final space and her eyes set on Rio with grim awareness, “Rio is…”

“Lilia!” Alice cried, grabbing the card from Lilia’s hand to slap it down on the table, stopping the ceiling from moving any closer and impaling them all.

Lilia didn’t flinch at Alice’s tone, nor did she celebrate the fact she had successfully beaten her trial. No, instead she simply continued to stare at Rio. Then she swallowed, almost nervously, “Rio…” Lilia's voice trembled from what sounded like partial fear, and partial reverence, “you… you’re…”

Agatha felt Rio stand taller beside her as she swept closer toward the divination witch, “I am…”

She didn’t sound angry or insulted, if anything she sounded gentle, speaking like a mother might to a child who had just learned that the earth was round or the sun was a star. “It’s alright,” Rio said softly, “you can say it, you can tell them”.

Lilia gulped, eyes scanning Rio’s expression for any hint of deception before nodding once and turning to address the others, “Rio, our green witch, she is the green witch”.

Agatha frowned, not completely understanding the weight of Lilia's revelation, before Jen gasped sharply and took an uneasy step backwards, “you can't mean?”

“Yes,” Lilia said to Jen before turning to stare at Rio with wonder, “she’s-”.

Lilia was cut off by Alice, who in her stoic, calm voice provided the answer for all of them, “Death”.

The moment the truth was revealed Rio spun, eyes set upon Agatha’s face, watching intently for her reaction, which was to pause for a moment as her synapses caught up to her ears and the true depths of what she had just heard came into sharp clarity.

“She’s what?! ” Agatha hissed, storming closer to Rio with narrowed eyes, “you’re what?! ”

And Rio, fool that she was, simply threw both hands up into a sad impression of jazz hands and said through a limp smile, “surprise”.

Agatha reeled back, throwing a palm to her forehead and knocking her hat to the ground as one of those familiar, aching pains shot through her mind at the knowledge she had just discovered, knowledge that must match the memories Wanda’s magic was still working so hard to hide from her.

Thankfully, the pain didn’t last long and Agatha was left staring at Rio, gaping in awe at the fact she, Agatha Harkness, had not only managed to pull one of the most disarmingly attractive people she had ever had the pleasure of staring at, but also, an immortal deity .

“ Holy shit ,” she breathed, running ravenous eyes up Rio’s body, as understanding and realisations fell into place. This was the reason Rio had refused to kiss her until she knew Agatha wouldn’t steal her magic, this is why Rio never feared for her life in these hellish trials, this was why she disappeared after every single death or brush with it on The Road, this was why she seemed so damn curious about such mundane human things like a fucking rubix cube ; because she wasn’t human.

It was clear that everyone, including Rio, were all holding their breath awaiting an eruption of anger that never came. Yet all Agatha did instead was smirk, a particularly devilish, wolfish expression as she drawled, “well, I’m certainly glad to learn my type hasn’t changed, even with all the brain damage. I always had a thing for the dangerous ones, after all”.

Rio’s mouth opened to reply, but whatever she was going to say, Agatha never got hear, because those same eery whispers that had woken them the night before started to echo around the tower.

The scurrying of rat’s feet, the ruffle of feathers, and the sound of a snake’s belly slithering along stone joined the ominous voices, as Lilia pointed toward the exit that had been revealed the moment the final card had been laid.

“The seven. They’re here! Quick, everyone in the iron maiden!”

They didn’t hesitate to do as ordered. Agatha went first, her hand this time firmly wrapped around Rio’s wrist, refusing to let her stay behind again as she had in the cabin. A pointless thing, considering her… girlfriend? Wife? Ex? (She still wasn’t entirely sure what they were to one another officially), was apparently Death incarnate.

Yet the moment she heard Jen yell “no!” from the stair below her own and the maiden door slam shut, with all of them except Lilia on the side of safety, she realised what Lilia intended to do.

“ Lilia! ” Jen cried, banging both her fists on the door.

“Ah no, RIP Lilia,” Agatha sighed and waited a solemn moment with a hand over her heart, before immediately trying to turn and carry on up the stairs. Yet, she was halted by Rio who was still stood in place watching Alice, who had quickly snapped into action.

“Jen, get away from the door,” Alice ordered, as she placed both of her glowing palms against it’s handle and pushed it open with a roar. The metal screamed as it was pushed away from the doorframe, before with a final cry through gritted teeth, Alice managed to shunt it open.

The scene that met them wasn’t the one they had left, for everything inside the tower was now upside down.

Three black shapes went sailing past the doorway; three of the Salem Seven falling to their deaths which were quicker than they deserved if the grim squelch of metal through flesh was any indicator.

Then, like a petal from a cherry blossom drifting on the breeze, Lilia dropped from the candelabra she had been clinging too. Her eyes were closed, her limbs were relaxed; the old witch was apparently ready to walk into Rio’s cold embrace.

Her peaceful descent to the end of her life was intercepted however by a current of yellow magic, one that acted as a trampoline and caught her mid-air, causing her to bounce inelegantly and her dress to flop over her face the moment she made impact with a grunted, “ umph! ”

“ Jen !” Alice ground out through gritted teeth, “conjure a rope and guide her in! I don’t know how long I can hold this for!”

“I’m bound!” Jen’s panicked voice echoed around them, and in that moment Agatha felt a strong desire for her own magic, a desire that, for once, wasn’t entirely rooted in self-gratification, but rather the ability to actually help someone else.

“ Aah !” Alice roared, eyes clenched tightly together with concentration to ensure her power didn’t waiver and drop Lilia to her Death, who had managed to scrabble onto her knees and was trying to crawl her way across Alice's field flickering magic towards the open doorway.

“I can help Alice!” Teen said, within moments he had closed his eyes and conjured a rope the colour of midnight. Without delay he tossed it to Lilia how a lifeguard would throw a safety ring to a drowning man, “Lilia! Grab hold, we’ll pull you in!”

Jen, who couldn’t conjure anything but who could still pull, was the first to grab hold of the rope and start helping Teen drag the rope and Lilia across the room and towards the doorway. She turned her head, even as she continued to pull and growled at Rio and Agatha, “ help us! ”

Rio paused for a moment, as though considering whether this would break some sort of universal rule before, after a single shrug, she too grabbed hold and started to help.

“ Agatha! ” Jen cried, just as Alice’s power field failed and Lilia dropped out of sight of the door. An unusual strike of fear resounded through Agatha’s chest at that image, of Lilia crawling to safety only to suddenly disappear from view, and before Agatha knew it, she too had grabbed hold of the rope, which thankfully still had a weight upon it’s end, and started to haul backwards with the others, cinching Lilia up the wall of the tower, until two scrabbling hands suddenly appeared upon the ledge from where Alice was able to grab her under the arms and drag her all the way to safety.

They all fell backwards in a domino line then; Lilia onto Alice, Alice onto Teen, Teen onto Jen, Jen onto Rio, and finally Rio onto Agatha. Which, if it was just Rio’s lovely body pressing into hers, she wouldn’t have minded, like at all. However, with the weight of her entire coven pressing down on her, she ended up slapping furious hands against any shoulder and arm she could reach, “ get off! Oh my god, get off of me! You’re the heaviest coven I’ve ever not killed, get off! ”

This, apparently, was the funniest thing all of them had ever heard, because none of them moved off of her as she demanded, instead they all started to cackle loudly, undoubtedly as a result of skimming yet another near-death experience and the adrenaline such experiences inspired.

“It’s like I said…” Lilia said, the relieved smile on her face could be heard clearly in her voice, even as she leaned back against the warm bodies beneath her own, using them all as an impermanent chaise lounge, “three of pentacles; collaboration, community, singular voices waiting to harmonise”.

She rolled then to stare at them all, her eyes shining with affection, affection that even Agatha felt warming her cold heart, much to her own disgust, “I needed you. My coven”.

And as those prophetic words settled even more profoundly between them all, considering they had only been able to save Lilia through the combined efforts of the entire group, Agatha found herself feeling, perhaps for the first time in her life, what it might be like to have a place amongst a group of witches, to truly know, and understand, what the word coven actually meant.

A sentimental silence descended then as they all considered Lilia’s words carefully, although it only lasted a few seconds, as Agatha was sure her right lung was about to pop, “alright, seriously now, get the fuck off of me”.

They finally did so, each of them still chuckling under their breath at the fact the great and infamous Killer-of-Witches Agatha Harkness had been their makeshift landing pad.

Agatha got to her feet with disgruntled grace, brushing her hands down her mud-stained trousers and throwing her stringy, filthy hair over her shoulders proudly, as though it wasn’t stuck together with grime.

“Well, now that little love-fest is over. We need to keep moving. One more trial to go and then we’ll finally claim whatever prize is waiting at the end of The Road”.

A murmur of excitement abounded at her statement, although it was cut short by Rio, who instead of heading up the stairwell like the rest of them, turned to head back through the iron maiden toward the upside down tower.

She stood facing them all, her back to the open doorway. A wicked grin bloomed upon her face as she tilted her chin over her shoulder, down towards the grisly remains of the three Salemites below, relishing a view only she could see.

“I’ll catch up with you guys in a bit,” she said, allowing her human face to melt away to reveal a half-skeleton, half-human visage, “duty calls”.

And then she dropped backwards in a swirl of black robes, disappearing from sight to complete her universally-bound duty.

“ Oh my god ,” Agatha groaned, feeling her knees weaken as she drooped backwards against the stone wall behind her.

“Oh for goodness sake,” Jen crowed as she passed Agatha on the stairs, “please don’t tell me that did it for you”.

Alice and Lilia cackled loudly at Jen’s jibe, even as Teen shook his head in teenage disgust.

But Agatha, whose weakness had always been powerful, deadly woman, simply squared her jaw, straightened her shoulders, and ascended the stairs as regally as a queen might. “It absolutely did,” she confirmed, throwing a longing stare over her shoulder to where Rio had disappeared from view, “what can I say? I like the bad boys”.

Glory at the End

Chapter Notes

My dudes. This chapter tormented me and made me write it twice. So there is a whole other version of this thing on my computer lmaooo. Why I thought trying to twine canon with my own story would be a good idea, I have no clue. But alas, I am foolish enough to continue with my endeavour.

Thank you to all of you guys who comment week in and week out, you guys really motivate me to finish this fic because for a moment there I was like hmmmmmmmmmm does it need an ending? But it does, and I am determined to finish it, by blood or high water it shall be done.

I apologise for the rambling nature of this chapter note, but I honestly feel like I have just gone three rounds in a boxing ring with this fic and it won. So, don't feel pressured to read this whole note, it's the concussion talking.

I really am hoping and praying you enjoy it, because like I said, it beat me up and took my lunch money. And of course, this one had to be the longest chapter too.

Only one more main chapter to go though! We're so close!

(This gets angsty in places - but I don’t do sad endings, so please do not fear!)

And so, I really hope you enjoy chapter eighteen, the bane of my life! <3

AGATHA

Being in a body bag was a morbid experience, one that Agatha had no interest in repeating.

Not whilst alive at least, or for that matter, not when she was dead either; her body deserved better than this .

It was claustrophobic, it was humid, and it was an exceptionally frustrating environment to be stuck in. One that brought to mind one of Agnes’s scarlet-stained memories to the forefront of her mind, one that included wrestling with a duvet cover whilst trying to change the sheets on her double bed. Which resulted in Agnes nee Agatha, becoming entangled inside of the blasted thing. Until Rio had stopped laughing long enough to actually help her escape it’s cotton clutches at least.

What's more, they didn't actually find the final trial, but rather, it found them.

They had stumbled over it when least expecting it. Or rather she had.

She had been mid-sentence, mid-outraged rant in fact. A completely justifiable tirade on the frustration she felt about tripping over shoes; shoes that they had left at the beginning of The Road.

One moment she had been yelling at them all, demanding they come up with at least one reasonable explanation as to how they were at the fucking start again , and the next she was here. On a small, cramped metal rectangle, stuffed inside a thick plastic bag.

She was suddenly jolted from her ire-fuelled contemplation however, when the tray her body bag was resting upon was jerked forward, quite violently too.

She peered out through narrowed eyes, only to flinch back the instant she did so for a single stream of bright, white light was permeating through the small gap in her body bag's zipper. Squinting to protect her eyesight, she quickly slid two scrabbling fingers into the zipper space to tug it apart, freeing herself enough to sit up with a gasp.

“What in the-” she glanced down at herself, finding this view of her body bag no better than the one she had possessed whilst sequestered away inside it. “Ugh,” she sneered, feeling a disturbing mix of disgust and fear at the stark symbolism of her body wrapped in a black plastic, laying on a cold morgue shelf.

Looking around, her eyes found Billy who was in a similar position to herself. They shared a brief look of relief to see the other, before a third tray burst from the wall.

“ Help! What is this?! Let me out! ” Jen’s voice was muffled, her body bag wriggling and writhing with panic.

Billy shot to his feet eager to help, but Agatha stayed still and brushed a lock of wayward hair from her face with a lazy hand, “don’t steal her struggle”.

Of course, noble Maximoff that he was, he ignored her and rushed to help Jen open the zipper on her bag, from which she immediately sat up gulping in great, panicked lungful’s of air.

Moments later a tray at the top of the wall sprung open, followed promptly by the soprano screams of Lilia, which only increased in pitch the moment she sat up from her body bag and realised she was a good six feet above the ground.

“ Oh my god! ” She cried, peering down at them all with wide, panicked eyes, “ get me down! ”

Agatha snorted and placed her hands on her hips, “oh yeah, let me just get the ladder I packed, or would you prefer the elevator? Or how about a crane?”

Lilia scowled at her sarcasm, even through her fear, “will you keep that tongue of yours pleasant for once in your life, and actually help!”

Agatha smirked, unable to resist the powder keg of inuendo she had just been handed for free. “My, my, my Lilia Calderu ,” she wiggled her eyebrows, relishing the moment Lilia’s expression dropped from fearful to unimpressed, “I didn’t know you even thought about my tongue all that much,” she winked, “good to know”.

“Oh please,” Lilia snorted waving Agatha's lecherous jest away with a flick of her hand, obviously already very tired of her antics, “will you just-” she gestured around herself, “help me!”

Before Agatha could say or do anything else in reply, another draw two tiers beneath Lilia’s slid open.

“Thank fuck that’s over,” Alice drawled, sitting up slowly and calmy, as though she was completely unphased to have been laying in a body bag on a morgue slab for the past ten minutes or so.

“Alice!” Teen cried, pleased to see her.

“What’s up Billy,” Alice grinned at him, saluted at Jen, and then glanced up at Lilia who had also shrieked her name the moment her tray had popped from the wall just below her own. “Lilia,” Alice said in greeting, trying valiantly to stifle a laugh at the older witch’s evident, and very shrill panic, “here, use my tray as a step down. I’ll help you”.

Alice did so, helping Lilia scramble from her own drawer onto Alice’s, and then down further onto the floor where Teen and Jen stood with open hands, ready to catch her. Once Lilia was safely on the ground, Alice climbed down too, making the whole thing look like a walk in the park compared to Lilia's nervous scrabbling.

“Where are we?” Jen asked, starting to circle the room to look for a hint or a clue as to how this trial could be started or won. She looked up and pointed, a frown marring her face, “these are grow lights… are we supposed to grow something?”

“In a place with no soil or water? ” Agatha sniped, leaning back against the wall behind her with her arms crossed over her chest. “It certainly has the irritating sting of a Witches Road trial”.

Jen ignored her jibe and continued running restless hands across the walls, still searching for clues whilst Agatha pinned her broach to the drab, grey gown she had been forced to wear. She immediately felt better the moment she had it attached to her person, and allowed herself a moment to inhale deeply, bracing herself for another round with The Witches Road.

Suddenly, making them all jump, a loud ticking noise echoed around the room. Lilia grabbed Alice’s arm to haul her close, whilst Teen started to glance around the room, spinning in a circle, as though searching for the source of the sound.

“And now we have our countdown,” Agatha drawled, her eyes following Jen, who seemed like the most proactive member of their coven, for she was the only one still trying to find a trial starting-point in this sealed, grey room. “You seem relaxed,” Agatha jeered at her, unable to stop herself; old habits die hard and all that. “Usually, at this point you’re either complaining loudly or freaking out loudly”.

“I’m thinking! ” Jen snapped back, her frustration at Agatha’s sniping unmistakable.

“Oh, about what?” Agatha asked brightly, as though enquiring where she had bought her necklace, and not a plan to escape an enchanted trial that would kill them all without hesitation.

Jen scowled at her from across the room, “how to save your ass”.

Agatha inhaled as though scandalised, before exclaiming with flare, " pardon? ”

Jen waved a hand at her, as though Agatha was little more than an irritating fly buzzing around her head. “We need to think about this logically. Every trial we have faced has had a point... or a lesson attached to it".

She pointed at Agatha, “you said it yourself, The Road tests us, one trial per skill. Potions: the beach house. Protection witch: killing a demon and breaking the curse”. Jen pointed at each of them as she listed their trials and skills.

“Dealing with Death…” Jen arched a pointed brow towards Agatha at that particular statement, although Agatha couldn't tell whether she was referring to Agatha’s long list of people she had killed, or what was more likely following Rio’s recent revelation, the fact she had been up close and personal with Death, and not in a life-threatening way.

Jen continued through a smirk, evidently pleased with herself for getting at least one jab in at Agatha, who had rolled her eyes in and scoffed petulantly in response. “The last trial was Lilia's: divination, which leaves one practice left: green magic ”.

Jen threw her hands up with realisation, gesturing around them, “this is Rio’s trial!” She then immediately sagged with disappointment, “...and Rio isn’t here”.

Quite suddenly, just as quickly as they had done so before, two drawers slammed open on the opposite side of the room, both of them side by side and casting a thick shadow across the grey floor.

Again, Lilia squealed as both Alice and Teen spun around to quickly locate the threat. Yet much to all of their confusion, no body bags were on either of the shelves, and Rio, who was the only unaccounted for member of their party, was not laid out on either table, much to Agatha’s disappointment.

Yet, as though her thoughts alone had summoned her, or perhaps it was Jen’s sulking, the morgue shelves shadows, started to stretch and bloom, until a black mass started to grow from the ground right in the centre of the room. The shadow started to take shape then, darkening into swirls of fabric that fell towards the floor in elegant swoops until finally, Rio was in front of them, dressed in robes crafted from the night sky, robes that allowed several devastatingly appealingly flashes of skin to show, including two long strips of thigh and a captivating glimpse of her ribs.

Rio glanced around. Her demeanour as always, was relaxed. “Yo,” she greeted them all, throwing a lazy hand up in a wave as though her face wasn’t still half skeleton. A frown fell across her expression at their frozen reaction to her sudden appearance, so in an attempt at levity she threw her hands up and did a lacklustre cheer, “woo final trial! We made it”.

Again, she glanced from face to face, taking note of their fearful expressions, “is it something I said?”

Agatha cleared her throat, drawing Rio’s dark eyes toward her which, unhelpfully in her current situation, caused a pulse of heat to stir low in her stomach at just how dangerous Rio looked like this; the all-powerful deity come out to play for all to see. A deity that was apparently, all Agatha's.

“I think they’re a bit taken aback by your…” Agatha waved a discreet finger at her own chin, indicating the lower half of her face.

Instantly, Rio’s eyebrows rose in surprise, as though she had completely forgotten half of her face was devoid of skin, “oh yeah, let me just-”. And then, with awe-inspiring ease, Rio brought an arm up and swiped it down in front of her own face, causing tanned skin to stitch itself together over bare bone.

“Better?” She asked once her face was human again, or at least human-looking.

Agatha smirked back at her, “I mean, I have no complaints either way". She took a few steps closer, feeling the curiosity that had gotten her into all sorts of trouble over the centuries bubbling to life as she studied Rio.

Rio who was Death. Rio who was also entirely dedicated to ensuring Agatha was happy; like her very own fallen angel. one she couldn’t remember, much to her ever-growing frustration.

“So you can dissolve your own face and travel by shadow?” She asked, eyes wandering up and down Rio’s outfit, enjoying seeing her in the infamous dark robe of her trade.

“I can,” Rio answered, “amongst other things”.

“Can you help us figure this trial out?” Lilia asked loudly, and rather boldly too, “time’s ticking and this is technically your trial”.

Rio glanced over her shoulder toward Lilia, who much to her credit, didn’t flinch the moment Death laid her eyes upon her person.

Rio shrugged, nonchalant as ever, "not much greenery in here for a green witch to work with”. She span in a circle, eyes dragging from the body bags to the morgue shelves, before falling to the grey robes each of them were dressed in. Everyone paused and held their breath, for it looked, for a brief moment at least, as though Rio was building up to impart some immortal knowledge to them, something that would rival the universe and its wisdom, something that would guide them toward the correct path and help them figure out what they had to do to pass this test.

Instead of that however, or anything remotely helpful, they received another shrug, this time accompanied by a loud sigh. Rio then hauled herself up to perch on one of the morgue shelves, where she sat like a child on a fence with her legs kicking in the air, waiting for them to figure it out for themselves.

Agatha snorted with amusement, “well aren’t you a font of helpful advice. Seriously, what is the point of having an immortal deity for a girlfriend if she isn’t going to help you escape deadly, enchanted trials?”

Teen's smile was smug and very middle school, making Agatha feel like she and Rio had just been paired together for seven-minutes-in-heaven, “ girlfriend? ”

And Rio, a figure feared across time, space, cultures and realms simply blushed and playing nervously with the edge of her robe, “well, that isn’t technically-”.

Whatever intriguing piece of information Rio was about to divulge was promptly disrupted by Jen, who once again threw her hands in the air and gestured to the room around them. “We do not have time for this right now. We couldn’t save Sharon, but I’ll be damned if the rest of us are going to die here”.

“Wow,” Agatha drawled, turning to smirk at Jen, “such purpose. How are you going to do that without magic?”

Billy stepped between the two of them. “She saved my life, she saved you from poisoning. All while bound…”, he said to Agatha before turning to address Jen with an endearing smile, “…maybe you don’t need it”.

Jen looked stricken at the thought, “well, if that’s true, that means I’ve wasted the last century of my life. That doctor in Boston didn’t take anything from me,” her eyes looked glassy as she said solemnly, “I gave it up”.

Agatha hardly heard the end of her sentence though, for it suddenly struck her that Jen had been bound in Boston . A city in which Agatha herself had been selling the odd witch-binding spell for a small fee back in the day.

The look of surprise that crossed her face, the one Agatha had been certain hadn't been clocked by anyone, was then promptly pointed out by Alice and her police-trained senses.

“Agatha?” She asked curiously, taking a step closer with a small crease between her brows.

Agatha span toward her with a forced air of innocence to answer the question Alice hadn't actually asked aloud, “nothing”.

“What is it?” Jen asked, having sensed as well that Agatha wasn’t been entirely honest about something; story of her life.

Agatha shrugged nonchalantly, “no, I just… I never knew you ever passed through there. That’s all”.

Apparently she had done a terrible job of being nonchalant however, because almost immediately, Jen’s face collapsed with fury, “are you the one who bound me!?”

Agatha threw her arms up, honestly not entirely sure of the answer herself, “I don’t know!”

“ What?! ” Jen hissed, “you nonstop sociopath! ”

Teen looked as shocked as Agatha felt, “ you’re the one who bound her?”

“You kept me like this for one hundred years?!” Jen growled, taking a few furious steps closer.

“I didn’t know it was you! ” Agatha argued, “it was the 1920s! I did the odd spell for bank notes,” she glanced at all of them one at a time, registering the anger in their expressions. All of them aside from Rio, who was frowning heavily at Jen from her perch with her muscles tensed and her hand firmly on her knife. As discreetly as Agatha could, she shook her head at Rio, certain that the last thing they needed right now was a civil war, before continuing to excuse her past actions. “I don’t know! The patriarchy really shelled out to shush a lady. It was bind or burn!”

“ One hundred years! ” Jen hissed, the anger and resentment sparking clearly in her dark eyes.

“This is so awkward ,” Agatha murmured, before yelping in pain from Jen ripping a chunk of hair from her head, “Ow! Oh god! Jen, that is my hair! ”

Jen didn’t hear her, or more likely didn't care to listen, for in the next instant she had grabbed Agatha’s wrists to start wrapping her own stolen hair around them, “why are you doing this right-“. She rolled her eyes, “look at where we are! Jen! ”

Teen looked between Jen and herself, announcing in a solemn voice what was obvious to all of them, “the unbinding ritual”.

Jen grabbed Agatha's bound wrists and hauled her closer, until they were standing face to face and Agatha could see the true extent of Jen’s pain in her expression.

“I deny your power over me,” Jen’s voice was a resounding order, a serious tone that denied any argument or adversary.

And like with all things, Agatha’s initial reaction was to mock and belittle the other, “attagirl, good for you”.

“ Agatha ,” Billy’s sharp voice cut her off, although it was echoed by both Lilia and Alice, who had also stepped closer to witness Jen’s reclamation of her power.

“You hold nothing ,” Jen said, voice shaking with anger and desperation.

“Say it like you mean it though Jen,” Agatha drawled, glancing down at Jen’s lips momentarily. She tried to play it off as a joke, but in truth, she found this dominant, powerful version of Jennifer Kale had succeeded in lighting a small spark of attraction in her stomach. A feeling that was not at all helped by having her wrists bound. What can she say, she’s only human and powerful witches were, and always had been, her weakness.

“You hold nothing ”.

“Yeah well…” Agatha felt a wave of shame overshadowing her attraction then as Jen's devastated expression hardened. It was a sensation she had only felt once or twice through her long life, a sensation she still despised as desperately as she had the first time she had felt it.

“ You hold nothing. You hold nothing. You hold nothing… ”

Jen continued to chant those three words over and over, and as she did so, Agatha felt herself softening entirely, watching with eyes that gentled the desperate desire playing out across Jen’s face to be reunited with her magic.

Agatha couldn't help but empathise, as her mind fell to thoughts of the green witch in the corner of the room, whose history with Agatha had been shackled within her mind in the same cruel way Jen’s magic had been bound one hundred years ago.

Suddenly, what felt like a wave of power rippled from Agatha through Jen who then gasped and stumbled backwards, releasing her hold on Agatha's wrists. Tears started to pool in Jen's eyes and dribble down her cheeks as she, with a mesmerised expression, flicked her hands to summon her pink power, which immediately sparked around her hands in beautiful, flashing swirls.

Jen collapsed to her knees, evidently overwhelmed at feeling her magic ripple under her skin again, and at having reclaimed control over such a huge part of herself. And then, quite suddenly, as though she had never been there in the first place, Jen gasped a second time and was gone.

Lilia shot forward to where Jen had been kneeling, eyes wide with alarm, “what happened? Where did she go? She was just there! Agatha?”

Suddenly, the meaning, followed promptly by the understanding of Jen’s disappearance, settled in Agatha’s mind like a single leaf on a pond; gently and with little fanfare.

It was obvious, almost insultingly so.

Of course that was the end of The Road, and of course it was Rio’s trial considering who she was; the ultimate ending.

The prize to be won wasn’t something that they had a choice over, nor was it something in-general, or to be requested. It was specific to each of them, just like their trials had been.

The prize was the resolution of their lives largest, and most profound hurdles.

Jen’s biggest issue was being bound, and having reclaimed it using her own voice and actions she had beaten The Road.

Spinning with urgency, Agatha shared her revelation with the others, “you need to claim your own power. That’s how you win”.

Lilia stared at her, eyes still wide with fear for Jen and her sudden disappearance.

"Seriously,” Agatha swept closer and grasped her shoulders with both hands, being for once, entirely serious and completely sincere. “Think about your trial. Think about what you learned about yourself”.

Lilia’s jaw wobbled as her eyes flickered across Agatha’s face, “I- I read for myself, I put it all in order, I made sense of all my flashes”.

“Yes,” Agatha breathed, not entirely sure what Lilia meant but still encouraging her to continue exploring her own success all the same, “and how long have the gaps between flashes been holding you back? How long has living that way stopped you from stepping forward and claiming everything you deserve out of this life?”

Clouding with the weight of her past, Lilia’s eyes glazed slightly, “my whole life”. Her confession was a quiet murmur, one that Agatha pursued relentlessly.

“And now? ” She tightened her grip on Lilia’s shoulders, shaking her slightly to bring the older witch’s focus back onto her words, “after The Road? After beating it?”

A proud smile started to bloom on Lilia’s face and her shoulders straightened, as she said with the brassy confidence of a woman who had been alive for four and a half centuries, “that I am not a forgotten woman. That I am not lost. That I am a traveller possessing a gift as valuable as the earth; that I am and always have been the queen of cups”.

Immediately, the warmth of Lilia was absent from beneath Agatha's palms, as she too claimed her reward and was whisked from The Road’s realm.

Agatha turned to Alice next, yet she, who was as sharp as Rio’s blade and as observant as a soldier, had already stepped forward. Her hand was gripped tightly over the scar on her shoulder with a white-knuckled hand.

“I, Alice Wu-Gulliver have finally freed my family from the curse that has haunted and killed us for centuries ,” the reality of her accomplishment seemed to settle now she knew she was at the end of The Road, that freedom was so close to being within her grasp. She laughed loudly, a disbelieving, joyous sound before slapping a hand over her mouth, evidently unused to making such happy sounds. “I did it,” she grinned at Teen, beamed at Rio, and finally smiled at Agatha. “I did it, I saved us ”. Her eyes started to well as she looked down and caught a glimpse of the tattoo on her arm, the one her mother had insisted she get to keep her safe, or as safe as a cursed child could be. With a shaky palm she cupped her arm directly over the dark ink, “I did it mom, I broke our curse”.

A joyful bout of relieved laughter echoed around the room as Alice was swept from The Road, having successfully completed its trials and tribulations.

“Woah,” Teen breathed, amazed that the others had done it, that they had actually won. Immediately his brow furrowed with panic, “I don’t think anything has changed for me, nothing drastic like that! I haven’t been alive long enough to have trauma that deep!”

For the first time throughout this entire process Rio moved, sliding from the morgue tray looking, quite unnervingly so, like the wraith Agatha now knew her to be.

Teen watched her too, looking almost afraid as she drew closer, her heavy stare set upon his pale face.

Agatha was aware they didn’t have time for whatever Rio was going to say or do, for the trial's clock was still ticking and the three of them, or the two of with mortal lives at least, only had a certain amount of time left.

She didn’t want to do it this way, she had wanted him to realise on his own. He was Wanda’s child after all, or at least partially, and he was definitely smart enough to figure it out too. Yet time was running out, and she knew from the first trial that his magic wouldn’t hesitate to kill them both, even subconsciously. So she would have to make him aware of just how The Road came to be, of just how similar to his mother he actually was.

“You have the power to break out of here Billy,” her voice for once, was soft, almost maternal, “to break us all out of this place”.

A wave of emotions flooded his face; from confusion, to fear, then uncertainty before finally whispering a shaky, “ what? ”

Agatha smiled at him, allowing the full extent of her pride to shine through. For it was true, she was proud of him. Exceptionally so. She was proud of the witch he was becoming, a witch with power enough to protect himself in the most hopeless of situations. “You are as powerful as your mother Billy, you have her power running through your veins. If anyone can break us out of here, it’s you”.

She sat on the floor with an elegant huff, grabbing his wrist to tug him down to sit opposite her as she did so.

He looked afraid, even more so too when she clamped both of her palms around the sides of his head, pressing his curly hair flat to his skull. She stared at him imploringly, before rolling her eyes and grabbing one of his hands to direct it towards her own head, “now, sit there and close your eyes”.

He did so, still looking unsure.

“ Agatha ,” Rio’s voice was closer than she had anticipated and she peeked through one eye to find Rio crouched beside them, with a mournful, regretful expression on her face.

Undoubtedly she was mourning the opportunity to request Agatha's memories be restored at the end of The Road, and for Agatha to remember Rio and all they are to one another.

Although, with the way Agatha’s heart constricted painfully at Rio’s melancholy expression, she was almost certain she had managed to fall in love with the same witch all over again anyway. And if that wasn’t a sign that she and this woman, this beautiful immortal goddess were meant for one another, she wasn’t entirely sure what would be.

Agatha shot her a broad grin, aiming for reassuringly cocky, “don’t worry sweetheart, we’ll be out of here soon enough. And when we are, we’ll find another way to get my memories back”.

But all Rio did was utter her name once again, a broken whimper of a word, “ Agatha ”.

Yet the pulse of magic she could feel stirring beneath her palms, buzzing within the boy sat across from her distracted her from Rio's plight. A rush of power had always been something she had been drawn to, and this kid had an abundance of the stuff, just sparking and rushing beneath his skin like his arteries were filled with the arcane and not blood.

She jolted slightly, feeling a spark of wayward magic bounce through her skull, sparked accidentally from one of his palms which were still pressed to either side of her head.

“That’s it,” she tried guiding him, hoping her voice would be a light leading him to their goal, “find the seam of this world Billy, find the seam and tear through it; take us home”.

Her own eyes were shut, clenched tightly, but she could picture his expression; one filled with furious determination, uncertainty in his own ability, and illuminated by blue light, the same shade that had thrown them from The Road, nearly drowning them all.

She flinched then, feeling another tendril of his magic come slicing through her skull. This one however, unlike the first, didn’t travel all the way through as though she was merely an object to traverse, no, this one stopped in her mind, right at back of her skull where that awful pain always originated whenever she thought too long, or too hard about Rio and their lost, mysterious history.

“ Ah ,” she gasped when Teen’s magic tugged, almost as though it were trying to pull a thick chain from around a closed chest, “what are you-”.

Her words were cut off by Billy’s voice, “I can feel something, something’s glowing in here Agatha, something red ”.

“ Get out of there ,” she hissed, furious that he was pursuing his own course through her mind, and not focussed on the task at hand; their escape from his damned hex.

“I- I- I- can’t, I don’t know how! ” His panic caused a wave of fear to rush through. She had been forced to endure too many hands rifling through her thoughts recently, but these uneducated, novice ones had the power to do irrevocable damage without even meaning to.

“ Billy ,” her words were a furious hiss, one that was cut short by a strangled gasp of pain, as once again his magic tugged stubbornly at the glowing lock in her mind, “ stop it! ”

“Agatha!” Rio’s panicked voice echoed clearly through all of the static; which was both a comfort, for it meant she was close by, but also a concern, as she had never heard Rio sound quite so fearful.

The pain sharpened, becoming almost unbearable to the point she could no longer speak or try to stop him. All she could do was endure the torment of his magic poking and prodding around what was already a tender, bruised part of her psyche until within the blink of an eye, a small shockwave of electric blue energy pulsed through her mind and behind her eyelids, before Billy too, was snatched from The Road, leaving Agatha and Rio alone in the morgue.

“ Fucking hell ,” she whimpered, raising both hands to her head as it continued to pound. It felt as though Teen had taken a chainsaw to her mind, yet the consistent ticking of the timer forced her to open her eyes, to peer around and finally find Rio, who was still crouched beside her with a desperately concerned expression on her face.

“Are you alright?!” Rio's words were ragged with worry.

Agatha flinched back the moment Rio spoke; her voice was far too loud for Agatha's pounding head to handle. “Fuck,” she hissed again, waving a weakened hand at Rio, “I’m fine, I don’t- I don’t know what he did, but it fucking hurt”. She glanced around as the reality of it just being the two of them, and the fact the boy who had unknowingly designed the hex was now gone, finally descended on her like grave dirt upon a coffin.

“Agatha,” Rio whispered, as one of her hands shot forward to clutch her wrist. The sudden touch caused her to flinch again; her body still recovering from such a sudden, and quite brutal, magical intrusion.

“Shit!” Agatha hissed, scrabbling backwards slightly to give herself some space to process whatever changes Billy had made to her mind. She closed her eyes, trying to look inward and focus on that infected part of her brain that Wanda had taken control of over a year ago. Although in truth, the moment she tried to feel it, it felt... weaker . A small frisson of pain resounded out the longer she prodded at it, thinking heavily of Rio and her secrets, which only an hour ago would have caused a sharp pain to shoot through her skull, yet whatever Billy had done to it had weakened it's defences and made it's attack feel far less potent.

“Are you alright?” Rio’s voice was urgent. She had stood up from her crouch, but didn’t come any closer, both her hands help up in a gesture universal good-will.

Agatha kept her eyes scrunched closed and brushed both her hands back through her hair, inhaling deeply for a long moment to regain control over herself.

Finally, she glanced over to Rio; the witch who she apparently knew but couldn't remember, the one who always tried to help her.

“Yeah,” she finally breathed out, “yeah I think so”.

She shook her head, “Billy’s magic just got a bit intense for a hot minute,” she scoffed, feeling rather hopeless for the first time, “before he left me here to die”.

Rio’s expression softened, before it hardened to an almost frightening degree, “Agatha”. Her own name was a request, one that demanded Agatha look back at her, which she did.

“I have to tell you something... about Billy,” Rio’s voice was nervous, almost shaking.

But whatever it was Rio wanted to say, she didn’t get a chance to, for in the very next moment the ground started to shake so violently a large crevasse appeared, zig-zagging its way through the cold tiles beneath their feet, baring the dark, damp earth below.

“ Shit! ” She hissed, looking around for an answer, “I don’t know what I need to do to get out!”

But as always, Rio was there, her pillar of calm in the storm. “ Think ,” she intoned her voice as measured and as ordered as one would expect from an ancient, immortal deity. “Think about your trial, about the meaning of it all. What were you asked to do?”

Agatha stumbled, for the room had started to shake even more violently, causing the morgue drawers surrounding them to shake and clang against the walls.

She threw her hands up, gesturing towards Rio herself, “death!” She couldn’t stop herself from scoffing with dark amusement, “my trial was about facing death! ”

“ Good ,” Rio breathed, “Good, and here I am, all yours. So what is it about death? What do you need to understand, or accept, or claim in order to escape?”

The thing is, Rio’s advice was good. It was solid, and it made sense. Agatha knew immediately the angle Rio was going for; she was aiming for Agatha to accept it, to accept Death as life's foil, to accept that Death would visit every single human to ever live and whisk them away to the great beyond. But, and it's a big but, Agatha had never not understood that particular concept. So that couldn’t possibly be the lesson The Road had plucked from her skull as the one that needed to be learnt.

After all, Agatha knew better than most the three intrinsic rules of the universe; that life was cruel, that death was greedy, and even the most innocent of souls were merely ripe fruit to be plucked away from grieving mothers.

So, it couldn't be an acceptance of death that was her challenge to best. She had accepted death before, in fact she had accepted centuries ago that death had stolen her child away. As much as she might despise it, she knew it was the truth.

So that left only one other answer.

For the one thing that Agatha had always desired, and the one thing she had always been working towards was simple. It wasn’t to accept Death, it was to best it.

And with that realisation, lightning struck.

“ Aah-ha! ” She cried, plucking her broach from her drab, grey gown to gently pull the dandelion seed from within it's delicate casing. She knew it was there, had kept it safely tucked away beneath the lock of Nicky’s hair as another reminder of her darling boy.

Rio’s eyes widened at her sudden shout of victory, before her brow furrowed the moment Agatha dropped to her knees to start scraping a small gouge into the soil that the room's quake had created.

“Er...?” Rio droned, “I'm not sure you can dig your way out of this one. It’s probably easier to just accept it. Accept me Agatha and The Road will let you go”.

Agatha grinned up at her wolfishly, feeling that familiar confidence burning in her blood from being one of the smartest people on the damn planet. “Oh honey,” Agatha drawled, before pressing a kiss to the small seed she still had pinched between her thumb and forefinger, “my trial wasn’t about accepting death”.

“It wasn’t?” Rio’s eyebrows shot up in disbelief.

“ Of course not . The point of the trial was to highlight the one thing we each wanted above everything else - Jen wanted her powers, Alice wanted to break her family’s curse, Lilia wanted her timeline straightened out, and Teen wanted to discover himself, to learn the truth about who he is”.

Rio crouched beside her again, watching intently as Agatha gently pressed the dandelion seed into the soil. Agatha closed her eyes, drawing thoughts of her son to the forefront of her mind, thoughts of the one person she would trade the whole world for, bringing tears to her eyes with ease; they were never far away when thoughts of Nicky lingered on her consciousness.

“Alright,” Rio said, going along with Agatha’s explanation, even if she wasn’t entirely sold, “and what is it you want beyond anything else?”

Agatha leaned down to blink a few of the tears pooling on her lashes onto the soil, right atop the seed she had kept to remember her son, now watered with tears she had wept for him. After, she looked up at Rio, this stranger with a face that mirrored her child's, a stranger sat here in the dark robes of her dark duty, and grinned at her like a wolf baring it’s teeth.

“To beat you”.

And with that truth exposed to the open air, the seed took root. The two of them watched in awed silence as life grew from nothing, from a world, as Agatha had exclaimed when Jen had first pointed out the grow lights shining above them, that this was a place without earth or water. And yet, here she was, scraping through the floor to reach soil, planting a seed that is centuries old and watered by the outpouring of grief from her own body.

The dandelion started to grow at an expeditious rate, cycling from a small green stalk to a bloom of fluffy yellow, before shrinking into a multitude of seeds that then withered and died.

She had done it, she had born life from nothing and beaten the universe.

A loud clunking sound echoed from behind her exposing the stairway out, just as the room started to shake and chunks of dirt started to fall from the ceiling, falling into her eyes and mouth.

“Ah, shit!” She cried, “the others get zapped out of here, but oh no lets drown Agatha in the fucking dirt,” she grumbled, grabbing hold of Rio’s hand to drag her up the staircase towards the exit.

The closed exit.

The exit that she couldn’t fucking use because it was closed.

Releasing Rio’s wrist, she started to bang both of her hands on the metal door in front of her, “ hey! I did it, I beat your trial! Let me out! ”

“ Agatha ,” Rio said, her voice full of warning for everything happening behind them, which by the level of rumbling occurring down the short stairwell, she could tell wasn’t good.

She gave the door one more shove and it finally loosened, leading up from Agnes’s basement, to Agnes’s garden, where she found Jen, Lilia, Alice, and Teen huddled together, heads bowed low, talking urgently.

“How do we get back though?!” Alice was asking, tone solemn and serious, “we can’t just leave them there to die”.

Jen sighed, “I know she wouldn’t hesitate to leave any of us, but, ugh ,” she threw her hands up petulantly, “I don’t think we should leave her to die either”.

Lilia smirked, looking past them all to Agatha who had come to a stop behind the others, where they couldn't see her unless they were to turn around. “I told you,” Lilia said knowingly, “the world isn’t rid of Agatha Harkness or her reign of chaos just yet”.

“Damn straight,” Agatha drawled loudly, prompting all of the others to spin around in surprise. It was amusing to compare their mix of reactions to her sudden appearance and survival of The Road, which ranged from a thrilled ' Agatha! ' from Teen, to a dry ' oh, you’re not dead ' from Jen.

Alice’s reaction was probably the sweetest though, which consisted of a broad grin and a hard slap to the shoulder, “Fuckin knew you’d make it Harkness. Bad bitch like you wasn’t dying today, hell no”.

Agatha smiled at her, a genuine one too, which surprised Agatha just as much as it surprised Alice, whose jaw dropped in shock. It made Agatha pout slightly immediately after, for the the sensation of directing a warm smile at anyone other than her child, or her green witch was a strange one.

Thoughts of green witches focussed her mind once more, prompting Agatha start looking around for a glimpse of dark robes and darker eyes. She felt certain Rio had been directly behind her whilst fleeing the collapsing basement after all, so wasn’t sure where she had gone.

“Where’s Rio?” Agatha asked, feeling a measure of fear rush through her at the thought of her being trapped on The Road all alone. Even though, she knew logically that it was an absurd thought, that Rio couldn’t be trapped anywhere .

“She was with you wasn’t she?” Alice asked, also starting to look toward the dark corners of Agnes’s garden, hoping to catch a glimpse of their wayward coven-mate.

“When she screams ‘ duck, I want the whole set ’, hit the deck,” Lilia’s urgent voice sounded from behind them, drawing Agatha’s attention, along with everyone else’s back onto the older witch. Lilia’s eyes were closed, and she was shaking her head slightly, as they had learned she did whenever returning from one of her timeline-mix-up episodes.

Agatha scoffed, still looking around for Rio whose disappearance she was finding alarming for a number of reasons, “I want the whole set? ” She repeated, tone mocking, “what the hell is that supposed to mean?”

Suddenly a flare of green light streaked through the sky, coalescing on the roof in a blur of dark emerald and smoky black.

“Found her,” Jen said, voice and face both blank and lacking inflection; now entirely unphased by Rio’s penchant for dramatic entrances.

Agatha turned with a display of eagerness she would have found embarrassing if she had been aware she had done so. And the moment her eyes landed on Rio, who was straddling the roof in her dark robes, looking as devilish as she did dangerous, Agatha felt her mouth go dry for wanting her.

“ Hi honey ,” she couldn’t stop herself from drawling lasciviously, smirking up at Rio who smiled back, although it wasn’t the beaming, feral grin she had been expecting, but a far more reserved expression.

Agatha didn’t get a moment to ponder it though, for in the very next instant Rio grit her teeth like a mother wolf might at another beast threatening her pack, and held a clawed hand out, before bellowing at them all through a deranged cackle, “duck! I want the whole set!”

Jen and Agatha turned to each other, their eyes wide as they both recalled Lilia’s earlier warning before promptly throwing themselves at the others, pushing them to the ground just as Agnes’s kitchen sink came crashing through the side of the house, directly towards the patch of grass they had all been standing only moments before.

“ Rio! ” Agatha scolded, “the rest of us aren’t fucking immor-” yet she was silenced quickly, because as the sink went soaring over their heads, she saw it hit it's actual target moments later; which happened to be one of the Salem Seven, who had been creeping up behind them.

“Oh,” Agatha breathed, nodding to herself, “ the set that makes sense now,” finally understanding Rio’s meaning, she scrabbled back to her feet, hauling Lilia up too as she went. Rio wanted the Salem Seven, and she wanted them dead.

But, if Agatha was not mistaken, by the laws of nature Rio herself couldn’t kill them. So, logically the next step was to hurl a kitchen sink at them to buy the rest of the coven more time to fight.

“ Lilia! Watch out! ” Alice cried, as a burst of power was sent towards their small group from the direction the kitchen sink had gone sailing. The Salemite was back on her feet and hissing at them from the shadows.

Now one Salem Seven member was eery enough, but not particularly intimidating, however the moment the other three remaining Salemites stepped out of the shadows, each of their brown, rotten teeth bared like the animals they resembled so closely, Agatha felt a thrill of fear run up her spine. Especially, as she was still without an ounce of magic.

An assessing pause caused everyone to freeze, as her coven sized up the remaining four members of the Salem Seven, and the Salemites did the same in return. And then, as though someone had simply flipped a switch or struck a match, everyone threw themselves into the fight.

Agatha did her best dodging and diving rogue streaks of magic and she caught a few impressive glimpses of her coven fighting as she army crawled for cover. In truth, she hadn't considered any of the other women particularly good fighters, having assumed they would suck.

Yet, she admitted her initial assumptions were wrong the moment she saw Alice use a burst of yellow energy to strip the sister known as crow of all her feathers, forcing her to return to her human form.

Or when Lilia used her powers of prediction to accurately guess from where and when the next bolt of magic was going to be sent her way, transporting herself with ease out of it’s range.

Even Jen, who hadn’t been able to use her powers for one hundred years was evidently enjoying the opportunity to flex them properly, using her pink magic as though it was a lasso and throwing it around the throat of one of the Salemites to drag her backwards, as she scrabbled at her throat with desperate fingers.

Teen was the only one who appeared frightened, having found an upturned piece of garden furniture to use as a makeshift shield. And although she scoffed at him, she was also jealous that he had found such decent cover before she did, a point she found even more unfair due to the fact she was currently entirely powerless, and he powerful enough to create The Road that had nearly killed them all by accident .

“ Scooch over! ” She shouted to him over the bellow of the battle going on behind her. However, just before she managed to crawl behind the garden table too, she felt sharp nails piercing the skin of her ankle and tug her backwards from her crawl, causing her to land painfully on her stomach and smack her jaw off the hard ground.

Scrabbling with desperate fingers, Agatha managed to turn enough to see one of the Salem Seven, the one with cicadas crawling all over her body and out of her gaping mouth lying flat on her front, and dragging Agatha back towards her with a feral intensity.

She tried kicking free, but the Salemite had utilised her magic to make her grip unbreakable. Agatha hated herself for it, but she did in fact scream in terror in that moment, for the realisation she was powerless against a witch who wanted her dead had settled into her stomach like a boulder in a pond.

Yet once again, Billy was unable to resist the Avenger blood burning in his veins, and quickly jumped up from behind the table with a desperate cry of “ no! ”

The Salemite didn’t listen to him, of course, and Agatha’s eyes met his as she was being dragged backwards. He looked panicked, unsure of what to do before his face evened out with determination and most alarmingly of all, trust .

“Don’t take it all,” was all he said before doing something every other witch on the planet wouldn’t ever dream of, he threw a beam of his electric blue power directly at her chest, allowing her starving body to feed off of his magic.

Her eyes closed with the euphoria of the moment, now completely unphased by the scrabbling nails on her ankle as her body did what it had always done and started to gulp greedily at the power source it had been exposed to.

“ Oh my ,” she sighed, “it feels so good!” The power lifted her upward, out of reach of the Salemite who had been holding her ankle captive. The combined power also did an excellent job of shielding her from any wayward arcane attacks, for the flow of magic from him to her was far too strong to be penetrated by a rogue strike of measly Salemite energy.

She could feel it sparking down every vein and artery, flashing inside every cell like a number of grenades going off, each one rearming her body with the magic it had always naturally possessed, reclaiming the power that had been ripped from her.

As Billy’s blue turned into Agatha’s purple, she felt a pulsing pressure start to build in her mind, a similar sensation to the one she had experienced in the final trial when Billy’s magic had been poking and prodding at Wanda’s hex, the one holding all of her memories back. Only this time, it was her own magic pouring through her consciousness, as though her purple was the arcane equivalent of a white blood cell, bringing the fight to the infection Wanda had left inside her mind.

And as she broke the connection of magic between herself and Teen, not desiring or willing to kill him, she felt those final shaky chains of scarlet shatter under the onslaught of her power, dissolving into nothing at all, like a wisp of smoke swept away by an ocean gale.

Much to her curiosity nothing changed immediately, even though any remnants of Wanda had been wiped from her mind like a damp cloth across a dusty table. She didn’t get an overwhelming resurgence of memories of Rio from across the centuries, she didn’t suddenly have all the answers to every question she had been puzzling over since returning to herself.

Instead it was eerily blank, quiet almost. Disturbingly so. And she couldn’t help but doubt what she had been told. Had Rio been honest? Did they actually know each other, or was the history Rio spoke of a falsification?

She didn’t even get an opportunity to ponder or worry over it anymore than that, because in the time it took for her to inhale once, settling into the familiar sensation of magic sparking under her skin once more, she felt a ripple of power heading straight towards her, sent upwards from the witch on the floor who had been scratching at her ankles.

“Ah yes,” she drawled, grinning down at the witch she was about to murder like a shark might leer at a passing seal, “ you ”.

The Salemite’s fear was only evidenced by the slight widening of her eyes behind her mask. After all, Agatha’s reputation had always preceded her, and if there was one thing she enjoyed it was killing witches, and if there was one other thing that she really, really enjoyed, it was killing witches who had pissed her off.

So she got to work straight away, cackling with glee the entire time, relishing the opportunity to use her magic once more, to feel her purple swirling inside her chest and immediately doing as she bid it with a mere flick of her wrist.

Her first victim, obviously, was the witch who had dared scrabble at her ankles like a rodent. That particular witch was dealt with quickly by a swift blow to the head from a powerful strike of magic from above, like a bolt of lightning through the top of her head that pinned her slumped form to the ground.

Prowling forward through the ongoing carnage she focussed on the Salemite Lilia was currently dodging with her powers of foresight. It was the perfect opportunity to gain even more power, so with very little concern or fear for her own safety, she sent a spark of electricity straight into the Salemite's skull, zapping her enough to get her attention. The witch responded as Agatha desired her to, turning with her teeth bared like the animal she was, before sprinting full pelt at Agatha with a wild scream.

Needing her angry, and hungering for more magic, Agatha did was she did best; she provoked a reaction.

“ Ha! ” She barked nastily, “you’re mother made a similar noise when I drained her dry. Most disgusting magic I’ve ever had the displeasure of tasting, mind you. I should have saved myself the endurance of it and simply slit her throat instead”.

Her words had their intended affect and the Salemite threw out a powerful burst of magic, aiming for Agatha’s heart which she then allowed to strike her. In a single, heady gulp her magic tugged and less than thirty seconds later the Salemite's desiccated corpse dropped to the grass with an empty thump.

Agatha paused momentarily, glancing around the battle scene to locate her next target, taking brief stock of the fact Rio had slid from the roof to the ground and was now in the process of harvesting the fallen Salemite’s souls which she was… putting in an old jar? A jar that already had four glowing orbs buzzing around inside of it?

Huh . It was interesting to watch her work, because Agatha was about ninety percent certain that Rio’s actions weren’t typical for harvesting the souls of the recently deceased.

Agatha didn’t get time to consider it beyond that, as the remaining two sisters of the Salem Seven coven had finally stopped trying to kill Alice and Jen, and had instead turned their attention onto their actual target, the target they had just watched murder two of their coven-mates without hesitation or mercy.

Agatha’s delighted cackle rang out amongst the quiet suburban street of Westview. She felt truly euphoric, and not only at having her magic back, but at surviving The Road, at knowing that Wanda’s presence in her mind had finally been slain like a roaring scarlet dragon pierced through the heart with a silver sword. And of course, to at long last be putting an end to the Salem Seven’s never-ending pursuit of her.

The two feral women circled her, as all of her own coven started to back off to watch the show from the edges of the garden.

“ Come on ladies! ,” Agatha crowed at them mockingly, “let’s see if we can finally avenge the mummy dearest's shall we”. She crossed her arms, appearing relaxed even as they started to crawl closer, wild down to their last cell. Their hissing had increased in pitch though, so she knew they could understand her taunting. “I mean, how long has it been since I murdered those dumb bitches? Three hundred years? And you still haven't been able to take me out?” She started to count on her fingers, “so the seven of you, couldn’t kill the one of me, over three hundred years? ”

She whistled, “those stats don’t look great guys, I’ll be honest. So, you can probably be assured that both of your mothers…,” she hardened her voice as she geared up for the final blow, “…who squealed like pigs when I sucked the life out of them, will be rolling in their graves, disgusted and horrified at the sad , pathetic , embarrassing job their daughters have done to avenge their death’s”.

Her words did as she had designed them too, and within seconds the final two members of the Salem Seven fell victim to their own angry grief, and shot powerful beams of magic directly at Agatha’s chest.

With a delighted, satisfied sigh she closed her eyes and gulped up every drop of power they possessed, enjoying it the same way she would enjoy an excellent meal. So distracted by the pleasure of it all, she only knew that they were dead by two resounding thumps hitting the floor moments apart.

Taking a moment, she rolled her shoulders and stretched her neck, sighing with fulfilment.

Fuck, did it feel good to be back.

It was only then that she remembered she actually had a coven now. One she didn't, or at least probably didn't, intend to kill.

She grinned at them all, a wild, feral expression feeling for all intents and purposes like a cat that had brought it’s owner a mauled bird as a gift, a cat that then stared at the bloody mess on the carpet with bright eyes, as if to say ‘ I did this for you, aren’t you proud of me. Look how well I can murder things ’.

Their reactions were, to be fair, not quite as terrible as she had imagined they might be after watching her slaughter four women.

Jen wore an expression of disdain marred with an undercurrent of acceptance, as if Agatha had done precisely what she had expected, but she wasn’t entirely mad about it.

Alice was wide-eyed, staring down at the desiccated bodies with a morbid fascination, although Agatha was delighted to see very little fear or judgement in her face, only curiosity.

On first glance Lilia looked bored, which took Agatha by surprise initially. But then, after narrowing her gaze to study her expression further it was clear she was in the midst of another flash through time and wasn’t actually with them at this given moment, as she was once more lost within the maze of her own timeline.

Teen’s reaction was mixed, as though not entirely sure what emotion to land on. He started with fatigued, obviously still recovering from the mass of power Agatha had eked from him, then thrilled that their enemies were dead, then horrified with himself for feeling thrilled that their enemies were dead.

Honestly, that kid’s moral compass was as unstable as his mothers.

Quite promptly however, she was distracted from any further review of her coven by a voice, a voice that caused that closed cell within her mind, the cell that had been locked tight and secured by Wanda’s chains of scarlet power, power that was now entirely gone, to creak open with a rusty squeak.

“Agatha?” Rio said from behind her.

Immediately, on hearing her voice Agatha flinched, as suddenly what felt like a thousand other words spoken across time echoed through her mind all at once; a constant hubbub of murmuring, muttering, whispering, and screaming as memories started to pour in, all of them of Rio, moments that then echoed through her mind as a rush of memories, a couple of centuries worth even, started to slam into her consciousness, one after the other.

Having witnessed Agatha’s startling reaction to her voice, Rio stepped closer. A concerned frown carving a groove between her eyebrows as she grasped hold of Agatha’s wrists, hoping to help keep her steady and standing.

Yet, Rio’s touch inspired the same result as her voice, summoning forth a thousand ghostly imprints of Rio’s hands from across time to brush across Agatha’s skin; soft touches, gentle caresses, furious grapples, and lust-filled gripping all suddenly started to haunt her flesh.

Rio jerked away, fearful that her touch was causing Agatha pain the moment she cried out and hunched forward, eyes clenched tightly together as each gap within her mind that Rio had been erased from, was returned to its original setting, like Rio was a blurred figure being brought into sharp clarity on an abundance of photographs, all at the same time. And a once hidden face was rediscovered until those dark eyes and those plump lips became as familiar and as dear as they always had been.

And at long last, after knowing in her very bones that something important, something truly integral had been taken from her this entire time, she got it back, in its entirety.

It all washed over her in chronological order, like their love story was playing on a loop in her mind.

She could remember the first time they had met, eyes meeting over the corpse of a dead Salemite; Agatha’s gaze hungry for the beautiful stranger, Rio’s wide with all that separated her from humanity.

She could recall their blossoming love, how Agatha had pursued Rio relentlessly, presenting coven after coven, witch after witch at Rio’s alter, until Rio had given in to the new flames of desire that she was experiencing.

She remembered their wedding, of the two of them joyously exclaiming their love for one another beneath a full moon in the ways of old, with a blood seal and the incantation to bond two souls together.
