She remembered Nicky, of how every part of him was a reflection of his other mother. His dimples, his smirk, his hair, his eyes. She remembered the moment they discovered Agatha was pregnant, of her flight from their home, of her fear for her son, of Rio’s desperate expression.

Then finally, she remembered the moments everything had fallen apart; giving birth beneath a dark canopy and begging Rio not to take their child from her. Of waking alone seven years later to that same child laying beside her, as cold and as still as ice.

And then the final few puzzle pieces, far newer than any of the others.

Memories of Rio finding her in Westview after hiding from her for one hundred years, of Rio’s anguished expression as she sliced an escape into the wall of Agnes's living room, promising to return even after Agatha had pushed her away again. All of it finally slid back into place, leaving only smoke after a fire and the mental equivalent of lactic acid burning through her thoughts.

She gasped desperately for air, as though she had been being held under water this entire time and had only now been allowed to return to the surface to breathe. Her eyes shot open and she stared at Rio, finally understanding precisely who this witch was to her, and why , after everything , all she had wanted to do, even with half of her memories locked away, was to be as close to Rio as possible.

Rio was staring back at her, eyes wide with concern for whatever was happening within Agatha’s mind, yet the moment their eyes met it was clear Rio could sense the weight of their history in Agatha's gaze. Perhaps her eyes once again possessed a sharpness that the Agatha without the full extent of her grief or anger didn't know how to wield.

Rio took a single step closer, eyes glistening with fresh tears and flickering hope that her theory was true, that Agatha, once again, knew exactly who she was.

“Agatha?” Her voice was timid, a fearful gasp, “do- do you know who I am?”

And on hearing the depth of Rio’s grief, Agatha could do little more than nod desperately, her own eyes welling with tears against her will, as the realisation of what exactly had been done to her settled into her tired bones, and then deeper still to rest in that grief filled part of her that every trauma she had ever experienced resided, a graveyard of past hurts and maltreatment.

Agatha was finding it hard to breathe, and she was finding it impossible to drag her eyes away from her wife, who looked close to collapsing from relief.

“ You- you know me? ” Rio asked again, needing reassurance that she wasn’t misunderstanding Agatha’s gesture, “you remember everything? ”

But Agatha couldn’t answer her question directly, now far too distracted by the heavy weight of what Wanda had done to her. She stumbled closer on unsteady feet, grasping Rio’s forearms beneath her hands, relishing the warmth of her body, the softness of her skin.

“She took you from me?” Agatha’s voice was a bereft whisper, “she stole you from me? She stole us? ”

Rio gasped on a sob, her relief at Agatha being whole once more almost physical as she dropped forward, all of her weight collapsing into Agatha as though she could finally take a moment to rest now she was herself again, “she did, she tore me from your head like a rogue weed”.

“Oh sweetheart ,” Agatha gasped through her tears, truly and fundamentally astounded at the level of devastation Wanda had wrought in her life. Having not only trapped Agatha behind the façade of Agnes, but to shroud all of the way’s Rio’s roots were twisted into her own was heinous and she felt a sharp, hungry flare of anger at the injustice of the Scarlet Witch's actions.

She ran her hands up Rio’s arms to cradle her jaw, tilting her head down so she could press desperate lips to her forehead, before then pressing even more kisses against every inch of Rio’s face that she could reach; her temple, her cheekbone, her jaw, the side of her lips.

Rio shuddered into Agatha’s kisses, clawing desperately at her back to haul her closer, to press herself against the length of Agatha’s body and bask in the warmth of her body.

It was an astoundingly difficult thing to comprehend and come to terms with.

Not just because she has always been desperately in love with her wife, a realisation she had come to accept throughout their time together in Westview, but also because all of her anger, anger that was entirely valid, over what Rio had done to them all those years ago, what she had done to Agatha, what she had done to their child, was now alive and roiling in her gut like an angry, furious beast.

All of the memories had come streaming in so quickly and so intensely, that so much of what she had experienced from across the centuries, both good and bad felt far more raw, and far more recent than it had before Wanda had locked those memories away inside her own consciousness.

Which left her at a difficult crossroads.

Because not only had her love for Rio been bolstered through recalling so vividly and quickly all of the moments they had shared from before Nicky was born. But also, all of her anger was sitting just below the surface too, freshly stoked and prodding at her grief like a brutish child might poke at an ant’s nest.

And that was before she even considered every new memory she had created with Rio since then, because now she had all of her post-amnesia memories floating through her mind too.

For she had, unknowingly, provided herself with everything she had been trying to avoid whilst under the shroud of the Darkhold, which was yet even more evidence and proof as to why Rio truly was, and always will be, the love of her fucking life.

And now, like new and improved software gifting her with a slideshow of intimate moments downloaded directly into her mind, she had an abundance of them. Of new memories, not at all tarnished by her own grief and pain, but rather memories that were and are entirely Rio, and all of the reasons she loved her so damn much.

Of Rio fighting Wanda so desperately, of the crumpled flowers she had been holding on her return to Agatha, as she had promised to do.

Of Rio throughout her time as Agnes, protective and attentive but unwilling to take advantage of Agatha’s lack of autonomy, all the while being as gentle as ever with the version of Agatha that was Agnes.

Of Rio trying again, and again, and again, to break her free from Wanda's curse. Of her joining Agatha in every single one of her mad fantasies, of never giving up the fight for Agatha and her freedom, even if it meant they would return to a dynamic Agatha knew, and had always known, hurt Rio the most.

Of Rio on The Road, helping her, protecting her, denying her too, because she knew a completely lucid Agatha would have an entirely different perspective on any intimacy they might share.

And finally of Rio now, breaking in her arms after bearing the weight of Agatha’s welfare for the past twelve months, at the detriment of the dead and the dying, and ultimately her own broken heart too.

“Rio,” Agatha whispered, drawing back only slightly as she failed as she always did at offering comfort, “I- don’t-“. She didn’t know what to say, still reeling herself from having three-hundred-and-fifty years’ worth of memories stuffed back into her consciousness, amidst the overwhelming realisation of just how devoted her wife was to her happiness.

Agatha leaner in close again and cradled Rio’s jaw with her palms, gently pulling her face upwards. She allowed her eyes to flicker over Rio’s features, features that only an hour ago had been appealing and familiar but didn’t hold any of the history her current examination did.

Rio stared back, her eyes wide and urgent, yet almost shielded, like a dog who was wary of an unpredictable owner, hoping desperately for love but expecting a strike.

So, with the right words absent from both her throat and mind, Agatha did the only thing she could think to do. And admittedly, the only thing she wanted to do too. She leaned in even closer and covered Rio’s mouth with her own, claiming her lips with an intensity that shocked both of them.

Rio yielded instantly, arching into Agatha like a flower would lean toward the sun, until, much to Agatha’s surprise Rio pulled away with a sharp jerk of her head. Agatha drew back too, unsure what had perturbed Rio so, only to find her looking, even more bizarrely, far more overwrought than she had before.

Rio bowed her head, her shoulders slumping and shaking as though she were crying. Panicked at Rio’s reaction, Agatha cradled her jaw and tried to pull her face upwards again.

“What is it? What’s wrong sweetheart? I’m here, I’m back,” she tried to reassure her softly, “I remember everything, all of it. I remember before Wanda, I remember the hex, and I remember every moment after, when you looked after me so well”.

Agatha couldn’t control her own softness, entirely overtaken by her need to soothe Rio’s despair. Despair that she didn’t entirely understand however, considering Agatha was whole once more and they were standing together, embracing, which was at least as far as Agatha knew, all Rio had wanted for the span of several lifetimes.

“I know,” Rio sighed, finally opening her eyes to stare into Agatha’s with unmitigated devastation, “but I have to tell you something”.

Agatha frowned, not expecting any sort of confession from her, “what is it?”

Rio looked beyond Agatha then, over her shoulder towards where the others were stood in a small circle of their own, laughing and recounting The Road they had just walked and the battle they had just won.

Rio closed her eyes as though bracing herself for what she was about to say, before they snapped open again, now with a firm, determined glint sparking in their depths, even through the sheen of her unspent tears, “Billy is Wanda’s child”.

Agatha smiled with relief, as she felt her shoulders relax in response to Rio’s words. If this was the grand reveal, Rio didn’t need to worry. Agatha had figured that out days ago. But before she could say anything, Rio continued to speak, her voice as solemn as a funeral knell.

“Or at least the soul of Wanda’s child has claimed the body of William Kaplan, a boy who died a year ago. A boy whose body is owed to the universe”.

Agatha frowned at Rio’s words, her sharp mind moving the pieces into place quickly.

Yet once again, before Agatha could say anything, Rio clarified her point, making her intention crystal clear.

“He is an abomination, and he is disrupting the sacred balance. I have to take him”.

The weight of what Rio was implying and the reality of what she was going to do settled on Agatha like the weight of an avalanche after an earthquake.

“No… No! It cannot be!” She could hear the panic in her own voice, as thoughts of Billy spun through her mind; of the waste of power, of the waste of youth, of the waste of sheer fucking goodness; something this planet was in dire need of.

And finally of how much Billy reminded her of another boy, another boy whose youth was stolen from him, who was pure, and good, and kind .

She took a stumbling step away from Rio, breaking their embrace as all of that anger, anger that still felt painfully new from her memories recent restoration in her mind, started to pour toward the surface of her skin, branding her with the heat of her fury.

Rio nodded slowly, as though she was merely a messenger and not the decider of these things, “it must be”.

And like a robot pre-programmed to say the lines of a script, one written three hundred years ago beneath the weighty boughs of dark evergreen’s, Agatha started begging, “ please let him live. Please my love! Please! ”

Rio sagged upon hearing Agatha’s pleading, just as Agatha gasped and clenched her eyes tightly together. For upon the completion of her final ‘ please ’ memories of her own son started to blossom behind her eyelids like poppies opening under the weight of morning dew.

Memories of Nicky smiling at her after waking from a nap, his head resting in her lap; of Nicky stood on a barrel and singing his small heart out, her maternal pride glowing golden in her heart; of Nicky coughing, a child so sickly Death was always stalking him.

A child Death was always stalking.

Death: the witch stood in front of her.

The witch stood in front of her: her wife, Rio , who she was still irrecoverably, desperately, painfully in love with.

Her wife, Rio: who was planning on taking a child from her.

Again.

It takes a Coven

Chapter Notes

Yoooooo, we made it guys! The penultimate chapter is here!

I thought that last one was long, yet this ones even longer! So brace yourselves for a bit of a marathon-read squad.

Thank you again for all of the lovely comments of support, especially on that last chapter where you were all very lovely about me enduring the struggle of writing chapter 18. You guys are so sweet, and this whole fic would have been abandoned a while ago if it wasn't for you and your endless well of support and kindness, so truly thank you so much!

I am praying this chapter will live up to expectations and hoping ardently that you enjoy it! (Please note the rating change too!)

This one's a rollercoaster gang, but hold on tight and trust the process!

So, without much else to say please enjoy! <3

RIO

The bolt of purple magic that struck her in the sternum wasn’t much of a surprise, nor did it hurt all that badly.

Not in the physical sense, at least.

She should have predicted it really. She should have known that an Agatha reeling from countless realisations since having her memories force themselves back into her consciousness would react like a scared dog; growling and snapping at the closest hand, which in this case, and most of them throughout time, was Rio. And even as she was thrown backwards to land in a heap of dark robes on the dew-kissed grass, she knew why her wife had thrown a bolt of magic at her, she understood the how and the what of it all.

Still, she would take the physical pain of Agatha's magic over the emotional torment of knowing she was going to lose her again, or more patently, had already lost her again.

For it was true and it was happening; the ultimate cosmic joke was already in motion. The ruinous jest of successfully transforming Rio into Sisyphus, and Agatha the relentless boulder she was never close enough or strong enough to prevent rolling away, out of her reach time and time again.

Rio allowed herself a minute to simply feel it as she lay on the grass, to draw that aching, familiar weight across her shoulders; one she had worn since their child’s life was snuffed out and she had been forced to collect him, to guide him home. It was the weight of her love for her wife, which grew all the more heavy the longer she existed in a world in which Agatha didn’t want her anymore.

A world she had been so close to banishing. A world that for a few short months had been shielded from view by Agatha’s love, which had once more been unfettered and as clear as the sun on a cloudless day, fuelling a spark of hope to dance within her blackened heart at the chance of reconcilement.

And then once she had let those dark, familiar feelings root down into the core of her soul, she did as she always did when facing the reality of Agatha's hatred. She wrapped her duty around her shoulders and used it as a shield to guard her from every human reaction she was so close to losing herself to. Which at this point, primarily consisted of falling to her knees and screaming with the injustice of it all.

On steady feet she hauled herself up to standing. She glanced around warily for a brief moment, searching the expressions of the other coven members. For she was sure they wouldn’t hesitate to throw their own beams of arcane energy her way the moment they too learned what Rio was planning to do.

It was clear they still didn’t know though, for all of their faces had dropped with expressions of shock, not disgust.

The second bolt of purple light struck her in the chest and this time it stung; the equivalent of a bee sting, or so she had been led to believe. Being Death had it’s perks after all, and not really suffering physical pain was one of them, even if her battered heart hadn’t yet received that particular memo from the universe, for it continued to scream at her from it's prison beneath her ribs.

Still, Agatha’s strike, which was entirely fuelled by her grief and rage, not to mention powered by the first rush of magic she had tasted in a year, was as powerful as ever, throwing Rio backwards to land on the same patch of grass as before, only this time flattened from her previous landing.

“ Fight back! ” Agatha thundered from across the yard, her fury causing magic to spark around her figure, illuminating the dark garden with streaks of purple light.

Rio swiped the back of her hand over her bleeding lip; the result of her front tooth slicing through soft skin the moment she made impact with the ground, and hauled herself back to her feet.

Agatha was staring at her, her face flooding with a mix of emotions like the ebb and flow of the tide: her anger at what Rio was planning to do; her grief at being in this position again , of caring so much for a child who was fated to die; her evident guilt for making Rio bleed, for throwing her magic at her as though Rio was little more than an errant fly; and finally, and most painfully of all, her love for Rio too, beaming back at her from those stormy eyes, as though Rio was to blame for it all, as though Rio had chosen this fate for herself and damned them both for the sheer the hell of it.

“ Damn you, fight back! ” Agatha roared as Rio simply stood there, waiting for her to work herself past this rush of anger so she could try and explain to the others, and most importantly of all, Billy, what needed to happen and why.

“No,” Rio said, voice quiet and sure. She would allow Agatha this moment, this burst of temper that she needed to release. It would make it all a lot easier after all, for she would burn herself out eventually.

Agatha looked as shocked by Rio’s refusal to fight than if she had turned around and sent an entire tempest toward her, screaming furiously and ripping tiles from roofs. Her jaw dropped, and her eyes glistened as the love beating in her heart for Rio, the love Rio knew existed because she could feel it in the heat of Agatha’s anger, started to roil with anguish. She tempered it quickly though, forcing her lip to curl back with disdain instead, as Agatha once again sent a bolt of purple fire screaming towards her.

Although it certainly said a lot, or at least it did to Rio’s poor hopeful heart, that this particular shot fell short and struck the soil at her feet, scorching the grass to blackened blades.

“ Fucking fight me! ”

“No,” Rio said again, squaring her jaw determinedly as she turned away from Agatha to sweep closer to the gaggle of witches still watching them with slack-jawed surprise.

“Billy,” Rio murmured, causing him to turn to her with wide, curious eyes.

“ No! You stay away from him!” Agatha’s voice came from just behind her; shrill, desperate, and furiously heartbroken.

Rio closed her eyes, breathing deeply to keep herself calm, to focus on the job at hand, and to continue pushing on as her duty and the sacred balance demanded.

“Billy,” she said again, with an apologetic edge to both her expression and tone, “you need to come with me”.

She watched his shock morph into confusion, “come with you? To where?”

“What is going on?” Jen asked, sweeping forward to stand beside Billy and place a protective hand on his arm. She turned toward Lilia and Alice, silently requesting support for her bid for answers.

Alice stepped forward too. Her hands were in her pockets, and she looked calm, but it was clear to see her senses were on high alert and she was primed to act if required. “Yea guys,” she said, voice as deceptively calm as her exterior, “what the hell’s got the pair of you so wrung out?”

Lilia however was once again out of it, her eyes vacant and lips drooping slightly as she journeyed through time, filling in the gaps of her own knowledge, stealing secrets from the past and hindsight from the future.

Deciding it would be easier to address Billy directly and ignore the others, Rio held out a hand, “Billy, you know as well as I do what this is about”. She smiled at him, hoping her expression was one of gentle acceptance and not the wild, feral grin that so often fell across her face.

He shook his head, appearing confused until the truth of Rio’s words started to dawn on him. He paled and brought a shaky hand up to run through his hair, “I- I don’t- you mean?”

However, before she could respond with words of reassurance or anything resembling an explanation, she was once again swept off her feet, only this time it wasn’t by magic.

Agatha had tackled her away from Teen. Probably, Rio thought as she flew through the air, out of both frustration over being ignored, and her need to protect yet another young soul from Rio’s deathly grasp, putting up the fight she was never given the chance to when it came to their own child.

They landed in a heap of robes and hair, rolling several times until they skidded to a halt with Agatha pinning Rio beneath her, as a snarl curled her lip up into something furious and wild.

“I said no ,” she hissed, lowering her face to Rio’s until they were a breath’s width apart, “no. You can’t have him, you can’t take him. Not this time, not again ”.

Rio sighed once more, feeling the weight of everything pressing down on her. It made her feel like all of the physicality she had gained and once adored through possessing a body was beginning to crush her.

“I have to. The threads of the universe will unravel if I don’t. You’ll curse everyone, including him, to a far worse fate if I don’t take him with me," she said tiredly, trying to appeal to Agatha with reason. But she should have known better; Agatha Harkness is many things, but reasonable has never been one of them.

“The world can fucking burn , for all I care,” she growled, “I won’t let you take him”.

“Agatha!” Jen cried, storming over to try and push her off of Rio, “can someone explain what the fuck is going on please? I feel like I have whiplash”.

Agatha refused to be moved though, tightening her grip on Rio’s wrists until her nails dug into her flesh and tensing her thighs on Rio’s hips, like a cowboy might on a bucking horse, determined to not be thrown from their saddle.

It wasn’t until Billy, as quiet and as fearful as a mouse facing down a lion, took a few steps closer and sunk to his knees beside them that Agatha's grip waivered slightly. Rio turned her head to face him, still pinned beneath her wife.

“It’s because this body isn’t mine, isn’t it?” He asked quietly.

Rio felt like sobbing as she looked up at him, at this boy who she had known for the same amount of time as Agatha had, who she could so plainly see her own child in, in the the gestures of kindness he handed out without expectation or fallacy. At this child she was going to have to take from the woman she loved above everything else, at the pain she was forcing Agatha to feel, at knowing there was nothing that could be done to rewrite this tragic ending.

“Yes kid, it is”.

He closed his eyes, grieving for a life he never got to live before opening them once more, “I didn’t think it was like... illegal”.

Rio chuckled wetly, before wincing the moment Agatha’s hands tightened at witnessing their interaction, evidently moved at seeing the teenager she had taken under her wing bonding with the woman she still loved, as much as she might despise and deny that particular truth.

“Illegal is one word for it,” she said through a weak smile, again attempting to offer comfort.

He attempted to smile back at her before a teary sniffle disrupting it’s bloom, forcing it into becoming more of a grimace, “and if I don’t come with you? If I refuse?”

Her responding chuckle was far more genuine at that particular response, for it was such a human thing to say when facing down death, the question of: does it have to be now?

“It would be bad kid, for everyone”.

“Everyone?”

“Every single soul who has ever existed, who exists right now, and who is fated to exist in the future”.

He drew in a ragged breath, obviously shocked at the ripples his stolen existence has had on the universe and it’s plans. “Well then,” he finally breathed, suddenly sounding far older than his actual age, “I suppose that answers that question then”.

“ No! ” Agatha hissed again, still pinning Rio beneath her as she whipped her head back and forth between Rio’s turned face and Teen’s, who was still staring back at Rio with a mix of fear and determination. “Teen don’t you dare give in to this. You’re a witch , you’re a survivor . You don’t need to go with her just because she tells you to. You can fight ; you can win! ”

His responding words, not that he knew it at the time unlike Rio, had the power to cut Agatha to her core, “I- I can’t , it’s not right. I can’t expect the world to suffer so I can keep living, what sort of life would that be? I’d die from guilt before I took two steps in the opposite direction”.

Agatha’s mouth quickly dropped to argue back; Rio could tell from the slant of her eyebrows and the curl of her lip. However, she didn’t get the opportunity to push her point because another voice suddenly sounded out from a few feet away.

“There is another way, one previously lost to time… but I am fortunate enough to possess a unique two-way ticket to the past and have received consultation from a very wise, and very old woman”.

It was Lilia, returned from her travels.

Everyone’s focus fell to her as she strode forward on confident feet, her chin tilted up regally. She was truly the Queen of Cups in that moment, stepping forward to guide them all towards resolution.

“Consultation with who?” Alice asked, voice sceptical.

Lilia smiled, looking fond as she spoke of the woman who had apparently provided her with the answer to their issue. “my Maestra from Sicily. An exceptionally wise witch, one who had already lived for centuries before she met her demise from influenza when I was a mere girl. She spoke of a spell, a specific incantation that can only be spoken by a true coven to try and save the soul of one of their own”.

Rio felt a flare of unease at Lilia’s words, for what she said wasn't entirely untrue. Ample spells had indeed come in and out of existence over the years as humans did as they were determined to do; fight Rio tooth and nail over a few more measly years of unexceptional life.

Still, the different range of spells that existed, and even more so, those that were actually effective and didn’t end up sucking the life from the coven in question were rare. Most of them had been lost to the consistent march of time.

Rio had never felt much fondness for them either if truth be told, for they caused complications in a process that should be, as nature dictated, straight forward and simple.

Realising things were spiralling out of her control and in a direction she didn't care for, she tried to roll Agatha off of her and get up. But Agatha, stubborn witch that she was, refused to be moved.

“Agatha,” Rio said, voice stern, “get off”.

Agatha scowled down at her, “what’s the matter? You’ve been begging to be under me for centuries”.

Rio frowned heavily, her heart shuddering painfully at Agatha using Rio's heartbreak as a cruel jibe, one that hit home, Just as she intended it to.

“Get off Agatha, let me up,” Rio insisted, trying to push upwards just as Agatha’s hands started to spark with purple light to keep holding her down.

Rio sighed and waved her hand, which was still partially trapped beneath Agatha’s, summoning vines to shoot from the ground and wrap around Agatha’s wrists, ankles, and waist, dragging her off of Rio with a shrill cry of rage.

Rio stood, dusting herself off as she turned to face Lilia, who was watching her with a knowing smirk tugging at the corner of her lips. Evidently, the divination witch knew exactly how this whole moment played out.

It was an unnerving moment for a deity; facing a mortal who knew more than you. It was a strange, abstract sensation, one that she didn’t enjoy.

She glanced toward Agatha, who she had spelled her vines to tie to a decorative trellis out of the way, who was now shouting furiously at being bound to a piece of garden furniture. Agatha would be furious at Rio for putting her in such a demeaning position, but Agatha already hated her, so what was one more slight in comparison to Rio's other offences, and she needed space and time to think, to listen to Lilia and figure out if this so-called spell actually held any weight.

“What spell do you speak of witch?” Rio demanded, wrapping her robe around herself in an attempt to appear like the untouchable deity she should be, even though they had all seen her tackled to the ground by her furious wife only ten minutes earlier.

“The Nexus Debitorum : an exchange of Irreformable souls for another life, one far more deserving,” Lilia’s voice was confident, highlighting her certainty over this particular spell and it's chances of success.

Rio’s eyebrows shot up high on her forehead, surprised that this was the spell Lilia intended to try. It was real for one thing, a genuine spell that did indeed work to exchange the souls of a few evildoers to gain a second chance for somebody the universe considered worthy.

It was an exceptionally tricky endeavour to complete however, not only because the souls offered up in exchange had to be truly beyond any semblance of reformation or genuine remorse, but also the soul who was being bargained on behalf of had to have proven themselves to the universe in their lifetime; however short it might have been. In other words, they had to have something worth exchanging for, something that Rio herself would want or deign worth saving.

It wasn’t a process to be taken lately, nor was it hardly ever successful. Which was why it had quite promptly fallen out of favour as an option to save a loved one.

“The Nexus-What? ” Alice asked, voice pitched up with evident disbelief, before turning to Jen to share a frustrated, bemused expression. "Guys, seriously. Please fill us in, we have no clue what the hell any of you are talking about?”

“Rio’s Death isn't she!? The evil bitch!” Agatha heckled from her trellis, “Billy stole a dying body when the scarlet witch destroyed her hex over Westview. She wants to take him because his existence upsets her precious balance ”.

She spat the word balance mockingly as though it were the root of all evil, as though Rio was evil, as though she gained personal joy and fulfilment from doing simply what nature demanded.

Sighing Rio pinched the bridge of her nose as the other’s gasped in horror, having put together the deeper meaning beneath Agatha’s words.

“Take him?” Alice repeated, “you mean like, take him to the other side?”

“Oh shit ,” Jen breathed out, eyes now wide with dawning understanding.

“But she won’t,” Lilia drawled out, sounding as confident as a woman who had seen into the future would, “because the Nexus Debitorum will work”.

“Okay!” Alice sighed out, frustrated once more, “again, please guys. Please explain what the fuck is the Nexus Debitorum is for those of us who haven’t been alive since the dawn of god-damned time”.

Lilia started to speak as though she were a tutor in a lecture hall, “ Nexus Debitorum is Latin, and it translates roughly to ' debt connection '. It's a complicated rite for a coven to complete. If a coven collects enough souls, souls without hope for reformation, souls of those evil enough to continuously do harm without an ounce of remorse, they can be offered up to Death..." Lilia gestured toward Rio, as though she were merely a cardboard cut-out of the grim reaper being presented for educations sake, "...In exchange for one single life. But that life has to be deemed worthy, and it has to possess something Death desires, or at least something Death considers worth saving”.

“Why do they have to be evil souls?” Jen asked with a heavy frown on her face.

“Because they cease to exist,” Lilia answered simply. “It’s a punishment worse than death. They are stitched back into the fabric of everything, losing any semblance of sentience; their energy absorbed and their personhood, everything that made them who they are simply… gone; disappearing entirely from the record of humanity and denied ever crossing over into the great beyond, which is all of our destiny".

Lilia turned to Rio then, “isn’t that right Rio? ”

She said Rio’s name as though it were a name Rio had simply made up then and there, as though she was merely humouring her by saying it. Which was frustrating, because Rio had made it up. But it had been her name for over three centuries now, so to hear it spoken in such a flippant manner made her brows furrow with offence.

Lilia’s smirk wasn’t remedied by her evident displeasure though, for it was clear she had returned from her latest voyage through time with all of the answers, and apparently far more attitude than she had possessed a mere hour ago.

“The spell exists,” Rio admitted, not allowing any level of opinion to bleed through into her tone, “but it has not been used or even attempted for centuries”.

“Well surely it's worth a try?” Alice asked, voice hopeful and filled with youthful optimism.

“And where …” Rio drawled, glancing from each set of eyes surrounding her; except for the pair burning into her from a few feet away, eyes the colour of an angry ocean tempest, “...exactly are you going to gather eight spiteful souls from in such a short space of time, hmm?”

None of them could answer her, so Rio pushed her point, “not to mention, that particular spell has to be attempted whilst the soul of the saved is hovering between this realm and the next. It can’t be performed before or after”.

A heavy silence descended then as the reality of what Lilia was proposing fell upon all of their shoulders, at the fact in order to be saved, Teen would have to be killed; his lungs frozen from drawing breath, his heart stopped from continuing it’s rhythmic beating.

Once again, a bolt of purple light to the stomach broke up the moment, as Agatha, who had finally burned through the thorny vines holding her captive, threw another strike of magic at Rio; this time hitting right on target.

Rio was shunted backwards a few paces, doubling over with the intensity of the impact, as Agatha swept forward with determination burning in her eyes.

“I’ll do it,” she said, voice dark with fury, “I’ll kill him. If it means he’ll live, I’ll do it”.

Rio’s temper flared, frustrated at consistently being on this side of these types of debates; arguing for natural balance, for the survival of the fucking universe, for the simple processes of life and death to be respected, and at being made to feel like the purest form of evil, for simply providing a service as vital to the continuation of life as birth.

After all, as much as Agatha would argue the point, Rio was no more evil than fungus rotting wood, or an insect gnawing on fallen leaves.

Put simply, she was doing her fucking job.

Yet Agatha still insisted on treating her like Rio did all of these things out of choice . As though Rio wasn’t a creature entirely bound by whatever the universe dictated to be law.

“You still need eight souls that are beyond saving,” Rio growled, folding her arms across her chest stubbornly.

Agatha’s eyes narrowed in that way they did whenever she knew Rio was withholding something, something important.

“We have at least four souls beyond saving,” Agatha said pointedly, gesturing around the yard at the bodies sprawled across the lawn, each one a crumpled figure of dark cloth and black lace. “And I’m sure I could find four more with no real issue," she shrugged, unphased at the thought of stealing a few more lives. The irony apparently entirely lost on her that she was willing to kill in order to preserve.

And she thinks Rio is the evil one.

“I saw you collecting them too,” Agatha pressed when Rio didn’t say anything, eyes as flinty as her voice. Evidently any warmth she had been feeling towards Rio following their reunion had been burned away by the heat of her anger, like a spring frost melting under the full glare of the sun's beaming light. “You were collecting them in a jar, and I don’t want to hear a single argument about how the Salem Seven are bound for anywhere other than the darkest pits of hell. At least this way their pointless lives will be given a shred of meaning”.

Rio looked around, feeling entirely outnumbered.

Not to mention, a part of her was entirely too eager to resolve this in a way that didn’t involve her taking another child from her wife.

Perhaps if it was possible, perhaps if it could be done, then she should allow it to be so.

Or at least she should allow them to try.

She bit her lip, thinking deeply on the possible outcomes, on whether attempting this particular sacrament would have any overtly negative impacts on the processes of the world, or whether this too would be an acceptable trade, one the universe blesses as justice.

Rio paused, glancing from one face to the next, taking in each of their expressions: Lilia’s small, knowing smirk; Jen’s wide-eyed frown; Alice, whose brows were drawn close together, carving a wrinkle into the skin between them; Billy, who was pale and shaking, but trying so hard to be brave whilst his demise was discussed so openly.

Before finally, her heavy gaze landed where it was always destined to, directly onto Agatha who was already staring back at her with a fierce, defensive scowl. She was glaring at her as though Rio were the enemy that her coven required defending from, as though Rio was no longer considered one of them anymore, as though Rio hadn’t fought alongside them through The Road's countless trials and tribulations.

It was that final vision, and the agonising knowledge that she would always exist within her love’s mind as an evil villain, that forced a trembling confession from between her lips, “I have four more”.

One of Agatha’s eyebrows arched curiously, “you have four what? Four more souls?”

Rio looked down, feeling caught. She had never actually intended on telling Agatha what she had done to her mother after the cabin; she had thought her wife need not endure another moment with that wretched woman at the forefront of her thoughts.

Alas fate, as it so often did, had deigned to push her down a different path.

She glanced back up, finding her gaze caught immediately by Agatha’s steely one once more, a gaze that always won in the end.

“The rest of the Salem Seven and… your mother,” she admitted, deciding it best to just admit the truth quickly, “I have your mother’s soul in there too”.

Agatha’s jaw dropped, “My mother?! ”

Rio shifted her weight from foot to foot, searching for the right words, words that might explain why, “I needed to deal with her, it’s my job”.

“ Rio ,” Agatha’s voice was sharp and pointed. Her name was an order for an explanation.

“I didn’t have time to decide what to do with her right then, and it was a good job I didn’t dally considering you were drowning at the bottom of a mud-pit by that point”.

Agatha's other eyebrow arching upwards to join it's twin was the only response she received, prompting her to continue explaining.

“So I just... caught her. I wanted time to think it through, to figure out a fitting punishment for the woman who tormented you..." Rio felt a spark of warmth light in her chest, burning the chill from her bones at Agatha’s current expression, at how it had softened ever so slightly towards her, “...whose memory still torments you. She didn't deserve a peaceful reaping, and she certainly doesn’t deserve eternal peace. I wanted her to suffer, and I wanted to take my time making it so”.

Agatha’s eyes glistened as she stared at Rio, first with tears and then with wonder. It was clear she was once again struggling to compartmentalise all of the feelings she was currently feeling, the same feelings she had spent a century burying beneath burning hatred whilst trying to keep Rio at arm’s length, intent on giving the impression that she was neither interested nor affected by anything Rio did or said.

After a stilted pause, one in which Agatha had simply stared at Rio as though trying to decide whether to throttle her or kiss her, she sniffed and looked away, throwing up an errant, nonchalant hand, “well, there we go then. Eight hideous souls ready to be exchanged”.

“I still need to be worthy of saving,” Teen said quietly, nervously glancing between the two of them.

Now that was an easy enough question to answer, and even though Agatha thought she was evil, and even though she thought of Rio as little more than a monster who gleefully devoured the souls of innocent children to spite grieving parents, Rio felt the impulse to reassure him all the same.

“You are worthy of saving Billy, that would have been clear to see even if we hadn’t travelled The Witches Road together”.

A pleased smile lifted one side of his face, before it drooped once more, “but I have to possess something you consider worth saving". He glanced at each of them, hoping for a hint or a clue to the answer to his quandary, “but I don’t have anything worth saving, not worthy of this , at least”.

Alice and Jen looked at one another hopelessly, each of them shrugging in turn to show they were out of ideas. Even Lilia looked unsure for the first time since flashing back from the past.

It was, of course, Agatha who swept closer to Rio, who had once again softened her eyes to the point Rio knew she was about to be played like a god-damned fiddle.

Still, even with that knowledge, she found herself leaning into the palm Agatha lifted to cup her jaw. With firm but gentle pressure, she guided Rio’s face toward her own, “he does own something you value, sweetheart”.

Weak fool that she knew herself to be, Rio could do nothing but nuzzle into Agatha’s warm palm, relishing the brush of her skin against her cheek, “and what would that be my love?”

“He owns your debt, Rio. Twice over too, if I’m not mistaken”.

Rio blinked, “my debts?”

“He saved your wife’s life. Twice . Once on The Road, and once right here when he trusted me enough to shoot a bolt of magic into my heart”.

Rio’s eyes widened with realisation, for the words Agatha spoke were true. He had indeed saved Agatha's life, twice .

Agatha drew Rio's attention back from her own thoughts with light pressure on her jaw, “do you not count that as something worthy of value? Something worthy of mercy and trade? ”

She was biting her lip, staring imploringly into Rio’s eyes as her thumb swept backwards and forwards across the line of Rio’s cheekbone.

Rio knew she was being manipulated, but she still wasn’t strong enough to resist it all the same.

“I do,” Rio said, her voice a solemn vow, “I value it above everything ”.

Agatha nodded slowly, like a snake hypnotising a mouse with wide, captivating eyes before it eventually struck out to pierce it's victims heart and pump it full of venom, “so, he does have something you want, doesn’t he? You want to clear the debt you owe him; you want to thank him for saving my life”.

Rio swallowed once, her eyes flickering across Agatha’s face. It was hard to get an honest read on her right now, for she was wrapped up so tightly behind her walls, all of the walls Rio had spent the past few months slowly breaking down again. Rio knew, after all, what Agatha’s mask looked like. She knew what it looked like when she wore the face of a woman who was manipulating for the sake of a scheme, as though Rio was little more than a mark who needed a little push to further one of her ploys and not her actual wife.

Her eyes drifted then, from Agatha’s face to Billy’s, who was still stood beside them all, shaking and pale, evidently not feeling confident in his ownership of Death's debts, debts she would indeed be willing to pay.

“Alright Agatha,” Rio drawled, keeping her eyes on Billy and taking a step backwards, suddenly in dire need of space from her wife's fake affection, no longer able to stomach false fondness from the woman she was willing to pause death for. Looking around she stared at each of them in turn, ensuring her gaze was solemn enough and weighted honestly with the task ahead, "you have my permission to attempt such a feat. But heed my warning, it doesn’t always work and it doesn’t always take”.

Her gaze fell upon Agatha’s once more, who now she had gotten from Rio what she desired, had taken to scowling at her as Rio spoke her final warning, “the universe will claim it’s pound of flesh either way. It always does”.

And with that she pulled the jar of souls from her robe, placed them on the ground at Agatha’s feet and drifted away to wait in the shadows, gifting them time to prepare for the ceremony that they were determined to attempt. Unwilling too, to stand there and be the focus of her wife’s disdain for another moment longer.

XXXXXX

AGATHA

with the souls already collected, it hadn’t taken them long to prepare.

In fact the preparations were simple:

A circle carved into the earth by Alice; their protection witch.

A blessing from Jen, who sprinkled her quickly brewed concoction over the engraved circle in generous doses; their potions witch.

Lilia, their divination witch, having taken heed from her Maestra, was designing the positions of their ceremony from the ways of old, crafting in her mind's eye the precise tableau their coven must create in order to complete the sacrement correctly.

Rio, their green witch, had inadvertently completed her part of the ritual already by providing them with a jar of recently harvested souls.

Agatha, their death witch, hadn’t asked to borrow Rio’s knife for her dark deed.

Instead she had stalked after Rio, following her into the dark shadows cast by the overhanging canopy, where they were hidden from view from the others who were still completing their preparations. There she had pinned Rio against the rough bark of an old oak tree with rougher hands and drawn the blade from it’s sheath on Rio's belt with a painfully slow drag. Their eyes had been locked the entire time, their gazes holding a myriad of conversations simultaneously; questions and answers, accusations and admissions, declarations and detestations.

Then, as though not entirely in control of her own impulses, Agatha found herself jerking closer to Rio in a singular jagged movement, as though her desire to capture Rio’s mouth, to punish her carnally for all she had done to their love had overtaken her body without prior thought or restraint. Fortunately, she managed to gain control of herself just as quickly, and before her lips could brush Rio’s and she lost herself completely to a temptation that was agonisingly painful to resist, she hauled herself backwards, stumbling away from the warmth of Rio’s body as though it had burned her. She turned on unsteady feet and with ragged breathing returned to the others, leaving Rio in the lonely shadows of the yard, berating herself internally for being so damn fickle the entire time.

For Agatha Harkness truly was the definition of heart vs head. Of impulse vs restraint. Of hate vs love.

Her mind felt like a constant battlefield when it came to Rio, especially now, with that same familiar fight feeling harder than it ever had before. It was a constant thing; a never-ending scrimmage to maintain this level of anger at the woman she wanted, more than anything, to turn and collapse into.

The others didn't say anything about her harried appearance, much to her relief, and after a few more long, tense minutes they were ready to begin.

Billy, as directed by Lilia, lay in the centre of the circle with his arms and legs stretched out; their very own renaissance man.

Agatha stood at his head, inside the carved circle so her visage would be upside down from his perspective. She swallowed nervously whilst looking down at him, taking note of just how young he looked, of how she would be his murderer if this all went wrong. Her thoughts spiralled slightly, for the realisation hit her then, that if that was indeed the case and he did actually die, his death would be the first she would both cause and mourn. An absurd thought for a serial killer, but alas it was the one haunting her as she looked down at him. Their eyes met and she attempted to give him a cocky grin, a grin that said you’ve beaten Death before, we’ll beat her again together .

Alice and Jen stood on either side of the circle, although they were outside of it. Their hands were raised, pressing forward and flat as though pushing against a solid barrier.

Lilia stood on a garden chair behind Agatha, the overseer of all. She was to lead to incantation and the ceremony, as though she was a conductor and they her grand orchestra.

And Rio, Rio stood at his feet. A dark wraith wrapped in darker robes, glaring at the scene with eyes that shone with barely hidden grief. Grief Agatha could see plainly, grief that Agatha wanted to heal.

But her fury wouldn’t allow her to soften, not right now, not until this was done and Billy was safe.

Death had to wait to be welcomed in to this particular ceremony Lilia had told them, like the vampires of old, waiting to be invited to cross the threshold into an unsuspecting victim's residence.

“ Silence! ” Lilia called out, her tone ancient and regal.

They all did as ordered; even the night-time crickets and the leaves fluttering in the breeze seemed to take heed of her order and faded into silence.

“This coven of mine has convened here today with intention of exchanging eight irredeemable souls to the majesty of the universe, in exchange for one singular soul. The soul of Billy Maximoff, a witch of our coven, a coven of mavericks joined together by the desire to unite and protect this young life from passing through that bleak veil and onwards still to where we cannot reach him”.

No one spoke. The wind didn’t whistle, the birds didn't sing, and no small mammal scurried through the underbrush to make the grass sway and rustle.

Lilia glanced around at each of them before continuing, “Death. We summoned you here today to cast your judgement on Billy Maximoff. To ask you if you find his heart true, or if you find it wanting, and most importantly if this soul possesses something you yourself covet, something that only his continued existence on this plain can provide”.

Rio swept closer, cutting an intimidating figure with her humanity dissolved from her person, leaving her skeletal and majestic beneath her dark hood. She was and always had been beautiful, and Agatha felt a lump start to burn in her throat at just how lonely she looked opposite her in the moonlight, as though she had already accepted the fact her place in this coven they had built together was merely temporary.

Shaking her head, she brought herself back to reality, forcing herself to focus on the ceremony at hand as Lilia continued to speak the words of the ancient sacrament, “Death. If it so pleases you, step forward into the circle if you are willing to consider our offering”.

Rio did so, pacing forward into the circle at Billy’s feet with a single graceful step.

“Death, you have accepted our invitation, we thank you”.

Agatha felt Lilia brush her shoulder and lean closer to whisper urgently, “ now , you need to do it now ”.

Agatha nodded and felt, for the first time, terrified to kill someone.

She gripped Rio’s knife tightly, finding comfort in the worn handle beneath her palm, smoothed over eons from Rio’s fingers holding it in just the same way. Breathing deeply, Agatha dropped to kneel over Billy’s head. Gently, she reached forward to move a few of his curls from his forehead with her other hand, which she noted with an absent thought, was shaking.

He smiled up at her, trying so hard to mask the fear she could see radiating through his tight expression. “Hey,” he breathed out, even now attempting levity to appease her. This boy, she couldn’t help but think, this dear boy so similar to her own.

“Hey,” she whispered back softly, “I’m sorry it has to be a knife. If I used magic it might interfere with the process, crossed streams and all that arcane nonsense”.

He eyed Rio’s curved knife nervously, gulping slightly before his widened eyes returned to her own, “it’s alright, at least if I survive this I’ll have a cool scar”.

Agatha smirked, feeling frustratingly endeared, “you mean when you survive this,” she insisted, “you'll have a cool scar. And guess what?”

“What?” He asked, wide-eyed and thankfully distracted enough, which is what she was aiming for.

“Boys dig scars,” she told him with a cheeky wink, before quicker than he would be able to flinch away from, she brought the knife up to thrust it down into his chest right through his heart. She left it there for a lingering moment before tugging it free with a grisly wrench to hold it by her side, where the blade started to drip scarlet beads onto the grass beside her feet.

Alice and Jen both flinched as she did so, choking back screams as a sharp, breathless gasp echoed out from behind her; all of them shocked at her fierce brutality, at how little she wavered when thrusting a knife through a teenagers ribcage.

How little they knew her still, how truly ruthless she could be.

Thankfully, Billy died quickly. He didn’t lay their writhing in agony, he didn’t scream or cry or beg, like any other number of people might have.

No, he simply coughed once, sputtered twice, and then drooped sideways with the smirk from Agatha’s last jest still frozen on his face.

In fact, it was Agatha who lost her composure, who whimpered loudly at his lax expression, at his glassy eyes. It was Agatha who was forced to stuff her sob back into her mouth with the flat of her palm, who then retreated on shaky feet to watch as Rio lifted one hand up towards the sky to draw Billy’s soul from his mouth, where it hovered just above blue lips, acting as the alter on which their dark exchange would occur.

“Death,” Lilia called out, her barely restrained horror evident in the warble Agatha could now hear in her voice, “we present to the universe these eight souls, eight souls cut from the darkest, most cruel fabric the cosmos possesses," she held up the jar and started to twist the lid free.

It was clear the souls of the Salem Seven and her mother could sense dark magic was afoot, for the glowing orbs behind the glass were vibrating, buzzing from side to side with the speedy flight of hummingbirds.

“We commit these souls to your grandness, and ask for these souls to be merged with you, to be threaded into your oblivion and removed from the cycle of life in exchange for this soul here,” Lilia gestured to life-force, providing the sign Agatha, Jen, and Alice had all been waiting for to do the same, each of them pointing a sparking finger at Billy’s soul as well.

“Are you willing to consider the trade?” Lilia asked, voice growing in confidence the longer she continued speaking.

“I am,” Rio intoned, her voice double-toned and bassy; appearing every bit the universe's ambassador in the shadowy darkness. Agatha would be lying if the figure Rio cut in that moment didn’t cause a frisson of electricity to zip up her spine. After all, knowing that Rio was entirely dedicated to her , that Agatha had a deity of Rio’s immensity at her beck and call, if she so desired that is, well, it was a pretty intoxicating sensation.

“What does this soul possess that you think interests me?” Rio asked plainly, the words falling from her mouth as though they were from a well-rehearsed script.

“This soul,” Lilia answered, continuing her part in this strange, dangerous dance, “possesses something you desire Death. He possesses absolution. Absolution of debts you owe him, two debts to be precise. For he saved the woman you love, the woman you soul-bonded with over three centuries ago. Does this, or does this does not hold worthy value to you? To be gifted forgiveness for these debts in exchange for saving his soul”.

Rio’s eyes found Agatha’s then like ships being called home through a storm, “I do, Lilia Calderu of Sicily. I crave absolution from these debts and hold nothing higher in my esteem than the safety of my wife”.

Agatha felt tears pool in her eyes at Rio’s words, that even now her focus was entirely on Agatha, on Agatha’s happiness, on her wellbeing.

“I thank you Death for answering our plea and our plight. Now, I must ask my sister-witches to chant the incantation, to expand our request outward and see if the universe agrees with it’s herald; that this is a debt worthy of payment, that these souls crafted from wicked matter are beyond reform, and that this soul,” she gestured toward Billy’s soul, shining blue and beautiful above his pale, still face, “is worthy of saving”.

They did as ordered and all of the coven, bar Rio who stood with her eyes closed and her lips parted, looking disarmingly melancholy and beautiful in the moonlight, started to chant the ancient words Lilia had taught them.

Over and over again, they repeated the incantation, and on the third repetition of the archaic song, Lilia released the lid on the jar, prompting the souls of her hideous mother and the Salem Seven to dart from their glass prison and attempt to fly for freedom.

They continued to chant, each of them keeping their eyes glued to the souls zipping through the night sky, glowing like large, bulbous fireflies, trying to escape the dangerous magic they could obviously feel thrumming around them.

Yet, as they reached the edge of the garden and started to slide through the heavy boughs of the dark overhanging canopy, Agatha felt her heart shudder fearfully in her chest, almost certain that her coven's plea had failed and the universe had declined their request. A single breath grew ragged in her lungs and she felt suddenly terrified to look down upon the boy she had killed, a boy she had murdered with a cold, curved knife.

Yet, before her grief could consume her she heard a resounding pop, as one of the fleeing souls quite literally exploded into a flash of raining sparks. Then, one by one, as though triggered by the first, each of the Salem Seven’s souls burst in a show of sparkling lights that fell to the earth like embers from a fire, glowing momentarily before fading to ash. Finally, there was only one soul left, her mother, who was zipping from side to side in a desperate bid to save herself.

But as they had all come to learn and as Rio had so aptly put it, the universe would claim it’s pound of flesh, one way or the other, and Agatha watched with dark delight as her mother’s soul came to a screeching halt, only to be devoured by the universe in a flurry of sparks, a universe hungry enough to consume her in one great big gulping bite.

Finally, Agatha breathed for the first time in what felt like hours as her eyes immediately dropped down to Billy’s face. She watched with desperate hope as his soul started to move too, although most alarmingly of all, not down towards his body but up higher away from it whilst swaying side to side, as though tempted to drift off and explore all of the secrets Death held close to her chest.

A curiosity that was confirmed the moment Rio’s eyes flickered from Agatha’s face, from where they had been planted this entire time, to her left where no one stood.

Or at least, no one Agatha could see.

Rio chuckled, eyes crinkling prettily even though her mouth was entirely bone and sinew, “yeah I know,” she said to thin air, pointing at her own face, “you're right, it would be a great Halloween costume”.

Agatha tilted her head, watching intently as Rio continued her ghostly conversation.

“I know, it feels cruel but trust me, they had it coming. Especially Agatha’s mother”.

“ – “

“Yes, I know. She’s a bitch. Or at least she was ,” Rio smirked at her own jest, before her smile widened at whatever Billy said in response.

“ – “

“I know, I understand your curiosity. But there are a lot of people here who have worked really hard to keep you around. You'll see it all in the end anyway, it doesn't remain a mystery for long. Trust me".

“ – “

“It’s only tempting you right now because being unattached from a body feels good. It’s lighter, and it feels like stretching muscles you didn’t even know needed stretching. But I don’t think Agatha would ever forgive you, or me for that matter, if you didn’t sink back into your body soon. And you have to do it soon, the windows for these sorts of exchanges are short and the universe is temperamental. It doesn’t like to have it’s goodwill abused or mocked”.

“ – “

Rio looked shocked at whatever Billy had said, before flushing heavily, an absurd image considering only half her face was flesh. Agatha felt suddenly desperate to know what Billy had said to her.

“Yes... well. I would be lying if I said my motives weren’t entirely selfish. Now please, do us all a favour, and just drop. That’s it, it will feel like that moment when your trying to go to sleep and it feels like your suddenly falling. That’s it Billy, just close your eyes and… drop ”.

The moment that final word left Rio’s lips, Billy’s soul darted back through his lips and his eyes shot open. He sat up quickly, hand to his chest clutching the spot Agatha had driven the knife into.

“ Holy shit ,” he gasped out through desperate pants. His hair was sticking up at all sorts of wild angles and blood was staining both his clothing and the patch of glass he was still sprawled on. He looked around at them all with wide, wild eyes, before finally panting out, “well, that was insane ”.

Agatha felt the breath that had been lodged painfully in her lungs finally wheeze out at seeing him filled with life once more. Relief nearly drowned her too, for the only real sign that he had recently been killed was a slight darkening of the bags beneath his eyes, as though all he needed to rectify any ailment he might have procured on his journey back to life was a good night’s sleep.

“ Billy ,” it was all she could find the strength to do, to breathe his name out into the night, so pleased that she could utter it with anything other than grief that it came out far more quiet and subdued than she ever normally was.

Her own relief was quite promptly overshadowed by Alice’s, who with a cry of joy promptly jumped atop him, tackling him back to the ground with a victorious, “fuck yeah, you’re alive!”

Jen, who was grinning broadly but still managing to maintain a semblance of dignity quickly had it ripped from her, because both Teen and Alice, with matching grins on their faces, each grabbed one of her wrists to tug her down atop their bundle.

Lilia, who had since clambered down from her chair, came to stand beside Agatha. She had a relieved grin blooming on her face and tear tracks shining on her cheeks as she watched the rest of their coven with affectionate eyes, laughing quietly when Jen tried to wriggle free from Alice and Teen’s hold, only to be quickly grabbed once more and tugged backwards to mix amongst their childish fit of limbs, despite her loud, dramatic protestations.

“Not tempted to join the party, Lilia?” Agatha drawled, her own amusement at their antics forcing her lips to quirk upwards too, as much as she would deny it if questioned.

“My back barely survived us piling out of that damned tower,” Lilia answered before asking rather abruptly, “where’s Rio?”

Agatha’s neck snapped up with telling speed to stare at the patch of darkness Rio had been standing in mere moments ago. Agatha scowled, aware of Rio’s ability to bend shadows to her will, and the fact she had the audacity to creep away the moment Agatha’s attention had been pulled down to the dying teenager at her feet. The knowledge that she had felt the need to do so in the first place settled heavily in Agatha’s stomach, prompting the reaction discontent so often did within her; anger.

Which wasn’t helped at all by the fact her feelings for Rio, which were still mixing violently together in her stomach, as they had been since she had regained her memories, were wavering from one state to the next with the ease of a button being pressed: turning her fury into guilt, guilt into yearning, yearning into love, love into lust, and then back to anger to restart to terrible cycle. All of which had been heightened and made worse through experiencing her greatest trauma a second time round, like some sort of sick mirror of past torments.

It was confusing .

She was confused .

And Rio dissolving into the darkness provided Agatha with a well-needed moment to simply think, to gather her thoughts, and try to stubbornly reassert to herself that she didn’t need Rio, that she was still furious at Rio, that she was far too angry to ever consider even trying to be with her again.

That the very thought of such an attempt was an impossibility.

And yet…

Her heart still started to keen as though it were a widow wailing at the graveside of a lost lover, broken at even the notion of Rio leaving her here alone.

It was a hideous thought, returning to the bleak reality of existing without Rio again, at having to force herself to pretend like her act of indifference didn’t cause her soul to freeze over as though her own personal winter had started to bloom beneath her ribs, spreading frost along bone and shooting it’s icy fingers into the depths of her lungs, turning warm breath to cold mist.

So, she did as she always did when feeling particularly vulnerable, she fell back on humour as a defence; humour and a forced nonchalance that hurt her heart to enact.

“I’m not her damn keeper Lilia, if she wanted to leave so badly she is free to do so,” Agatha snapped, before sniffing once and tilting her chin up arrogantly.

Lilia hummed from beside her, a knowing sound that immediately prompted Agatha’s hackles to rise. “Oh, I just thought… I thought I saw a different end-” she waved a wayward hand, chuckling as though she was simply an old woman rambling on about the weather. “Ignore me, I must have seen wrong”.

Agatha narrowed her eyes at the other witch, crossing her arms across her chest as she did so, “I know when I’m being played, Lilia”.

The older witch shrugged faux-innocently, “I have no idea what you’re implying. All I know is that woman has been by your side through every damn phase of this ordeal, and if that isn’t worth at least a conversation then I’m not sure what is”.

Agatha scowled at having the truth pointed out to her quite so bluntly. She was having a hard enough time battling with herself, without Lilia pointing out just how Rio had acted with such loyalty and devotion, how she had shown her love for Agatha with every action the had committed, and at how hard she had worked to keep her safe whilst Agatha had been unable to defend herself properly.

Jen, Alice, and Teen all clocked their conversation, as though Agatha’s emotional instability was a prime steak and the three of them a pack of hungry hyenas.

“Are you going to go get her?” Alice asked, as though the answer were an easy one. Which to Alice, Agatha couldn’t help but think bitterly, it must have been. None of them knew after all, they didn’t know the depths of her and Rio’s connection, the levels and tiers of devotion and pain that their relationship was constructed from, like the Frankenstein's monster of love stories.

“No. No, I am not,” Agatha ground out through clenched teeth, “she’s done some terrible things”. She threw an impatient hand at Billy, who was still laying on the ground with his hands behind his head, as though he was simply stargazing and not taking part in an ancient spell to save his soul, “she tried to take Teen!”

Billy angled his head to look at her from over his shoulder, “she was just doing her job Agatha,” he shrugged, the movement awkward from how he was still lying prone, “I did steal this body”.

“Yeah but-” her argument was promptly cut off by Jen, whose voice was as snarky as ever, evidently delighting in the team venture of emotionally beating Agatha to a pulp.

“No but’s. You’ve been both alive and a witch long enough to know certain laws are to be upheld. Death is one of them”.

Her no-nonsense tone was the worst of them so far, not at all helped by how simple Jen made it seem. As though Death merely was something to accept like Rio had said in the final trial, and not something to fight and beat into submission.

“Plus,” Alice drawled, climbing to her feet before offering a hand to both Jen and Teen to haul them up to stand beside her, “she didn’t even take him, she did her part without argument as far as I could see. Even persuaded him to come back”. She dug her elbow into Teen’s side, “when the little shit was going to drift off towards the light, after all the effort we put in to get him back”.

He flushed and rubbed a sheepish palm over the back of his neck, “I know, I know,” he droned, “I just- it’s hard to explain just how good it felt. It felt like complete freedom”. He sighed then shrugged, as a small embarrassed grin spread across his face, “at least I’m not afraid of death anymore”.

Agatha couldn’t share in his amusement, for it felt like her head was reeling, violently so.

It was hard enough experiencing the sensation of her fear masking itself as fury at the thought of pursuing Rio and having a genuinely honest conversation with her, without hearing everyone else’s opinion and input on the matter.

She didn’t know which impulse to give in to, and found circling between the two was making her dizzy.

Did she do as her stubborn streak wanted and insist she was better off without her, or did she give in to the louder voice and sprint from this garden to get her wife back where she belonged: by her side.

Should she give in to everything her heart was screaming out for so loudly it was getting harder and harder to ignore with every moment that passed without Rio in front of her, or silence it with an act of callous indifference that she knew would poison them both.

Her confusion must have been clear in her expression, because for the first time since she had met this rabble of witches their voices were warm, almost gentle when addressing her.

“Agatha,” Jen said softy, “it’s quite straightforward; do you love her?”

Agatha’s eyes shot up from staring at the ground, latching onto Jen’s dark gaze who was staring back at her with a small, knowing smile.

And Agatha, who felt her final defence crumble to the ground at such a simple question, could do nothing but nod.

“Then what are you doing still standing here kiddo? Go get our green witch back,” Lilia said softly, squeezing Agatha’s arm in what was, sadly, one of the first gestures of maternal affection Agatha had ever experienced.

Agatha paused for a mere moment as a thousand different thoughts rushed through her mind at once. Thoughts of Agnes, of the hex, of the Scarlet witch and her children, of Rio beside her; first to help her with her scheme and then simply to help her survive. The Road was next, of feeling so deeply drawn to her; to her smile, to her laugh, to her quirks and eccentricities, to her power, and her ability to match Agatha stride-for-stride in all they did.

Moments of the past blurred with instances of the present. Of her darling Nicky, a child as much Rio’s as her own. Of Teen, a boy so like Nicky, who had woken from death to say he didn’t blame Rio for what she had to do.

Would Nicky think the same?

Would Nicky understand?

Would he forgive Agatha for still loving his mother so desperately, even though she was the one who had taken him and led him towards the beyond, out of Agatha’s reach.

As she glanced at Billy’s face, so open and free of bitterness, even after everything he had endured in his short life the answer became clear, an answer that had been blurred from her view through the haze of her grief for so long.

Of course he would .

That was all it took for her to turn and grab Lilia's shoulders with both hands, her urgency now eclipsing all other thoughts and feelings.

“I’m going to get our green witch back”.

Lilia smiled at her as a few more tears slid from her eyes to graze over her lined cheeks, “damn straight”.

And before Agatha could even ask, Lilia tilted her head towards the house shrouded in shadow in front of the yard, “she’s not far”.

Agatha didn’t need to hear anything else beyond that and on nimble feet, she shot forward, taking the porch steps three at a time before slamming through the back door into the house.

It was silent inside and there was no definitive clues as to where Rio was, but she allowed her instincts and heart to lead her upstairs to Agnes’s bedroom; the bedroom she and her dear neighbour Rio had shared more often than not, even whilst under the flaky disguise of mere friendship.

She turned into the room and felt her heart start to pound in fear when she found it empty. Spinning in a wide circle, her panic only heightened until a shadow in the corner rippled and from it swept her wife, with a subdued, almost fearful expression on her face.

Chapter Notes

My guys, we made it. I am in shock that I wrote a fic this long and actually finished it! But at last it's finally here, the final chapter!

This chapter is, to put it plainly, basically fluff. I figured this entire fic has been a rollercoaster of up's and down's with a predominance for angst. So, I wanted to sweeten the happy ending with a chapter of fluff that reflected how I, in a dream world, wanted the show to end.

I said in my first ever note for this fic that I needed to exorcise my Agathario demons by writing this, and I think it worked gang. I think writing this long, long story healed me and I hope, ever the optimist, that it helped heal all of you guys who wanted a happy ending for this chaotic pair too.

Of course, I would like to once again thank all of you guys who have left the sweetest comments and given kudos. I cherish each comment and appreciate your feedback/support more than I can say. It really does help motivate fic writers, especially when we hit a bit of a slump in a story, so thank you <3

And of course, for a final time, I really hope you enjoy! It's been a blast! xoxox
