" Agatha Harkness! ” Jen cried out, evidently horrified at her lewd insinuation.

“These bitches,” Agatha murmured with an eyeroll, talking over Jen's muffled ranting. She then winked and shot Rio a lascivious smirk as she drawled, “now where were we?”

Rio didn’t hear anything else Jen shouted through the door after that, for her one-sided argument was promptly drowned out by the husky groans Agatha was drawing from Rio’s throat.

XXXXXX

Four hours promptly turned into six.

It would have been five, but Rio had felt the urgent need to repay her wife’s arduous generosity and didn’t cease or desist until Agatha was flushed pink, panting breathlessly, and damp with sweat.

Rio crawled up her body, relishing the slide of her skin against Agatha’s to plant a possessive kiss against her lips. Lips that felt far drier than they had a few hours before, promptly reminding Rio that although she didn’t experience things like hunger or thirst, her mortal wife certainly did.

“I think...” Rio whispered between branding kisses across Agatha’s throat, “...you are in need of some sustenance”.

“No, I don’t. I just need you to do that thing with your tongue again," Agatha groaned petulantly, before then groaning again. Although, this time it wasn’t a petulant sound, but rather one of arduous recollection, “fuck, I missed your mouth”.

Rio smirked at her and pressed another soft kiss to her lips, “and you have my mouth, forever. But right now I need to do my duty as your wife and feed you”.

Agatha rolled her eyes, although Rio could see the humour in the gesture, before poking a single sharp finger right into Rio’s forehead, “I nearly forgot how attentive you are to my humanly needs". She dragged her hands around to the small of Rio's back and started to gently scratch her nails up the length of her spine, “I can think of something else you can feed me though, something that begins with a P and rhymes with -”.

Her sentence was cut short by Rio pressing a hand over her mouth, although Rio's amusement at Agatha's determination to stay precisely where they were was promptly evidenced by the deep chuckle that escaped her throat.

“Come on,” Rio drawled, lifting herself up from Agatha’s body so she could grab her by the hand and haul her up. Agatha, ever the helpful witch, went entirely limp and refused to stand.

Rio tugged at her for a few more moments before with a faux-aggrieved sigh, she snapped her fingers to transport Agatha with a flash of emerald green smoke, from laying prone on the bed to standing by the door.

Agatha’s jaw dropped at being magically manhandled, although she quickly caught herself and narrowed her eyes instead, crossing her arms tightly over her chest. Which admittedly, was rather distracting for Rio, considering she was still entirely nude.

“How about this…” Rio murmured, sauntering closer to Agatha in order to press her against the wall with the length of her body, “...you come downstairs with me for half an hour to eat some food and have a drink, and afterwards I’ll do that thing with my tongue as many times as you want”.

One of Agatha’s eyebrow arched with interest as she looped both her arms around Rio’s neck, “as many times as I want?”

Rio nodded before bowing her head beneath Agatha’s jaw to whisper kisses along her throat, “as many times as you want”.

Agatha paused, pretending to consider Rio’s generous offer before sighing loudly, “fine. I’ll bite”.

She then clicked her fingers, conjuring silk robes for each of them. A Rich amethyst for herself and a deep emerald green for Rio. Agatha then grabbed her hand and started to drag Rio through the bedroom door and down the stairs, now entirely focussed on meeting Rio’s terms in order to cash in her prize.

The murmur of voices could be heard from the lounge, but Agatha swept passed the open doorway, hauling Rio behind her the entire length of the corridor to the kitchen, where a selection of empty pizza boxes stained with grease had been abandoned on the kitchen island.

Agatha rifled through them with her free hand, hunting for an uneaten piece, only to come up empty. “ Those bitches ,” she hissed, before once again dragging Rio after her back towards the living room.

“Did you hags eat all the pizza?” She demanded the moment they crossed the threshold, glaring with narrowed eyes at the small gaggle of witches.

“Oh Agatha, how lovely to see you,” Lilia drawled from the couch, dabbing a napkin to the corner of her mouth as though she were finishing a meal in a five-star restaurant, and not a greasy pizza slice straight out of the box.

“Don’t give me that fake sweet shit Calderu,” Agatha snapped, turning her attention to Alice who had smothered a laugh in her elbow at the sight they made in the doorway, each of them flushed, with unmistakable bed hair, and bruises speckling their throats, “something funny to you Alice ?”

“Oh no,” Alice said slowly, dragging her eyes up and down their barely robed figures, “there’s absolutely nothing funny about this”.

“Funny isn’t the word for it,” Teen said, pulling that universal expression all teenagers managed to adopt when facing the reality the adults they knew actually had sex sometimes, “more like mortifying ”.

“It’s alright,” Agatha sniped back, pulling Rio toward the free armchair in the corner where she promptly sat and tugged her down onto her lap with both hands, “we used protection”.

Teen mimed throwing up over the side of the sofa, much to Alice’s amusement who slapped the back of her hand against his shoulder to make him stop.

“We ate all of the pizza,” Lilia advised, ever the voice of reason, “but we can order a few more if you’re hungry?”

“Er, duh ,” Agatha replied, running her fingers through the back of Rio’s hair to untangle the knots she had put in it, “we are as hungry as you guys were before you stuffed yourselves stupid… or even more now considering how many calories we just burned fuc-”.

“Okay! Yikes ,” Jen cut her off quickly, pulling her cell phone out to redial the pizza place in the centre of town, “what do you both want?”

“Meat-Feast,” Agatha yelled out immediately.

Jen looked to Rio next, awaiting her order. Rio glanced around, eyes widening slightly for not knowing the correct option to select for herself.

“You strike me as a pineapple-on-pizza type,” Billy said, although not at all unkindly.

“Oh totally,” Alice agreed, nodding solemnly, almost as though this particular decision would define Rio's character in her mind. Human's and their strange formalities , she couldn't help thinking to herself.

Rio shrugged, truly unbothered by whatever pizza she ended up with. She wasn’t hungry after all, like usual. But she still enjoyed the motion of eating, and felt a sudden strong desire to take part in this most human of rituals, especially with these particular humans, her coven.

“One meat feast, and one Hawaiian,” Jen repeated and rang the order through, “it will be here in twenty minutes”.

Agatha groaned loudly, as though the very thought of waiting for her pizza was beyond arduous, before poking Teen with her bare toes, “get your auntie Agatha a drink won’t you. I’m parched”.

“Get your own drink Agatha,” Jen scolded, standing up to push her leg away from Billy, who laughed at their antics and got to his feet anyway, “what do you want?”

Agatha smirked triumphantly at Jen before pointing a single finger at the cabinet set against the back wall, “ol’ Agnes had a bottle of Jack hidden away behind that stack of dusty encyclopaedia's”.

This was news to Rio, who turned toward Agatha with an arched eyebrow, “oh she did, did she?”

She received a devilish smirk in reply, “you had your secrets sweetheart, and I had mine”.

Billy fetched the bottle and passed it over to Agatha. She took a deep swig before offering it up to Rio, who shook her head in reply. She didn’t see the point in alcohol, she couldn’t really feel the effects of it after all and she didn’t think it tasted all that nice either.

Alice made grabby hand motions at Agatha who scowled back, but did eventually give the bottle up to be passed around the adults of the group.

“Death doesn’t drink?” Lilia commented, taking a ladylike sip of her own after Alice's not quite ladylike one, “I suppose it’s a comfort that you don’t reap under the influence”.

“Nope,” Rio said, leaning back against Agatha who wrapped both arms around her waist and held onto her tightly, whilst leaning closer to rest her chin on Rio’s shoulder. “I can’t get drunk and it tastes grim, so never saw the point”.

“You can’t get drunk?” Teen asked, his voice lilting curiously.

“Nah,” she confirmed, “don’t know what thirst feels like either”.

Teen stared at her with awed, fascinated eyes for a few moments, before breathing out, “that’s so cool". His eyes flickered then, taking in the entirety of Rio’s face as he started to gear himself up to ask the question she knew he had been dying to since it was revealed she was Death.

She wondered if he was going to ask if he could ask the question first, or whether the question itself would escape his mouth like an eager rabbit wriggling free from a snare.

“Can I ask you a question? I don’t want to be rude”.

She smirked to herself and nodded her consent to hearing his enquiry.

“Your face…” he began, evidently unsure of how to phrase his question without saying something offensive, “you can just like… dissolve your skin?”

“Sure can,” she said, voice deadpan, “I can do this too”. She then morphed her face from the beautiful visage they were all used to into a detailed impression of Edvard Munch’s Scream, including the elongated mouth, deathly pale skin, and white eyes with mere pinpricks for pupils.

All of the witches in the room, besides Agatha, reared back in horror as she allowed her face to return to it’s normal façade. she looked round at them all, grinning broadly with wide, mad eyes, “cool, huh?”

Agatha chuckled huskily from over her shoulder, knowing precisely what face Rio had just shown them all.

Teen was the first to recover from the shock and was quick to lean forward again, now appearing even more intrigued than he had before.

“That’s so freaky ,” he laughed, “can you change everything about your face? Like on a whim?”

“Sure,” she admitted with another vague shrug of her shoulders for it was true, she could. Yet, ever since their child had been born resembling the face she wore now, the same face Agatha had fallen in love with, she had claimed this particular face as hers to keep forever, “I can do this too”.

She blinked and suddenly her hair was platinum blonde. Teen drew in a sharp breath, although this time not from fear, but out of sheer admiration for her ability to gift herself the type of dye-job many women would willingly spend hundreds of dollars on.

Jen whistled appreciatively, “damn, that colour suits you”.

Alice nodded her agreement, looking impressed, “I guess it's true. Blonde’s really do have more fun”.

Agatha placed her fingers on Rio's jaw and drew her round to face her so she could see the change properly. By the darkening of her eyes, Rio knew she liked it, “ why haven’t you done this before? You look…” Her jaw flapped uselessly for a few moments as she tried to find a word that would summarise how good she thought Rio looked. But Rio, who had always preferred her hair brown, like their son, simply smirked, blinked once and turned the blonde strands back to their original dark chestnut.

Agatha’s eyes narrowed and her mouth opened to argue when she did so, however Rio never got to hear whatever quip she was going to say, for a knock on the door distracted them all from Rio’s demonstration.

“Pizza!” Agatha cried loudly, before once again lifting a leg to poke Teen with her toes, “be a dear and fetch auntie Agatha and auntie Rio’s pizza’s, won't you. We’re exhausted after all that time we spent-”.

And once again, Agatha’s sentence was cut off by a joint cry of horror, as Teen sprung to his feet and sprinted to fetch their pizzas from the delivery guy.

Rio smirked at her wife’s antics, ever amused at Agatha’s ability to sow chaos wherever she was, even here, in the most domestic of settings. She shuddered when Agatha leaned in close to press a long kiss to the side of her neck, before dragging her lips up to whisper even more mischief into Rio’s ear.

“ Works like a charm, every damn time ”.

And as Rio chomped down on her first slice of pizza, enjoying the sweet tang of pineapple and the satisfying pull of stringy cheese, she couldn’t help but agree.

It didn’t take them long to eat or drink themselves to satisfaction and predictably, as soon as they had finished their meal Agatha was digging impatient fingers into her waist, hinting very unsubtly that she wanted them to proceed back upstairs and for Rio to make good on her part of their bargain.

Rio turned to glance at her from over her shoulder, a wolfish smirk on her face at Agatha’s insistence. Agatha grinned back at her, without any shame nor concern that everyone in the room knew the type of sinful things that were currently on her mind.

However, just as Rio was sliding from her lap to lead her back upstairs, the entire house shook and a series of loud bangs echoed through the floor from the basement below.

“What the hell was that?” Jen asked, eyes wide with concern as Lilia stood and started to drift towards the door that led to the kitchen.

“Ah right on time,” she sighed as though expecting such a moment, which considering Lilia’s talents, she probably was.

Teen, Jen, and Alice immediately followed after her, but Agatha held Rio back and tried to tug her in the other direction towards the stairs, evidently still intent on picking up where they had left off.

Rio allowed herself to be led toward the stairs as a smirk started to blossom across her face at Agatha's impatience, however it soon dropped into a frown when one of her internal threads, the threads that were unique to Death and demanded her attention, started to insist she follow the others down to the basement instead.

Agatha turned when she felt Rio’s body halt in place. Her jaw dropped to say something, something undoubtedly snarky and rude, yet the moment she saw Rio’s frown she knew duty was calling out to her.

She sighed loudly and dramatically, “even now? We can’t even have a day?”

Rio smiled at her softly and brought her wife’s hand to her lips so she could press a kiss to the back of it, “unfortunately death doesn’t wait for anything, not even afternoon tryst’s”.

She continued speaking over Agatha’s petulant humph of frustration.

“But you’ll be pleased to hear I don’t have to travel far for this one. For whatever... or whoever needs my attention… is currently in your basement”.

Agatha’s eyes widened before immediately narrowing, “my basement? ” She said, her voice heavy with disbelief.

“Yep,” Rio confirmed, tugging Agatha after the others toward the stairs that led down into the basement. It was here they found the rest of their coven standing awkwardly around what appeared, to them at least, to be a hovering cloud of fog which had materialised just above the section of floor that had been the entrance to The Road.

Rio knew what it was the moment she saw it, and so did Agatha, if the groan of frustration she let out the moment she spotted it from over Rio’s shoulder was any sort of indicator.

“Oh for fuck sake , I thought we were done with all of this bullshit,” she groaned out, before storming forward to wave a flippant hand at the cloud, trying to forcefully disperse it back into the atmosphere.

“Agatha,” Rio choked on a burst of sudden laughter, “you can’t just... shoo her away, you know that”.

“ Ugh ,” she groused, before turning with the same flapping hand still held out in front of her, although this time it was directed at Rio, “get rid of it”.

Rio rolled her eyes at her wife's impatience and stepped closer to the fog. “She’s not an it,” Rio said with an arched look at Agatha, before addressing the fog directly, “are you?”

The fog flickered slightly, as though in response to Rio’s question before it started to shimmer and shift even more so, like static being sped up.

“Er,” Alice drawled, “can someone fill the rest of us in?”

“It’s a ghost,” Rio explained as the haze continued to swirl and crystalise, “I did wonder where she got to”.

“Where who got to?” Jen asked pointedly, stepping closer to Rio in order to study the fog and see if she could pick out any identifiable features from it's misty haze.

It was Billy who stepped forward, having put all of the clues together, “it’s Sharon isn’t it?”

Agatha frowned at him, “who's Sharon?”

“What’s up Mrs Davies, it's good to see you,” Alice said politely, even though it was clear she was as perturbed as the others to be facing the ghost of a woman she had recently watched die. “Er yeah, totally! Heey Sharon,” Jen drawled as Lilia gave an airy, unbothered wave, and Agatha forced one of those overtly false grins onto her face as she hissed at Rio.

“ Mrs Hart's ghost?! ” Agatha exclaimed, pointing a severe finger at Rio, “you disappeared to fetch her when she died! How is she still here?!”

Rio shrugged, not at all phased by Mrs Davies sudden appearance. This wasn’t her first rodeo after all. “She freaked out the moment she realised she was dead, and then went full spectral before I could grab her”. She shrugged again and peered at Agatha over her shoulder. “I knew she’d turn up at some point, her soul couldn’t stay on The Road forever. She was probably spat out the same time as us, the moment Billy’s hex failed”.

But her error immediately became clear the moment Jen grabbed Rio’s arm and pulled her round to face her, her eyes wide with alarm, “ Billy’s hex?! ”

“Nope,” Agatha ground out, “none of them did”.

Must have been out of date, I swear these grocery store's are getting more and more lazy when it comes down to labelling their produce. It's like a friend of mine, Helen from salsa class, she ate some bad salmon from Walmart. She took one bite and the next morning: dead”.

If Teen were to try and explain, it could make her spirit stubbornly cling around until all of her questions were answered. And Rio didn't want to consider how long that might take. After all, the less ghosts floating around the mortal plain intent on evading Rio, the better.

Next, Rio’s eyes drifted to Lilia who also nodded at her once before promptly sweeping towards Teen in a whirl of colourful fabric, efficiently corralling him upstairs in a flurry of maternal concern, “come on Teen, let’s go see if there’s any of Agatha’s pizza left to eat”.

“This really is so bizarre!” Mrs Davies said as she glanced around at the rest of them, before bringing her transparent hand up to her face, “being dead isn’t at all what I thought it would be like”.

That was Rio's cue.

“Sharon?” She asked, voice soft, “are you ready to go?”

Sharon jerked when Rio spoke, as though she had already started fading away. It was pretty standard for ghosts who weren’t determined to be so to do that, for the moment they calmed down and accepted they were dead the call of the beyond started to draw them home.

“Ready now?” She repeated, suddenly sounding like a lost child.

Rio nodded at her and smiled kindly, She was always relieved when a ghost was amicable and willing to go with her, “are you ready to come with me? I can take you to see your mother. Would you like that?”

Mrs Davies gasped and covered her mouth as her eyes started to glisten with pale, misty tears, “I get to see my mom? ”

She drew closer and cupped Agatha’s jaw with her palm, smirking slightly at the way her wife was now staring at her through narrowed eyes.

“You’re leaving,” It was a statement, one gilded with clinginess. Clinginess Rio cherished.

“I am. But it won’t take long,” Rio tilted her head towards Sharon, “she’s ready”.

Agatha pouted for a moment before rolling her eyes, “fine, go be a wraith”. She grabbed Rio by a fistful of her dark robes, robes she had conjured to flow around her body the moment she knew a soul was in need of her, “but you better hurry back to me".

Rio grinned and pressed a lingering kiss to Agatha’s lips, “wild horses couldn’t stop me”.

“Yeah, yeah,” Agatha droned at Rio’s smooth-talking. Although, the small smile that blossomed on her face afterwards gave away her true thoughts on Rio's words of devotion, “go on. Mrs Hart won’t reap herself”.

And for the last time, Mrs Davies rolled her eyes at Agatha Harkness and groaned out a frustrated, “it’s Sharon! ” She then took Rio’s hand in hers and allowed herself to be led through the veil to a home with a white picket fence, a home where her mother had been waiting for her, a home where her mother met her with open arms, a broad, beaming smile, and cheeks shining with tears.

Rio found her way home a few hours later, having been delayed by the call of another soul from one town over on her way back.

She decided to come in through the front door, just like a human might. There was something so appealingly domestic about it, about returning to this house that she had lived in with Agnes, only now knowing it was Agatha she was returning to.

An Agatha who loved her, an Agatha who, if the light shining through the bedroom window was any indication, was still waiting up for Rio to come home.

She closed the front door quietly, and just before reaching the bottom of the stairs paused at an unusual noise coming from the living room.

Sweeping forward on silent feet, for Rio was Death and had been crafted to creep unheard through the world, she peered inside and was forced to immediately smother a laugh at the sight her eyes landed upon.

Lilia was asleep on the armchair, head tilted back and legs up on coffee table, mouth open and snoring loudly.

Alice had claimed the couch. Both her arms were thrown above her head, and her face was tucked into the back cushion.

Teen, being the youngest member of this strange coven that continued to hang around, like a group a stray cats who they had fed a single time and now gathered together everyday expecting more treats, had been demoted to the rug on the floor, on which he was sprawled under a thin blanket, with a decorative couch cushion shoved under his head.

Rio snorted in amusement and turned silently to head up the stairs. The first bedroom, the one Rio had used during Agatha’s year as Agnes, was closed off from the hallway, the door shut tight.

Rio smirked to herself, sensing a heartbeat from behind the wood.

Obviously Jen had either won a bet, or simply demanded the privilege of her own bedroom. Either could be true.

Rio considered banging loudly against the wood for a moment, the thought of winding Jen up amusing enough to draw a small chuckle from her throat. However she resisted the urge, for a far more enticing prize was on the horizon, one beckoning her closer by the spill of warm light pouring through a small gap in the doorframe into the hallway, and by the second, far more familiar heartbeat she could hear thrumming peacefully on the second floor of this strange, stolen house.

She pushed the door open and stood still for a moment, savouring the scene before her.

Agatha was asleep too, although she was propped up on the bed by a mass of pillows behind her, still sitting above the covers. Stubborn witch that she was, it was clear that she had been intent on staying awake until Rio came home. But her fatigue, which was entirely justifiable following their adventures on The Road, battling the remaining members of the Salem Seven, and having her memories returned to her mind rather forcefully, had evidently won the war and she had nodded off.

She was still wrapped in the robe she had spelled to appear earlier on in the day, with only a thin blanket thrown over the top of her bare legs to keep the worst of the chill off. An old spell book was resting in her lap, still open on the page she had been reading when sleep had finally managed to claim her.

Rio stepped quietly into the room and closed the door behind her, unwilling to remove her eyes from Agatha as she did so.

For this image, this homely scene that she had returned to, was all she had craved for as long as she had known what the sensation of craving even felt like.

It was a picture she had born witness to before, although it was a fair statement to claim that although the witch at it’s centre hadn’t changed all that much, the environment that surrounded her certainly had.

Before it had been wooden walls, a simple mattress stuffed with straw, the smell of woodsmoke, and the glow of candlelight.

Now it was thick carpet, Egyptian cotton sheets, cheap artwork on the walls, and the gentle hum of electricity.

Though it was still, as it had been then, the most beautiful thing Rio had ever seen.

And Rio had seen the universe.

Silently, so as to not disturb her, Rio waved a single hand down herself, transforming her dark robes of duty and death into a robe of emerald green, the same one Agatha had conjured for her earlier that day.

On silent feet, she padded round to Agatha’s side first. She put her book on the bedside table, switched off the lamp, and tugged the covers out from beneath her legs to cover her with them properly, before moving around the bed to her own side, where she also slid under the thick duvet.

Rolling over, she wrapped her arm around Agatha’s waist and pulled. Gently, she tugged her further down the bed so her head would rest on Rio’s shoulder and not on the stack of pillows she had been resting against before.

She closed her eyes, hopeful Agatha would remain undisturbed and reclaim some of the sleep Rio knew she was in dire need of. Yet, she knew her wife had woken up the moment she felt her stretch languidly beside her and tightly grab a fistful of Rio’s collar, keeping her close.

“You’re here,” was mumbled tiredly against the skin of her throat, her breath a gentle flutter.

“I am,” Rio whispered back, pulling Agatha even closer with the arm she was using to support her wife's body.

“I was waiting for you,” Agatha sighed out, stretching a second time before, as though she had never awoken, she was suddenly asleep again; her body growing relaxed beside Rio's, slumping into her slightly as her breathing deepened.

And Rio, suddenly taken aback and deeply moved by the reality of finally being here, with Agatha, at feeling the warmth of her body against her own, of her heartbeat thrumming beneath her ribs, and the gentle inhalation and exhalation of her chest, Rio couldn’t help but grin to herself, a broad beaming smile that almost seemed to glow in the shadows of the dark, still night.

“I was waiting for you too sweetheart, for a long time,” Rio admitted quietly, pressing her lips to Agatha’s forehead. She then finally allowed her body to relax into the soft mattress beneath her, and the soft body beside her, “but we’re here now, where we should be. Together”.

And even though Agatha had fallen asleep, she still snuggled closer to Rio as though she had heard her declaration and was responding to it. Her fist tightened even more around her handful of Rio’s robes, and she mumbled two words into the skin of Rio’s throat, two words that made Rio’s loving smile bloom all the brighter, and tears of relief fall from her eyes.

“ Missed you ”.

Rio pressed another kiss to her wife’s forehead, knowing that Agatha’s subconscious confession didn’t just mean the few hours they had been separated that very evening, but rather a far larger timespan, entire lifetimes even.

“I missed you too, my love. So much," she brought her hand up and pushed a wayward lock of Agatha’s wild hair back from her face, “sleep now. I’ll be here in the morning, and every day after. I promise”.

And Death, as she did with all things, kept her word to her wife, who slept peacefully in her arms that night, and every night after too.
